# Pi Integration Contract

The runtime depends on a small, named surface from `@earendil-works/pi-coding-agent`. Each item below is the loom 1.0 contract; behaviour outside this surface is non-load-bearing and may be revised without spec changes. The loom 1.0 contract is anchored to `@earendil-works/pi-coding-agent` at the range declared by [*Host prerequisites — Pi SDK pin*](#pi-sdk-pin) below (the single source of truth for the supported Pi minor in the spec corpus); the lock-step pin requiring `@earendil-works/pi-agent-core`, `@earendil-works/pi-ai`, and `@earendil-works/pi-tui` to resolve to the same minor-version line as the installed `@earendil-works/pi-coding-agent`, the provenance for that lock-step, and the re-validation obligation on a Pi minor bump are owned by *Host prerequisites — Pi SDK pin* below. The contributor checklist that gates any such bump — the artefacts produced and the build-time tests that must be green before the `peerDependencies` range moves — is owned by [Pi version bump procedure](#pi-version-bump-procedure) at the end of this page.

**Host prerequisites.** Four host-side prerequisites are load-bearing for the contract below:

1. <a id="pi-sdk-pin"></a>*Pi SDK pin.* The supported Pi minor is pinned at `@earendil-works/pi-coding-agent ~0.75.5`. This anchor (`#pi-sdk-pin`) is the **single source of truth** for that literal range in the spec corpus: every other reference to the supported Pi minor in the spec corpus MUST cite this anchor rather than restating the literal range, so each Pi minor bump is a one-character edit at this site (mirrored mechanically by the manifest lock-step sub-paragraph below) rather than an N-site sweep. The spec orientation block (see [`spec.md` — Orientation — Prerequisites](../spec.md#orientation)) references this pin by location rather than restating the literal value, as do every other Pi-version-mentioning paragraph elsewhere in PIC and on the sibling topic pages ([`binder.md`](./binder.md#strict-capability-requirement), [`diagnostics.md`](./diagnostics.md), [`future-considerations.md`](./future-considerations.md#v1-non-goals)). The lock-step minor-version line is inherited from `@earendil-works/pi-coding-agent`'s own `dependencies` block, which pins `@earendil-works/pi-agent-core`, `@earendil-works/pi-ai`, and `@earendil-works/pi-tui` at the same `~X.Y.Z` minor-version line. All four packages are released together from the `pi-mono` monorepo; no skew across the four is supported, and loom does not attempt to detect or accommodate skew. A Pi minor bump moves all four together; before the loom `peerDependencies` range is widened, the contributor MUST follow [Pi version bump procedure](#pi-version-bump-procedure) below — the build-time `peerDependencies` literal-read assertion and the build-time SDK surface-inventory assertion are the mechanical gates that fail the build until the procedure has been completed. Loom does not at runtime read `pi-coding-agent`'s `package.json` to verify the upstream pin — doing so would re-introduce the very skew-tolerance disclaimed above; the build-time literal-read assertion is the gate that keeps the four `peerDependencies` minors aligned. Loom's `peerDependencies` block declares all four packages as belt-and-braces; the redundancy is intentional and surfaces a clear install-time error under package managers (pnpm/yarn) that do not auto-deduplicate transitive peer-dep ranges.

   <a id="pi-sdk-pin-manifest-lock-step"></a>*Manifest lock-step (one legitimate restatement site).* The four `@earendil-works/*` entries in `package.json#peerDependencies` (`pi-coding-agent`, `pi-agent-core`, `pi-ai`, `pi-tui`) MUST literally equal the canonical `~0.75.5` range stated above, because npm consumes the manifest mechanically and the manifest cannot anchor-cite. The manifest is therefore the one legitimate non-spec restatement of the pin literal, and is lock-stepped to this anchor on the same editorial-convention basis as [GOV-12](./governance.md#gov-12)'s aggregator lock-step convention (a PR that bumps the literal at this anchor co-edits the four `package.json` entries in the same commit; the build-time `peerDependencies` literal-read assertion gated by [Pi version bump procedure — step 2](#pi-version-bump-procedure) below is the mechanical witness on the manifest side, and a partial landing where the spec literal and the manifest literal disagree fails that assertion). The `typebox` peer-dep entry is **not** part of this lock-step — it is pinned to `"*"` per the *typebox* sub-paragraph below.

   *Deliberate deviation from Pi's bundled-package convention.* Pi's `@earendil-works/pi-coding-agent` `docs/packages.md` — *Dependencies* prescribes `"*"` as the `peerDependencies` range for all five bundled packages it names (`@earendil-works/pi-ai`, `@earendil-works/pi-agent-core`, `@earendil-works/pi-coding-agent`, `@earendil-works/pi-tui`, `typebox`). Loom deliberately deviates from that convention for the four `@earendil-works/*` entries by pinning them to the [loom 1.0 Pi-SDK pin range](#pi-sdk-pin) rather than `"*"`. The deviation gives up Pi-prescribed alignment (a future reader auditing loom's packaging against `packages.md` will find four entries that do not match the convention) and buys install-time skew detection on the package managers most production hosts use: `pnpm` (in its default `node-linker=isolated` mode) and `yarn` do not auto-deduplicate transitive peer-dep ranges, so a tilde-range pin in loom's `peerDependencies` causes the install to fail loudly when the host has resolved any of the four `@earendil-works/*` packages outside the pinned minor line, whereas a `"*"` declaration would silently accept the skew and defer the failure to a runtime `TypeError` at the first SDK call site. The four-anchor invariant is what the build-time `peerDependencies` literal-read test, the [Step 0 (d) Peer-dep version](#entry-capability-probe) probe, and the literal-anchor list in [Pi version bump procedure](#pi-version-bump-procedure) below are built around. The fifth package, `typebox`, follows the convention (`"typebox": "*"`) — see the sub-paragraph immediately below — because the runtime's only `typebox` dependency is `Type.Unsafe`, whose call shape is stable across the TypeBox `0.x` → `1.x` line and therefore does not need install-time minor-skew detection. The `typebox` `"*"` declaration MUST NOT be collapsed into the four-entry tilde-pinned group: the two ranges are deliberately distinct and reflect different stability arguments (lock-step minor for the `@earendil-works/*` four; convention-following floor for `typebox`).

   *`typebox` (the fifth Pi-bundled package).* The four `@earendil-works/*` packages above are pinned at the [loom 1.0 Pi-SDK pin range](#pi-sdk-pin) per the lock-step rule. `typebox` is the fifth Pi-bundled package the loom runtime imports (only `Type.Unsafe`, per [*Target surface categories*](#audit-target-surface-categories) below (typebox carve-out)); per Pi's bundled-package convention (`@earendil-works/pi-coding-agent` `docs/packages.md` — *Dependencies*) it MUST be declared as `"typebox": "*"` so the host's bundled version wins. <a id="typebox-single-instance-precondition"></a>That bundled-version-wins outcome rests on two host-side preconditions the `"*"` declaration cannot itself guarantee: that the host bundles `typebox` at all, and that the package manager dedupes the `"*"` range to the host's single bundled instance. The `"*"` range carries no version-pinning guarantee of its own — it expresses only "accept whatever the host resolves" — so neither precondition is enforced at install time. No runtime probe verifies `typebox` provenance or single-instance resolution beyond the `Type.Unsafe`-callability check owned by **Step 0 (e)** below: a deduping failure that resolves a second, separately-resolved `typebox` instance alongside the host's passes that callability check and is treated with the same undefined-behaviour posture as the **Silent shape drift** carve-out at [Post-probe SDK-shape drift](#post-probe-sdk-shape-drift) — the runtime is not required to detect it, and no diagnostic is owed for it. In that case the mis-resolution surfaces downstream of `pi.registerTool` as a wrong-schema-shape failure rather than as a clean `loom/load/host-incompatible` refusal at factory entry. The `"*"` literal MUST NOT be folded into the four-entry tilde-pinned group asserted by the build-time lock-step assertion; it is asserted by its own one-line build-time literal-read assertion. The runtime's single load-bearing dependency on the bundled `typebox` namespace — the presence of `Type.Unsafe` as a callable function — is checked at extension-factory entry by **Step 0 (e)** below, which routes a missing or renamed member to `loom/load/host-incompatible` with `details.kind = "typebox-shape"` rather than to a runtime-time `TypeError` at the first tool-registration call (factory time for prompt mode, spawn time for subagent mode). This mirrors the framing already used for `AgentSession.prototype.abort` in **Step 0 (c)**: both are single-symbol Pi-bundled imports whose absence would otherwise crash the runtime at a registration call site rather than refuse cleanly at factory entry.
2. *Binder model.* Non-bypass looms require a structured-output-capable LLM resolved via `ctx.modelRegistry` for the binder pass described in [Slash-Command Argument Binding](./binder.md). When the registry cannot resolve a binder model, the loom fails to load with `loom/load/binder-model-unresolved`. Under the [loom 1.0 Pi-SDK pin](#pi-sdk-pin) the strict-capability probe is degraded and surfaces as `loom/load/binder-model-strict-capability-unknown` (W). Bypass cases (no-params, single-string with no default) skip the binder call entirely. loom 1.0 has no global binder opt-out; bypass is structural and per-loom.
3. *Binder credentials.* The binder reaches its model through the same `ctx.modelRegistry` / `Model<Api>` path (pinned at [model-registry surface](#model-registry-pin) below) Pi uses for its own queries; credentials are not stored, fetched, or cached by loom. Loom relies on whatever credential resolution Pi already performs for the resolved model.
4. *Pi-supplied `AbortSignal`.* Pi delivers an `AbortSignal` to every extension entry point loom uses — `ctx.signal` on the slash-command `ExtensionCommandContext` and the `signal` parameter of `tool.execute(...)`. The Web-standard `AbortSignal` / `AbortController` shape (the Node-bundled WHATWG implementation) is a fixed-shape SDK precondition; the canonical member-with-kind enumeration the runtime depends on is pinned by [Step 0 (b)](#entry-capability-probe) below. Subagent mode does not consume a `createAgentSession({ signal })` option — `CreateAgentSessionOptions` has no `signal` field in the loom 1.0 Pi SDK pin, so passing one would be silently ignored — and instead consumes the `AgentSession.abort()` capability on the handle returned by `createAgentSession(...)`, invoked from a one-shot `loomAbort.signal` listener registered at spawn time; see **Subagent session lifecycle** and **Cancellation source** below. The loom runtime's own `AbortController` wrapping rule is in **Cancellation source** below; this prerequisite is what guarantees the inputs that rule consumes.

<a id="loom-package-implementation-dependencies-loom-1-0"></a><a id="loom-package-implementation-dependencies-v1"></a>
**Loom-package implementation dependencies (loom 1.0).** The two `*Recommended recipe (non-normative).*` paragraphs under [Step 0 (Capability probe)](#entry-capability-probe) — [(a) Node floor](#step-0-a-recommended-recipe) and [(d) Peer-dep version](#step-0-d-recommended-recipe) — consume `semver.satisfies` and `semver.valid`; the loom 1.0 implementation choice that satisfies those recipes is the [`semver`](https://www.npmjs.com/package/semver) npm package, declared in the loom package's `dependencies` block, with `@types/semver` declared in `devDependencies` for the corresponding TypeScript bindings. This is an implementation-side recipe rather than a normative contract: the comparator-swap escape hatch already promised by those two paragraphs remains genuine, and a future swap to a different SemVer implementation is permitted on the conditions they enumerate. The pinned version range that satisfies loom 1.0 is an implementation choice carried in the loom package's `package.json`; this paragraph names the dependency, not its version.

<a id="session-binding-contract"></a>
**Session-binding contract.** A Pi extension instance is bound to exactly one active user session at any given time. The closed set of reason values Pi delivers to the runtime's teardown handler on session-end matches the `SessionShutdownEvent['reason']` union declared at `dist/core/extensions/types.d.ts` in `@earendil-works/pi-coding-agent` (the [loom 1.0 Pi-SDK pin](#pi-sdk-pin) from item 1 above); the closed reason set itself is owned by sub-step 4's [Unknown-reason rule](#unknown-reason-rule) below and is pinned at build time by the bidirectional `SessionShutdownEvent['reason']` type-equality assertion described at [Pi version bump procedure — step 5](#pi-version-bump-procedure) below. The premise that a session-only swap keeps the same extension instance loaded against the swapped-in session is pinned as [Host prerequisites for the degraded-state branch — presupposition (a)](#degraded-state-host-prerequisites) below.

<a id="degraded-state-host-prerequisites"></a>
**Host prerequisites for the degraded-state branch.** The [`reason: "new" | "resume" | "fork"` edge-case bullet](#session-only-reason-degraded-state) under **Extension entry point** sub-step 4 below depends on three Pi SDK behaviours that neither the loom 1.0 Pi-SDK pin's `dist/core/extensions/types.d.ts` nor the `ExtensionAPI` / `ExtensionContext` surfaces enumerated above pin as a typed contract. The loom 1.0 runtime treats each as a **presupposition** in the same sense as [Future Considerations — No concurrent user sessions in the same host process](./future-considerations.md#v1-non-goals) (which the same paragraph cites as the framing precedent for an unpinned host-behaviour assumption); detection of a Pi minor that violates any of them is by editorial review under [Pi version bump procedure](#pi-version-bump-procedure) below — the build-time SDK surface-inventory assertion is a presence check on the seven named SDK capabilities and does not enumerate behavioural invariants of this kind, so contributor-side editorial review against this enumerated list is the gate.

  (a) *Extension-instance survival across session-only `session_shutdown`.* When `event.reason ∈ {"new", "resume", "fork"}`, Pi keeps the same extension instance loaded against the new user session after the `session_shutdown` handler returns, and continues to route slash invocations on the swapped-in session to the same instance (so the closed-over `LoomRegistry` handle the slash-command `handler` registered in step 3 below consults — including its drained flag and `drainStateTag` — is the very registry the prior handler invocation drained and tag-transitioned). This is what makes the post-handler `"degraded-needs-reload"` slash note pinned by the bullet observable to the operator on the swapped-in session. A Pi minor that instantiates a fresh extension on `"new"` (or that re-routes post-swap slash invocations to a fresh closed-over registry) would silently invalidate the bullet's recovery-by-`/reload` framing — the fresh instance/registry would start with a non-drained `LoomRegistry` and dispatch normally, hiding the degradation rather than surfacing it. No SDK surface pins this behaviour.

  (b) *Multi-`session_shutdown` delivery permitted to a single instance.* Pi may deliver more than one `session_shutdown` event to the same extension instance — both re-entrant deliveries during an in-flight teardown and fresh follow-up deliveries after a prior session-only handler has returned. The handler's [**idempotent**](#idempotent-handler-clause) clause and the at-most-once-per-extension-instance-lifetime bound on `loom/host/session-shutdown-runtime-degraded` are written against this multi-delivery shape; a Pi minor that fires only one `session_shutdown` per instance leaves the **idempotent** clause vacuous but does not break the contract (the at-most-once bound holds trivially under at-most-one delivery). No SDK surface pins multi-delivery either way.

  (c) *`/reload` and `ctx.reload()` recovery.* Operator-issued `/reload` invokes Pi's `ctx.reload()` against the live (degraded) extension instance, and `ctx.reload()` tears down the extension runtime and re-invokes the registered extension factory, yielding a fresh runtime with a non-drained `LoomRegistry`. loom 1.0 has no fallback recovery path, so a Pi minor that changes either the slash dispatch routing of `/reload` or the runtime-invalidation/re-invocation semantics of `ctx.reload()` MUST be caught by editorial review under the bump procedure. The `reason: "new" | "resume" | "fork"` edge-case bullet's *Operator-issued `/reload`* sentence below and acceptance criterion (g) (the post-`/reload` fresh-runtime fixture) both presuppose this behaviour, and the at-most-once-per-extension-instance-lifetime bound on `loom/host/session-shutdown-runtime-degraded` is calibrated against the assumption that a fresh runtime starts a new lifetime; a Pi minor that no-ops `ctx.reload()` on an already-degraded extension, or routes `/reload` through a different facet, silently breaks recovery without tripping any other gate. No SDK surface pins this behaviour. Two corollaries follow from the *Operator-issued `/reload`* sentence above and govern how loom and Pi cooperatively keep that recovery path reachable on the degraded branch: **(c-i)** `/reload` is a Pi-host-owned slash name that Pi's slash dispatcher routes to `ctx.reload()` independently of any loom-registered `pi.registerCommand` handler, so the [drain-state-gated dispatch](#slash-handler-registration) short-circuit pinned at sub-step 3 below — which scopes only to loom-registered handlers (the `handler` value passed to every `pi.registerCommand(name, { description, handler })` call sub-step 3 makes) and routes through the `LoomRegistry.readDrainState()` three-arm enumeration — does **not** intercept `/reload` on the degraded `"degraded-needs-reload"` arm; the operator's `/reload` therefore reaches `ctx.reload()` even when every loom-registered slash handler in the same extension instance is short-circuiting on arm (c) of that enumeration. A Pi minor that demoted `/reload` to a `pi.registerCommand`-shaped handler (so loom's drain-state short-circuit would intercept it) is the same editorial-review failure mode the *slash dispatch routing of `/reload`* clause above already names. **(c-ii)** Loom MUST NOT register a `.loom` whose effective slash name (per [Discovery — Filename validity](./discovery.md), after `pi.looms` mapping, `as` rename, and basename hyphen-normalisation) is `reload`. A pending loom whose derived slash name resolves to `reload` is dropped at sub-step 3 below's session-start cross-format collision check on the same footing as any other collision against the [loom 1.0 cross-format collision source set](#v1-seam-pi-owned-subagents-collision-source-set) — assuming Pi's `/reload` surfaces in `pi.getCommands()` under a `SlashCommandSource` arm in that set, which is itself part of this prerequisite (c) and a Pi minor that hides `/reload` from `pi.getCommands()` MUST be caught by editorial review under the bump procedure on the same footing as the other clauses of (c) above — and emits the same `loom/load/cross-format-collision` diagnostic. The two corollaries together guarantee that on the degraded branch the operator's `/reload` reaches `ctx.reload()` without being shadowed by either the drain-state-gated short-circuit (covered by (c-i)) or a colliding loom registration (covered by (c-ii)).


**Extension entry point.** A single Pi extension module (`extensions/index.ts`, the file Pi auto-discovers from `package.json#pi.extensions = ["./extensions"]`) exporting the standard `default function (pi: ExtensionAPI)` factory.

<a id="entry-capability-probe"></a>
**Step 0 — Capability probe (precedes step 1 below).** Before any `pi.registerFlag`, `pi.registerCommand`, `pi.registerTool`, `pi.registerMessageRenderer`, or `pi.on` call — collectively, the **factory-time host-binding calls** — the factory runs a synchronous probe of three host preconditions in the **fixed order (a) → (b) → (c)** below and stops at the first failure (short-circuit). This paragraph is the **canonical source of truth** for every probe rule, the floor literal, the member-with-kind enumeration, and the factory-probable capability list; [`spec.md` — Host runtime preconditions 1–3](../spec.md#orientation) is informative orientation that forward-links here under [Governance — GOV-12](./governance.md). The JavaScript engine value model is a non-checked invariant by design and is **not** probed; it is owned by [Runtime Value Model — JavaScript engine assumptions](./runtime-value-model.md#javascript-engine-assumptions).

*The four pinned constants the probe consumes — Node floor, `AbortSignal` / `AbortController` member-with-kind list, factory-probable capability list, peer-dep range — live in **one source of truth** inside the extension module that the build-time literal-read assertions also consume.*

**(a) Node floor.** Compare `process.versions.node` against the pinned floor `>=22.19.0` under SemVer ordering, treating prerelease tags as eligible — a Node nightly or release-candidate build (e.g. `"23.0.0-nightly20250101abcdef"`) whose stable equivalent satisfies the floor MUST satisfy the check. The prerelease-eligibility clause is load-bearing and is part of the normative contract; an implementation that rejects qualifying prerelease builds violates this rule. `process.versions.node` is the bare version string (no leading `"v"`); do not pass `process.version`. A `process.versions.node` value that is not a syntactically valid SemVer string routes to `kind: "probe-failed"` (see *Self-failure* below), not `kind: "node-floor"`.

<a id="step-0-a-recommended-recipe"></a>
*Recommended recipe (non-normative).* `semver.satisfies(process.versions.node, ">=22.19.0", { includePrerelease: true })` from the [`semver`](https://www.npmjs.com/package/semver) npm package satisfies this contract; `semver.valid(process.versions.node)` discriminates the `"probe-failed"` route. A future swap to a different SemVer implementation (or a hand-rolled comparator) is permitted as long as the contract above — range membership with prerelease tags eligible, and a syntactic-validity check that routes failures to `"probe-failed"` — is preserved end-to-end.

**(b) `AbortSignal` / `AbortController` shape.** This sub-step is the **canonical source of truth** for the WHATWG `AbortSignal` / `AbortController` member surface the loom runtime depends on; spec.md Host runtime precondition 2 is informative orientation that forward-links here. The probe applies a per-member rule keyed on the member's `kind` (the table below is the source of truth, co-located with the member name in the extension module's pinned-constants block that the build-time surface-inventory assertion also consumes):

| Member                                       | Kind                  | Check                                                          |
|----------------------------------------------|-----------------------|----------------------------------------------------------------|
| `AbortController` (global)                   | `constructor`         | `typeof AbortController === "function"`                        |
| `AbortSignal` (global)                       | `constructor`         | `typeof AbortSignal === "function"`                            |
| `AbortController.prototype.abort`            | `prototype-method`    | `typeof AbortController.prototype.abort === "function"`        |
| `AbortSignal.any`                            | `static-method`       | `typeof AbortSignal.any === "function"`                        |
| `AbortSignal.timeout`                        | `static-method`       | `typeof AbortSignal.timeout === "function"`                    |
| `AbortSignal.prototype.throwIfAborted`       | `prototype-method`    | `typeof AbortSignal.prototype.throwIfAborted === "function"`   |
| `AbortSignal.prototype.addEventListener`     | `prototype-method`    | `typeof AbortSignal.prototype.addEventListener === "function"` |
| `AbortSignal.prototype.aborted`              | `prototype-property`  | `"aborted" in AbortSignal.prototype`                           |
| `AbortSignal.prototype.reason`               | `prototype-property`  | `"reason" in AbortSignal.prototype`                            |

The `prototype-property` rule is `in`-based, not `typeof`-based: `aborted` and `reason` are accessor properties whose getters throw `TypeError: Illegal invocation` when read off the prototype, so a `typeof === "function"` rule would refuse every conformant host. The probe MUST NOT instantiate `new AbortController()` to read instance members — the `in` operator against the prototype answers the question without depending on the constructors the probe is itself checking.

On an `abortsignal-shape` failure the `loom/load/host-incompatible` payload's `details.observed` / `details.required` depend on the failing member's `kind`: for a `constructor`, `static-method`, or `prototype-method` member (the `typeof`-checked members), `details.observed` is the `typeof <path>` string (e.g. `"undefined"`) and `details.required` is the literal `"function"`, mirroring `typebox-shape` in step (e); for a `prototype-property` member (`aborted`, `reason`, checked by `"<name>" in AbortSignal.prototype`), `details.observed` is the literal `"absent"` and `details.required` is the literal `"present"`, naming the absent-property condition rather than the `in`-operator boolean (a bare `false` is not a self-describing payload value). The [`loom/load/host-incompatible` per-`kind` enumeration](./diagnostics.md#host-incompatible-observed-required) restates these as the diagnostics-side test contract.

**(c) Factory-probable SDK capabilities.** Check the ten named function members listed below by `typeof <path> === "function"`, **in the listed order — including the within-bullet order of the one bullet that names two members (`pi.setActiveTools` then `pi.getActiveTools`) — stopping at the first member whose check returns false** (the same first-failure short-circuit discipline the other probe steps follow). This fixed iteration order is normative: it makes the failing member deterministic, so a conformance test that removes exactly one of the ten members can predict which member the runtime names in the emitted payload. These are the runtime-detectable members of the **factory-probable subset** of the seven SDK capabilities owned by [SDK capability inventory](#sdk-capability-inventory): items 1, 2, 3, 4, and 6 (five capabilities, ten function members — capability 1 contributes one, capabilities 2, 3, and 6 each contribute two, and capability 4 contributes three). Item 5 (cancellation propagation) is covered jointly by step (b) above (the WHATWG `AbortSignal` / `AbortController` shape probe) and step (c) below (the `AgentSession.prototype.abort` member listed alongside `createAgentSession`); see [SDK capability inventory](#sdk-capability-inventory) item 5 for the inventory-side framing. Item 7 (binder LLM model) is **not** factory-probable because `ctx.modelRegistry` does not exist at extension-factory entry; it is detected at per-loom load time and surfaces as `loom/load/binder-model-unresolved` per [Slash-Command Argument Binding — Strict-capability requirement](./binder.md#strict-capability-requirement), with no `details.kind` discriminator on this diagnostic. The two diagnostic surfaces (`loom/load/host-incompatible` and `loom/load/binder-model-unresolved`) MUST stay disjoint.

  - `pi.registerCommand` (capability 1)
  - `pi.sendUserMessage` (capability 2)
  - `ExtensionCommandContext.waitForIdle` (capability 2; checked at slash-handler invocation, not at factory time — the probe verifies only the static export shape on the `ExtensionAPI`-imported namespace)
  - `createAgentSession` (capability 3)
  - `AgentSession.prototype.abort` (capability 3 / capability 5; the cancellation primitive the runtime invokes from the one-shot `loomAbort.signal` listener registered at spawn time — see **Subagent session lifecycle** and **Cancellation source** below. Probed at factory time as `typeof AgentSession.prototype.abort === "function"` against the imported `AgentSession` class on the `@earendil-works/pi-coding-agent` namespace; the import path is load-bearing — `AgentSession` is re-exported by `dist/core/index.d.ts` of `@earendil-works/pi-coding-agent` (at the [loom 1.0 Pi-SDK pin](#pi-sdk-pin)) from `./agent-session.js`, and the loom runtime depends on the re-export specifically, not on direct consumption from `@earendil-works/pi-agent-core` (where the underlying class lives), so a Pi minor that drops the re-export surfaces at this probe as `loom/load/host-incompatible` rather than as a silent fallback to a different import path. A missing or renamed `abort` member surfaces through the same diagnostic rather than as a runtime-time `TypeError` at the spawn site)
  - `pi.registerTool` (capability 4)
  - `pi.setActiveTools` and `pi.getActiveTools` (capability 4)
  - `pi.registerMessageRenderer` (capability 6)
  - `pi.sendMessage` (capability 6)

On an `sdk-capability-missing` failure the `loom/load/host-incompatible` payload carries `details.observed = <typeof <path>>` (e.g. the literal string `"undefined"`) and `details.required = "function"` (mirroring `typebox-shape` in step (e)), plus the sibling field `details.member = "<path>"` naming the failing member — the first member in the normative listed order above whose `typeof <path> === "function"` check returned false (e.g. `"createAgentSession"`, `"AgentSession.prototype.abort"`, `"pi.setActiveTools"`). `details.member` is a sibling field that refines the existing `"sdk-capability-missing"` kind, mirroring the `details.package` precedent the peer-dep kinds establish in step (d) below; the `kind` discriminator enumeration in **On failure: refusal and diagnostic** below does not grow. The [`loom/load/host-incompatible` per-`kind` enumeration](./diagnostics.md#host-incompatible-observed-required) restates the `details.observed` / `details.required` substrings as the diagnostics-side test contract.

**(d) Peer-dep version (lock-step, four packages).** This check is folded into step (c)'s same source-of-truth pinned-constants block but runs after the factory-probable capability checks complete (i.e. it is the last of the four pinned-constants checks). The probe iterates over the fixed array of four lock-step `@earendil-works/*` peer-dep packages in this normative order (the same source-of-truth list order shared with the build-time per-package coverage assertion):

  1. `@earendil-works/pi-coding-agent`
  2. `@earendil-works/pi-agent-core`
  3. `@earendil-works/pi-ai`
  4. `@earendil-works/pi-tui`

  For each package in turn, read the installed version from its `package.json` by an `exports`-independent mechanic: resolve the package's main entry via `createRequire(import.meta.url).resolve("<pkg>")` (resolution context is the loom factory's module, since the extension may be installed globally), then walk parent directories from the resolved entry path up to the first `package.json` whose `name` field equals the iteration's `<pkg>` and read its `version` field. Resolving the package's main entry rather than a `./package.json` subpath avoids `ERR_PACKAGE_PATH_NOT_EXPORTED`, which Node's ESM resolver throws when an `exports` map does not enumerate the requested subpath. Compare against the [loom 1.0 Pi-SDK pin range](#pi-sdk-pin) under tilde-range SemVer membership — the conventional npm tilde semantic, which pins the minor uniformly across all major versions (so `~X.Y.Z` admits `X.Y.Z` through `<X.(Y+1).0`, applied to the pinned range sourced from [`#pi-sdk-pin`](#pi-sdk-pin)). The check terminates on the first out-of-range or malformed package in this fixed iteration order — the four-package iteration shares step (c)'s short-circuit slot and does not aggregate failures across packages. A `version` field that is not a syntactically valid SemVer string, a missing `version` field, a `MODULE_NOT_FOUND` on the main-entry resolution call, a parent-directory walk that reaches the filesystem root without finding a `package.json` whose `name` field equals the iteration's `<pkg>`, or any other foreseeable shape failure of the read routes to `kind: "peer-dep-malformed-version"` with `details.observed = <raw-string-or-"<unresolvable>">`, `details.required = <loom 1.0 Pi-SDK pin range>` (sourced from [`#pi-sdk-pin`](#pi-sdk-pin)), and `details.package = "<scoped-name>"` naming the offending package. An installed `version` that parses but falls outside the pinned range routes to `kind: "peer-dep-out-of-range"` with the same `details.package` field set. The `kind` discriminator enumeration in **On failure: refusal and diagnostic** below does not grow — `details.package` is a sibling field that refines the existing two `kind`s. Foreseeable shape failures are *not* `kind: "probe-failed"`; only unforeseen throws inside step (d) (permission errors, hostile `Proxy` on the resolved object, `JSON.parse` against a binary file) escalate to `kind: "probe-failed"` (see *Self-failure* below; `details.package` carries the offending package name on that route too).

  The fifth Pi-bundled package `typebox` is **not** included in this iteration — it is pinned to the literal `"*"` per the bundled-package convention (see **Host prerequisites — Pi SDK pin**, the `typebox` sub-paragraph) and therefore has no lock-step minor obligation. Its single load-bearing host-shape check (the presence of `Type.Unsafe` as a callable function) is owned by **Step 0 (e)** below, not by this iteration; the lock-step iteration MUST NOT be extended to cover `typebox`.

<a id="step-0-d-recommended-recipe"></a>
*Recommended recipe (non-normative).* `semver.satisfies(installedVersion, <pinned-range>)` and `semver.valid(installedVersion)` from the [`semver`](https://www.npmjs.com/package/semver) npm package satisfy this contract for each iteration step, where `<pinned-range>` is the literal sourced from the pinned-constants block (in turn sourced from the [loom 1.0 Pi-SDK pin](#pi-sdk-pin)). A future swap to a different SemVer implementation is permitted as long as the tilde-range semantic above and the syntactic-validity discriminator that routes failures to `"peer-dep-malformed-version"` are preserved end-to-end.

**(e) `typebox` host-shape.** Check `typeof Type.Unsafe === "function"` against the `Type` namespace imported from the `typebox` peer dependency declared in `package.json`. Position in the short-circuit order: after `(d)`, since `(e)` depends on the `typebox` peer-dep import resolving and is therefore meaningful only once the lock-step `@earendil-works/*` peer-dep iteration in `(d)` has succeeded. Failure routes to `kind: "typebox-shape"` with `details.observed = <typeof Type.Unsafe>` (e.g. the literal string `"undefined"` when the namespace lacks the member) and `details.required = "function"`. The probe MUST NOT itself construct a TypeBox schema (no `Type.Unsafe<unknown>({})` call); the `typeof` check alone is sufficient and preserves the probe-wide invariant that the probe never exercises the member it is checking. `details.observed` carries the `typeof` string rather than the namespace contents to keep the diagnostic payload small. The asymmetry with `AgentSession.prototype.abort` in `(c)` is removed by adding this check: both single-symbol Pi-bundled imports now surface absence as `loom/load/host-incompatible` rather than as a runtime-time `TypeError` at the first tool-registration call.

For brevity the probe is described above as five sub-steps `(a)`–`(e)`; `(d)` is part of step `(c)`'s pinned-constants execution group and shares its short-circuit slot, and `(e)` is the trailing `typebox` host-shape check. The fixed normative order for short-circuit is: `(a)` Node floor, then `(b)` `AbortSignal` shape, then `(c)+(d)` capability list and peer-dep version, then `(e)` `typebox` host-shape. A simultaneous-failure host (e.g. Node 18 *and* a polyfilled `AbortSignal` missing `AbortSignal.any`) emits the `(a)` failure; the implementation MUST NOT race or aggregate.

**Probe-wide invariants.**

- The probe MUST NOT use any member it is itself checking. The kind table above is constructed so this rule holds without instance construction.
- The probe is `typeof`- and `in`-only — no arity sniffing, no return-shape sniffing, no construction.
- Probes MUST NOT be added beyond the five enumerated checks.
- The factory MUST NOT throw. Each check is wrapped in a try/catch (see *Self-failure* below).

**On failure: refusal and diagnostic.**

- (i) The factory skips **every** subsequent factory-time host-binding call — the four `pi.register*` calls **and** every `pi.on` call (and every `pi.subscribe` call, if the SDK exposes one). Steps 1–5 below MUST NOT execute. The refusal is enforced once at the `PiExtensionAPI` adapter layer, not by per-call defensive checks.
- (ii) The factory emits exactly one `loom/load/host-incompatible` diagnostic (per [Diagnostics — `loom/load/*`](./diagnostics.md)) with `details: { kind, observed, required, ...optional }` where `kind ∈ { "node-floor", "abortsignal-shape", "sdk-capability-missing", "peer-dep-out-of-range", "peer-dep-malformed-version", "typebox-shape", "probe-failed" }`. Routed through the **System notes** fallback chain below (`sendSystemNote` → `ctx.ui.notify` → `console.error`), since the renderer itself may be the missing capability.
- (iii) The factory returns normally.

**Self-failure.** If any check throws (including `process.versions` evaluation, `typeof` evaluation against a hostile getter or `Proxy`, `"in"`-operator evaluation against a `null` prototype, `package.json` resolution / read / parse outside the foreseeable shape failures step (d) routes to `"peer-dep-malformed-version"`, or a hostile getter / `Proxy` on the imported `typebox` namespace in step (e)), the probe traps the throw, terminates immediately, and emits `loom/load/host-incompatible` with `details.kind = "probe-failed"`, `details.step ∈ { "node-floor", "abortsignal-shape", "sdk-capability-missing", "peer-dep-out-of-range", "typebox-shape" }` naming which check threw, and `details.cause = <error.message>` carrying the underlying error text. When `details.step = "peer-dep-out-of-range"`, `details.package = "<scoped-name>"` additionally names which of the four lock-step packages was being checked at the moment of the throw; the deterministic iteration order pinned in (d) above guarantees this assignment is unambiguous. `details.cause` is the JS `Error.message` string, not the `Error` object — diagnostics are serialisable per the existing diagnostics contract. A `"probe-failed"` event supersedes any in-order `kind` for that check; the `(a)→(b)→(c)+(d)→(e)` short-circuit ordering applies only to comparison verdicts.

**Idempotency.** A `/reload` re-runs the probe with no carried state. Subagent mode is unaffected because it runs only after a session has been created, by which point step 0 has already gated the factory.

<a id="post-probe-sdk-shape-drift"></a>
**Post-probe SDK-shape drift.** The capability probe above runs **exactly once** per factory invocation (a `/reload` is a fresh factory invocation per *Idempotency* above) and is **not** re-run on subsequent SDK calls. Any post-probe interaction with a previously-probed Pi member — including the snapshot-side `pi.setActiveTools` of the swap, the per-invocation `pi.sendUserMessage` call, the per-call `ctx.modelRegistry.getAvailable()` re-resolution of the binder model handle (which [Slash-Command Argument Binding](./binder.md) constructs afresh on every binder call), `createAgentSession` and `AgentSession`-handle members past creation, `pi.sendMessage` for system notes, and any `pi.register*` or `pi.on` member touched after factory entry — that **throws synchronously, returns a Promise that rejects, or returns a value of the wrong shape** routes to `loom/runtime/internal-error` per the catch-all row in [Diagnostics](./diagnostics.md), *except* where one of the four dedicated codes already applies: `loom/runtime/active-set-restore-failed` (the **restore-side** `pi.setActiveTools` of the swap, after a successful snapshot-side call; the snapshot-side throw remains on the `internal-error` route and aborts the swap before the wrapped `fn` runs), `loom/runtime/system-note-delivery-failed` (synchronous throw from `pi.sendMessage` for a `loom-system-note`, after the `ctx.ui.notify` fallback has been attempted), `loom/runtime/subagent-dispose-failure` (`AgentSession.dispose()` throw inside the subagent-mode teardown `finally`), and `loom/runtime/registry-swap-failed` (the watcher's mid-rebuild throw on a changed `.loom`/`.warp` file). `pi.sendUserMessage` returns `void` per the `ExtensionAPI` surface (the `Promise<void>` shape is exclusive to `AgentSession.sendUserMessage` and `ReplacedSessionContext.sendUserMessage`); the runtime MUST NOT `await` it, so its observable post-probe failure mode is the synchronous-throw arm above. **Silent shape drift** — a previously-probed member that no longer matches its probed shape but does not throw, reject, or return a wrong-shape sentinel the catch-all wrap can observe (e.g. `pi.setActiveTools` becoming a `Promise<void>`-returning function whose rejection the runtime never sees because it does not `await`) — is **undefined behaviour**: the runtime is not required to detect it, and no diagnostic is owed for it. Operator triage of `loom/runtime/internal-error` therefore cannot, in loom 1.0, distinguish a host-drift failure from a loom-runtime defect on the `error.message` / `error.stack` payload alone; both surface through the same `"loom /<name> aborted with internal error: <message>"` system-note template (and the same `Err(InvokeInfraError { kind: "invoke_failure", cause: "internal_error", ... })` envelope on the `invoke` parent surface). A `details.kind` discriminator on `loom/runtime/internal-error` distinguishing host-drift from loom-defect is an additive registry-minor change deferred past loom 1.0 per [Diagnostics](./diagnostics.md)'s registry-change rules; nothing in the loom 1.0 routing contract precludes adding it later without breaking emitted shapes.

If step 0 succeeds, the factory then:

1. Registers the `--loom` CLI flag via `pi.registerFlag('loom', { type: 'string', description: 'Loom file or directory paths, joined with the OS path-list separator' })` **before** subscribing to `resources_discover`, so the value is readable from inside the discovery handler via `pi.getFlag('loom')`. Walks the five discovery sources defined in [Directory Convention](./discovery.md) directly — the global directory `~/.pi/agent/looms/`, the project directory `.pi/looms/`, every installed package's `pi.looms` entry or conventional `looms/` directory (per [Package discovery](./discovery.md#package-discovery)), the `looms` settings array (per [Settings file reads](./discovery.md#settings-file-reads)), and the `--loom` CLI flag (whose `pi.getFlag('loom')` value is split on `path.delimiter` per [Directory Convention](./discovery.md)) — at factory time and again on every `resources_discover` event. The event payload (`{ cwd, reason }`) supplies the project root used for the project-local source (`event.cwd` is preferred over any factory-captured `cwd`, so a future per-session cwd change is honoured on reload) and distinguishes initial scan (`reason: "startup"`) from reload (`reason: "reload"`); Pi delivers no paths to the handler — `ResourcesDiscoverResult` has no `loomPaths` slot — and the `pi` manifest namespace does not enumerate `pi.looms`. The loom extension owns the walk for all five sources; the event is purely a re-trigger, and the handler returns the empty result `{}` to satisfy the typed return.
2. Parses each discovered `.loom` file and builds a *pending registration list* keyed by slash name. The factory does **not** call `pi.registerCommand` synchronously — Pi's prompt templates and other extensions' commands are not yet enumerable at factory time, so cross-format collision detection cannot run here. Concretely, on the pre-bind runtime returned to the extension factory by `createExtensionRuntime()`, every action method that reads or mutates session-bound state — including `getCommands`, `getActiveTools`, `getAllTools`, `setActiveTools`, `sendMessage`, `sendUserMessage`, `setModel`, `getThinkingLevel`, `setThinkingLevel`, and the rest of the `notInitialized`-tagged slots in `@earendil-works/pi-coding-agent`'s `dist/core/extensions/loader.js` — is bound to a throwing closure (`Error("Extension runtime not initialized. Action methods cannot be called during extension loading.")`) that `Runner.bindCore()` later overwrites with the real implementation alongside `session_start`. The token `notInitialized` is the internal variable name of that throwing closure inside Pi's loader source; it is **not** an observable sentinel value an extension can compare against or switch on. Calling any of these methods from inside the factory raises an unhandled exception that aborts factory load. The methods Pi documents as safe before bind are `pi.registerCommand` / `pi.registerTool` / `pi.registerFlag` / `pi.registerMessageRenderer` (registration sinks) and `refreshTools` (a no-op on the pre-bind runtime). Every other reach for session state is deferred to a `session_start` (or later) handler. The signature pinned by loom 1.0 is `pi.getCommands(): SlashCommandInfo[]` (synchronous, returns the current registered-commands snapshot, where `SlashCommandInfo` is the interface exported from `@earendil-works/pi-coding-agent`'s `core/slash-commands.d.ts` with fields `{ name, description?, source: SlashCommandSource, sourceInfo }`); the returned array is mutable in the type system but MUST be treated as read-only by convention (the loom 1.0 collision check is a single forward pass and never mutates it); the snapshot is only meaningful on or after `session_start`. The build-time SDK surface inventory (per *Host prerequisites*) MUST list `SlashCommandInfo` and the three-arm `SlashCommandSource = "extension" | "prompt" | "skill"` explicitly so a Pi minor that renames either fails the build.
3. Subscribes a `session_start` handler that consults `pi.getCommands()`, drops any pending loom whose slash name collides with an existing entry whose `source` is in the [loom 1.0 cross-format collision source set](#v1-seam-pi-owned-subagents-collision-source-set) defined below — the three arms of Pi's `SlashCommandSource` union (`"prompt"`, `"extension"`, `"skill"`), per `@earendil-works/pi-coding-agent`'s `core/slash-commands.d.ts` and per [Discovery — Slash-name collisions across formats](./discovery.md) — <a id="slash-handler-registration"></a>registers each survivor via `pi.registerCommand(name, { description, handler })` — one slash command per loom — and emits a `loom/load/cross-format-collision` diagnostic for each drop through the channel defined in [Diagnostics](./diagnostics.md). The `description` field passed to `pi.registerCommand` carries `frontmatter.description` verbatim and only that — `argument-hint` is **not** concatenated, since Pi's extension-command autocomplete UI has no `argumentHint` slot and the binder is the only loom 1.0 consumer of `argument-hint` (see [Slash-Command Argument Binding](./binder.md)). loom 1.0 passes only the two keys `description` and `handler`; the optional `getArgumentCompletions` key is omitted, since Pi's `RegisteredCommand` interface types it as optional and loom 1.0 exposes no autocomplete-completion surface (a deferred `argumentHint`-style upstream is tracked in [Future Considerations](./future-considerations.md#surface-extensions-without-a-dedicated-topic-page-seam)). The same handler also de-registers any previously-registered loom whose name now collides with a newly-appeared `.md` template or extension command (e.g. after a settings reload or another extension's activation), emitting the same diagnostic. *Drain-state-gated dispatch.* The `handler` value passed as the `handler` field of every `pi.registerCommand(name, { description, handler })` call above MUST, on every slash dispatch, invoke `LoomRegistry.readDrainState()` as its first action and route through the closed three-arm enumeration (a)/(b)/(c) pinned by the **`LoomRegistry` drain-state contract**'s *Methods* paragraph below — including that paragraph's *Read-failure fallback* clause, which pins arm (c) (the `"loom /<name>: extension degraded; /reload to recover"` system note) as the conservative fail-safe when the `readDrainState` call itself throws. This obligation is normative at this registration site; the arm enumeration and the read-failure routing are owned by the *Methods* paragraph below and are not restated here.
4. Subscribes a `session_shutdown` handler (`pi.on("session_shutdown", handler)`) that owns disposing every resource the extension instance holds. The Pi SDK documents `session_shutdown` as fired before an extension runtime is torn down due to quit, reload, or session replacement, with `event.reason: "quit" | "reload" | "new" | "resume" | "fork"`; loom uses it as the single teardown contract for the outgoing extension instance so that Pi's subsequent `ExtensionRuntime.invalidate(...)` call does not strand subagent provider connections, chokidar file handles, debounce timer handles, or `AbortController` listeners across `/reload`, `/new`, fork, or quit.

   <a id="unknown-reason-rule"></a>
   **Unknown-reason rule.** Before sub-step 1 runs, the handler validates `event.reason` against the closed set `{"quit", "reload", "new", "resume", "fork"}`. The validation read of `event.reason` MUST be wrapped in a `try`/`catch` so a property-access throw (e.g., a getter that throws) is treated as an unknown reason rather than escaping the handler. The three pre-sequence operations the handler performs are exactly (1) the snapshot lookup-and-`literals` read described later in this paragraph (a throw-prone read whose failure modes route to `loom/host/session-shutdown-pinned-constant-unreadable` per the catch-arm discriminator below), (2) the `event.reason` read (a throw-prone read whose failure mode routes to `loom/host/session-shutdown-reason-unknown` per the catch-arm discriminator below), and (3) the set-membership comparison of `event.reason` against the snapshot's `literals` field (the only branch the handler MAY take, whose non-member result also routes to `loom/host/session-shutdown-reason-unknown` per this rule's unknown-reason fallback above); operations (1) and (2) are the throw-prone reads covered by the widened `try`/`catch` with catch-arm discrimination later in this paragraph; the only pre-sequence work permitted in addition to operations (1)–(3) is the closed two-item carve-out (a) the `LoomRegistry.readDrainState()` call and short-circuit predicate evaluation that constitute step (I) of the *Handler control-flow ordering* clause in the [**idempotent**](#idempotent-handler-clause) clause below (which precedes operations (1)–(3) on every invocation per that clause's fixed (I)→(VI) ordering, and short-circuits the entire handler before operations (1)–(3) run when the predicate fires per step (II) of that ordering), and (b) the handler-entry pre-initialisations of the two handler-scoped variables — `capturedEventReason` to the literal string `"<unreadable>"` and `pinnedConstantReadOk` to `false` — pinned later in this paragraph as the pre-init sites that operations (1) and (2) may subsequently overwrite on their success arms; no other pre-sequence operation is permitted beyond operations (1)–(3) and carve-outs (a) and (b), and all three of operations (1)–(3) feed the same downstream behaviour of running the full five-sub-step teardown sequence as if the reason were `"quit"` or `"reload"`. On an unknown reason — or on a throwing access — the handler emits exactly one `loom/host/session-shutdown-reason-unknown` (W, runtime) diagnostic via `console.error` with `details: { observed: <String(event.reason)> }` *before* sub-step 1 runs (so the diagnostic survives even if the handler later throws), then runs the full five-sub-step sequence as if the reason were `"quit"` or `"reload"`. The no-active-invocations fast-path described in the *Edge cases* paragraph below MUST NOT be taken on the unknown-reason path: the registry drain, the bounded `Promise.allSettled` await, the watcher closure, and the listener detachment all run unconditionally. The `String(event.reason)` coercion in the `details.observed` payload tolerates symbols, `undefined`, numbers, booleans, and objects without itself throwing; on a throwing property access (where the value never materialised) `details.observed` is the literal string `"<unreadable>"`. The handler captures this single coerced string into a handler-scoped variable at handler entry — the same site this rule's `try`/`catch` runs, before sub-step 1 — and the same string is reused as `details.event.reason` by every `loom/runtime/cancelled-by-session-shutdown` note emitted under the **Per-invocation operator visibility (clean-cancel path)** rule below; the per-invocation `finally` does not re-read `event.reason`. The captured value is a closed-set member when Pi delivered one of the five literals (`"quit" | "reload" | "new" | "resume" | "fork"`), `String(event.reason)` on the unknown-reason path, `"<unreadable>"` on the throwing-access path, or `"<unreadable>"` on the snapshot-failure path (where the fixed read order above means sub-step 1's `event.reason` read was never reached because the snapshot read failed first; to make this case well-defined, the handler-scoped variable is pre-initialised to `"<unreadable>"` at handler entry before either of the two reads runs, and the snapshot-failure path simply leaves that pre-initialisation unchanged). A second handler-scoped variable, the boolean `pinnedConstantReadOk`, is pre-initialised to `false` at the same handler-entry site before either of the two reads runs, and is set to `true` on the success arm of the snapshot lookup-and-`literals` read — i.e., when the catch arm that emits `loom/host/session-shutdown-pinned-constant-unreadable` (pinned later in this paragraph) does not fire on this shutdown; on the snapshot-failure path the pre-initialised `false` is left unchanged. This parallels the captured-string pre-init above and is the same `pinnedConstantReadOk` seam the *Predicate split* clause of the [*Edge cases* `reason: "new" | "resume" | "fork"` bullet](#session-only-reason-degraded-state) below consumes as the narrower diagnostic-emission predicate's first conjunct. The captured value reaches the per-invocation `finally` of the **Per-invocation operator visibility (clean-cancel path)** rule below via sub-step 2's stamp onto each `ActiveInvocationRegistry` entry's `shutdownReason` field — that field is the spec-pinned channel for all four captured-value cases, including the snapshot-failure `"<unreadable>"`; the `finally` MUST NOT use a runtime singleton (forbidden by the no-globals rule) or the `AbortSignal.reason` payload (Pi-side shape not pinned). The snapshot-failure path deliberately overloads the `"<unreadable>"` sentinel with a fourth meaning beyond the throwing-property-access case it already covers; operators distinguish the two by the co-emitted teardown-handler diagnostic (`loom/host/session-shutdown-pinned-constant-unreadable` for the snapshot-failure path versus `loom/host/session-shutdown-reason-unknown` with `details.observed = "<unreadable>"` for the throwing-access path), not by the per-invocation `details.event.reason` value alone. The same-string reuse between the handler-scoped capture and `details.observed` of `loom/host/session-shutdown-reason-unknown` is therefore preserved on the closed-set and unknown-reason paths only — on the snapshot-failure path no `details.observed` is emitted at all (the `loom/host/session-shutdown-pinned-constant-unreadable` diagnostic carries `details.failure` instead per the catch-arm discriminator above), and the per-invocation `details.event.reason` defaults to the sentinel with no `details.observed` counterpart to compare it against. Pin the coercion to `String(event.reason)` explicitly — a template-literal coercion (`` `${event.reason}` ``) re-introduces the symbol-throw bug `String()` is chosen to avoid. The closed set `{"quit", "reload", "new", "resume", "fork"}` literal in this paragraph is sourced from the `SessionShutdownEvent['reason']` closed-set snapshot entry inside the extension module's source-of-truth pinned-constants block — the static `SDK_SURFACE_INVENTORY` constant under `src/extension/` that the SDK surface-inventory test also consumes, and the same block that already holds the [Step 0 (Capability probe)](#entry-capability-probe) constants. The `session_shutdown` handler MUST import `SDK_SURFACE_INVENTORY` directly from that module rather than re-declare a runtime-only copy of the snapshot entry — single source of truth across build-time test and runtime handler is the load-bearing invariant; the runtime's set-membership check above consumes that snapshot entry's `literals` field directly (single-site edit, no separate copy in the handler). The runtime locates that snapshot entry by looking it up in the same block and reading its `literals` field; the lookup MUST be keyed on the composite predicate `(entry.kind === "type-union-snapshot") && (entry.path === "SessionShutdownEvent.reason")` against the entry shape `{ kind: "type-union-snapshot", path: "SessionShutdownEvent.reason", literals: [...] as const }` (there is no separate stable identifier field on the entry, and one MUST NOT be invented for this lookup) rather than on the entry's position in the block (which the implementation owns and may reorder without semantic breakage). Both clauses of the composite are required: matching on `kind` alone would silently shadow on a future second `type-union-snapshot` entry covering a different SDK union, and matching on `path` alone — acceptable today, since `path` is unique across the current pinned-constants block — is a fragile invariant once additional non-snapshot entry kinds may carry a `path` field of their own (e.g. an `abortsignal-member` entry whose `path` happens to collide), so the `kind` clause is retained as a cheap structural defence whose cost is one additional `===` per handler entry. The composite predicate above is the same predicate `diagnostics.md`'s `loom/host/session-shutdown-pinned-constant-unreadable` row pins as the lookup site whose failure modes that diagnostic surfaces; the two pages MUST stay aligned on the predicate text in any future edit. *Lookup-failure-to-discriminator routing.* The iteration primitive used to scan `SDK_SURFACE_INVENTORY` for the matching snapshot entry — `Array.prototype.find`, a `Map.get` against a derived index, an explicit `for`/`switch`, or any equivalent — is **leaf-owned** and not pinned here; the routing of the failure modes that primitive can produce to the closed `details.failure` discriminator set is **spec-owned**, and is pinned as four arms that together exhaust the snapshot-side failure space the catch-arm discriminator below disambiguates: (1) **`SDK_SURFACE_INVENTORY` itself resolves to `undefined`** (a circular-init or live-binding gap in which the source-of-truth pinned-constants block has not finished initialising by handler-entry time — the dominant loom 1.0 failure mode for the snapshot read) — discriminator MUST be `"missing-entry"`, **not** any `"throw:TypeError: …"` value, and to satisfy this routing the handler MUST guard the lookup with an explicit `SDK_SURFACE_INVENTORY === undefined` check **before** invoking the iteration primitive (a naive `SDK_SURFACE_INVENTORY.find(…)?.literals` pattern routes this case to the throw arm instead and would split operator deduplication buckets across implementations whose iteration-primitive choice is otherwise immaterial); (2) **the iteration primitive returns no matching entry** (the composite predicate above matches nothing) — discriminator is `"missing-entry"`; (3) **the iteration primitive returns a matching entry but the subsequent `.literals` access throws**, or **a per-entry `.kind` or `.path` read itself throws during iteration** (a getter-style trap on a non-matching entry, or a frozen-but-mutated import whose property reads now throw) — discriminator is `"throw:<String(error)>"` per the discriminator-grammar rule below; (4) **the matching entry's `.literals` field is structurally invalid** per the four sub-cases of the catch-arm-discriminator paragraph below — discriminator is `"literals-shape-invalid"`. An implementation that routes any of (1)–(4) to a different discriminator is non-conformant regardless of which iteration primitive it chose. The two reads MUST run in the fixed order **(1) snapshot lookup-and-`literals` read, then (2) `event.reason` read**, and both MUST be inside the same handler-entry `try`/`catch` discipline as the `event.reason` read above. The implementation choice between (a) widening the existing `try`/`catch` to cover both reads with a state variable tracking which read was in progress, and (b) using two adjacent `try`/`catch` blocks (snapshot first, then `event.reason`), is left to the implementation — the load-bearing pin is behavioural: no throw escapes the handler, and the catch arm selects the diagnostic that corresponds to the read that actually threw. The catch-arm discriminator is fully determined by the fixed read order: if the **snapshot read** (lookup or literal-array read) threw, was missing, or returned an entry whose `literals` field has a structurally invalid shape (circular module init, a frozen-but-mutated import, an import resolved to the wrong shape after a buggy patch), the handler emits exactly one `loom/host/session-shutdown-pinned-constant-unreadable` (W, runtime) diagnostic via `console.error` with `details: { failure: <discriminator string describing the failure mode — one of the literals `"missing-entry"`, `"literals-shape-invalid"`, or `"throw:<String(error)>"`> }`. The TypeScript type of the `details.failure` field is the closed template-literal union ``"missing-entry" | "literals-shape-invalid" | `throw:${string}` `` — operator-tooling consumers MAY type-narrow on this union (e.g. against the literal arm `"missing-entry"`, the literal arm `"literals-shape-invalid"`, or the template-literal arm via `startsWith("throw:")` per the operator-key rule pinned later in this paragraph) and the runtime MUST emit only values that inhabit it. The `"literals-shape-invalid"` discriminator covers four structurally-distinct sub-cases that all leave the runtime with no usable closed set and warrant the same operator response (the snapshot itself is broken; resolve under [Pi version bump procedure](#pi-version-bump-procedure) step 5 below): (1) the `literals` field is not an array at all; (2) the `literals` field is an array but at least one element is not a string; (3) the `literals` field is the empty array; (4) the `literals` field is an array of strings but at least one element is the empty string `""`. The `"missing-entry"` discriminator covers both the literal lookup-returned-nothing case and the defensive kind-mismatch case (an entry exists at the matching `path` but its `kind` is somehow not `"type-union-snapshot"`, e.g. after future entry-shape drift); both reach the catch arm via the same `(entry.kind === "type-union-snapshot") && (entry.path === "SessionShutdownEvent.reason")` composite predicate above failing to match, so the handler cannot — and need not — distinguish them, regardless of whether `event.reason` would itself be readable (the snapshot-side failure is dominant precisely because the snapshot read ran first and the `event.reason` read was never reached); if the snapshot read **succeeded** and the subsequent `event.reason` read threw, the handler emits the `loom/host/session-shutdown-reason-unknown` diagnostic per the **Unknown-reason rule** above, with `details.observed = "<unreadable>"` per that rule's throwing-property-access clause. The pinned-constant-unreadable diagnostic, when emitted, fires *before* sub-step 1 runs (so the diagnostic survives a later handler throw, symmetric with the **Unknown-reason** emission), then proceeds as if `event.reason` were unknown — routing through the unknown-reason path above for the **teardown sequence only** (the set-membership check is skipped for this shutdown, the full five-sub-step sequence runs, and a faulty constant import never escapes the handler). The fixed snapshot-first ordering is load-bearing: it makes the disambiguation deterministic across implementations (the fixture for a throwing-getter `event.reason` paired with a successful snapshot read always observes `loom/host/session-shutdown-reason-unknown`; the fixture for a throwing snapshot lookup always observes `loom/host/session-shutdown-pinned-constant-unreadable` regardless of whether `event.reason` is itself readable), and it routes the dominant failure mode (a throwing `event.reason` getter on an otherwise-healthy snapshot) to the diagnostic whose message most directly identifies the cause. The unknown-reason path's own diagnostic emission is **not** also performed on this path: `loom/host/session-shutdown-pinned-constant-unreadable` and `loom/host/session-shutdown-reason-unknown` are mutually exclusive — at most one of the two fires per `session_shutdown` event, with the snapshot-lookup-failure path firing `pinned-constant-unreadable` instead of `reason-unknown`. This avoids the misleading-message failure mode in which a corrupted snapshot lookup, paired with an `event.reason` that is in fact a closed-set member (e.g. `"quit"`), would otherwise surface a `session_shutdown event.reason outside closed set: quit` `loom/host/session-shutdown-reason-unknown` message whose claim is wrong by inspection — the snapshot was broken, not `event.reason`. Operator deduplication is well-defined under either code — `(code, details.observed)` for `session-shutdown-reason-unknown` and `(code, details.failure)` for `session-shutdown-pinned-constant-unreadable` — and a given `session_shutdown` event contributes at most one such pair across the two codes (the codes are mutually exclusive per the rule above). The `"throw:<String(error)>"` discriminator's grammar is pinned: the literal colon between the `"throw:"` prefix and the coerced payload is a fixed prefix separator and is **not** escaped; the `String(error)` payload is truncated to at most 256 UTF-16 code units (`String.prototype.length`) before concatenation with the prefix, so a thrown `Buffer`, a multi-MB stack trace, or any other `error` whose `String()` coercion expands to a large blob does not blow up the discriminator string or the teardown `console.error` write cost it carries; control characters in the truncated payload are escaped before concatenation — `\n`, `\r`, and `\t` as the two-character literal escapes `\\n`, `\\r`, `\\t`, and every other Unicode code point in U+0000–U+001F (excluding the three named above) and U+007F–U+009F as the six-character escape `\\uXXXX`; all other characters are passed through unchanged. A literal colon inside the truncated payload is not escaped (the prefix separator is positional, not delimiter-based — operators key on `startsWith("throw:")` against the discriminator, not on splitting at the first colon), and a `"throw:"` substring inside the truncated payload receives no special handling either (the same `startsWith("throw:")` predicate is the only operator-side parse the rule pins; an inner `"throw:"` substring is contract-compatible noise). The `String(error)` coercion MUST itself be wrapped in `try`/`catch`; on inner throw, the discriminator is the literal `"throw:<unreadable>"`. On a coercion failure (the `String(error)` call itself throws — e.g. an `error` whose `Symbol.toPrimitive` or `toString` throws), the discriminator falls back to the literal string `"throw:<unreadable>"` — the `"throw:"` prefix is preserved so operator deduplication on `(code, details.failure)` continues to bucket coercion-failure rows under the throw discriminator rather than collapsing them into a separate `"<unreadable>"` bucket that an operator filter on `startsWith("throw:")` would silently miss. The bare `"<unreadable>"` fallback convention is shared with the `details.observed` and `details.error` payloads pinned elsewhere in this paragraph and under **Per-step isolation** below — those payloads carry no `"throw:"` prefix to preserve and are unchanged by this rule; the `details.failure` field name itself is deliberately **not** reused from `details.observed`, since `details.failure` carries an internal failure-mode discriminator from a closed discriminator set (two literal forms — `"missing-entry"`, `"literals-shape-invalid"` — plus the `"throw:<…>"` template family whose payload is constructed at this emission site per the truncation-and-escape rule above) whereas `details.observed` carries an externally-observed SDK value, and operator triage tooling that keys on `details.observed` MUST NOT silently extend that key's semantics to the constant-unreadable code. The `loom/host/session-shutdown-pinned-constant-unreadable` emission is itself wrapped per the [**Diagnostic-emission isolation**](#diagnostic-emission-isolation) rule below; it is **not** added to the always-log set, matching the `reload-teardown-timeout`, `session-shutdown-reason-unknown`, and `session-shutdown-teardown-step-failed` exclusions. (See [Pi version bump procedure](#pi-version-bump-procedure) step 5 for the build-time gate that catches snapshot/SDK union drift.) A snapshot whose `literals` field is a structurally-valid non-empty array of non-empty strings but whose element values do not match the Pi-side `SessionShutdownEvent['reason']` union (e.g. a typo like `["quitt", "reload", "new", "resume", "fork"]` in place of the intended `"quit"`) is **not** runtime-detectable: the four `"literals-shape-invalid"` sub-cases above are the only structural failures the handler can recognise without an oracle for the SDK union, and a value-level mismatch passes all of them. Such a typo is caught exclusively by the build-time `loom/typecheck/session-shutdown-reason-snapshot` assertion owned by [Pi version bump procedure](#pi-version-bump-procedure) step 5 below, which fails `npm run typecheck` before the snapshot ever reaches a user runtime.

   *Sub-anchors and pinned substrings.* The three runtime-side obligations this rule pins are independently verifiable and each carry their own stable sub-anchor so a reviewer marking one "satisfied" cannot silently elide the other two: <a id="unknown-reason-rule-membership-check"></a>**(i) Closed-set membership check** — the runtime's set-membership branch above against the snapshot's `literals` field, including the unknown-reason fallback (`loom/host/session-shutdown-reason-unknown` plus the full five-sub-step teardown), pinned at [`#unknown-reason-rule-membership-check`](#unknown-reason-rule-membership-check); <a id="unknown-reason-rule-constant-source"></a>**(ii) Constant-source pinning (single-site edit)** — the rule that the closed set above is sourced from the `SessionShutdownEvent['reason']` snapshot entry in the extension module's source-of-truth pinned-constants block and that the runtime's set-membership check consumes that snapshot entry's `literals` field with no separate copy in the handler, pinned at [`#unknown-reason-rule-constant-source`](#unknown-reason-rule-constant-source); <a id="unknown-reason-rule-handler-trycatch"></a>**(iii) Handler-internal `try`/`catch` discipline (including the unreadable-constant diagnostic)** — the handler-entry `try`/`catch` discipline covering both the snapshot lookup-and-literal-array read and the `event.reason` read in the fixed order (snapshot first, then `event.reason`), the implementation freedom between a single widened `try`/`catch` with an in-progress state variable and two adjacent `try`/`catch` blocks, the catch-arm-per-failing-read discriminator (snapshot-side failure → `pinned-constant-unreadable`; snapshot-OK and `event.reason`-side throw → `reason-unknown` with `details.observed = "<unreadable>"`), the routing through the unknown-reason path on a throwing lookup / missing entry / non-array `literals`, and the `loom/host/session-shutdown-pinned-constant-unreadable` (W, runtime) diagnostic with its `"missing-entry"` / `"literals-shape-invalid"` / `"throw:<String(error)>"` discriminator literals, pinned at [`#unknown-reason-rule-handler-trycatch`](#unknown-reason-rule-handler-trycatch). The build-time obligations that pair with this rule (the bidirectional `SessionShutdownEvent['reason']` type-equality assertion, its `loom/typecheck/session-shutdown-reason-snapshot` brand string, and the tsconfig-include / import-specifier obligations) are owned by [Pi version bump procedure](#pi-version-bump-procedure) step 5 below — not by this rule — and are not in scope for sub-anchor (i), (ii), or (iii). The following substrings are **anchor-stable contract surface** wherever they appear as inbound references from other sections, topic files, or downstream documents that key on the literal substring: a future edit MUST NOT drift them without updating every such inbound reference in the same commit — <a id="unknown-reason-rule-substring-a"></a>(a) the diagnostic code `loom/host/session-shutdown-reason-unknown`; <a id="unknown-reason-rule-substring-b"></a>(b) the diagnostic code `loom/host/session-shutdown-pinned-constant-unreadable`; <a id="unknown-reason-rule-substring-c"></a>(c) the brace-form closed-set literal `{"quit", "reload", "new", "resume", "fork"}`; and <a id="unknown-reason-rule-substring-d"></a>(d) the three pinned-constant-unreadable discriminator literals `"missing-entry"`, `"literals-shape-invalid"`, and the `"throw:<String(error)>"` template. Editorial drift in any of (a)–(d) at an inbound-reference site is a contract change, not a wording change, and is subject to the same inbound-reference sweep as a sub-anchor rename — where an *inbound-reference sweep* means searching the spec corpus (`docs/spec.md` and `docs/spec_topics/`) for the literal substring or anchor fragment, and updating each citation in the same commit as the substring change. The in-prose occurrences of the (c) literal inside the **Unknown-reason rule** paragraph immediately above — namely the introductory listing in the `event.reason` validation sentence (`the closed set {"quit", "reload", "new", "resume", "fork"}`) and the `"quit" | "reload" | "new" | "resume" | "fork"` parenthesised re-listing later in that same paragraph — are explicitly **out of scope** for the anchor-stable contract surface above: they are illustrative restatements of the `SessionShutdownEvent['reason']` snapshot constant per [Pi version bump procedure step 1](#pi-version-bump-procedure)'s carve-out and may transiently lag the snapshot during a patch-skew window without triggering an inbound-reference sweep. The carve-out is symmetric for the (a), (b), and (d) literals when they appear inside the **Unknown-reason rule** paragraph as restatements of the diagnostic codes and discriminator literals defined there; only inbound references from outside that paragraph are anchor-stable.

   <a id="patch-skew-degradation-contract"></a>
   **Patch-skew degradation contract.** The *patch-skew window* is the interval during which a user's installed `@earendil-works/pi-coding-agent` patch is newer than the loom patch on the same machine — the [loom 1.0 Pi-SDK pin range](#pi-sdk-pin) permits patch-only Pi updates without re-running [Pi version bump procedure](#pi-version-bump-procedure) below, so the Pi-side `SessionShutdownEvent['reason']` union and the loom-side `literals` snapshot can transiently disagree. During the window, the runtime fallback above (the `loom/host/session-shutdown-reason-unknown` diagnostic and the full five-sub-step teardown for any reason not in the snapshot's `literals`) is the **sole** user-facing contract for any new reason; no other surface promises observability or graceful degradation. The skew is detected by the bidirectional type-equality assertion below firing red on the next loom typecheck cycle that imports the candidate Pi patch — loom does **not** run an automated cadence (no Renovate, no scheduled CI re-install, no nightly cron) that proactively re-imports patches in loom 1.0, so the build-time gate is best-effort: the window's duration depends on contributor cadence and is not bounded by spec, and it detects the skew only as fast as a loom contributor next runs `npm run typecheck` against the candidate patch (the window itself closes only when a release shipping the resulting snapshot edit reaches the user; an automated cadence for re-importing Pi patches is deferred to [Future Considerations — Tooling deferrals](./future-considerations.md#tooling-deferrals-no-v1-impact)). The window is silent on the user side until a non-snapshot reason actually arrives at runtime (routed through the unknown-reason path above) or the contributor's next typecheck cycle catches the drift; this is intentional loom 1.0 behaviour. The contract is asymmetric across widening and narrowing of `SessionShutdownEvent['reason']`, with the mixed widening+narrowing case handled by the **Mixed** sub-rule below. **Widening** (a Pi patch adds a new literal): every shutdown carrying the new literal routes through the unknown-reason path above, with `details.observed` carrying the `String(event.reason)` coercion of the new literal so operator triage identifies the cause without a code change; the full five-sub-step teardown still runs and the snapshot edit step 5 below prescribes is the loom-side resolution. **Narrowing** (a Pi patch removes a literal): the snapshot's `literals` array is transiently superset to the SDK union, but Pi never delivers the removed literal at runtime, so the stale snapshot entry is harmless — no runtime regression, no diagnostic, no observable behaviour change. The build-time bidirectional assertion fires red on the next typecheck (the SDK-union side becomes the strict subset and the right-to-left direction breaks); the only required follow-up is the snapshot-edit-only sweep under [Pi version bump procedure](#pi-version-bump-procedure) step 5 below (which step 1's carve-out keeps prose-update-free). **Mixed** (a Pi patch both adds and removes literals in the same release — rename, replace, or swap): the patch decomposes into its widening half (the added literal is treated per the **Widening** rule above — runtime routes the new literal through the unknown-reason path with `details.observed` carrying the coerced value) and its narrowing half (the removed literal is treated per the **Narrowing** rule above — the snapshot's `literals` array is transiently superset and the stale entry is harmless until the snapshot edit ships); both halves are observed and handled independently, and no composite handling is owed.
