Three behaviours pin this contract and MUST be covered by build-time fixtures; the (P-a)/(P-b)/(P-c) labelling here uses a `"P-"` prefix to be deliberately distinct from both the (i)/(ii)/(iii) sub-anchor labelling of the *Sub-anchors and pinned substrings* paragraph immediately above **and** the (a)–(d) anchor-stable substring labelling of that same paragraph (the substring labels are anchor-stable surface and cannot themselves be relabelled), so the three adjacent enumerations cannot collide on cross-reference: (P-a) an *unknown-reason runtime* fixture that synthesises a `session_shutdown` event whose `reason` is not a snapshot `literals` member and asserts the handler emits exactly one `loom/host/session-shutdown-reason-unknown` with `details.observed` carrying the coerced literal, then runs the full five-sub-step teardown; (P-b) a *snapshot-only widening* fixture pair that constructs a synthetic value with the same shape as the production `SDK_SURFACE_INVENTORY`'s `SessionShutdownEvent['reason']` snapshot entry — same composite-predicate keys (`kind: "type-union-snapshot"`, `path: "SessionShutdownEvent.reason"`) and same `literals: [...] as const` shape — whose `literals` array contains one extra string `"synthetic-new-reason"` not present in the production constant (no mutation of the production `SDK_SURFACE_INVENTORY` import — the `as const` declaration on the production constant remains intact and is not written through), and exercises the runtime's set-membership check against that synthetic value through a *test-only* substitution of the production `SDK_SURFACE_INVENTORY` module export — the substitution mechanic MUST preserve the handler's static import of `SDK_SURFACE_INVENTORY` from the source-of-truth module (sub-anchor (ii) of the **Unknown-reason rule** above); the choice of primitive that achieves that preservation is an implementation choice. PIC pins only the static-import-preservation behavioural property above and the behavioural assertions below; the synthetic constant's exact source is an implementation choice. The fixture pair asserts both directions: **(P-b-1, positive)** with the substitution applied so the handler's static import resolves to the synthetic constant, a `session_shutdown` event with `reason: "synthetic-new-reason"` is accepted as a closed-set member — **no** `loom/host/session-shutdown-reason-unknown` is emitted, the full five-sub-step teardown still runs, and no other failure-mode diagnostic from the **Unknown-reason rule** above fires; **(P-b-2, negative)** a parallel test in which the substitution is **not** applied (so the handler's static import resolves to the unmodified production `SDK_SURFACE_INVENTORY`, whose `literals` array does not contain `"synthetic-new-reason"`) MUST emit exactly one `loom/host/session-shutdown-reason-unknown` for the same `reason: "synthetic-new-reason"` event. The differential between (P-b-1) and (P-b-2) — same input event, opposite outcomes, with the only varying factor being whether the substitution is applied — proves the handler reads through the live module export rather than a hardcoded copy of the snapshot's `literals` field (a hardcoded copy would not swing on the substitution state and the two halves would observe the same outcome). The pair together — and only together — proves the single-source-of-truth wiring above; (P-c) a *narrowing no-regression* fixture pair that proves the asymmetric-skew property — runtime tolerance plus build-time gating — across two separate test phases that cannot share a single process invocation (the runtime-acceptance assertion requires compiled code to run, while the build-time-red assertion requires `tsc` to fail, and a `tsc` failure aborts `npm run typecheck` before any vitest harness starts; no single-process harness can assert both, so the obligation is split into two sub-fixtures with the same logical pairing pattern as (P-b-1)/(P-b-2)). **(P-c-1, runtime)** constructs a synthetic snapshot value with the same shape as the production `SDK_SURFACE_INVENTORY`'s `SessionShutdownEvent['reason']` snapshot entry whose `literals` array is a strict superset of the SDK union (e.g., the SDK has narrowed to drop `"fork"` but the synthetic snapshot still pins it alongside the rest of the narrowed union), substitutes it through the same static-import-preserving substitution mechanic (P-b) uses, dispatches a `session_shutdown` event with `reason: "fork"` (the previously-snapshotted literal that the synthetic SDK union no longer contains), and asserts the runtime accepts it as a closed-set member — **no** `loom/host/session-shutdown-reason-unknown` is emitted, the full five-sub-step teardown still runs, and no other failure-mode diagnostic from the **Unknown-reason rule** above fires. **(P-c-2, build-time)** is a separate test (one whose harness is the `tsc` invocation itself, not a vitest case) that exercises the bidirectional type-equality assertion of [Pi version bump procedure](#pi-version-bump-procedure) step 5 below against a synthetic SDK type one literal narrower than the synthetic snapshot, and asserts the assertion produces a `tsc` diagnostic carrying the literal brand string `loom/typecheck/session-shutdown-reason-snapshot` verbatim. The two sub-fixtures together — and only together — prove the asymmetric-skew property the **Narrowing** paragraph above pins. The fixtures are normative-by-reference here; the implementation owns their `<file>` placement and exact assertion shape.

   *Fixture-obligation categories.* This contract and the [Pi version bump procedure](#pi-version-bump-procedure) below together pin four distinct *categories* of fixture obligation the implementation MUST cover — the headline count "four" refers to categories, not individual fixtures, since each category may comprise multiple sub-fixtures. The categories are: the three *patch-skew* fixture-obligation categories named immediately above (the *unknown-reason runtime* category, the *snapshot-only widening* category whose (P-b-1, positive) and (P-b-2, negative) sub-fixtures together comprise it, and the *narrowing no-regression* category whose (P-c-1, runtime) and (P-c-2, build-time) sub-fixtures likewise together comprise it), and the *per-sub-trigger negative-test fixtures* category named in [Pi version bump procedure](#pi-version-bump-procedure) step 5 below (one sub-fixture per Step-0-probe-constant failing entry under [trigger (i)](#bump-step-5-trigger-i), and one sub-fixture per `SessionShutdownEvent['reason']` snapshot-entry sub-trigger under [trigger (ii)](#bump-step-5-trigger-ii)). PIC does not enumerate concrete `<file>` placements or assertion shapes; those are implementation choices.

   The handler runs in fixed order regardless of `event.reason`:

   1. **Stop accepting new work.** <a id="substep-1-drain-flag"></a>Mark the extension-scoped `LoomRegistry` as drained <a id="substep-1-init-drain-state-tag"></a>and initialise its drain-state tag to `"shutting-down"`. <a id="substep-1-act-order"></a>The two acts run in fixed normative order — `LoomRegistry.drain()` first, then `LoomRegistry.initDrainStateTag()` — so downstream sites that key on which act threw and which succeeded (the **Per-step isolation** paragraph below, which routes the two throws to distinct `(code, details.step, details.call)` dedup buckets; the [**idempotent**](#idempotent-handler-clause) clause's enumeration of the prior-state combinations a follow-up `session_shutdown` may observe; the `LoomRegistry.initDrainStateTag` method-contract clause below that pins it as called *immediately after* `LoomRegistry.drain`; and any acceptance criterion that distinguishes between the first and second sub-step-1 act) can refer to "the second sub-step-1 act" unambiguously; the per-call **Per-step isolation** rule continues to apply independently to each of the two calls regardless of the order pin. On entry into a drained registry the slash-command `handler` registered in step 3 returns a `loom-system-note` (`display: true` — the `display` setting is fixed by this umbrella opener and applies uniformly to **both** arms below, so the `"degraded; /reload to recover"` note is operator-visible on the same footing as the `"shutting down"` note; only the `content` differs across arms) — without dispatching the loom — whose `content` is selected from the closed two-arm drain-state tag set: <a id="substep-1-shutting-down-arm"></a>the `"shutting-down"` arm (the default set here, used for every shutdown whose runtime the host will tear down regardless — `"quit"`, `"reload"`, and the in-flight teardown window of any branch up to the post-sub-step-4 transition below — including the snapshot-failure path's own in-flight window before that interstitial transition runs; the *in-flight teardown window* is the interval from `session_shutdown` handler entry up to (but not including) the post-sub-step-4 `"shutting-down" → "degraded-needs-reload"` tag transition pinned in the `reason: "new" | "resume" | "fork"` edge-case bullet below, and is enumerated here only for closed-set completeness — so every transient state of the drain-state tag during the handler is accounted for by exactly one arm of this two-arm set — and (scoped to that *in-flight teardown window only*, **not** to the `"shutting-down"` arm as a whole) is in practice unreachable by a slash invocation under the loom 1.0 Pi SDK pin, because Pi's per-session slash-handler serialisation pinned under **Tool-registration lifetime and visibility** below means no slash invocation can run concurrently with the `session_shutdown` handler on the same session; the runtime MAY therefore assume the in-flight window is unreachable and need not implement additional reader-side defence beyond the reader behaviour pinned in this arm. Post-handler slash invocations on the `"shutting-down"` arm — including the seam-tag-write-throw recovery path of branch (k) under *Acceptance criteria* below, where the post-sub-step-4 `LoomRegistry.markRuntimeDegraded` write was swallowed and the registry retains its `"shutting-down"` tag value — are reachable and MUST be serviced normally per the slash-handler short-circuit rule (returning the `"loom /<name>: extension shutting down"` system note); the unreachability clause above does **not** extend to them) emits the cancelled-binder-style content `"loom /<name>: extension shutting down"` shared with binder cancellation; <a id="substep-1-unset-tag-fallback"></a>the slash-handler reader MUST also treat an *unset* drain-state tag (a runtime *state* of the field, distinct from the closed two-arm *value* set above — the value set admits only the two literals `"shutting-down"` and `"degraded-needs-reload"` in loom 1.0.0, but the runtime state of the field may additionally be unset, reachable when sub-step 1's `LoomRegistry.initDrainStateTag` per-call site threw and was caught by the **Per-step isolation** paragraph below — leaving the registry drained but tag-less) as the `"shutting-down"` arm and emit the same legacy template, so a tag-init throw degrades safely to the cancelled-binder-style content rather than producing undefined slash-handler short-circuit behaviour. <a id="substep-1-degraded-needs-reload-arm"></a>The `"degraded-needs-reload"` arm (written **only** by the post-sub-step-4 transition pinned in the `reason: "new" | "resume" | "fork"` edge-case bullet's *Predicate split* clause below, on the branches that clause's broader tag-transition predicate `capturedEventReason ∉ {"quit", "reload"}` covers — i.e. the session-only `{"new", "resume", "fork"}` triplet, **and** the snapshot-failure path, **and** the unknown-reason path with a successful snapshot read (the latter two paths absorbed by the complement check via the `"<unreadable>"` sentinel and the off-snapshot `String(event.reason)` coercion respectively, even though the `loom/host/session-shutdown-runtime-degraded` *diagnostic emission* is suppressed on both per the same clause's narrower diagnostic-emission predicate) — where the runtime remains live but permanently degraded until operator-issued `/reload`) emits the distinct content `"loom /<name>: extension degraded; /reload to recover"`. The tag *value* set is closed at these two literals in loom 1.0.0 (no third literal value beyond `"shutting-down"` and `"degraded-needs-reload"` may be written to the field without a spec edit); the unset runtime state called out above is an implementation-side artefact of the **Per-step isolation** swallow rule, not a third literal value, and the slash-handler reader's unset → `"shutting-down"` mapping above ensures the closed value set is preserved in the observable behaviour of the slash note. The two `content` templates are deliberately disjoint at the substrings `"shutting down"` and `"degraded"` so operator tooling that grepped the legacy single-template surface MUST extend its match to both substrings, and so an operator on a stdio-capturing host (where the best-effort `console.error` visibility of `loom/host/session-shutdown-runtime-degraded` may be lost) still has an in-band signal — the `"degraded; /reload to recover"` substring — telling them to issue `/reload` rather than treating repeated `"shutting down"` notes as a transient teardown.
   2. **Cancel in-flight invocations.** For every entry in the **`ActiveInvocationRegistry`** (introduced below), first stamp the handler-scoped captured `event.reason` string (per the **Unknown-reason rule** above — the closed-set member, the `String(event.reason)` unknown-reason coercion, the throwing-access `"<unreadable>"`, or the snapshot-failure `"<unreadable>"`) onto the entry's `shutdownReason` field, then call `loomAbort.abort(reason)` where `reason` is the synthesised teardown value pinned by [Cancellation — Abort-reason propagation](./cancellation.md). The stamp MUST happen before `loomAbort.abort()` on the same entry so the per-invocation `finally` (which is what reads `entry.shutdownReason` per the **Per-invocation operator visibility (clean-cancel path)** rule below) observes a populated field by the time the abort propagates and the `finally` runs; the per-entry `try`/`catch` (per the registry contract below) wraps both the stamp and the `abort()` call — on a stamp throw (frozen entry, proxied entry, write-rejecting setter, OOM during property assignment) the per-entry `catch` arm proceeds to the next entry (the `abort()` for this entry is skipped, since the stamp failed) so a per-entry write failure cannot escape sub-step 2's loop and defeat the no-throw-escapes-the-handler invariant; on an `abort()` throw, behaviour is unchanged from the registry-contract rule below. No diagnostic is emitted on a stamp-throw catch, symmetric to the existing `abort()`-throw rule. The `abort()` call propagates through the [`Checkpoint` seam](#checkpoint-seam) and, in subagent mode, through the one-shot `loomAbort.signal` listener that the runtime registered at spawn time and that calls `AgentSession.abort()` on the spawned session — per [Cancellation — Forwarding into `loomAbort`](./cancellation.md). The listener is detached in the same per-invocation `finally` that calls `AgentSession.dispose()` (see **Subagent session lifecycle** below).
   3. **Await subagent disposal.** `await Promise.allSettled(activeInvocations.map(inv => inv.disposeBarrier))`, where `disposeBarrier` is the promise that the **Subagent session lifecycle** `finally` block below settles after `AgentSession.dispose()` returns (subagent mode) or settles immediately (prompt mode). The await is bounded by the constant `SHUTDOWN_AWAIT_CAP_MS = 2000` measured against the runtime's injected [`Clock`](#clock--fakeclock-interface) seam: at handler entry the runtime captures `deadline = Clock.now() + SHUTDOWN_AWAIT_CAP_MS`, and the await resolves on the earlier of `Promise.allSettled(...)` settling or `Clock.setTimeout(SHUTDOWN_AWAIT_CAP_MS, ...)` firing. The deadline is absolute, not a refreshing slide — a slow `loomAbort.abort()` propagation in sub-step 2 does not extend the await. The pending `Clock.setTimeout` handle is cleared on the success path so a reload that completes early does not leak a timer onto the about-to-be-invalidated runtime. On timeout the runtime emits one `loom/runtime/reload-teardown-timeout` diagnostic naming the still-in-flight invocations and proceeds to step 4. The `SHUTDOWN_AWAIT_CAP_MS` constant lives in the same source-of-truth pinned-constants block as the Step 0 capability-probe constants so the build-time literal-read assertions can assert it.
   4. **Close watchers.** Call `discoveryWatcher.close()` (the chokidar watcher established in step 5 below) and `settingsWatcher.close()` (the settings-file watcher per [Discovery — Settings file reads](./discovery.md#settings-file-reads)); cancel any pending debounce timer handles via `Clock.clearTimeout`.
   5. **Detach forwarding listeners.** Remove every listener the runtime attached to Pi-side `ctx.signal`, tool `execute(signal)`, and parent-`invoke` signals — the same listeners [Cancellation](./cancellation.md) requires the per-invocation `finally` to remove, duplicated here for the reload-during-invocation path where Pi tears the runtime down before that `finally` ever reaches its forwarding-listener cleanup.

   **Per-step isolation.** Sub-steps 1, 4, and 5 each run inside their own `try`/`catch`; a throw from any of them MUST be caught, MUST emit exactly one `loom/host/session-shutdown-teardown-step-failed` (W, runtime) diagnostic via `console.error` with `details: { step: 1 | 4 | 5, call: <static call-site label>, error: <error.message> }`, and MUST NOT prevent the remaining sub-steps from running. Within sub-step 1 the rule applies independently to each of `LoomRegistry.drain` (the drain-flag set) and `LoomRegistry.initDrainStateTag` (the `"shutting-down"` tag-init write — the two acts sub-step 1 now performs per the prose above, two potential emissions, one per failing call); a drain-flag throw and a tag-init throw therefore occupy distinct `(code, details.step, details.call)` dedup buckets in operator logs and a future addition of a third sub-step-1 act MUST be added here on the same footing rather than collapsed into one of the existing labels. Within sub-step 4 the rule applies independently to each of `discoveryWatcher.close()`, `settingsWatcher.close()`, and the debounce-handle `Clock.clearTimeout(...)` call (three potential emissions, one per failing call). Within sub-step 5 the rule applies independently to each enumerated listener-detach call. Sub-steps 2 and 3 retain their existing per-entry isolation rules (per-entry `try`/`catch` around `loomAbort.abort()`; `Promise.allSettled` over `disposeBarrier`s) and do not emit `teardown-step-failed`. <a id="interstitial-seam-tag-write-swallow"></a>The **interstitial seam between sub-steps 4 and 5** — the `"shutting-down" → "degraded-needs-reload"` drain-state tag write pinned in the `reason: "new" | "resume" | "fork"` edge-case bullet below — is similarly wrapped in its own dedicated `try`/`catch`: a throw from the tag write (frozen `LoomRegistry`, proxied setter, OOM during property assignment) MUST be caught and silently swallowed, MUST NOT, by itself, suppress the subsequent `loom/host/session-shutdown-runtime-degraded` emission whose own diagnostic-emission predicate licenses it on this branch, nor prevent sub-step 5 from running, and MUST NOT emit `teardown-step-failed` or any other diagnostic. The trade-off this swallow accepts is that the degraded-arm `"loom /<name>: extension degraded; /reload to recover"` slash note will not fire on subsequent invocations of this extension instance (the registry tag retains its `"shutting-down"` value, so subsequent slash invocations short-circuit on the `"shutting-down"` arm instead); the rest of the handler — the emission and sub-step 5 — completes regardless. This handler-internal teardown-bookkeeping swallow is **not** a relaxation of the [Diagnostics — *Persistent diagnostics*](./diagnostics.md) "no ceiling fails silently" closure: that closure scopes to the runtime diagnostic-delivery ceiling (the defended `console.error` sink the **Diagnostic-emission isolation** rule below wraps), not to handler-internal state-bookkeeping writes — the tag write has no diagnostic of its own, and its failure mode's downstream effect (the degraded-arm slash-note suppression noted in the trade-off sentence above) is documented prose rather than a silent backstop failure of a delivery sink. The emission's own [**Diagnostic-emission isolation**](#diagnostic-emission-isolation) wrap continues to cover the `console.error` that immediately follows. The static call-site label in `details.call` is a fixed string per call site, drawn from a **closed normative set per `(code, details.step)`** so operator dedup on `(code, details.step, details.call)` is meaningful both across runs and across independent implementations of this contract — the labels are wire contract, not implementation-chosen stable-per-impl strings. The closed set is: sub-step 1: `"loomRegistry.drain"`, `"loomRegistry.initDrainStateTag"`; sub-step 4: `"discoveryWatcher.close"`, `"settingsWatcher.close"`, `"Clock.clearTimeout(debounce)"`; sub-step 5: `"ctx.signal.removeEventListener"`, `"toolSignal.removeEventListener"`, `"parentInvokeSignal.removeEventListener"` (one label per inbound Pi-side signal source sub-step 5 enumerates by name — Pi-side `ctx.signal`, the tool-exposed adapter's `signal` parameter, and the `invoke`-parent signal respectively). Adding a new call site under any of these sub-steps requires a spec edit to extend this closed set in the same commit; an implementation MUST NOT introduce a `details.call` value outside this enumeration. The interstitial seam's tag write per the **`LoomRegistry` drain-state contract** below carries the fixed label `"loomRegistry.markRuntimeDegraded"` for prose cross-reference only and is not part of the closed set above, because no `details.call` is emitted for it: the seam's own dedicated `try`/`catch` swallows silently per the rule above. When the captured throw is not an `Error` instance, `details.error` is `String(error)`, falling back to the literal string `"<unreadable>"` if that coercion itself throws — symmetric with the `details.observed` convention pinned by the **Unknown-reason rule** above. The `console.error` call this paragraph mandates is itself wrapped per the **Diagnostic-emission isolation** rule defined under *Edge cases* below; a throw from `console.error` MUST be swallowed and MUST NOT prevent the remaining sub-steps from running. The new code is **not** added to the always-log set defined under **Runtime event channel** below, matching the existing `reload-teardown-timeout` and `session-shutdown-reason-unknown` exclusions.

   <a id="idempotent-handler-clause"></a>The handler is **idempotent**: any `session_shutdown` invocation that observes the extension-scoped `LoomRegistry` either already drained or already carrying a drain-state tag in either arm of sub-step 1's closed two-arm tag set at handler entry — whether a re-entrant invocation fired *before* the first returns, a fresh invocation fired *after* the first returned on a `reason: "new" | "resume" | "fork"` branch and left the runtime in the `"degraded-needs-reload"` arm of sub-step 1's drain-state tag set per the edge-case bullet below, or a fresh invocation fired *after* a prior invocation on which sub-step 1's `LoomRegistry.drain` call threw (and was caught by the **Per-step isolation** paragraph above, leaving `drained = false`) but on which a subsequent state-setting call (sub-step 1's `LoomRegistry.initDrainStateTag` setting the tag to `"shutting-down"`, or the post-sub-step-4 `LoomRegistry.markRuntimeDegraded` setting it to `"degraded-needs-reload"`) succeeded and recorded a tag value — is a no-op: the handler returns immediately without re-executing any of sub-steps 1–5 (so sub-step 4 never double-closes the already-closed `discoveryWatcher`/`settingsWatcher` or re-`Clock.clearTimeout`s the already-cleared debounce handle, and chokidar's unpinned double-close behaviour is consequently off the load path — no second `loom/host/session-shutdown-teardown-step-failed` row can be emitted from a re-entry sub-step 4 because sub-step 4 does not re-run) and without re-emitting any of the five teardown-handler diagnostics enumerated in the **Edge cases** bullet on diagnostic emission below; in particular, `loom/host/session-shutdown-runtime-degraded` fires **at most once per extension-instance lifetime, except on the all-three-throw corner case enumerated later in this paragraph and the `readDrainState`-throw re-entry case enumerated under the [*Read-failure fallback*](#read-failure-fallback) clause of `LoomRegistry.readDrainState`'s bullet below, on each of which one additional row is emitted per follow-up `session_shutdown` event whose handler proceeds through the diagnostic-emission predicate** — on the steady path the row is emitted by the first invocation that takes the post-sub-step-4 transition; on the *all-three-throw corner case* enumerated later in this paragraph (sub-step 1's `LoomRegistry.drain`, sub-step 1's `LoomRegistry.initDrainStateTag`, and the post-sub-step-4 `LoomRegistry.markRuntimeDegraded` all throw on a session-only `session_shutdown`, leaving `drained = false` and `tag = undefined` so the broadened short-circuit predicate `snapshot.drained === true || snapshot.tag !== undefined` does not fire on re-entry), additional `loom/host/session-shutdown-runtime-degraded` rows MAY be emitted on follow-up session-only `session_shutdown` events against the same extension instance — the per-instance bound is breached for this corner case only, and operator deduplication on `(code, details.event.reason)` collapses the resulting duplicate rows; and the diagnostics-row phrase "exactly once per `session_shutdown` event in this branch" is to be read as scoped to invocations that actually reach the branch, which a short-circuited re-entry does not. This applies symmetrically across `event.reason`: a follow-up `"quit"` (or any other closed-set reason, or an unknown reason, or a snapshot-failure path) fired after an initial `"new"`/`"resume"`/`"fork"` left the runtime degraded is short-circuited at handler entry just like a same-reason re-entry, and the "runtime is being torn down anyway" rationale that suppresses `session-shutdown-runtime-degraded` on the primary `"quit"`/`"reload"` paths is preserved on the re-entry path because the entire handler (including the post-sub-step-4 transition that would otherwise write the `"degraded-needs-reload"` tag and emit the diagnostic) is short-circuited before any sub-step runs. The short-circuit predicate is the disjunction `snapshot.drained === true || snapshot.tag !== undefined` observed at handler entry — i.e., either the registry-drained flag is set **or** the drain-state tag carries either arm of sub-step 1's closed two-arm tag set — so a prior invocation on which `LoomRegistry.drain` threw (leaving `drained = false`) but on which `LoomRegistry.initDrainStateTag` or the post-sub-step-4 `LoomRegistry.markRuntimeDegraded` subsequently succeeded still establishes the short-circuit on the next handler invocation, and the rule is uniform across the `"shutting-down"` and `"degraded-needs-reload"` arms; the **Unknown-reason rule**'s pre-sub-step-1 emissions (`loom/host/session-shutdown-reason-unknown`, `loom/host/session-shutdown-pinned-constant-unreadable`) are likewise skipped on a short-circuited re-entry because the predicate check happens before those emissions on the re-entry path, preserving the at-most-one-per-extension-instance-lifetime bound on every teardown-handler diagnostic. *Handler control-flow ordering.* To make the relative ordering above unambiguous on both first-entry and re-entry, the handler's fixed control-flow at entry is exactly: **(I)** `LoomRegistry.readDrainState()` and evaluation of the short-circuit predicate `snapshot.drained === true || snapshot.tag !== undefined` per the broadened predicate above — this is the first observable side-effect of the handler on every invocation; carve-out (b) of the **Unknown-reason rule**'s pre-sequence-operations enumeration permits the variable pre-initialisations of `pinnedConstantReadOk` (to `false`) and `capturedEventReason` (to the literal string `"<unreadable>"`) to precede step (I) as handler-entry preamble (those pre-initialisations write only handler-scoped local variables and produce no observable side-effect outside the handler frame); **(II)** if the predicate fires, return immediately, with **no** snapshot lookup-and-`literals` read, **no** `event.reason` read, **no** diagnostic emission, and **no** sub-step run; **(III)** only on a false predicate, the snapshot lookup-and-`literals` read of the **Unknown-reason rule** above (which sets `pinnedConstantReadOk`); **(IV)** the `event.reason` read of the **Unknown-reason rule** above (which populates the handler-scoped `capturedEventReason`); **(V)** the **Unknown-reason rule**'s pre-sub-step-1 `loom/host/session-shutdown-pinned-constant-unreadable` / `loom/host/session-shutdown-reason-unknown` emissions per the catch-arm-discriminator rules above; **(VI)** sub-step 1 onward. The pre-sub-step-1 actions enumerated by steps (I) and (III)–(V) of this ordering, together with the handler-entry pre-initialisations of `capturedEventReason` and `pinnedConstantReadOk` that step (III)/(IV) and the *Predicate split* clause consume, are the same set the **Unknown-reason rule** above's *exactly three pre-sequence operations* enumeration permits — operations (1)–(3) of that enumeration cover the snapshot lookup-and-`literals` read (step (III)), the `event.reason` read (step (IV)), and the set-membership comparison whose non-member arm drives step (V), and the carve-out (a)/(b) of that enumeration covers step (I)'s `readDrainState` short-circuit and the two variable pre-initialisations respectively; the two enumerations are aligned by reference and a future edit to either MUST sweep both in the same commit. The Unknown-reason rule's *emits before sub-step 1 runs* obligation is satisfied on first-entry by step (V) preceding step (VI) of this ordering, not by being the absolute first action of the handler; an implementation that places the predicate check after the snapshot lookup, after the `event.reason` read, or after the unknown-reason / pinned-constant-unreadable emissions leaks a `loom/host/session-shutdown-pinned-constant-unreadable` (or `loom/host/session-shutdown-reason-unknown`) row on the re-entry path and is non-conformant, and an implementation that places the predicate check before step (VI) but skips steps (III)–(V) on a *false* predicate (i.e. on first-entry) suppresses the Unknown-reason rule's emissions entirely and is also non-conformant. The all-three-throw corner case (drain throws, `initDrainStateTag` throws, `markRuntimeDegraded` throws) leaves both `drained = false` and `tag = undefined` so the predicate evaluates to `false` and a follow-up `session_shutdown` re-runs the full handler — including sub-step 4 against the already-closed `discoveryWatcher`/`settingsWatcher` and the already-cleared debounce handle, on chokidar's acknowledged-unpinned double-close behaviour; this is the loom 1.0 acceptance, the per-call `try`/`catch` of the **Per-step isolation** paragraph already routes any double-close throw through one additional `loom/host/session-shutdown-teardown-step-failed` row per failing call site, and no further compensation is pinned because all three swallow rules above already individually fired and the runtime carries no further state seam to recover from. *Slash-dispatch interaction.* The same `(drained: false, tag: undefined)` post-handler state means slash dispatches arriving between the failed handler returning and the next `session_shutdown` event observe the steady-state tuple at the slash-handler `LoomRegistry.readDrainState` site and route through arm (a) of that read's three-arm enumeration below — i.e., dispatch the loom — into a runtime where sub-step 4 has already closed both `discoveryWatcher`/`settingsWatcher`, sub-step 5 has already detached the forwarding listeners on `ctx.signal`, the tool-exposed adapter's `signal`, and the `invoke`-parent signal, and sub-step 2 has already aborted any then-in-flight `loomAbort`s. loom 1.0 accepts this silent dispatch into the half-torn-down runtime as an additional residual gap on the same loom 1.0-acceptance footing as the duplicate-emission and double-close behaviour pinned in the rest of this paragraph (the corner case is rare — it requires three independent swallowed throws on a single session-only `session_shutdown` — and operator recovery is one `/reload` away regardless, on the same recovery footing as every other arm of the degraded-state branch). The runtime MUST NOT introduce a third boolean drain-state field, an arm-specific "post-failed-handler" gate on `LoomRegistry.readDrainState`, or any other suppression mechanism that would conditionally short-circuit slash dispatch on this post-handler tuple — the `readDrainState` arm enumeration in the **`LoomRegistry` drain-state contract**'s *Methods* paragraph below is closed at three arms ((a) dispatch, (b) shutting-down note, (c) degraded-needs-reload note) and a fourth arm or an alternative gating field is forbidden by that contract on the same footing as the *Methods* paragraph's prohibition against a fifth drain-state method or a sibling drain-state public accessor. The full re-run also re-evaluates the *Predicate split* clause's diagnostic-emission predicate `pinnedConstantReadOk && capturedEventReason ∈ {"new", "resume", "fork"}` from scratch — so on a follow-up session-only `event.reason` (`"new"`/`"resume"`/`"fork"`) with a successful snapshot read on that follow-up, the runtime emits an additional `loom/host/session-shutdown-runtime-degraded` row, breaching the at-most-once-per-extension-instance-lifetime bound stated earlier in this paragraph for this corner case only (cross-referenced from the bound itself above and from the *Predicate split* clause's *all-three-throw corner-case interaction* sub-paragraph below); operator deduplication on `(code, details.event.reason)` collapses the resulting duplicate rows. It does **not** call `ctx.reload()` (Pi is already executing it) and does **not** call `pi.unregisterTool` (Pi exposes none; the registration-cache leak is the loom 1.0 cosmetic acceptance documented under **Tool-registration lifetime and visibility** below).

   <a id="loom-registry-drain-state-contract"></a>**`LoomRegistry` drain-state contract.** The `LoomRegistry` defined in step 5 below — whose entry table is a `Map<slashName, parsedLoom>` per that step — additionally carries two drain-related fields and exposes a closed four-method call surface for them; method-call framing is normative throughout the **`session_shutdown`** handler and step 5 above, and the property-write framing elsewhere in this section (frozen `LoomRegistry`, proxied setter, OOM during property assignment) names the implementation-side *throws* those methods may surface to the per-call `try`/`catch` discipline pinned by the **Per-step isolation** paragraph and by the [interstitial-seam swallow rule](#interstitial-seam-tag-write-swallow), not an alternative property-access API the spec sanctions.

   *Fields.* (1) A boolean `drained` flag, initialised to `false` when the factory constructs the registry in step 5 below (the only pre-factory state — there is no constructor argument and no other writer establishes this field) and flipped to `true` exactly once by sub-step 1's `LoomRegistry.drain` call; never reset for the lifetime of the extension instance, so an operator-issued `/reload` re-establishes a fresh `LoomRegistry` with `drained = false` rather than reusing the existing one. (2) A `drainStateTag` field of TypeScript type `"shutting-down" | "degraded-needs-reload" | undefined` (interpreted normatively per [sub-step 1's *unset tag fallback*](#substep-1-unset-tag-fallback) above as the closed two-arm value set `"shutting-down" | "degraded-needs-reload"` plus the unset runtime state `undefined` — the latter being an implementation-side artefact of the **Per-step isolation** swallow rule rather than a third literal value), initialised to `undefined` at registry construction (the third state outside the closed two-arm tag set sub-step 1 pins, reachable also after a sub-step-1 `LoomRegistry.initDrainStateTag` throw the **Per-step isolation** paragraph caught — both initial-`undefined` and tag-init-throw-`undefined` cases share the same field value); set to `"shutting-down"` by sub-step 1's `LoomRegistry.initDrainStateTag` call when that call returns successfully; transitioned to `"degraded-needs-reload"` by the interstitial-seam `LoomRegistry.markRuntimeDegraded` call between sub-steps 4 and 5 on the branch the *Predicate split* clause of the `reason: "new" | "resume" | "fork"` edge-case bullet below pins; never otherwise mutated. The two fields are independent: `drained` does not constrain `drainStateTag` and vice versa, and the slash-handler short-circuit predicates below consume them as a tuple rather than via any derived single-value collapse.

   *Methods.* The runtime exposes exactly four method-call surfaces on `LoomRegistry` for the two fields above; no other writer or reader of either field is permitted, and the spec MUST NOT be read to authorise direct property writes (`registry.drained = true`, `registry.drainStateTag = "shutting-down"`) as an alternative to the calls below. The internal field is named `drainStateTag`; the public snapshot key on `readDrainState`'s return value is the shorter `tag`. The rename is intentional — the snapshot's tuple keys are kept short to keep slash-handler dispatch sites concise (`snapshot.tag === "shutting-down"` rather than `snapshot.drainStateTag === "shutting-down"`) — and the two names refer to the same field; an editorial unification of either name to the other would have to sweep the sibling method names that already embed the longer field name (in full or as its `DrainState` prefix) — `initDrainStateTag` (embedding `DrainStateTag`) and `readDrainState` (embedding the `DrainState` prefix), the only two of the four `LoomRegistry` methods that do so — plus the `"loomRegistry.initDrainStateTag"` `details.call` label under the **Per-step isolation** paragraph above (the only label in that closed call-site set that embeds `DrainStateTag`), and every prose site that references the longer field name (including the **Host prerequisites for the degraded-state branch** bullet (a) above and sub-step 1's *unset tag fallback* clause), and is out of scope for loom 1.0.

   - `LoomRegistry.drain(): void` — sets `drained = true`. Called from sub-step 1 of the `session_shutdown` handler above; the per-call `try`/`catch` of the **Per-step isolation** paragraph above wraps this call under `details.call = "loomRegistry.drain"`. Self-idempotent on re-call (a re-entry would re-write the same `true`), but re-entry is short-circuited at handler entry by the [**idempotent**](#idempotent-handler-clause) clause above before this call is reached.
   - `LoomRegistry.initDrainStateTag(): void` — sets `drainStateTag = "shutting-down"` iff `drainStateTag === undefined`; a no-op when `drainStateTag` is already a member of the closed two-arm tag set (so a re-call after a successful first call cannot down-grade `"degraded-needs-reload"` back to `"shutting-down"`). Called from sub-step 1 immediately after `LoomRegistry.drain` and wrapped under `details.call = "loomRegistry.initDrainStateTag"` per the **Per-step isolation** paragraph above.
   - `LoomRegistry.markRuntimeDegraded(): void` — sets `drainStateTag = "degraded-needs-reload"` unconditionally (a tag-init throw the **Per-step isolation** paragraph caught leaves the field `undefined`, and this call's contract is to overwrite that, not to assert on the prior state). Called from the interstitial seam between sub-steps 4 and 5 whenever the broader **tag-transition predicate** `capturedEventReason ∉ {"quit", "reload"}` of the *Predicate split* clause below fires (the broader predicate, NOT the narrower diagnostic-emission predicate); the seam's dedicated `try`/`catch` per the **Per-step isolation** paragraph above wraps this call and silently swallows on throw — no `loom/host/session-shutdown-teardown-step-failed` row is emitted, the call-site label `"loomRegistry.markRuntimeDegraded"` exists for prose cross-reference only; emits no `details.call` due to the swallow rule.
   - `LoomRegistry.readDrainState(): { drained: boolean; tag: "shutting-down" | "degraded-needs-reload" | undefined }` — returns a snapshot of the two fields above. This is the **single read API** the slash-command `handler` registered at the [slash-handler registration site](#slash-handler-registration) in step 3 above consults at handler entry to choose between three behaviours: (a) **dispatch** the loom when `snapshot.drained === false && snapshot.tag === undefined` (the steady-state path — both fields at their factory-construction values); (b) short-circuit on the `"shutting-down"` arm, returning the cancelled-binder-style `"loom /<name>: extension shutting down"` system note, when `snapshot.tag === "shutting-down"` or `(snapshot.drained === true && snapshot.tag === undefined)` — the former covering both the steady drained-and-tag-init-succeeded case and the `LoomRegistry.drain`-threw-but-`LoomRegistry.initDrainStateTag`-succeeded recovery case (where `drained` is `false` but the tag carries the in-progress arm), and the latter covering the tag-init-throw degraded-safely fallback sub-step 1 above pins; (c) short-circuit on the `"degraded-needs-reload"` arm, returning the distinct `"loom /<name>: extension degraded; /reload to recover"` system note, when `snapshot.tag === "degraded-needs-reload"` — regardless of `snapshot.drained`, which covers both the steady post-sub-step-4 case (`drained === true`) and the `LoomRegistry.drain`-threw-but-`LoomRegistry.markRuntimeDegraded`-succeeded recovery case (`drained === false`). The three arms are mutually exclusive and exhaust the field-tuple state space (six tuples: `(false, undefined)` → arm (a); `(false, "shutting-down")` and `(true, "shutting-down")` and `(true, undefined)` → arm (b); `(false, "degraded-needs-reload")` and `(true, "degraded-needs-reload")` → arm (c)); the slash handler MUST NOT introduce a fourth arm or read the two fields through any other accessor. The **idempotent** clause above's short-circuit predicate is the disjunction `snapshot.drained === true || snapshot.tag !== undefined` over this same accessor's return value, read once at `session_shutdown` handler entry; the predicate keys on the union of the drained flag and tag-presence and is uniform across the `"shutting-down"` and `"degraded-needs-reload"` arms per that clause — equivalently, the short-circuit fires on every tuple except the steady-state `(drained: false, tag: undefined)` that arm (a) above dispatches. <a id="read-failure-fallback"></a>*Read-failure fallback.* The `readDrainState` call itself MUST be wrapped in a per-call `try`/`catch` at both of its two call sites (the slash-command `handler` registered in step 3 above on every dispatch, and the `session_shutdown` handler at step (I) of the *Handler control-flow ordering* clause in the **idempotent** clause above), to absorb a throw out of the read (a frozen-but-mutated-import edge case, a future Proxy-backed field with a getter trap, OOM during the snapshot construction, or any other read-side throw at all the four sibling methods' per-call swallow rules already protect against on the write side). On a `readDrainState` throw the catch arm is the conservative fail-safe: at the **slash-command** call site the dispatch MUST short-circuit on arm (c) (returning the `"loom /<name>: extension degraded; /reload to recover"` system note) — the runtime cannot determine from a thrown read whether it is in the steady-state, shutting-down, or degraded-needs-reload arm and the degraded-arm note is the only one whose operator action (`/reload`) is correct on every non-dispatch arm; at the **`session_shutdown` handler-entry step (I)** call site the catch arm MUST treat the read as if it had returned the steady-state tuple `(drained: false, tag: undefined)` — equivalently, as if the predicate had **not** fired — so the handler proceeds into steps (III)–(VI) and runs the full five-sub-step teardown sequence as a fail-safe, rather than short-circuiting and silently stranding every resource the handler is responsible for releasing (chokidar `discoveryWatcher`/`settingsWatcher` handles, the debounce-handle `Clock.clearTimeout(...)` call, the forwarding listeners sub-step 5 detaches, the in-flight `loomAbort.abort()`s sub-step 2 fires, and the `disposeBarrier` awaits sub-step 3 owns) on a first-entry `session_shutdown` (the only event the handler will receive in a `/quit` or `/reload` window). This fail-safe is **asymmetric** with the slash-command call site's arm-(c) short-circuit above: at the slash-command site the degraded-arm note is the conservative operator action on every non-dispatch arm, but at the handler-entry site short-circuiting on a first-entry read failure would leak every teardown resource above silently (the rule explicitly forbids any diagnostic from this catch arm), so the spec routes the handler-entry catch arm in the opposite direction — towards executing the teardown rather than skipping it. The trade-off this fail-safe accepts is that on a re-entry the **idempotent** clause's predicate would otherwise have caught, the read-failure conceals the prior-shutdown signal from the predicate and the full sub-step sequence re-runs against an already-drained registry — additional `loom/host/session-shutdown-runtime-degraded` and other teardown-handler diagnostic rows are then emitted, breaching the at-most-once-per-extension-instance bound for this read-failure case on the same loom 1.0-acceptance footing as the *all-three-throw corner case* enumerated by the **idempotent** clause above (whose *all-three-throw corner-case interaction* sub-paragraph in the [`reason: "new" | "resume" | "fork"` edge-case bullet](#session-only-reason-degraded-state) below explicitly enumerates the same duplicate-emission shape on its own re-entry path); the duplicate emission on this read-failure branch is the loom 1.0-accepted path on the same footing as that corner case, and the runtime MUST NOT add a suppression mechanism — a sentinel flag, an in-handler dedup cache, or any other gate — that would conditionally swallow the second-and-later emissions on the read-failure re-entry; operator deduplication on `(code, details.event.reason)` collapses the resulting duplicate rows. The fail-safe also re-traverses sub-step 4 against the already-closed `discoveryWatcher`/`settingsWatcher` and the already-cleared debounce handle on chokidar's acknowledged-unpinned double-close behaviour on the re-entry path, on the same loom 1.0-acceptance grounds the *all-three-throw corner case* paragraph above pins (the per-call `try`/`catch` of the **Per-step isolation** paragraph already routes any double-close throw through one additional `loom/host/session-shutdown-teardown-step-failed` row per failing call site). No dedicated `readDrainState`-throw diagnostic is emitted from either catch arm in loom 1.0 — the slash-handler symptom (every subsequent dispatch returning the degraded-arm note rather than dispatching) is operator-observable in-band, and the handler-entry fail-safe surfaces any sub-step-internal throws through the existing per-step-isolation `loom/host/session-shutdown-teardown-step-failed` channel and the existing `(code, details.step, details.call)` deduplication keys; this is the loom 1.0 acceptance, on the same footing as the interstitial-seam swallow of `LoomRegistry.markRuntimeDegraded`'s own throw under the **Per-step isolation** paragraph above. A future edit MAY add a dedicated diagnostic for this read-failure path (e.g., `loom/host/loom-registry-read-failed`), but doing so requires a parallel edit to [Diagnostics](./diagnostics.md) and is out of scope for loom 1.0.

   The four-method call surface above is the source of truth for the method names referenced from sub-step 1, the **Per-step isolation** paragraph, the [**idempotent**](#idempotent-handler-clause) clause, and the [`reason: "new" | "resume" | "fork"` edge-case bullet](#session-only-reason-degraded-state)'s interstitial-seam transition reference; an editorial rename of any method MUST sweep all four sites in the same edit. The runtime MUST NOT add a fifth **drain-state** method to this surface or expose either of the two drain-state fields through a public accessor beyond `readDrainState`. *Scope of the closed surface and the property-write prohibition.* The closed four-method surface above governs the **drain-state** contract only — the two drain-state fields (`drained`, `drainStateTag`) and their reader/writer methods. The underlying entry-table `Map<slashName, parsedLoom>` interface that the slash-command [`handler`](#slash-handler-registration) consults to dispatch the loom (per the *Drain-state-gated dispatch* clause's arm (a) above, which routes the dispatch through this entry-table lookup after `readDrainState` returns the steady-state tuple) is unchanged from step 5 below's original `LoomRegistry` description; direct read access via that map's standard read interface (`Map.prototype.get`, `Map.prototype.has`, `Map.prototype.keys`, `Map.prototype.values`, `Map.prototype.entries`, the `for...of` iteration the watcher's rebuild path consumes per step 5 below, and the `Map.prototype.size` accessor the [Diagnostics](./diagnostics.md) row counts read) is permitted on the same footing as before this contract was added. The opening sentence of this paragraph's `no other writer or reader of either field is permitted` clause and the `direct property writes` prohibition that follows it are likewise **scoped to the two drain-state fields only** (`drained` and `drainStateTag`); they do not apply to the entry table or to any other `LoomRegistry` member step 5 below establishes. Methods unrelated to drain state (e.g., the entry-table lookup above) are out of scope of the closed-surface prohibition — additions are spec edits to this paragraph rather than implementation freedom.

   <a id="active-invocation-registry"></a>

   The **`ActiveInvocationRegistry`** is an extension-instance-scoped `Set<{ loomAbort: AbortController; disposeBarrier: Promise<void>; shutdownReason: string | undefined; loom: string; invocationId: string }>` that the runtime maintains in lock-step with each loom invocation: the `loom` field carries the invocation's canonical-key name (the *final derived name* per [Discovery — Slash-name collisions across formats](./discovery.md) — post-`pi.looms` mapping, post-`as` rename, basename-hyphen-normalised — with **no leading `/`**) and is populated at insertion time when the entry is created at each of the three insertion sites enumerated below (slash-command handler entry, `tool.execute(...)` adapter entry, and `invoke` spawn-site entry). All three insertion sites consume the **same canonical-name resolver**: the `loom` field is read from the canonical key under which the callee is registered in the runtime's loom catalog (the `LoomRegistry` `Map<slashName, parsedLoom>` entry-table whose framing the [`LoomRegistry` drain-state contract](#loom-registry-drain-state-contract) above pins, accessed via that contract's existing entry-table accessor — by name in loom 1.0 the slash-command handler's dispatch lookup against that same table — for slash-registered looms; an analogous canonical-key lookup over the loaded-`.loom`-file set for callee-only `.loom` files reached via literal `invoke("./path.loom", ...)` or via `tool.execute(...)` for subagent-mode tool-only callees that are never slash-registered, sourced from the per-load-pass static-resolution cache per [Invocation — Static resolution](./invocation.md#static-resolution) for the `invoke("./path.loom", ...)` arm and from the parent loom's load-time `tools:` resolution snapshot per [Parameters and Frontmatter — `tools`](./frontmatter.md#tools) for the subagent-mode `tool.execute(...)` arm, both of which carry the same canonical-key field on which the `LoomRegistry` entry-table keys), keyed on each arm by the slash-name lookup result the arm's underlying registration / cache / snapshot already carries: the `LoomRegistry` `Map<slashName, parsedLoom>` key for slash-registered looms, and — for callee-only `.loom` files reached via literal `invoke("./path.loom", ...)` or via `tool.execute(...)` for subagent-mode tool-only callees — the slash-name field the [Invocation — Static resolution](./invocation.md#static-resolution) cache entry and the [Parameters and Frontmatter — `tools`](./frontmatter.md#tools) snapshot entry already carry on those entries (the same final-derived-name form per [Discovery — Slash-name collisions across formats](./discovery.md): post-`pi.looms` mapping, post-`as` rename, basename-hyphen-normalised, no leading `/`). loom 1.0 carries no separate canonical-key minting obligation on the [`invocation.md#static-resolution`](./invocation.md#static-resolution) cache entries or the [`frontmatter.md#tools`](./frontmatter.md#tools) snapshot entries beyond that already-present slash-name field; the resolver consumes the slash-name lookup result on those entries only, rather than reading a separate canonical-key field that loom 1.0 does not require those entries to carry. Two callee-only `.loom` files whose basenames would otherwise collide on the same final-derived form are dropped at load time via `loom/load/cross-format-collision` per [Discovery — Slash-name collisions at the same priority](./discovery.md) (the same-priority `.loom`-vs-`.loom` arm), so the resolver never observes a collided callee-only basename at insertion time and no path-namespacing step is introduced into the canonical form to disambiguate one, so no `<callee-only>` sentinel value is introduced and the wire shape on `details.event.loom` admits this slash-name verbatim on every arm; the canonical name is **not** re-derived at the insertion site from the authored identifier the call site carries (the slash-command handler's registered command name, the `tool.execute(...)` adapter's source loom, or the `invoke(...)` literal's authored path — the third of which would otherwise leave the `pi.looms` mapping → `as` rename → basename-hyphen-normalisation order ambiguous at the spawn site and split operator dedup buckets on `details.event.loom` between two implementations that converged on different canonical forms). The resolver **fails the load-time validation that precedes any insertion-site code** when its callee would otherwise be unresolvable: callee-only basename collisions and `pi.looms` collisions are caught at discovery / load time and trigger `loom/load/cross-format-collision` per [Discovery — Slash-name collisions](./discovery.md) before reaching the insertion site, so the resolver never sees an unresolvable callee at the insertion site. By the time an entry is inserted into `ActiveInvocationRegistry` the callee has already been resolved against the loom catalog above (slash entry points dispatch off the `LoomRegistry` arm; `tool.execute(...)` entry points dispatch off the `LoomRegistry` arm for slash-registered tool-exposed looms (the prompt-mode case, where the tool reaches the model via `pi.registerTool` / `pi.setActiveTools` against a loom that is also slash-registered) and off the parent loom's load-time `tools:` resolution snapshot per [Parameters and Frontmatter — `tools`](./frontmatter.md#tools) for subagent-mode tool-only callees that are never slash-registered (the `customTools`-only case); `invoke(...)` spawn sites consume the parent loom's load-time `tools:` resolution snapshot for `tools:`-routed callables and the per-load-pass static-resolution cache per [Invocation — Static resolution](./invocation.md#static-resolution) for literal `invoke("./path.loom", ...)` callees, all of which fail their own load-time validation before any insertion-site code is reachable), so the `loom` field is **read** from the resolved catalog entry's slash-name field rather than constructed at the insertion site. The field is set on entry creation and never mutated thereafter, so it is observable in its registered form for the entire lifetime of the entry — including the [**Per-invocation operator visibility (clean-cancel path)**](#session-shutdown-semantics) rule's `details.event.loom` read in the per-invocation `finally`, on every arm including the [*Accepted loom 1.0 residual gap — sub-step-2 stamp-throw case*](#substep-2-stamp-throw-residual-gap) below where the `shutdownReason` stamp threw before the `abort()` ran (the `loom` field's pre-stamp registration means it is unaffected by the stamp throw). The `shutdownReason` field is `undefined` at insertion and is populated only by sub-step 2 of the `session_shutdown` handler above (the stamp happens before that entry's `loomAbort.abort()` call) so the per-invocation `finally`'s `loom/runtime/cancelled-by-session-shutdown` emission per the **Per-invocation operator visibility (clean-cancel path)** rule below has a handler-captured-string channel that does not depend on a runtime singleton (forbidden by the no-globals rule) or on `AbortSignal.reason` payload shape (Pi-side shape not pinned). The `invocationId` field is a per-invocation UUID in canonical lowercase 8-4-4-4-12 hex form per the [§7 `<invocation-id>` placeholder convention](./diagnostics.md#7-identifier--descriptor--and-closed-enum-placeholders), allocated at registry-insertion time inside the **Dispatch-site setup wrap** `try`/`catch` (see *Registry contract* below) before any awaitable work, and set on entry creation and never mutated thereafter; downstream consumers — the per-invocation `finally`'s `loom/runtime/cancelled-by-session-shutdown` `details.event.invocation_id` per the **Per-invocation operator visibility (clean-cancel path)** rule below, and the `RuntimeEvent.invocation_id` wire field defined under **Runtime event channel** below — read this single registry-sourced value rather than re-deriving an id at the emission site, and `loom/runtime/reload-teardown-timeout`'s `<list>` rendering reads the same field per its row in [Diagnostics](./diagnostics.md). The registry-side identifier is spelled `invocationId` in lowerCamelCase (matching this section's other runtime-state members `loomAbort`, `disposeBarrier`, `shutdownReason`), while the corresponding wire-side names — `details.event.invocation_id`, `RuntimeEvent.invocation_id`, and the `<invocation-id>` placeholder in `loom/runtime/reload-teardown-timeout`'s `<list>` — are rendered in snake_case (matching the rest of this corpus's wire-payload field surface); downstream consumers therefore read the registry entry's field as `entry.invocationId` and surface its value under the snake_case wire name at each emission site (e.g. the *Runtime construction obligation* in [Diagnostics — `details` shape conventions for the `session_shutdown` event payload](./diagnostics.md#session-shutdown-details-conventions) constructs `details.event` with the static property name `invocation_id` assigned from `entry.invocationId`). The sibling `loom` field happens to spell identically on both sides because its token is already in snake-shape, not because the registry-side and wire-side names are uniformly identity-mapped. The runtime maintains the registry in lock-step with each loom invocation: the slash-command `handler`, the `tool.execute(...)` adapter for tool-exposed looms, and the parent-`invoke` spawn site each insert their own entry on entry and remove it from the same `finally` block that already disposes any subagent session (per **Subagent session lifecycle** below). The `disposeBarrier` is the promise that the per-invocation `finally` settles after `AgentSession.dispose()` returns (subagent mode) or immediately (prompt mode). Concurrent loom invocations therefore each carry one entry; the registry is the structure the teardown handler iterates.

   *Registry contract.*

   - **Insertion** happens at slash-command handler entry, `tool.execute(...)` adapter entry, and `invoke` spawn-site entry, before any awaitable work.
   - **Removal** happens in the same `finally` block that disposes the subagent `AgentSession`, after `disposeBarrier` settles.
   - **Dispatch-site setup wrap.** Each of the three insertion sites MUST wrap the pre-evaluation setup sequence — `new AbortController()` for `loomAbort`, the registry-`Set.add` insertion, the per-entry-point `source.addEventListener('abort', …)` attach that registers the forwarding listener on the inbound Pi-side `AbortSignal` (the slash-command handler's `ctx.signal`, the tool-exposed adapter's `signal` parameter, or the `invoke`-parent's parent-signal — see [Cancellation — Forwarding into `loomAbort`](./cancellation.md)), and (subagent mode only) the awaited `createAgentSession(...)` call followed by the post-resolution `loomAbort.signal.addEventListener('abort', …)` attach that wires the one-shot `AgentSession.abort()` listener — in a `try`/`catch` whose `catch` arm routes the captured throw or rejection through the **runtime-defect surface** defined in [Errors and Results — Runtime panics](./errors-and-results.md#runtime-panics) (single rule, three call sites; the `createAgentSession`-rejects paragraph in **Subagent session lifecycle** below is a worked example of this rule rather than a one-off). No new `details.kind` discriminator is introduced for the listener-attach throws — the existing `loom/runtime/internal-error` surface carries `error.message` and `error.stack` and that is sufficient for triage. On a throw before the `Set.add` insertion completes no registry entry leaks (nothing to remove); on a throw after insertion the same per-invocation `finally` removes the entry and settles `disposeBarrier`. The `cause: "internal_error"` arm of [`InvokeInfraError`](./errors-and-results.md#invoke-variants) and the slash-command system-note template `"loom /<name> aborted with internal error: <error.message>"` defined in [Errors and Results — Runtime panics](./errors-and-results.md#runtime-panics) apply unchanged. A throw from `loomAbort.abort()` invoked by the `catch` arm during cleanup of a half-constructed entry is itself swallowed by the per-entry `try`/`catch` of the **`session_shutdown`** sub-step 2 rule above and MUST NOT mask the original setup throw.
   - **Iteration order** in the `session_shutdown` handler's sub-step 2 (`loomAbort.abort()` over every entry) and sub-step 3 (`Promise.allSettled` over every entry's `disposeBarrier`) is insertion order, matching the V8 `Set` insertion-order invariant the rest of the spec already relies on. The order is observable to tests asserting on the order of `loom/runtime/reload-teardown-timeout`'s `<list>` rendering.
   - **`loomAbort.abort()` throwing inside the sub-step 2 iteration** is swallowed by a per-entry `try`/`catch`; the handler continues to the next entry. No diagnostic is emitted (the abort is best-effort and the entry's own `finally` will still settle `disposeBarrier`, which sub-step 3 already awaits with `Promise.allSettled`).
   - **The registry name is internal.** It is not part of the loom-facing or extension-facing contract; tests assert on observable side effects (entry counts via probe seams, ordered `loomAbort.abort()` calls, `disposeBarrier` settlement) rather than on the symbol itself.
   - **Per-mode concurrency invariants.** The registry tracks both prompt-mode and subagent-mode entries (so the `session_shutdown` teardown above reaches every in-flight invocation); the *insertion shape* differs by mode, but the entry shape and the iteration rule do not. *Subagent-mode* entries may be genuine concurrent siblings: parallel tool calls into the same `.loom` callable, sibling `invoke(...)` sites whose children resolve to subagent mode, and parent→child stacks of subagent-mode invocations all coexist as distinct registry entries that progress on the event loop independently. *Prompt-mode* entries are constrained to **linear nesting** within a single user session: at most one prompt-mode body holds an open `pi.setActiveTools` snapshot/restore window at a time, but a prompt-mode parent suspended on an `invoke(...)` to a prompt-mode child legitimately keeps its own registry entry while the child's entry is also live (the parent is suspended at the call site, not dispatched, and only the child's snapshot/restore window is open). The teardown `loomAbort.abort()` iteration in sub-step 2 above must reach the suspended parent's entry as well as the child's. The supporting mechanisms that pin prompt-mode linear nesting — Pi's per-session slash-handler serialisation pinned under **Tool-registration lifetime and visibility** below, the load-time rejection of prompt-mode `.loom` callees in another loom's `tools:` per [Parameters and Frontmatter — `tools`](./frontmatter.md#tools), and the suspend-on-invoke rule from [Invocation — Cross-mode semantics](./invocation.md) — are owned by those pages; the registry contract above relies on them but does not restate them. Subagent-mode children spawned from a prompt-mode parent are genuinely concurrent and add their own registry entries on the same insertion-site rules above.

   *Edge cases the handler must observe:*

   - `ExtensionRuntime.invalidate()` may already have been called by Pi when the handler runs; any `pi.*` call that reaches the stale runtime throws. The teardown sequence above touches only loom-internal state and the SDK objects (`AbortController`, chokidar `FSWatcher`, `AgentSession`) directly — it does not call back into `pi.*`.
   - The `sendSystemNote` fallback chain (the best-effort chain defined under **System notes** below) MUST NOT be invoked from the teardown handler — `pi.sendMessage` against a stale runtime throws, and the fallback to `ctx.ui.notify` would re-enter the same stale surface. Diagnostics emitted from the teardown handler use `console.error` directly, bypassing the persistent-diagnostic channel defined in [Diagnostics](./diagnostics.md). Five diagnostics may be emitted from this handler, all via `console.error`: `loom/runtime/reload-teardown-timeout` (referenced in sub-step 3), `loom/host/session-shutdown-reason-unknown` (referenced in the **Unknown-reason rule** above), `loom/host/session-shutdown-pinned-constant-unreadable` (referenced in the **Unknown-reason rule** above, on a failure of the handler-entry pinned-constant lookup), `loom/host/session-shutdown-teardown-step-failed` (referenced in the **Per-step isolation** paragraph above), and `loom/host/session-shutdown-runtime-degraded` (referenced in the `reason: "new" | "resume" | "fork"` bullet below, after sub-step 4 returns on the three session-only reasons; emission is independent of sub-step 4's per-call outcomes per that bullet). No other diagnostic code may be emitted from this handler.
   - <a id="diagnostic-emission-isolation"></a> **Diagnostic-emission isolation.** Each `console.error` call inside the `session_shutdown` handler — the five teardown-handler emissions enumerated in the bullet immediately above (`loom/runtime/reload-teardown-timeout`, `loom/host/session-shutdown-reason-unknown`, `loom/host/session-shutdown-pinned-constant-unreadable`, `loom/host/session-shutdown-teardown-step-failed`, `loom/host/session-shutdown-runtime-degraded`) — MUST be wrapped in `try`/`catch`. *Wire format.* Each such `console.error` call carries a single argument: a serialised structured object containing the four required fields `code`, `severity`, `message`, and `details` (matching the row's columns in [Diagnostics](./diagnostics.md) and the `details` shape pinned per code in this paragraph and the **Unknown-reason rule** above), plus the optional `hint?` field from the [`Internal diagnostic shape`](./diagnostics.md) declaration when set; of the five teardown-handler codes only `loom/runtime/reload-teardown-timeout` pins `hint` (its row in [Diagnostics](./diagnostics.md) pins `hint` to the elapsed wall time and that pin stands; implementations MUST set `hint` accordingly on that code), and implementations MAY omit `hint` on the other four codes (`loom/host/session-shutdown-reason-unknown`, `loom/host/session-shutdown-pinned-constant-unreadable`, `loom/host/session-shutdown-teardown-step-failed`, `loom/host/session-shutdown-runtime-degraded`), none of which pins `hint`; the other optional fields of the `Internal diagnostic shape` — `file`, `range`, `related?`, `masked?` — are likewise not pinned by any of the five codes and MAY be omitted, on the same footing as `hint` on those four codes; the exact serialisation primitive (e.g. `JSON.stringify`) is leaf-owned and not pinned here, but the field names and the per-code `details` shapes MUST be preserved verbatim so log-pipeline and operator-tooling consumers can parse a single contract across all five codes. *`details` nesting convention.* The wire-format nesting convention for `details` payloads that surface the `session_shutdown` event payload — the `details.event.{reason}` shape `loom/host/session-shutdown-runtime-degraded` carries (mirroring `loom/runtime/cancelled-by-session-shutdown`), the closed-at-`{reason}`-in-loom-1.0.0 pin governing additions, and the carve-out keeping the four sibling teardown-handler codes' runtime-constructed failure-mode payloads (`details.observed`, `details.failure`, `details.step` / `.call` / `.error`) flat under `details` — is owned by [Diagnostics — `details` shape conventions for the `session_shutdown` event payload](./diagnostics.md#session-shutdown-details-conventions); this paragraph imports that contract by reference and adds no per-code shape rules of its own. The same wire-format pin applies to the terminal `console.error` of the `sendSystemNote` fallback chain referenced at the end of this paragraph. The entire serialisation-and-emission sequence — the leaf-owned serialisation primitive call followed by the `console.error` call it feeds — MUST be wrapped in a single `try`/`catch`; on a serialiser throw (e.g. a circular `cause`, a `BigInt` field, a host-shimmed `JSON.stringify` getter, or any other foreseeable serialiser failure) the catch arm MUST fall back to emitting `console.error(code)` — the bare diagnostic code string for the diagnostic that was being serialised — so the code remains grep-able in operator logs even when structured emission failed, and MUST NOT re-throw. *Two-token fallback for nested-shape codes.* For the two codes whose `details` payload nests the `session_shutdown` event under `details.event.*` per the [`details` shape conventions for the `session_shutdown` event payload](./diagnostics.md#session-shutdown-details-conventions) — `loom/host/session-shutdown-runtime-degraded` and `loom/runtime/cancelled-by-session-shutdown` — the catch arm MUST instead emit the two-token form `` console.error(`${code} ${detailsEventReason}`) ``, where `detailsEventReason` is the `details.event.reason` string the structured payload would have carried (already a string per the captured-value cases the **Unknown-reason rule** above pins for `loom/host/session-shutdown-runtime-degraded`, and per the **Per-invocation operator visibility (clean-cancel path)** bullet below's `entry.shutdownReason` channel for `loom/runtime/cancelled-by-session-shutdown`; no further coercion is needed and the interpolation MUST NOT itself re-throw). *Hoist obligation.* The runtime MUST hoist that `details.event.reason` value into a local string binding (e.g. `const detailsEventReason: string = ...`) **before** entering the wrapped serialisation-and-emission sequence — i.e. as part of the same payload-construction code that, on the per-invocation clean-cancel path for `loom/runtime/cancelled-by-session-shutdown`, already performs the unset-`entry.shutdownReason` `"<unreadable>"` substitution pinned by the [*Accepted loom 1.0 residual gap — sub-step-2 stamp-throw case*](#session-only-reason-degraded-state) paragraph below (the substitution lives at payload-construction time so the structured `details.event.reason` field carries a string, never `undefined`) — and the catch arm MUST interpolate the pre-hoisted local rather than re-reading from the partially-constructed structured object or from `entry.shutdownReason` directly. This decouples the catch arm from the structured-object-construction order (so a serialiser throw mid-construction cannot leave the catch arm reading from an unbuilt or absent field) and from any defensive coercion the catch arm itself would otherwise need. On a sub-step-2 stamp-throw entry that later reaches the per-invocation `finally`'s clean-cancel emission, the hoisted local therefore carries the literal string `"<unreadable>"` per the same residual-gap paragraph, and the two-token catch arm interpolates that sentinel verbatim on the same footing as the closed-set, `String(event.reason)`-coerced, and throwing-property-access captured-value cases. This preserves the `details.event.reason` dedup discriminator that operator deduplication keys on for those two rows in [Diagnostics](./diagnostics.md) — without it, every session-only reason (and every cleanly-cancelled invocation across `event.reason` values on the per-invocation note) would collapse into a single bare-`code` dedup bucket on serialiser throw, splitting nothing rather than preserving the per-reason buckets the structured emission would have produced. The two-token form is otherwise governed by the same MUST-NOT-re-throw and silent-swallow obligations as the bare-`code` fallback above, and remains part of the *same* wrapped sequence per the *Count semantics* pin below (it does not count as a second invocation against per-event "exactly once" bounds). *Construction-site wrap.* The runtime construction of the structured payload's `details.event` field per the [Runtime construction obligation](./diagnostics.md#session-shutdown-details-conventions) — the explicit-static-property construction of `{ reason }` for `loom/host/session-shutdown-runtime-degraded` and `{ reason, loom, invocation_id }` for `loom/runtime/cancelled-by-session-shutdown` — runs *before* the wrapped serialisation-and-emission sequence above, and the *Hoist obligation* clause's construction of the `detailsEventReason` local likewise lives at payload-construction time outside that wrap. A throw from either construction site (a frozen target object, a throwing setter on a host-shimmed `Object` prototype, an out-of-memory failure during property assignment, or any other foreseeable construction-site failure) is therefore not defended by the serialisation-and-emission wrap. The runtime MUST wrap the entire payload-construction code — both the `details.event` construction and the `detailsEventReason` hoist — in its own `try`/`catch` so a construction-site throw cannot escape the handler. *Scope.* The construction-site wrap rule applies **only to the two nested-shape codes** (`loom/host/session-shutdown-runtime-degraded`, `loom/runtime/cancelled-by-session-shutdown`), since by the wrap definition above (`details.event` construction + `detailsEventReason` hoist) those are the only payload-construction acts under this rule's coverage. The three flat-`details` teardown-handler codes (`loom/host/session-shutdown-reason-unknown`, `loom/host/session-shutdown-pinned-constant-unreadable`, `loom/host/session-shutdown-teardown-step-failed`) build their `details` payloads outside this wrap — via the `String(event.reason)` coercion (Unknown-reason), the closed-discriminator-literal selection on `details.observed` / `details.failure` (pinned-constant-unreadable), and the `String(error)` / `"<unreadable>"` coercion (teardown-step-failed) — all of which already tolerate non-string values per the **Unknown-reason rule** above and the *Per-step isolation* paragraph and are by construction infallible at the payload-build site. They therefore cannot enter this catch arm, and this rule pins no construction-site fallback for them; their bare-`code` fallback under the serialisation-and-emission wrap above remains unchanged. On a construction-site throw the catch arm MUST skip the structured serialisation-and-emission sequence and emit directly through a per-code fallback form whose token count differs by row. For `loom/host/session-shutdown-runtime-degraded`, the catch arm emits the two-token form `` console.error(`${code} <unreadable>`) `` — interpolating the literal `"<unreadable>"` sentinel rather than the (potentially-unbuilt) `detailsEventReason` local — and substitutes that literal for `details.event.reason` (the only payload field this row carries under `details.event`). For `loom/runtime/cancelled-by-session-shutdown` (the per-invocation note), the catch arm MUST instead read `entry.loom` separately from the [`ActiveInvocationRegistry`](#active-invocation-registry) entry the per-invocation `finally` already holds and emit the three-token form `` console.error(`${code} ${entry.loom} <unreadable>`) `` — substituting the `"<unreadable>"` literal for `details.event.reason` while preserving `details.event.loom`'s per-invocation discrimination via the interpolated `entry.loom` token. The separate `entry.loom` read on the catch arm is no riskier than the per-invocation `finally`'s structured-emission read of the same field, because the [`ActiveInvocationRegistry`](#active-invocation-registry) lifetime guarantee above pins `loom` as set on entry creation and never mutated thereafter, observable in its registered form for the entire lifetime of the entry — including on a construction-site throw that interrupts payload-construction code reading or stamping other fields. The `"<unreadable>"` literal remains the **single source of truth for catch-arm payload defaults** for `details.event.reason` under this clause on both rows, so the construction-site failure path's `details.event.reason` value space remains inside the captured-value enumeration the **Unknown-reason rule** above pins for that field, and the per-reason dedup buckets the two-token fallback preserves on serialiser throw also cover this path on the same footing as the throwing-property-access and snapshot-failure paths. The per-invocation note's three-token form additionally preserves the per-loom dedup bucket the `details.event.loom` field carries on the structured-emission path, which the runtime-degraded row's two-token form has no field to preserve (that row carries no `loom` under `details.event`). The catch-arm `console.error` invocation is itself subject to the inner-throw swallow obligation below: a throw from `console.error` MUST be swallowed on the same footing as the wrapped sequence's swallowed write, and the construction-site catch arm MUST NOT re-throw or attempt a second emission against the same event. *Construction-site catch-arm self-wrap.* Because the construction-site `console.error` invocation is structurally outside the serialisation-and-emission `try`/`catch` (whose catch arm is the inner-throw swallow obligation below's syntactic locus), the construction-site catch arm cannot inherit that catch arm's swallow by structural containment alone.
