The construction-site catch arm MUST therefore wrap its own fallback `console.error` call in a dedicated `try`/`catch` whose catch arm silently swallows the throw and returns control to the handler so it can continue to the next sub-step (or, for the **Unknown-reason rule** emission that runs *before* sub-step 1, into sub-step 1) on the same footing as the serialisation-and-emission wrap's swallowed write. No further fallback is available; the handler is the bottom of the stack with no further sink, and the construction-site path's *Count semantics* framing (the construction-site emission counts as the single emission against the per-event bound, per the previous sentence) is preserved on inner-throw exactly as the serialisation-and-emission wrap's bare-`code` fallback is. The construction-site path and the wrapped-sequence path are mutually exclusive — at most one of the two emits per event/invocation — and the construction-site emission counts as the single emission against the per-event "exactly once" / "at most once" bound the *Count semantics* clause below pins (neither path counts as a second invocation against the other). <a id="pic-emission-swallow"></a> *Handler-isolation swallow.* A throw out of `console.error` (closed stdio, file-descriptor exhaustion, a host that proxies `console` and rejects writes during teardown) MUST be swallowed; the handler MUST continue to the next sub-step (or, for the **Unknown-reason rule** emission that runs *before* sub-step 1, MUST continue into sub-step 1). No further diagnostic is emitted on the inner throw — the only sink available to the teardown handler has already failed and the handler is the bottom of the stack with no further fallback. *Count semantics — invocation-site framing.* All "exactly once" / "at most once" / "emits exactly one" / "Emitted exactly once" / "Emitted at most once" emission-count bounds that this paragraph's five wrapped teardown-handler diagnostic codes (and the terminal `console.error` of the per-invocation `sendSystemNote` fallback chain referenced at the end of this paragraph) cite — wherever they appear, including the **Unknown-reason rule** above's per-event bounds on `loom/host/session-shutdown-reason-unknown` and `loom/host/session-shutdown-pinned-constant-unreadable`, the **Per-step isolation** paragraph's per-failing-call-site bound on `loom/host/session-shutdown-teardown-step-failed`, the [`reason: "new" | "resume" | "fork"` edge-case bullet's](#session-only-reason-degraded-state) per-event-in-this-branch bound on `loom/host/session-shutdown-runtime-degraded` (and that bullet's *Acceptance criteria* per-branch "the handler emits exactly one" obligations, which inherit this framing), the **idempotent** clause above's at-most-once-per-extension-instance-lifetime bound on the same code, the **Per-invocation operator visibility (clean-cancel path)** bullet below's per-cleanly-cancelled-invocation bound on `loom/runtime/cancelled-by-session-shutdown`, sub-step 3's at-most-once-per-event bound on `loom/runtime/reload-teardown-timeout`, and the corresponding row wording in [Diagnostics](./diagnostics.md) for each code — are measured at the **handler invocation site**: the bound counts the number of times the handler enters the leaf-owned serialisation-and-emission sequence this rule wraps (the serialisation primitive call followed by the `console.error` call it feeds, including the bare-`code` fallback `console.error(code)` on serialiser throw) for the same `session_shutdown` event (or the same cleanly-cancelled invocation, for the per-invocation note), not the number of rows that reach an operator sink. A host that silently drops the resulting `console.error` write therefore still satisfies the bound — the invocation occurred even if the row never reached the sink — and a retry-on-inner-throw is forbidden, because issuing a second serialisation-and-emission sequence for the same event after the first inner-threw would breach the at-most-once half of the bound. The bare-`code` fallback on serialiser throw is part of the *same* wrapped sequence as the original structured `console.error` (the catch arm of the serialisation-and-emission `try`/`catch`, per the wrap clause above), not a second invocation, and therefore does not count against the bound. The wrap is around the serialisation-and-emission sequence (serialisation primitive call plus `console.error` call, including the bare-`code` fallback `console.error(code)` above) only; the `String(event.reason)` coercion that builds the **Unknown-reason** diagnostic's `details.observed` payload, and the `String(error)` / `"<unreadable>"` coercion that builds the **Per-step isolation** diagnostic's `details.error` payload, already tolerate non-string values per the rules above and are outside the wrap. Emission ordering is preserved: a swallowed `console.error` throw leaves the handler in the same position it would be after a successful emit (in particular, the **Unknown-reason rule**'s "emits *before* sub-step 1 runs" obligation is satisfied even when the emission inner-throws). The rule is symmetric for all five teardown-handler diagnostic codes; no per-code carve-outs. <a id="pic-emission-visibility"></a> *Pi-side stdio visibility.* Teardown-time `console.error` visibility is **best-effort**: the runtime emits through the channel and wraps each emission per this rule so a swallowed write never unwinds the handler, but the spec makes no normative claim that the write reaches an operator surface (see [Future Considerations — loom 1.0 non-goals — No reliance on a Pi extension-host stdio-capture facet](./future-considerations.md#pi-stdio-capture-facet) for the host presupposition this rests on, and for the future-work disposition if Pi adds an explicit stdio-capture facet). The same isolation MUST be applied to the terminal `console.error` of the `sendSystemNote` fallback chain when that chain is reached from the per-invocation `finally` of the **Per-invocation operator visibility (clean-cancel path)** paragraph below: a throw from that terminal `console.error` MUST be swallowed and MUST NOT propagate out of the per-invocation `finally`.
   - <a id="session-only-reason-degraded-state"></a> `reason: "new" | "resume" | "fork"` does not always tear down the *extension* runtime (only the user session), but Pi's `session_shutdown` type doc states the event "is fired before an extension runtime is torn down" — the handler runs the full fixed five-sub-step sequence — including watcher closure in sub-step 4 — for every reason in the closed set, and the loom 1.0 position accepts that watchers may be closed on a reason (e.g. `"fork"`) that did not in fact tear the extension down. The three Pi SDK behaviours this branch silently relies on (extension-instance survival across session-only `session_shutdown`; multi-`session_shutdown` delivery permitted to a single instance; and the `/reload` and `ctx.reload()` recovery semantics on which the *Operator-issued `/reload`* sentence later in this bullet and acceptance criterion (g) both depend) are enumerated explicitly under [**Host prerequisites for the degraded-state branch**](#degraded-state-host-prerequisites) above; the editorial-review obligation pinned there on a Pi version bump is what catches a Pi minor that violates any of them. After such a closure the extension runtime remains live but is *degraded for the remainder of its lifetime*: sub-step 1 has marked the `LoomRegistry` as drained and there is no rule that ever un-drains it, and the handler — immediately after sub-step 4 returns on this branch (and on the snapshot-failure path AND on the unknown-reason-with-successful-snapshot path, both per the broader **tag-transition predicate** of the *Predicate split* clause below — the broader predicate is `capturedEventReason ∉ {"quit", "reload"}` and covers all three arms, each of which routes there for the same factual-degradation reason: sub-step 4 has unconditionally closed both watchers and the runtime is degraded for the remainder of its lifetime regardless of whether Pi delivered a session-only, always-tear-down, or unknown `event.reason`) and before sub-step 5 runs — writes the registry's drain-state tag to `"degraded-needs-reload"` unconditionally — a **state-independent write** that overwrites whatever value the tag held (`"shutting-down"`, `undefined` from a prior `initDrainStateTag` throw, or any unexpected residual) without reading the prior state, per the `LoomRegistry.markRuntimeDegraded` contract in the *Methods* paragraph above (and, per sub-step 1's closed two-arm tag set, the **only** writer of the second arm), so an unset source state (reachable when sub-step 1's `LoomRegistry.initDrainStateTag` threw and was caught by the **Per-step isolation** paragraph above, leaving `drainStateTag = undefined`) is overwritten on the same footing as a `"shutting-down"` source state and a tag-init throw therefore cannot silently defeat the degraded-arm signal; an implementation that gated this write on observing a `"shutting-down"` source state (so an unset tag would no-op the transition and the runtime would remain on the `"shutting-down"` arm forever) is non-conformant — so every subsequent slash invocation short-circuits with the distinct `"loom /<name>: extension degraded; /reload to recover"` system note rather than the misleading `"shutting down"` template (which would falsely suggest the runtime is in a transient teardown state and leave an operator on a stdio-capturing host — where the best-effort `console.error` visibility of `loom/host/session-shutdown-runtime-degraded` may be lost — with no in-band signal that `/reload` is required); the post-sub-step-4 closed `discoveryWatcher` and `settingsWatcher` mean editor-driven `.loom` and settings edits silently no-op. Operator-issued `/reload` (which invokes Pi's `ctx.reload()` and re-executes the extension factory) is the **only** loom 1.0 recovery path that re-establishes a fresh runtime; the runtime MUST NOT un-drain the registry, MUST NOT re-subscribe or re-establish the closed `discoveryWatcher` or `settingsWatcher`, MUST NOT poll for `.loom` or settings changes after watcher closure, and MUST NOT introduce any other discovery, re-scan, or self-recovery path on the degraded branch. The "editor-driven `.loom` and settings edits silently no-op" guarantee in the previous sentence is delivered by this exhaustive prohibition rather than by the implicit absence of other paths; a future relaxation (e.g. a polling fallback) MUST be routed through a spec edit to this bullet, and the post-shutdown re-emission half of the silence — that subsequent `session_shutdown` events fired against the same extension instance emit no further `loom/host/session-shutdown-runtime-degraded` row (the row is emitted only from the `session_shutdown` handler between sub-steps 4 and 5, so re-entry of that handler is the only path that could re-emit it; slash invocations have no `runtime-degraded` emission path to suppress) — is already pinned by the **idempotent** clause above (the at-most-once-per-extension-instance-lifetime bound covers post-return re-entry on the degraded branch). To make the degradation observable rather than silent, the handler emits exactly one `loom/host/session-shutdown-runtime-degraded` (W, runtime) diagnostic via `console.error` *between sub-steps 4 and 5* (i.e. after sub-step 4 returns and before sub-step 5 runs, on the same handler-scoped seam as the unconditional `"degraded-needs-reload"` drain-state tag write pinned in the previous sentence — the tag write runs first and the emission, when its narrower predicate of the *Predicate split* clause below is satisfied, immediately follows (on the snapshot-failure path the tag transition runs alone — the diagnostic emission is suppressed because the snapshot-failure path's own `loom/host/session-shutdown-pinned-constant-unreadable` row already pins the diagnostic-channel observability for that shutdown event and a co-emission of `runtime-degraded` would split operator deduplication buckets across two codes describing the same event without adding an operator-actionable distinction), both outside any sub-step's per-call `try`/`catch` and each wrapped by its own dedicated `try`/`catch` per the **Per-step isolation** paragraph above (the tag transition by the [interstitial-seam swallow rule](#interstitial-seam-tag-write-swallow) pinned there; the emission by its own [**Diagnostic-emission isolation**](#diagnostic-emission-isolation) `try`/`catch`) so neither a tag-write throw nor a swallowed `console.error` throw unwinds the handler before sub-step 5 runs; placing the emission *after* sub-step 5 returns is non-conformant because a sub-step 5 listener-detach throw would route through `loom/host/session-shutdown-teardown-step-failed` and the degraded-state notification would then either co-emit out of the documented order or be skipped if a future edit grew an early-return on that sub-step) and *only when `event.reason ∈ {"new", "resume", "fork"}`* (the three *session-only reasons*: the closed-set members on which Pi swaps the user session without tearing the extension runtime down; the three-literal subset is **inlined at the handler emission site** rather than read off the `SessionShutdownEvent['reason']` snapshot's `literals` field — the partition `{"quit", "reload"}` vs. `{"new", "resume", "fork"}` reflects Pi's documented `session_shutdown` teardown-vs-session-swap distinction, which is not pinned by a single SDK identifier the snapshot could carry, and a parallel snapshot entry for the subset would double-pin the same SDK union in two places that can drift independently. The inline triplet at this emission site is therefore a **normative runtime literal** (not an illustrative restatement of the full closed-set snapshot under [Pi version bump procedure](#pi-version-bump-procedure) step 1's carve-out, whose enumeration covers in-prose closed-set listings only), whose source-of-truth pin is this bullet; a Pi version bump that renames a session-only literal — e.g., `"fork" → "branch"` — surfaces as a bidirectional `SessionShutdownEvent['reason']` type-equality red carrying the literal brand string `loom/typecheck/session-shutdown-reason-snapshot` per [Pi version bump procedure](#pi-version-bump-procedure) step 5 below, and that step's inbound-reference sweep MUST update this inline triplet at the same emission site in the same edit so the diagnostic does not silently no-op for the renamed reason); on `"quit"` and `"reload"` the diagnostic is **not** emitted (the runtime is being torn down anyway), and on the unknown-reason and snapshot-failure paths it is **not** emitted (the unknown-reason path's own `loom/host/session-shutdown-reason-unknown` and snapshot-failure path's own `loom/host/session-shutdown-pinned-constant-unreadable` already pin observability for those paths). The emission is **independent of sub-step 4's per-call outcomes**: it fires whether or not any of sub-step 4's three call sites (`discoveryWatcher.close()`, `settingsWatcher.close()`, the debounce-handle `Clock.clearTimeout(...)` call) entered its per-call `try`/`catch` arm under the **Per-step isolation** paragraph above. The discriminator is the **branch** the handler is on (the closed-set membership check above), not any intra-sub-step-4 success flag — the **Per-step isolation** rule's own per-call `try`/`catch` already guarantees sub-step 4 always returns to the handler, so a literal "sub-step 4 completed without a throw" predicate would be vacuous and the runtime MUST NOT introduce one. Concretely, the runtime MUST gate the emission on the conjunction of two handler-scoped seams the rules above already mandate: a boolean `pinnedConstantReadOk`, captured at handler entry and set to `true` iff the snapshot lookup-and-`literals` read of the **Unknown-reason rule** above succeeded (i.e. the `loom/host/session-shutdown-pinned-constant-unreadable` catch arm did not fire on this shutdown), AND the handler-scoped captured `event.reason` string (the same variable the **Unknown-reason rule** pins, which sub-step 2 stamps onto each entry's `shutdownReason` field) being a member of the inline triplet `{"new", "resume", "fork"}` — i.e. the **diagnostic-emission predicate** is `pinnedConstantReadOk && capturedEventReason ∈ {"new", "resume", "fork"}`, with no third conjunct. *Predicate split.* The predicate above gates **only** the `loom/host/session-shutdown-runtime-degraded` emission. The **tag-transition predicate** governing the unconditional `"degraded-needs-reload"` write pinned in the early prose of this bullet is **deliberately broader**: `capturedEventReason ∉ {"quit", "reload"}` — equivalently, "anything other than a captured `"quit"` or `"reload"`", i.e. the broader predicate fires whenever the handler cannot determine that the runtime is being torn down anyway. Three arms inhabit this predicate and each invokes the same factual-degradation rule (sub-step 4 has unconditionally closed both watchers, there is no un-drain rule, and the runtime is therefore *factually degraded for the remainder of its lifetime*): (1) the **session-only triplet** `{"new", "resume", "fork"}` directly, where `capturedEventReason` carries the closed-set member Pi delivered; (2) the **snapshot-failure path**, where `capturedEventReason` retains its `"<unreadable>"` pre-initialisation per the **Unknown-reason rule**'s fixed read order (the `event.reason` read was never reached because the snapshot read failed first), so the comparand is the sentinel string and is therefore not in `{"quit", "reload"}`; and (3) the **unknown-reason path with a successful snapshot read**, where `capturedEventReason` is the `String(event.reason)` coercion of the off-snapshot literal Pi delivered or the `"<unreadable>"` sentinel from a throwing-property-access read, neither of which inhabits `{"quit", "reload"}`. The complement-form `capturedEventReason ∉ {"quit", "reload"}` is the value-independent state seam that pins the conservative tag write across all three arms — ensuring an operator on a stdio-capturing host (where the `console.error`-routed `loom/host/session-shutdown-pinned-constant-unreadable` and `loom/host/session-shutdown-reason-unknown` writes may be lost) still observes the in-band `"loom /<name>: extension degraded; /reload to recover"` signal on the next slash invocation rather than the misleading `"loom /<name>: extension shutting down"` template that would otherwise front the unmodified `"shutting-down"` arm. The two `"<unreadable>"`-carrying arms (snapshot-failure on (2), throwing-property-access on (3)) are absorbed by the same complement check as a side benefit of the four-case captured-value enumeration the **Unknown-reason rule** above pins; the runtime MUST NOT introduce a separate `!pinnedConstantReadOk` disjunct or a sentinel-string equality check to back them, since the complement form already exhausts the predicate's information requirement. On the snapshot-failure-with-`quit`/`reload` sub-case the broader tag write is harmless: `capturedEventReason` is the `"<unreadable>"` sentinel (the `event.reason` read was never reached) and is therefore in the predicate's fire set, the host is tearing the runtime down anyway, no subsequent slash invocation reaches the tag, and the diagnostic-channel observability remains carried by `loom/host/session-shutdown-pinned-constant-unreadable`. The same harmlessness argument covers any unknown-`event.reason` literal Pi might deliver whose semantics turn out to coincide with `"quit"`/`"reload"`: the snapshot edit under [Pi version bump procedure](#pi-version-bump-procedure) step 5 below would then admit the literal into the closed set, the post-edit captured value would be the new closed-set member, and the predicate would correctly suppress the tag write on it. The diagnostic-emission predicate retains its narrower form on **both** the snapshot-failure path and the unknown-reason-with-successful-snapshot path because each path's own diagnostic (`loom/host/session-shutdown-pinned-constant-unreadable` and `loom/host/session-shutdown-reason-unknown` respectively) already pins the diagnostic-channel observability for that shutdown event; a doubled-up `runtime-degraded` emission on either path would describe the same event from a second angle and split operator deduplication buckets across two codes without adding an operator-actionable distinction. The asymmetry between the broader tag-transition predicate and the narrower diagnostic-emission predicate is therefore a dedup-bucket-symmetry argument that applies uniformly to (2) and (3) — the residual case in which both the tag-write and the path-specific `console.error` are lost is the *Accepted loom 1.0 residual gap — compound-failure case* paragraph below; that paragraph's three-failure conjunction is unchanged by the predicate widening here (it concerns the diagnostic-emission predicate's narrower form, which the widening preserves). The runtime MUST NOT introduce any handler-scoped state seam beyond `pinnedConstantReadOk` and `capturedEventReason` to back either predicate (no `branchTakenWasClosedSet` flag, no per-sub-step success roll-up, no separate sentinel-string equality check against `"<unreadable>"`): the two seams above already exhaust both predicates' information requirements — `pinnedConstantReadOk` gates the diagnostic-emission predicate's narrower form, and the captured-value enumeration of `capturedEventReason` already exhausts the broader tag-transition predicate's complement check across all three arms above. *All-three-throw corner-case interaction.* The diagnostic-emission predicate above is re-evaluated from scratch on every handler invocation that the [**idempotent**](#idempotent-handler-clause) clause's broadened short-circuit predicate (`snapshot.drained === true || snapshot.tag !== undefined`) does not catch — including the loom 1.0-accepted *all-three-throw corner case* enumerated in that clause above (sub-step 1's `LoomRegistry.drain`, sub-step 1's `LoomRegistry.initDrainStateTag`, and the post-sub-step-4 `LoomRegistry.markRuntimeDegraded` all throw on a session-only `session_shutdown`, leaving `drained = false` and `tag = undefined`). On a follow-up session-only `session_shutdown` against the same extension instance with a successful follow-up snapshot read, this predicate fires again and an additional `loom/host/session-shutdown-runtime-degraded` row is emitted, breaching the at-most-once-per-extension-instance-lifetime bound for this corner case only; operator deduplication on `(code, details.event.reason)` collapses the resulting duplicate rows. No additional handler-scoped seam is introduced to suppress the duplicate, on the same loom 1.0-acceptance grounds the [**idempotent**](#idempotent-handler-clause) clause's all-three-throw paragraph already pins (all three swallow rules above already individually fired and the runtime carries no further state seam to recover from). *Accepted loom 1.0 residual gap — compound-failure case.* On the conjunction of three failures — (1) the snapshot-failure path is taken (so the diagnostic-emission predicate's narrower form suppresses `loom/host/session-shutdown-runtime-degraded`), (2) the post-sub-step-4 `LoomRegistry.markRuntimeDegraded` tag write throws (caught and swallowed by the [**Per-step isolation** paragraph's interstitial-seam `try`/`catch`](#interstitial-seam-tag-write-swallow) per the *Methods* paragraph above, so the registry remains on the unmodified `"shutting-down"` arm), and (3) the host is a stdio-capturing host on which the `console.error`-routed `loom/host/session-shutdown-pinned-constant-unreadable` write is silently dropped (per the *Pi-side stdio visibility* clause of the [**Diagnostic-emission isolation**](#diagnostic-emission-isolation) rule above) — the operator's next slash invocation returns the misleading `"loom /<name>: extension shutting down"` system note with no in-band signal that `/reload` is required, and recovery on this branch depends on out-of-band discovery of the need to `/reload`. loom 1.0 accepts this residual gap rather than widening the diagnostic-emission predicate to also fire on `!pinnedConstantReadOk` or demoting the interstitial-seam swallow to emit a fallback diagnostic, on the grounds that the assessed probability of the three-way conjunction (a snapshot-read failure compounded with a tag-setter throw compounded with a host whose `console.error` writes are silently dropped) is low enough that the ripple in the diagnostics catalogue is not warranted in loom 1.0; the gap is documented here so a future edit that reduces any one of the three failure probabilities (e.g. an explicit Pi stdio-capture facet per [Future Considerations — loom 1.0 non-goals — No reliance on a Pi extension-host stdio-capture facet](./future-considerations.md#pi-stdio-capture-facet)) can be considered against this acknowledged baseline rather than as the discovery of a new defect. *Accepted loom 1.0 residual gap — edit-without-slash-invocation case.* On the degraded branch a separate residual gap exists for the operator who edits a `.loom` file or `settings` between the `session_shutdown` handler returning and the operator's next slash invocation: the watchers are closed by sub-step 4 above, the runtime MUST NOT poll, re-subscribe, or re-establish them per the exhaustive prohibition pinned above, and the only in-band signal that the edit was ignored — the distinct `"loom /<name>: extension degraded; /reload to recover"` slash note carrying the `degraded` token and the `/reload` recovery instruction — fires only when the operator next invokes a slash command (the `console.error` row `loom/host/session-shutdown-runtime-degraded` is the out-of-band signal on hosts that surface stdio, and is independent of the edit itself). An operator who edits but issues no subsequent slash invocation before their next `/reload` therefore has no in-band evidence that the edit was ignored. loom 1.0 accepts this residual gap rather than introducing a polling fallback, a re-subscribe path, or a separate edit-rejection diagnostic — each of which would either contradict the exhaustive prohibition above or require a new persistent-diagnostic channel scoped to the degraded branch — on the grounds that a forthcoming slash invocation is the natural recovery signal in operator workflow and the slash note above already names watcher closure as the cause when that invocation arrives; the gap is documented here so a future edit reducing the cost of any one of those alternatives (e.g., a Pi facet that surfaces extension-degraded state to the slash UI without an explicit slash invocation) can be considered against this acknowledged baseline rather than as the discovery of a new defect. <a id="substep-2-stamp-throw-residual-gap"></a>*Accepted loom 1.0 residual gap — sub-step-2 stamp-throw case.* On a sub-step 2 per-entry stamp throw (frozen entry, proxied entry, write-rejecting setter, OOM during property assignment — per the per-entry `catch` arm pinned in sub-step 2 above), the per-entry `catch` arm proceeds to the next entry and the `loomAbort.abort()` call for that entry is **skipped** (the stamp failed, so the abort is suppressed), leaving the affected invocation un-cancelled by the handler — a partial-failure path on which sub-step 2's broader "cancel in-flight invocations" framing is silently relaxed for that one entry. The operator-visible signal for this case is the affected entry's eventual appearance in the single `loom/runtime/reload-teardown-timeout` `<list>` of sub-step 3 (the un-cancelled invocation does not settle its `disposeBarrier` inside the `SHUTDOWN_AWAIT_CAP_MS` window because nothing aborted it, so it is necessarily still in flight at the deadline); that diagnostic carries no discriminator distinguishing "I never called `abort()` on this entry because the stamp threw" from "I called `abort()` and `disposeBarrier` did not settle", and loom 1.0 accepts the lack of such a discriminator rather than introducing a new diagnostic code or extending the `reload-teardown-timeout` row's `<list>` element shape. Should the affected invocation's per-invocation `finally` later reach the **Per-invocation operator visibility (clean-cancel path)** rule below (e.g., a separate downstream cancellation eventually settles its `disposeBarrier`), the `details.event.reason` value it emits when its entry's `shutdownReason` field is unset because the stamp threw is the literal string `"<unreadable>"`, on the same footing as the **Unknown-reason rule**'s sentinel-string convention pinned above for the throwing-property-access and snapshot-failure captured-value cases (the `finally` reads `entry.shutdownReason` per the **Per-invocation operator visibility (clean-cancel path)** rule below; on this stamp-throw arm the field carries the sentinel rather than `undefined` so the type pinned for `details.event.reason` on that rule (`"quit" | "reload" | "new" | "resume" | "fork" | string`) is preserved). The `"<unreadable>"` substitution applies to `details.event.reason` only; the companion `details.event.loom` field on the same row is **unaffected** by the stamp throw — the affected entry's `loom` field was populated at invocation-start insertion (per the registry contract above, before sub-step 2's `shutdownReason` stamp ran) and is never mutated thereafter, so the slash-name discriminator the [*Runtime-constructed sibling carve-out* clause of the `details` shape conventions for the `session_shutdown` event payload](./diagnostics.md#session-shutdown-details-conventions) requires on every emission of `loom/runtime/cancelled-by-session-shutdown` survives the stamp-throw arm unchanged in its registered canonical form. This co-emission — the affected invocation contributing to the single `loom/runtime/reload-teardown-timeout` `<list>` of sub-step 3 above AND later emitting `loom/runtime/cancelled-by-session-shutdown` from its own per-invocation `finally` — is the carve-out the [`loom/runtime/cancelled-by-session-shutdown` row's mutual-exclusion clause](./diagnostics.md#cancelled-by-session-shutdown-mutual-exclusion) calls out as the sole residual-gap exception to its otherwise-pinned "never both" invariant; operator-tooling consumers reading that clause are entitled to treat the dual appearance on the same shutdown as a residual-gap signal rather than a contract violation. loom 1.0 accepts this residual gap rather than routing the per-entry catch arm to a new diagnostic with an extended `details.step` enumeration on the grounds that a stamp throw on a `Set` entry the runtime itself allocates as a plain mutable object — whose `shutdownReason` field is `undefined` at insertion per the registry contract above and is never frozen, proxied, or made write-rejecting by the runtime — is low-probability; the gap is documented here so a future edit that reduces the cost of a routed diagnostic (e.g. extending the `details.step` enumeration to carry a sub-step-2-stamp-throw discriminator) can be considered against this acknowledged baseline rather than as the discovery of a new defect. The `pinnedConstantReadOk` term is load-bearing on the snapshot-failure-with-closed-set-`event.reason` path: Pi may deliver `event.reason = "new"` on a shutdown whose snapshot read failed, but the **Unknown-reason rule**'s fixed read order means the `event.reason` read was never reached and the handler-scoped captured variable retains its `"<unreadable>"` pre-initialisation, so the captured-string triplet check would already exclude this case in practice — `pinnedConstantReadOk` is the explicit, value-independent state seam that pins that exclusion against an implementation that grew a fresh `event.reason` re-read at the discriminator site (forbidden, see next sentence) or that mistakenly stamped the raw delivered value rather than the captured one. The captured-string triplet check (rather than a fresh `event.reason` property access at the discriminator site) is the load-bearing seam against the unknown-reason path: the captured value on that path is the `String(event.reason)` coercion or the `"<unreadable>"` sentinel per the **Unknown-reason rule** above, neither of which inhabits the triplet, and a fresh property access at this discriminator site would either re-throw (on the throwing-property-access path) or read a value the handler has already classified as unknown — both bypass the catch-arm classification the rules above pin and are non-conformant. **Co-emission** with one or more `loom/host/session-shutdown-teardown-step-failed` rows for the same `session_shutdown` event is therefore expected when any sub-step 1 call site (`LoomRegistry.drain`, `LoomRegistry.initDrainStateTag`), any sub-step 4 call site (`discoveryWatcher.close()`, `settingsWatcher.close()`, the debounce-handle `Clock.clearTimeout(...)` call), or any sub-step 5 call site (`ctx.signal.removeEventListener`, `toolSignal.removeEventListener`, `parentInvokeSignal.removeEventListener`) threw, and is **not** a deduplication target: the two codes describe distinct facts (which call site threw vs. the runtime is now degraded until `/reload`), and operator-tooling deduplication keys (`(code, details.step, details.call)` for `teardown-step-failed`; `(code, details.event.reason)` for `session-shutdown-runtime-degraded`) bucket them separately by construction. *Co-emission with `loom/runtime/cancelled-by-session-shutdown`.* One `loom/runtime/cancelled-by-session-shutdown` row per cleanly-cancelled in-flight `ActiveInvocationRegistry` entry per the **Per-invocation operator visibility (clean-cancel path)** rule below is symmetrically expected for the same `session_shutdown` event: sub-step 2 above stamps each entry's `shutdownReason` field with the handler-scoped captured `event.reason` and calls `loomAbort.abort()` on each entry, sub-step 3 awaits each entry's `disposeBarrier` within the `SHUTDOWN_AWAIT_CAP_MS` window, and the per-invocation `finally` of each invocation that settled cleanly inside that window emits the row from its own `finally` (not from this handler). The row count therefore equals the number of `ActiveInvocationRegistry` entries the handler observed at sub-step 2 entry whose `disposeBarrier` then settled inside sub-step 3's bounded await: zero on a session-only `session_shutdown` whose handler entered with an empty registry (e.g. an operator who typed `/new` from an idle prompt, where the [Pi behavioural preconditions for the snapshot/restore protocol](#snapshot-restore-pi-behavioural-preconditions) above's precondition (b) — Pi serialises slash-command dispatch per session — together with the same paragraph's symmetric in-process LIFO-nesting guarantee for nested prompt → prompt `invoke(...)` calls means no slash invocation is in flight before the operator's next slash entered), and one row per cleanly-cancelled in-flight invocation otherwise (e.g. an operator who typed `/new` mid-tool-loop, where the in-flight invocation is exactly the case sub-step 2's per-entry stamp + abort and sub-step 3's bounded await are designed to handle on the session-only branch on the same footing as the always-tear-down branch). The two codes describe distinct facts (which invocation cancelled cleanly within the `SHUTDOWN_AWAIT_CAP_MS` window vs. the runtime is now degraded until `/reload`) so the pair is symmetrically **not** a deduplication target — operator-tooling dedup keys bucket them separately by construction (`(code, details.event.reason)` for `runtime-degraded`; a per-invocation key for `cancelled-by-session-shutdown` whose `details.event.loom` slash-name discriminator is pinned by the [*Runtime-constructed sibling carve-out* of the `details` shape conventions for the `session_shutdown` event payload](./diagnostics.md#session-shutdown-details-conventions)), so no co-suppression is owed. The watcher-close-failed sub-case — where co-emission carries the most operator value — is the partial-failure case the diagnostic was added to surface and MUST NOT be silenced by the implementation. The sub-step-1 co-emission cases (each call site individually) are pinned in fuller detail by acceptance branches (i) and (j) below (which additionally cover the post-handler drain-state arm observed via `LoomRegistry.readDrainState`). The emission is wrapped per the [**Diagnostic-emission isolation**](#diagnostic-emission-isolation) rule above — a throw out of `console.error` MUST be swallowed and MUST NOT unwind the handler. The diagnostic carries `details: { event: { reason: "new" | "resume" | "fork" } }`, where `details.event.reason` is the handler-scoped captured variable `capturedEventReason` per the *Predicate split* clause above (the same handler-scoped variable the **Unknown-reason rule** pins, which sub-step 2 stamps onto each entry's `shutdownReason` field; the row's source is the handler-scoped capture itself, **not** the registry-derived per-entry `shutdownReason` stamp, so the value is independent of any sub-step-2 per-entry stamp throw the **Per-step isolation** paragraph above caught — necessarily a closed-set member on this branch, since the diagnostic-emission predicate `pinnedConstantReadOk && capturedEventReason ∈ {"new", "resume", "fork"}` excludes the unknown-reason and snapshot-failure paths above). The diagnostic fires exactly once per `session_shutdown` event in this branch. *Acceptance criteria.* The above rule decomposes into the following per-branch fixture obligations, all of which the implementation MUST satisfy (the leaf owns the fixture-shape decisions, but the branch coverage and observable outcomes below are normative). *Count-semantics framing for the per-branch "the handler emits exactly one" / "emits zero" obligations below.* Emission counts in the branches below are measured at the **handler invocation site** per the [**Diagnostic-emission isolation**](#diagnostic-emission-isolation) rule's *Count semantics* pin above — i.e., the count is over the number of times the handler enters the leaf-owned serialisation-and-emission sequence for the same `session_shutdown` event, not over the number of rows that reach an operator sink. The fixtures' own assertions on emission count therefore key on the invocation-site count (e.g., a test sink that records each call into the wrapped sequence) rather than on a sink-side row count that may be zero on a host that silently drops the `console.error` write; the isolation rule's silent swallow on inner throw satisfies the "emits exactly one" obligation (the invocation occurred), and a fixture that observed zero invocations after the wrap entered would surface a non-conformant retry-suppression or short-circuit rather than a dropped-write artefact. **(a) Positive — clean session-only reason.** For each `event.reason ∈ {"new", "resume", "fork"}` (three fixtures) on a shutdown whose pinned-constant snapshot read succeeded and whose three sub-step-4 call sites all returned without throwing, the handler emits exactly one `loom/host/session-shutdown-runtime-degraded` row whose `details.event.reason` equals the supplied reason; no `loom/host/session-shutdown-teardown-step-failed` row is emitted. **(b) Positive — session-only reason with sub-step throw (co-emission).** For each `event.reason ∈ {"new", "resume", "fork"}` × each individual call site configured to throw alone (other call sites succeeding) — the two sub-step-1 sites (`LoomRegistry.drain`, `LoomRegistry.initDrainStateTag`), the three sub-step-4 sites (`discoveryWatcher.close()`, `settingsWatcher.close()`, the debounce-handle `Clock.clearTimeout(...)` call), and the three sub-step-5 sites (`ctx.signal.removeEventListener`, `toolSignal.removeEventListener`, `parentInvokeSignal.removeEventListener`), totalling 3 × 8 = 24 fixtures with one call site throwing per fixture — the handler emits exactly one `loom/host/session-shutdown-runtime-degraded` row alongside exactly one `loom/host/session-shutdown-teardown-step-failed` row whose `details.call` field is the failing call-site label — confirming the *independent of sub-step 4's per-call outcomes* invariant pinned above and its sub-step-1 and sub-step-5 analogues (neither the diagnostic-emission predicate `pinnedConstantReadOk && capturedEventReason ∈ {"new", "resume", "fork"}` nor the broader tag-transition predicate carries any sub-step-1 success conjunct, so a caught sub-step-1 throw still reaches the post-sub-step-4 emission seam; sub-step 5's listener-detach calls run **after** that emission seam, so a caught sub-step-5 throw cannot retroactively silence the already-emitted degraded-state row either; the degraded-state row MUST NOT be silenced or deduplicated against the per-call failure row). Combinations of multiple simultaneously-failing call sites are **out of scope for branch (b)** and are exercised only by the *all-three-throw corner case* enumerated by the **idempotent** clause above (sub-step 1's `LoomRegistry.drain`, sub-step 1's `LoomRegistry.initDrainStateTag`, and the post-sub-step-4 `LoomRegistry.markRuntimeDegraded` all throwing on the same session-only `session_shutdown`); branch (b)'s 24-fixture grid is the single-failing-call-site scope statement and does not enumerate any subset-coverage of multiple co-failing call sites. The sub-step-1 sub-cases of branch (b) are also covered, with the additional post-handler drain-state observability assertions appended, by branches (i) (`LoomRegistry.initDrainStateTag` throws) and (j) (`LoomRegistry.drain` throws) below; branch (b) here is the co-emission scope statement. **(c) Negative — always-tear-down reasons.** For each `event.reason ∈ {"quit", "reload"}`, the handler emits zero `loom/host/session-shutdown-runtime-degraded` rows (the runtime is being torn down anyway). **(d) Negative — unknown-reason path (with successful snapshot read).** For an `event.reason` outside the closed set (and for the throwing-`event.reason`-property-access fixture), where the handler-entry pinned-constant snapshot read succeeded (so `pinnedConstantReadOk` is `true` and the captured value is either the `String(event.reason)` coercion of the off-snapshot literal Pi delivered or the `"<unreadable>"` sentinel from the throwing-access fixture), the handler emits zero `loom/host/session-shutdown-runtime-degraded` rows; the path's own `loom/host/session-shutdown-reason-unknown` row covers diagnostic-channel observability per the **Unknown-reason rule** above. The fixture additionally asserts that the next slash invocation against the still-live extension instance returns the `"loom /<name>: extension degraded; /reload to recover"` system note (the `"degraded-needs-reload"` arm of sub-step 1's closed two-arm drain-state tag set), **not** the `"loom /<name>: extension shutting down"` note that fronts the `"shutting-down"` arm — confirming the broader **tag-transition predicate** of the *Predicate split* clause above (the unknown-reason-with-successful-snapshot path writes the degraded tag despite the suppressed diagnostic, via the predicate's complement-form coverage of arm (3)), so an operator on a stdio-capturing host has the in-band signal that `/reload` is required even when the `loom/host/session-shutdown-reason-unknown` `console.error` is lost. **(e) Negative — snapshot-failure path.** For a fixture that forces the handler-entry pinned-constant lookup to fail (so `pinnedConstantReadOk` is `false`), the handler emits zero `loom/host/session-shutdown-runtime-degraded` rows even when Pi delivers a session-only `event.reason` such as `"new"`; the path's own `loom/host/session-shutdown-pinned-constant-unreadable` row covers diagnostic-channel observability. The fixture additionally asserts that the next slash invocation against the still-live extension instance returns the `"loom /<name>: extension degraded; /reload to recover"` system note (the `"degraded-needs-reload"` arm of sub-step 1's closed two-arm drain-state tag set), **not** the `"loom /<name>: extension shutting down"` note that fronts the `"shutting-down"` arm — confirming the broader **tag-transition predicate** of the *Predicate split* clause above (the snapshot-failure path writes the degraded tag despite the suppressed diagnostic, via the predicate's complement-form coverage of arm (2) — the `"<unreadable>"` sentinel that `capturedEventReason` retains on the snapshot-failure path is not in `{"quit", "reload"}` and is therefore in the predicate's fire set), so an operator on a stdio-capturing host has the in-band signal that `/reload` is required even when the `loom/host/session-shutdown-pinned-constant-unreadable` `console.error` is lost. The fixture covers both the snapshot-failure-with-session-only sub-case (e.g. delivered `event.reason = "new"`) and the snapshot-failure-with-always-tear-down sub-case (e.g. delivered `event.reason = "quit"`); the slash-invocation arm-check is meaningful only on the former (on the latter Pi tears the runtime down before any subsequent slash invocation can reach the tag), but the zero-`runtime-degraded`-rows assertion holds on both. **(f) Drain-state observability (pre-recovery).** After any branch-(a) or branch-(b) shutdown completes whose interstitial-seam `LoomRegistry.markRuntimeDegraded` tag write did not throw (the throwing-tag-write arm is covered separately by branch (k) below, where the documented swallow trade-off pinned in the [interstitial-seam clause of the **Per-step isolation** paragraph above](#interstitial-seam-tag-write-swallow) accepts a `"shutting-down"`-arm slash note instead), the next slash invocation against the still-live extension instance returns the `"loom /<name>: extension degraded; /reload to recover"` system note (the `"degraded-needs-reload"` arm of sub-step 1's closed two-arm drain-state tag set per sub-step 1 above), **not** the `"loom /<name>: extension shutting down"` note that fronts the `"shutting-down"` arm — this is the in-band signal the bullet's main text invokes for stdio-capturing hosts where the `console.error` emission may be lost. **(g) Recovery.** After operator-issued `/reload` re-executes the extension factory and a fresh runtime is in place, the next slash invocation does not short-circuit on either drain-state arm and dispatches its loom normally (neither the `"shutting down"` nor the `"degraded; /reload to recover"` system note is returned), confirming that `/reload` is the loom 1.0 recovery path and that the fresh runtime starts with a non-drained `LoomRegistry`. **(h) Idempotent re-entry on the degraded branch.** A follow-up `session_shutdown` (of any `event.reason`, including a fresh `"quit"`) fired against the degraded extension instance after a branch-(a) or branch-(b) shutdown returned MUST be short-circuited at handler entry per the **idempotent** clause above: zero additional `loom/host/session-shutdown-runtime-degraded` rows are emitted (preserving the at-most-once-per-extension-instance-lifetime bound), and zero additional rows of any other teardown-handler diagnostic code are emitted. **(i) State-independent post-sub-step-4 write — tag-init throw still routes to the degraded arm.** For each `event.reason ∈ {"new", "resume", "fork"}` (three fixtures) on a shutdown whose pinned-constant snapshot read succeeded but whose sub-step-1 `LoomRegistry.initDrainStateTag` call was configured to throw (so the per-call `try`/`catch` of the **Per-step isolation** paragraph above catches the throw and emits one `loom/host/session-shutdown-teardown-step-failed` row under `details.call = "loomRegistry.initDrainStateTag"`, leaving `drainStateTag = undefined` after sub-step 1 returns), the handler nonetheless reaches the post-sub-step-4 `LoomRegistry.markRuntimeDegraded` write, that write completes the unconditional `"degraded-needs-reload"` write (per the **state-independent write** pin in the bullet's main text — the transition is unconditional in source state and an unset tag is overwritten on the same footing as a `"shutting-down"` tag), and the handler emits exactly one `loom/host/session-shutdown-runtime-degraded` row whose `details.event.reason` equals the supplied reason; the next slash invocation against the still-live extension instance returns the `"loom /<name>: extension degraded; /reload to recover"` system note (the `"degraded-needs-reload"` arm of sub-step 1's closed two-arm drain-state tag set), **not** the `"loom /<name>: extension shutting down"` note that would falsely surface if the post-sub-step-4 transition had been gated on a `"shutting-down"` source state. The fixture confirms the state-independent-write pin against an implementation that mistakenly conditioned the transition on observing a `"shutting-down"` source state, which would silently strand the runtime on the `"shutting-down"` arm whenever `initDrainStateTag` threw. **(j) Drain-throw recovery — short-circuit established by tag setter.** For each `event.reason ∈ {"new", "resume", "fork"}` (three fixtures) on a shutdown whose pinned-constant snapshot read succeeded but whose sub-step-1 `LoomRegistry.drain` call was configured to throw (so the per-call `try`/`catch` of the **Per-step isolation** paragraph above catches the throw and emits one `loom/host/session-shutdown-teardown-step-failed` row under `details.call = "loomRegistry.drain"`, leaving `drained = false` after sub-step 1 returns), the handler nonetheless continues into the second sub-step-1 act (`LoomRegistry.initDrainStateTag` succeeds and sets `tag = "shutting-down"`), runs sub-steps 2–4, and reaches the post-sub-step-4 `LoomRegistry.markRuntimeDegraded` write, which transitions the tag to `"degraded-needs-reload"` (per the **state-independent write** pin above); the handler emits exactly one `loom/host/session-shutdown-runtime-degraded` row whose `details.event.reason` equals the supplied reason. After the handler returns, the next slash invocation against the still-live extension instance MUST return the `"loom /<name>: extension degraded; /reload to recover"` system note (arm (c) of the `LoomRegistry.readDrainState` arms above, which keys on `snapshot.tag === "degraded-needs-reload"` regardless of `snapshot.drained`) rather than dispatching the loom against the drain-flag-still-`false` runtime, AND a follow-up `session_shutdown` (of any `event.reason`) fired against the same extension instance MUST be short-circuited at handler entry per the **idempotent** clause above (whose predicate is `snapshot.drained === true || snapshot.tag !== undefined` and therefore fires on `(drained: false, tag: "degraded-needs-reload")`): zero additional `loom/host/session-shutdown-runtime-degraded` rows are emitted (preserving the at-most-once-per-extension-instance-lifetime bound), no second sub-step 4 runs (so chokidar's acknowledged-unpinned double-close behaviour on the already-closed `discoveryWatcher`/`settingsWatcher` is off the load path), and zero additional rows of any other teardown-handler diagnostic code are emitted. The fixture variant for `event.reason ∈ {"quit", "reload"}` (two additional fixtures) MUST emit zero `loom/host/session-shutdown-runtime-degraded` rows (the always-tear-down branch suppresses the diagnostic per branch (c) above), and the post-handler tag observed via `readDrainState` is `"shutting-down"` (the `markRuntimeDegraded` write does not run on this branch). (For the `{"quit", "reload"}` fixture variant, the post-shutdown slash invocation is unreachable in loom 1.0 because Pi tears down the runtime before any subsequent slash dispatch can reach it; the fixture variant MUST NOT include a slash-arm assertion.) The session-only triplet variant retains the arm-check pinned for the session-only triplet earlier in this branch. The fixture confirms the *broader* short-circuit predicate (`drained || tag !== undefined`) the **idempotent** clause above pins, against an implementation that mistakenly keyed the predicate on `drained` alone, which would silently dispatch slash invocations and re-run the full handler on every subsequent `session_shutdown` whenever `drain` threw. **(k) Interstitial-seam tag-write throw.** For each `event.reason ∈ {"new", "resume", "fork"}` (three fixtures) on a shutdown whose pinned-constant snapshot read succeeded and whose three sub-step-4 call sites all returned without throwing, but whose interstitial-seam `LoomRegistry.markRuntimeDegraded` tag write was configured to throw (so the seam's dedicated `try`/`catch` per the [interstitial-seam clause of the **Per-step isolation** paragraph above](#interstitial-seam-tag-write-swallow) silently swallows the throw and the registry retains its `"shutting-down"` tag value), the handler nonetheless emits exactly one `loom/host/session-shutdown-runtime-degraded` row whose `details.event.reason` equals the supplied reason (the seam swallow does not affect the diagnostic emission, which runs immediately after the seam under its own [**Diagnostic-emission isolation**](#diagnostic-emission-isolation) `try`/`catch` wrap), no `loom/host/session-shutdown-teardown-step-failed` row is emitted for the seam itself (the seam's swallow is silent per the explicit *MUST NOT emit `teardown-step-failed` or any other diagnostic* clause of the [interstitial-seam swallow rule in the **Per-step isolation** paragraph above](#interstitial-seam-tag-write-swallow) — sub-step 4's three call sites and sub-step 5's listener-detach calls retain their own `teardown-step-failed` emission obligations and may emit independently if they themselves throw, but on this fixture they do not), and the next slash invocation against the still-live extension instance returns the `"loom /<name>: extension shutting down"` system note (the `"shutting-down"` arm of sub-step 1's closed two-arm drain-state tag set, since the tag write was swallowed and the registry tag retains its `"shutting-down"` value) **rather than** the `"loom /<name>: extension degraded; /reload to recover"` note that branches (a), (b), and (f) above pin for the non-throwing tag-write arm — confirming the documented trade-off the interstitial-seam swallow rule explicitly accepts (the degraded-arm slash note is sacrificed so the swallow can be silent and the rest of the handler can complete; the `loom/host/session-shutdown-runtime-degraded` row remains the diagnostic-channel signal of degradation on this arm). The fast-path framing applies to sub-steps 2 and 3 only (the abort-and-await over `ActiveInvocationRegistry`): a session-only reason often leaves those two sub-steps with an empty registry (e.g. a `/new` issued from an idle prompt, where no slash invocation is in flight at the boundary per the [Pi behavioural preconditions for the snapshot/restore protocol](#snapshot-restore-pi-behavioural-preconditions) above's precondition (b) and the same paragraph's symmetric in-process LIFO-nesting guarantee), but the registry MAY be non-empty when the operator issues a session-only `event.reason` mid-invocation (e.g. `/new` issued mid-tool-loop) — sub-step 2's per-entry stamp + abort and sub-step 3's bounded await handle that case on the same footing as the always-tear-down branch — and a session-only reason does not skip sub-step 4 or any other sub-step. This emergent fast-path is available only for the five enumerated reasons; an unknown `event.reason` is routed by the **Unknown-reason rule** above and MUST run the full five-sub-step sequence even when the registry is empty.

   <a id="session-shutdown-semantics"></a>

   *Session-swap behaviour for in-flight invocations.* The five-sub-step sequence above defines the abort-and-await sequence; this paragraph closes the three obligations the sequence does not by itself state — per-invocation operator visibility on the cancellation path, partial-append fate during teardown, and the `invoke`-parent observation rule.

   - **Per-invocation operator visibility (clean-cancel path).** For each `ActiveInvocationRegistry` entry whose `disposeBarrier` settles (whether inside the `SHUTDOWN_AWAIT_CAP_MS` window of sub-step 3 — i.e., the invocation cancelled cleanly within the bounded await — OR, on the [*Accepted loom 1.0 residual gap — sub-step-2 stamp-throw case*](#substep-2-stamp-throw-residual-gap) above, after the deadline via a downstream cancellation per the EXCEPT clause below) — the cancellation path inside that invocation's own `finally` block emits exactly one `loom/runtime/cancelled-by-session-shutdown` (E, runtime) note on `loom-system-note` with `display: false`, `details.event.reason` carrying the handler-captured `event.reason` string typed as `"quit" | "reload" | "new" | "resume" | "fork" | string`: a closed-set member when Pi delivered one of the five literals, otherwise the `String(event.reason)` coercion captured by the **Unknown-reason rule** above (or the literal string `"<unreadable>"` when the property-access read threw, or the same `"<unreadable>"` sentinel — overloaded per the **Unknown-reason rule**'s captured-value enumeration above — when the snapshot-side read failed before sub-step 1's `event.reason` read was reached and the handler-scoped variable retained its `"<unreadable>"` pre-initialisation; on this snapshot-failure path the same-string reuse with `details.observed` does not apply because the co-emitted teardown diagnostic is `loom/host/session-shutdown-pinned-constant-unreadable` carrying `details.failure` rather than `loom/host/session-shutdown-reason-unknown` carrying `details.observed`). The per-invocation `finally` reads this string from the entry's `shutdownReason` field (stamped by sub-step 2 of the `session_shutdown` handler above immediately before that entry's `loomAbort.abort()` call, per all four captured-value cases enumerated by the **Unknown-reason rule**) rather than re-reading `event.reason` — the `event.reason` read is handler-scoped and the `finally` runs in a different async context, so `entry.shutdownReason` is the spec-pinned channel by which all four captured-value cases reach this emission site. On the post-deadline arm of the widened opening precondition above (the [*Accepted loom 1.0 residual gap — sub-step-2 stamp-throw case*](#substep-2-stamp-throw-residual-gap)), the per-invocation `finally` STILL reads `entry.shutdownReason` by the same channel and emits the row; on that arm the field carries the literal `"<unreadable>"` sentinel per the residual-gap paragraph (sub-step 2's stamp threw before populating it, and the residual-gap paragraph pins payload-construction substitution of the sentinel for the otherwise-unset field), so the type pinned for `details.event.reason` (`"quit" | "reload" | "new" | "resume" | "fork" | string`) is preserved on the post-deadline arm on the same footing as the four `Unknown-reason rule` captured-value cases above. The wider `string` arm is the unknown-reason path; the value is always a string. The handler-captured string is the same single coerced value the **Unknown-reason rule** populates `details.observed` with — both diagnostics surface byte-identical reason strings for the same shutdown event, and `details.event.loom` carrying the invocation's canonical-key name (post-`pi.looms` mapping, post-`as` rename, basename-hyphen-normalised, no leading `/`) per the [`ActiveInvocationRegistry`](#active-invocation-registry) `loom`-field source-of-truth above. The same `finally` also populates `details.event.invocation_id` by reading the registry entry's `invocationId` field (the same channel by which `details.event.loom` is read, per the [`ActiveInvocationRegistry`](#active-invocation-registry) registry-insertion-site source-of-truth above), rendered as the per-invocation UUID in canonical lowercase 8-4-4-4-12 hex form per the [§7 `<invocation-id>` placeholder convention](./diagnostics.md#7-identifier--descriptor--and-closed-enum-placeholders); the field is not re-derived at the emission site, so concurrent siblings of the same loom carry distinct `details.event.invocation_id` values on the operator-visible row. The note is emitted from the invocation's own teardown — not from the `session_shutdown` handler itself — so the "`sendSystemNote` MUST NOT be invoked from the teardown handler" edge-case bullet above does not apply to it; the note routes through the standard `sendSystemNote` fallback chain (`pi.sendMessage` → `ctx.ui.notify` → `loom/runtime/system-note-delivery-failed` → `console.error`) defined under **System notes** below, which degrades through `ctx.ui.notify` and ultimately `console.error` if `ExtensionRuntime.invalidate(...)` has already invalidated `pi.sendMessage` by emission time. The chain's terminal `console.error` is wrapped per the [**Diagnostic-emission isolation**](#diagnostic-emission-isolation) rule above: a throw from that terminal `console.error` MUST be swallowed and MUST NOT propagate out of the per-invocation `finally`. An invocation either emits `cancelled-by-session-shutdown` (cleanly cancelled within the window) or contributes to the single `loom/runtime/reload-teardown-timeout` `<list>` of sub-step 3 (still in flight at the deadline), never both — the per-invocation note is the operator-visibility counterpart to the timeout diagnostic — EXCEPT on the [*Accepted loom 1.0 residual gap — sub-step-2 stamp-throw case*](#substep-2-stamp-throw-residual-gap) above, where an affected invocation MAY both contribute to the `reload-teardown-timeout` `<list>` (because sub-step 2's `abort()` was skipped) AND later emit `cancelled-by-session-shutdown` from this rule (if its per-invocation `finally` settles via a downstream cancellation after the deadline); the [`loom/runtime/cancelled-by-session-shutdown` row's mutual-exclusion clause](./diagnostics.md#cancelled-by-session-shutdown-mutual-exclusion) restates this carve-out and pins the operator-tooling consumer guidance for the dual appearance. The `cancelled-by-session-shutdown` code is **not** in the always-log set defined under **Runtime event channel** below; the exclusion mirrors the existing `cancelled` exclusion (operator-initiated, self-explanatory in context) and so the per-invocation note does not produce a `details: { event: RuntimeEvent }` group-A emission in addition to itself.

   - **Partial-append fate during teardown.** Conversation turns the runtime had already appended into the user session (prompt mode) or the spawned subagent session (subagent mode) before sub-step 2's `loomAbort.abort()` fired remain in whatever conversation Pi assigns them to under the swap's `event.reason`; the runtime makes no rollback, migration, or compensation attempt. This is the `event.reason`-scoped restatement of the [Errors and Results — Partial-append contract](./errors-and-results.md#partial-append-contract): `?`-propagation, panic, and steady-state cancellation already preserve appended turns, and a `session_shutdown`-driven cancellation preserves them on the same rule. The outgoing user session (when Pi tears it down on `reason: "new" | "resume" | "fork"`) carries the partial appends Pi assigns to it under the swap; the loom runtime makes no attempt to discard them, migrate them to the incoming session, or surface a manifest of what was appended. Authors who need teardown-safe append semantics must use [Errors and Results — No rollback](./errors-and-results.md#no-rollback)'s steady-state author obligations (idempotency, compensation in `match` arms before re-`Err`-ing).

   - **`invoke`-parent observation rule.** Parent and child invocations are aborted in the same iteration of sub-step 2: the registry is iterated once and `loomAbort.abort()` is called on every entry, parents and children alike. The parent's `?` / `match` arms covering the child's `Err(QueryError { kind: "cancelled" })` (or `kind: "invoke_callee_error"` wrapping it, per [Cancellation — Surfacing](./cancellation.md)) do **not** run inside the bounded-await window of sub-step 3: the parent's own `loomAbort` has already fired in the same iteration, its next [`Checkpoint` seam](#checkpoint-seam) await observes the abort, and the parent unwinds without re-entering interpreter dispatch. The parent's `disposeBarrier` settles independently of whether its child surfaced an `Err` to it — the registry treats every entry symmetrically. The downward-only propagation rule of [Cancellation — Propagation](./cancellation.md) is not contradicted: parent and child are not propagating into each other, they are both aborted by the same external `session_shutdown` trigger, and the parent's `Err`-handling arms remain inert during teardown for the same checkpoint reason that any cancelled invocation's post-abort code is inert.

5. *Factory-ordering pin.* The `session_shutdown` handler MUST be subscribed (step 4 above) only after the `LoomRegistry` and watcher handles the handler reads are constructed (this step). The implementation MAY reorder steps 4 and 5 internally provided that subscription happens after registry/watcher construction; a `session_shutdown` MUST NOT be reachable against a partially-constructed extension state, so the closure-captured `LoomRegistry` handle the handler reads at handler entry (per step (I) of the *Handler control-flow ordering* clause in the [**idempotent**](#idempotent-handler-clause) clause above) is never `undefined` and `LoomRegistry.readDrainState()` cannot throw a `TypeError` against a missing dispatch in the gap between step 4 returning and step 5 completing. Registers a chokidar file watcher over the discovered roots and maintains an internal mutable `LoomRegistry` (a `Map<slashName, parsedLoom>`) plus a `.warp` import graph. The slash-command `handler` registered in step 3 closes over the registry and dispatches by slash name on every invocation, so a registry swap takes effect on the next call without a `pi.registerCommand` re-registration. On a chokidar event for an **existing** loom or `.warp` file the watcher debounces (250 ms window, to coalesce editor `change` + `rename` bursts; the 250 ms window is measured against the runtime's injected `Clock` seam (per the runtime's DI skeleton — see [`Clock` / `FakeClock` interface](#clock--fakeclock-interface) below), the seam exists to make burst-coalescing assertions deterministic and is not a tunable runtime knob), re-parses just the changed file plus every transitive `.warp` importer reached through the import graph, and atomically swaps the affected entries in `LoomRegistry` via build-aside-then-publish: the runtime re-parses the changed file plus every transitive `.warp` importer into a staging set, recompiles their AJV validators into a staging cache, and only after every step succeeds installs both into `LoomRegistry` and the validator cache in a single synchronous step. If any rebuild step throws, the staging set is discarded and the prior `LoomRegistry` snapshot and AJV validator cache remain live; the failure surfaces as a single `loom/runtime/registry-swap-failed` diagnostic (see [Diagnostics](./diagnostics.md)). Compiled AJV validators for swapped entries are dropped from the per-loom cache as part of the publish step (not before). Tools synthesised from prompt-mode `.loom` callables are re-registered through `pi.registerTool` when the swap produces a new schema slug (`pi.registerTool` is documented as supported after startup); existing cached registrations under unchanged slugs are reused. The runtime does **not** call `ctx.reload()` for content edits — doing so would tear down every Pi extension, skill, prompt, and theme in the session for a single keystroke and would also race the post-`await` runtime-deadness rule that `ctx.reload()` documents.

   **In-flight invocation rule.** The slash-handler closure registered in step 3 (which calls `LoomRegistry.readDrainState()` per the [*Drain-state-gated dispatch*](#slash-handler-registration) clause and routes through the entry table for the dispatch arm) reads the entry exactly once at handler entry; a swap mid-execution does not affect a running invocation. Slash-command dispatch is gated by the three-arm `LoomRegistry.readDrainState()` enumeration pinned in the [*Drain-state-gated dispatch*](#slash-handler-registration) clause appended to step 3 above and the [`LoomRegistry` drain-state contract](#loom-registry-drain-state-contract) below (including that contract's *Methods* paragraph's [*Read-failure fallback*](#read-failure-fallback) clause); that contract supersedes the prior single-arm `drained`-keyed short-circuit and is the sole authority on which non-dispatch system note (the `"shutting-down"` arm's legacy `"loom /<name>: extension shutting down"` template, the `"degraded-needs-reload"` arm's `"loom /<name>: extension degraded; /reload to recover"` template, or arm (a) dispatch) the handler returns. The next invocation sees the post-swap version. In-flight invocations therefore complete against the pre-swap snapshot and any tool calls or queries they have already committed remain final, consistent with [Errors and Results — No rollback](./errors-and-results.md).

   **Structural changes.** Adding a brand-new `.loom` file or removing an existing one cannot register / unregister a slash command after extension load (Pi exposes no symmetric `pi.unregisterCommand` for the removal case, and adding a new command after the extension factory has run is not a documented post-startup mutation). When the watcher observes such an event, it emits a single `loom-system-note` with `content` formatted as `loom watcher: <N> file(s) added or removed; run /reload to refresh the slash command list`, `display: true`, and the `details` payload defined under System notes. The substitution rule is fixed: only `<N>` is substituted; every other character of the template — including the literal token `file(s)` (always rendered with the parenthesised `s`, never pluralised), the literal slash-command name `/reload` (not substituted from any registered command), and the trailing `; run /reload to refresh the slash command list` clause — ships verbatim regardless of `N`. `<N>` is rendered in base 10 with no thousands separator, no leading zero, and no sign, and equals `details.structural.added.length + details.structural.removed.length` (a path that appears in both arrays — e.g., a rename observed as removal-then-addition within the same debounce window — counts twice, since the two arrays are disjoint by role and not deduplicated against each other). Worked examples: with `added.length = 1, removed.length = 0`, the rendered content is `loom watcher: 1 file(s) added or removed; run /reload to refresh the slash command list`; with `added.length = 3, removed.length = 2`, it is `loom watcher: 5 file(s) added or removed; run /reload to refresh the slash command list`. The note MUST NOT be emitted when `added.length + removed.length === 0`. A debounce window that closes with no resolved add or remove paths produces no `loom-system-note` — including a settings-file edit whose post-merge `looms` array is byte-identical to the previous resolved set, an edit that touches only `looms.binderModel` or unrelated keys, and a chokidar burst over discovery roots that does not net any added or removed `.loom` / `.warp` files. The watcher's other obligations for the window (validator-cache invalidation per the **In-flight invocation rule** above, settings-file cache invalidation per the settings-file watcher path) still run; only the note is suppressed. A rename observed within the same debounce window as `removed` of path P followed by `added` of path P still has `added.length + removed.length === 2` and MUST emit the note (the two arrays are disjoint by role and not deduplicated against each other, per the rule above); the suppression applies only to the strictly-empty case. The note prompts the user to run `/reload` (which invokes Pi's `ctx.reload()` and re-executes the entire extension factory). Multiple structural events observed within a single 250 ms debounce window coalesce into one note; events in distinct windows fire separately. The note is informational, not a diagnostic; no `loom/load/*` code is registered for it. Settings-file edits affecting the `looms` array are treated as structural changes and routed through the same prompt; per-`.loom`-file content edits are not.

**Extension-bootstrap SDK failures.** A throw or rejection from any of the registration calls in steps 1–5 above is fatal at the granularity of the failing surface; the granularity rule is per call type, not per call site:

- **`pi.registerMessageRenderer` failure (factory-time, step 0 having succeeded so the capability is present but the call itself rejects).** The renderer registration is dropped; the extension factory still completes the remaining steps. System notes for this extension instance permanently degrade to the `ctx.ui.notify` arm of the **System notes** fallback chain below (the persistent-transcript surface is unavailable; the transient toast and the `console.error` last-resort arms remain). The runtime emits `loom/load/extension-bootstrap-failed` (E, load) with `details: { capability: "pi.registerMessageRenderer", error: <error.message> }` and proceeds.
- **`pi.registerCommand` failure (factory-time *or* `session_start`-time, per-loom).** Only the loom whose registration call failed is dropped; sibling looms in the pending registration list still register through their own `pi.registerCommand` calls. The runtime emits one `loom/load/extension-bootstrap-failed` (E, load) per failing loom with `details: { capability: "pi.registerCommand", loom: <slash-name>, error: <error.message> }`. The factory does not re-attempt the failing call within the same factory invocation; a `/reload` is the recovery path.
- **`pi.registerFlag` failure (factory-time, step 1).** Fatal to the whole extension because step 1's `--loom` flag value is what step 1's discovery walk and every subsequent `resources_discover` re-walk consume via `pi.getFlag('loom')`; a flag-less factory cannot honour the `--loom` source. The factory skips every subsequent `pi.register*` and `pi.on` call (steps 2–5 do not execute, mirroring the step-0 failure semantics) and emits a single `loom/load/extension-bootstrap-failed` (E, load) with `details: { capability: "pi.registerFlag", error: <error.message> }`.

The `loom/load/extension-bootstrap-failed` diagnostic routes through the same channel that step 0's `loom/load/host-incompatible` uses (the **System notes** fallback chain — `sendSystemNote` → `ctx.ui.notify` → `console.error`), because the renderer may itself have failed. The factory MUST NOT throw out of `default function (pi: ExtensionAPI)`; per-call `try`/`catch` around each step keeps the failure local to its granularity rule above. None of these three rules apply to the step-0 capability probe — a missing capability is `loom/load/host-incompatible` and stops the factory before it ever attempts a `pi.register*` call. `pi.registerTool` failures at factory time are governed by the prompt-mode registration cache rule under **Tool-registration lifetime and visibility** below; this paragraph does not duplicate that rule.

**Per-loom registration.** For each `.loom` file:

- The slash-command `handler` runs the binder (when applicable) and then the loom interpreter against the appropriate conversation.
- When a loom is referenced by another loom's `tools:` (i.e., exposed as a tool to a model), the runtime materialises a Pi `ToolDefinition` for it. *How* that definition reaches the model depends on the calling loom's mode and is specified in **Tool-registration lifetime and visibility** below; the *shape* of the definition is mode-independent and is specified here. The runtime constructs the definition through `defineTool(...)` (exported from `@earendil-works/pi-coding-agent`) rather than a bare object literal, so TypeBox's generic inference on `parameters` is preserved when the resulting value is spread into a `customTools: ToolDefinition[]` array (consumed by the subagent path) or passed to `pi.registerTool` (consumed by the prompt-mode path). All five fields (`name`, `label`, `description`, `parameters`, `execute`) are required by Pi's `ToolDefinition` interface. Field derivations:
    - `name` — the loom's registered tool name from its frontmatter / discovery (per [Directory Convention](./discovery.md)).
    - `label` — the loom file's basename with hyphens preserved and the leading character capitalised: `summarise.loom` → `"Summarise"`, `code-review.loom` → `"Code-Review"`. For the synthesised typed-query one-shot tool described in [Implementation Notes — Runtime](./implementation-notes.md#runtime) the label is the literal string `"Loom typed-query response"`.
    - `description` — the loom's frontmatter `description`.
    - `parameters` — a TypeBox `TSchema`, **not** a raw JSON Schema document. The lowered JSON Schema artefact produced by [Schema Subset — Lowering Algorithm](./schema-subset.md#lowering-algorithm) is wrapped via `Type.Unsafe<unknown>(loweredJsonSchema)` (imported from the `typebox` peer dependency declared in `package.json`; the presence of `Type.Unsafe` as a callable function is the load-bearing host-shape precondition checked at extension-factory entry by **Step 0 (e)** above, so a missing or renamed member surfaces as `loom/load/host-incompatible` with `details.kind = "typebox-shape"` rather than as a runtime-time `TypeError` at this call site) before being handed to `pi.registerTool`. The `Type.Unsafe` wrapper exists solely to satisfy Pi's structural type and to let TypeBox carry the JSON Schema through to the provider lowering layer; `Static<…>` is unused at runtime. Because the wrap is `Type.Unsafe<unknown>`, the `params` argument observed inside `execute` is effectively `unknown`, so the adapter MUST AJV-validate `params` against the original lowered JSON Schema before forwarding — Pi's structural typing offers no guarantees here. The optional `prepareArguments?: (args: unknown) => Static<TParams>` hook on `ToolDefinition` is the documented site for argument shaping in Pi's `ToolDefinition` contract; loom's respond-repair flow instead operates at the response-validation boundary (see [Query — Schema-validation respond-repair](./query.md)) rather than at this per-call argument boundary.
    - `execute` — the adapter that spawns the loom as a subagent invocation (equivalent to `invoke<T>(path, ...)`) and returns its result envelope.

    The adapter is **re-entrant**: when the model emits parallel tool calls (Pi's parallel-tool-mode behaviour, see [Tool Calls — Concurrency](./tool-calls.md)) targeting the same `.loom` callable, two concurrent calls into the same `execute` adapter spawn two independent subagent invocations on the event loop. Adapter implementations MUST NOT serialise calls on shared closure state.

<a id="tool-registration-lifetime-and-visibility"></a>**Tool-registration lifetime and visibility.** Pi's tool registry has no `unregisterTool` API — `pi.registerTool` is the only mutation, and entries persist for the process lifetime. The runtime therefore wires loom-synthesised tools (`.loom` callables from another loom's callable set, and the typed-query `__loom_respond_<slug>` one-shot tool described in [Implementation Notes — Runtime](./implementation-notes.md#runtime)) into the model's reach by two distinct mechanisms, one per **calling-loom** mode, designed so that tool *visibility* tracks the loom's invocation rather than the process lifetime, and so the [Parameters and Frontmatter](./frontmatter.md#tools) "ambient tools are deliberately *not* inherited" invariant holds.

*Subagent mode (caller is `mode: subagent`).* The runtime never calls `pi.registerTool` for the synthesised tool. The `ToolDefinition` is passed through `createAgentSession({ customTools, tools, ... })` (see **Conversation drive — subagent mode** below).
