The tool exists only inside the spawned `AgentSession`, dies with `dispose()`, and is invisible to the user's bare Pi session and to every other extension or concurrent loom.

*Prompt mode (caller is `mode: prompt`).* The runtime maintains an extension-scoped registration cache: `Map<schemaSlug, registeredToolName>`, where the slug is the schema slug of the lowered tool `parameters` (produced by the recipe in [Schema Subset — Canonical schema hash](./schema-subset.md#canonical-schema-hash)). On first encounter of a unique slug the runtime calls `pi.registerTool` once with a content-addressed name (`__loom_callee_<slug>__<post-rename-name>` for loom callees; `__loom_respond_<slug>` for the typed-query one-shot tool). Subsequent uses of the same lowered shape reuse the existing registration.

On a subsequent cache hit (a new lowered schema hashing to a slug already present in the cache), the runtime MUST verify byte-equality of the cached canonical-form schema bytes against the new entry's canonical-form bytes before reusing the registration. The slug is a 64-bit truncation of SHA-256 (per [Schema Subset — Canonical schema hash](./schema-subset.md#canonical-schema-hash)), so silent collision is statistically negligible but not impossible; treating slug equality as schema equality without verification would silently alias two distinct tool schemas to one registered name. On byte-mismatch the runtime emits `loom/runtime/registration-cache-collision`, refuses to dedup, and registers the new schema under a disambiguated name with a monotonically increasing per-slug counter (`__loom_callee_<slug>_<n>__<post-rename-name>` for loom callees; `__loom_respond_<slug>_<n>` for typed-query one-shot tools, starting at `n = 2`). The cache stores the canonical-form bytes alongside the registered name so the equality check is a byte comparison, not a re-serialisation. Around each query — both untyped and typed — the runtime gates visibility via the active-set:

1. Snapshot `pi.getActiveTools()` into a local list.
2. Call `pi.setActiveTools([...loomCallableSetNames, respondToolName?])` — the set the model sees for this turn is exactly the loom's declared callable set, plus the respond tool when the turn is a typed-query response turn. The user-session snapshot taken in step 1 is held only for the step-4 restore; it is deliberately not unioned into the active set installed here, so the [Parameters and Frontmatter](./frontmatter.md#tools) "ambient tools are deliberately *not* inherited" invariant holds during the query.
3. Issue the query.
4. In a `finally` block (so cancellation, panic, and provider exceptions all preserve the invariant), call `pi.setActiveTools(snapshot)` to restore the user session's prior active set.

**Restore-failure protocol.** If the restoring `pi.setActiveTools(snapshot)` call inside the `finally` block of step 4 throws or rejects, the runtime MUST: (a) re-attempt the restore exactly once with the same snapshot (covering transient failures); (b) on a second failure, emit `loom/runtime/active-set-restore-failed` (E, runtime) with `message` carrying the underlying error's message and `hint` listing the snapshot tool names so an operator can manually restore via Pi's `/tools` interface; (c) emit a `display: true` `loom-system-note` whose `content` is the verbatim template `loom: failed to restore tool active-set after /<name>; the user session may have unexpected tools active. Run /reload to reset.` (only `<name>` is substituted — every other character ships verbatim, including the literal `/reload` and the trailing clause); and (d) propagate the original exception (or terminal `Err`) that the `finally` was protecting — restore failure does not mask the inner error, and the cascade-twin dedup rule under **Runtime event channel** below treats the active-set-restore note as independent of any inner-failure note. The retry MUST NOT chain back into `pi.setActiveTools` beyond the single re-attempt above (no exponential backoff, no third try). Subagent-mode invocations are unaffected — the subagent's tools are scoped to the spawned `AgentSession` and released by `dispose()`, so this rule applies only to the prompt-mode and prompt → prompt cross-mode `invoke` snapshot/restore paths in this section.

The snapshot/restore is the only control surface for visibility; the cached `pi.registerTool` entries themselves are intentionally permanent. Consequences:

- `pi.getAllTools()` and `/tools` listings accumulate one entry per distinct lowered schema seen in the extension's lifetime; this is bounded (looms author a small finite number of typed-query and `.loom`-callable shapes) and is documented as cosmetic loom 1.0 behaviour.
- The user's bare Pi session — and every other extension — never sees a loom-synthesised tool in its active set, because no code path other than the loom runtime's own swap ever activates them.
- Hot reload (the `_loom-reload` path described in **Extension entry point** step 5) drops the registration cache so a fresh extension instance starts empty; the orphaned registry entries persist in Pi's global registry but are unreachable, matching the loom 1.0 acceptance of cosmetic accumulation.
- `pi.setActiveTools` snapshots are name lists, not snapshots of the global registry. The `pi.setActiveTools(names: string[]): void` and `pi.getActiveTools(): string[]` signatures are pinned by `ExtensionAPI` in `dist/core/extensions/types.d.ts` of `@earendil-works/pi-coding-agent` (the [loom 1.0 Pi-SDK pin](#pi-sdk-pin) from **Host prerequisites** above) and are covered by the [Step 0 (c)](#entry-capability-probe) factory-probable capability inventory; a Pi minor that renames either member, widens the return type of `pi.setActiveTools` past `void`, or splits the snapshot/restore pair surfaces at the SDK surface-inventory test before the spec contract drifts. <a id="snapshot-restore-pi-behavioural-preconditions"></a> The snapshot/restore protocol additionally relies on two Pi *behavioural* preconditions that the type signature does not encode: (a) the loom runtime treats `pi.setActiveTools(string[])` as synchronous-and-atomic on the JS event loop (a single swap or restore call cannot be interleaved with anything else); and (b) Pi serialises slash-command dispatch per session — two loom-invocation slash dispatches against the same session cannot overlap their snapshot/restore windows. This property is a *behavioural* precondition, **not** a build-time-asserted SDK capability of [SDK capability inventory](#sdk-capability-inventory) above — the source-line citations that follow are loom 1.0-pin **evidence** that the property holds at the pin, not a binding contract on Pi internals (which is precisely why [item (e)](#bump-checklist-slash-dispatch-serialisation) of the *Editorial-review checklist for unpinned host presuppositions* under [Pi version bump procedure](#pi-version-bump-procedure) below re-audits it on each Pi minor bump rather than the SDK surface-inventory test catching a regression — the inventory test cannot detect a weakening here from the type surface alone). At the [loom 1.0 Pi-SDK pin](#pi-sdk-pin) on `@earendil-works/pi-coding-agent` the evidence trail is `AgentSession.prototype.prompt` in `dist/core/agent-session.js`, whose body awaits the registered slash-command handler end-to-end (`await command.handler(args, ctx)`, dispatched via the private `_tryExecuteExtensionCommand` step) before returning, together with the per-mode user-input drivers — `dist/modes/rpc/rpc-mode.js` lexically awaits each `session.prompt(...)` call site before initiating the next, and `dist/modes/interactive/interactive-mode.js` dispatches user input via the `Editor.onSubmit` callback registered during mode setup whose submit pump establishes the equivalent non-overlap invariant (the per-driver audit recipe and its known-fragile-evidence caveats are owned by [item (e)](#bump-checklist-slash-dispatch-serialisation) below). The leading-underscore name `_tryExecuteExtensionCommand` (semver does not protect a `_`-prefixed symbol — a Pi *patch* may rename or inline it), the `Editor.onSubmit` TUI-layer detail (orthogonal to the snapshot/restore protocol — a TUI refactor that preserves the cooperative `await` may rename or replace the `onSubmit` pump), and the deep `dist/*.js` bundler-output paths above (which neither **Host prerequisites** above nor the SDK-surface inventory asserts remain un-bundled, un-minified, or stably named across the loom 1.0-pinned minor) are flagged as **known-fragile evidence** — diffable artefacts at the loom 1.0 pin sufficient to satisfy item (e)'s audit recipe on a pass outcome, but not load-bearing claims about their stable shape across patches. [Item (e)](#bump-checklist-slash-dispatch-serialisation) below absorbs that fragility by routing a textual-diffability failure of the audit recipe (the loom 1.0-cited symbols or paths no longer locatable under their pinned names in a candidate minor — e.g. because Pi has minified, re-bundled, or renamed the `_`-prefixed symbol) to the same defensive-mutex recovery path as a substantive cooperative-await regression, so the contributor is never left with an undefined verdict on a Pi minor that mangles the evidence trail without weakening the underlying behavioural property. The loom 1.0.0 driver set is asserted closed at exactly these two files; the bump-procedure (e) checklist below applies the glob `dist/modes/*/*.js` against the candidate Pi minor and treats any additional matching file with a reachable `session.prompt(...)` call site (per [(e.ii)](#bump-checklist-slash-dispatch-serialisation-ii)'s call-graph reachability rule below — literal substring grep on the file's text is not the predicate, since the call may be wrapped in a callback registration during mode setup rather than appearing at the lexical top level) as audit-positive evidence of a driver mode beyond the loom 1.0.0 driver set's two files whose cooperative-await contribution to this precondition has not been load-tested and which triggers the recovery path. The property is therefore established cooperatively across the `AgentSession.prototype.prompt` body and the per-mode user-input driver(s) rather than by a single per-session dispatch lock the SDK exposes. The recovery path on a fail outcome — a defensive per-extension-instance runtime mutex wrapping the snapshot → swap → body → restore sequence, keyed on the factory-captured `pi: ExtensionAPI` reference (the only identity the loom holds at the snapshot/restore site, since `ExtensionCommandContext` is per-slash-handler-invocation and the user `AgentSession` is not exposed to prompt-mode looms) — is enumerated under [item (e) of the editorial-review checklist below](#bump-checklist-slash-dispatch-serialisation). The per-extension-instance keying granularity is well-defined only while **both** the page-pinned one-`pi`-per-extension-instance lifetime (see the [loom 1.0 seam — mid-loom user-session replacement](#v1-seam-mid-loom-user-session-replacement) paragraph below) AND the loom 1.0 one-active-user-session-per-extension-instance presupposition (pinned at *No concurrent user sessions in the same host process* in [Future Considerations](./future-considerations.md#v1-non-goals)) hold; together, on the recovery path, the keyed mutex is the unique serialisation point per user session (the mutex exists only when the recovery path is engaged on a fail outcome of the [item (e)](#bump-checklist-slash-dispatch-serialisation) audit recipe — loom 1.0 ships without it on a pass outcome, since precondition (b)'s cooperative-`await` chain establishes the non-overlap property in that case), and a future Pi minor that weakens **either** invariant requires revisiting the keying granularity at the same time the precondition is re-validated. Precondition (b) covers only the slash entry point; the symmetric in-process guarantee that nested prompt → prompt `invoke(...)` calls cannot overlap their snapshot/restore windows is owned by the loom runtime itself — the `invoke(...)` to a prompt-mode callee suspends the parent's body until the child returns per [Invocation — Cross-mode semantics](./invocation.md), loom 1.0 exposes no parallel-`invoke` surface, and prompt-mode `.loom` callees in another loom's `tools:` are rejected at load time per [Parameters and Frontmatter — `tools`](./frontmatter.md#tools), so two prompt-mode snapshot/restore windows against the same user session can only ever be **strictly LIFO-nested**, never concurrently overlapping. If either Pi behavioural precondition above weakens in a future Pi minor, the snapshot/restore protocol above MUST be re-validated as part of [Pi version bump procedure](#pi-version-bump-procedure) below; the SDK surface-inventory test cannot detect either weakening from the type surface alone.
- If another extension calls `pi.setActiveTools` between a loom's snapshot and its `finally` restore, the loom's restore overwrites that change. Extensions wishing to coexist with loom should mutate the active set outside of any in-flight loom invocation, or accept the overwrite. The loom runtime emits no diagnostic for this case. This overwrite rule covers prompt-mode untyped queries, prompt-mode typed-query free and forced phases, and prompt → prompt invocation bodies — same protocol, same rule. It does NOT apply to subagent mode, which never touches `pi.setActiveTools` on the user session.
- The `unknown_tool` cause on `CodeToolError` (see [Tool Calls](./tool-calls.md)) and the captured-reference dispatch model from [Parameters and Frontmatter — Resolution snapshot](./frontmatter.md#resolution-snapshot) are unaffected: code-side `<name>(...)` calls never touch the active-set machinery — they dispatch directly through the loom's load-time callable table.

No Pi-side change is required for loom 1.0; if Pi later adds `pi.unregisterTool`, the registration cache becomes the natural site to call it from on extension teardown without altering the per-mode wiring rule above.

<a id="no-extra-mediation"></a>

**No additional access channels.** The runtime interposes no privilege layer between loom code and the Pi extension host. Loom-side filesystem, network, and Pi-API access are bounded only by Pi's extension-host grants and by the per-loom `tools:` allowlist whose enforcement is specified above. The runtime MUST NOT introduce additional access channels (sandbox, capability filter, mediated proxy) in any loom 1.x release; widening or narrowing this rule is a major-version concern. The `tools:` allowlist constrains the *model's* reachable callable set, not the host process: a loom that declares a high-privilege callable (e.g. `bash`) exposes the full underlying capability of that callable to its model. Host-side denials of filesystem, network, or Pi-API access reach loom code through the tool that issued the request: a thrown or `isError: true` return is mapped to `Err(QueryError { kind: "code_tool", cause: "execution", ... })` per [Tool Calls — Failures](./tool-calls.md) and [Tool execution from loom code](#tool-execution-from-loom-code) below; silent success on denial is forbidden.

**Conversation drive — prompt mode.** The loom interpreter drives the user's session by:

- Issuing untyped queries via `pi.sendUserMessage(text)` when the agent is idle, or `pi.sendUserMessage(text, { deliverAs: "steer" })` when the agent is mid-stream. `pi.sendUserMessage` returns `void` — the `ExtensionAPI` surface declares both `sendUserMessage(...)` and `sendMessage(...)` as `void`-returning; the `Promise<void>` shape exists only on `AgentSession.sendUserMessage` (subagent mode, see **Conversation drive — subagent mode** below) and on `ReplacedSessionContext.sendUserMessage` (post-replacement contexts, out of scope here per the *captured `pi` reference* clause below). Only synchronous throws — e.g. argument-validation rejections inside Pi — are observable directly from the call. The runtime MUST NOT `await pi.sendUserMessage(...)` and MUST NOT attach a `.catch` handler — matching the rule pinned for `pi.sendMessage` under **System notes** below. The **primary** prompt-mode transport-failure surface is therefore the post-`waitForIdle()` `AgentSession.errorMessage` probe pinned under *Error detection* below, not the `pi.sendUserMessage` call site itself. As a narrow secondary mapping, a synchronous throw from `pi.sendUserMessage` (the only failure mode the call surface itself can signal) is mapped to `Err(QueryError { kind: "transport", message: <error.message>, http_status: null, provider: <resolved-model-provider>, retryable: false })` — not to `loom/runtime/internal-error`. The `provider` field is populated from the loom's resolved `model:` regardless of which surface (synchronous throw at the call site vs. the `errorMessage` probe) detected the failure, since the `errorMessage` string carries no structured provider field and the **Runtime event channel** always-log emission for `kind: "transport"` requires the field. The same dual-surface mapping applies when `pi.sendUserMessage` is the transport call inside a typed query's free phase or its forced respond turn. The `pi` reference here is the `ExtensionAPI` captured by the extension factory (the `pi` parameter of `default function (pi: ExtensionAPI)` from the **Extension entry point** above), which the runtime holds for the lifetime of each loom invocation; `sendUserMessage` is **not** a method on `ExtensionCommandContext`, so the per-handler `ctx` is consulted only for `ctx.isIdle()` to choose between the two forms (calling the no-options form mid-stream throws — see Pi's `examples/extensions/send-user-message.ts`). loom 1.0 prompt-mode looms always use `deliverAs: "steer"` when not idle (the loom is the active driver and wants its message delivered to *this* turn); `deliverAs: "followUp"` is reserved for future considerations and is not emitted by loom 1.0. The captured `pi` reference assumes the user session is **not** replaced mid-loom (`ctx.newSession()` / `ctx.fork()` / `ctx.switchSession()` invalidate it); loom 1.0 looms never trigger replacement (see [Future Considerations — Mid-loom user-session replacement](./future-considerations.md#mid-loom-user-session-replacement) for the post-loom 1.0 re-acquisition seam). Completion is awaited by `await ctx.waitForIdle()` on the `ExtensionCommandContext` passed to the slash-command handler. `waitForIdle` is session-scoped — it observes only the user session bound to this command — and is the prompt-mode driver's authoritative completion signal. *Resolution.* `waitForIdle()` returns `Promise<void>` and resolves once Pi emits `agent_end` for the user session and every awaited `agent_end` listener settles; it never rejects, so the runtime MUST NOT wrap the `await` in a `try`/`catch` expecting rejection as a failure signal. *Error detection.* Because `pi.sendUserMessage` returns `void` (no rejection path) and `waitForIdle()` never rejects, every transport- or provider-level failure of the user turn that is not a synchronous throw at the call site lands on the user `AgentSession`'s error state. This post-`waitForIdle()` probe is the **primary** transport-failure surface for prompt mode; the synchronous-throw branch above is the narrow secondary. Immediately after `waitForIdle()` resolves the runtime probes that state (the `errorMessage` field on the `AgentSession`, named per the pinned Pi version from **Host prerequisites** above), and a non-empty value maps to `Err(QueryError { kind: "transport", message: <errorMessage>, http_status: null, provider: <resolved-model-provider>, retryable: false })` per [Query](./query.md). The probe MUST read `errorMessage` synchronously on `waitForIdle()` resolution, before the runtime issues any subsequent `pi.sendUserMessage` on the same context — Pi may clear or overwrite the field on the next turn. The runtime MUST NOT install a global `pi.on("agent_error", …)` listener for this purpose, by the same per-session cross-fire reasoning given for the `agent_end` ban below. *Hang handling.* `waitForIdle()` has no internal deadline; hangs are bounded only by the cancellation path. `loomAbort.abort()` invokes `ctx.abort()` on the captured slash-command handler context (the `ExtensionCommandContext.abort` member already in the forwarded set per **`ExtensionContext` (member surface loom touches)** below), which cancels the active user run and lets `waitForIdle()` resolve; the runtime guards the propagation with a one-shot flag so a re-entrant `loomAbort.abort()` (e.g. from an `agent_end` observer that itself observes the abort) does not double-cancel. The post-`waitForIdle` error-state probe runs unconditionally on resolution, but if `loomAbort.signal.aborted` is true the runtime synthesises `Err(QueryError { kind: "cancelled" })` per [Cancellation](./cancellation.md) instead of reading session error state — even when Pi tore down cleanly and `waitForIdle()` resolved without any error written to the session. The symmetric statement on the abort side lives at [Cancellation — Forwarding into `loomAbort`](./cancellation.md). The runtime MUST NOT subscribe to the global `pi.on("agent_end", …)` event for query completion: that event fires for every `AgentSession` in the process (the user shell session and any concurrent subagent-mode sessions) with no per-session origin marker, so a global handler cross-fires across concurrent looms or sibling subagents and resolves the wait on the wrong turn. <a id="untyped-query-ok-extraction"></a>The `Ok(string)` value of an untyped query is the accumulated assistant text of the final turn, extracted from the user session after `waitForIdle()` resolves and only once the cancellation short-circuit (`loomAbort.signal.aborted`, which synthesises `Err(QueryError { kind: "cancelled" })`) and the non-empty-`errorMessage` transport short-circuit pinned above have both been passed — the extraction runs downstream of those branches and never reorders or bypasses them. The runtime reads the source from the same `ReadonlySessionManager` `Pick<>` members the binder uses: `ctx.sessionManager.getEntries()` and `ctx.sessionManager.getLeafId()` (both enumerated in the `sessionManager` row of **`ExtensionContext` (member surface loom touches)** below), fed to `buildSessionContext(...)` exactly as [Session-context truncation](./binder.md#session-context-truncation-bind_context-session) does, yielding the same chronological `Message` list. The *final turn* is the trailing turn of that list — the last `user` message (the loom-issued `pi.sendUserMessage` turn) plus every subsequent `assistant` / `toolResult` / `custom` message through the end of the list, using the turn boundary defined in that section; turns from earlier slash-command invocations on the long-lived user session precede that trailing `user` message and are excluded. The string is the `text` content of every `assistant` message in the final turn, concatenated in chronological order with a single `\n` separator between successive assistant messages; the provider-internal `thinking` array and all `toolCalls` entries are omitted, identical to the `[assistant]` body selection in [Compact-transcript format](./binder.md#compact-transcript-format-normative) item 4. A final turn that produced no assistant text (a pure tool-use turn) yields the empty string. `pi-loom` performs no buffering, suppression, or re-styling of Pi's stream; user-visible behaviour is specified in [Slash-Command Invocation — User-visible streaming](./slash-invocation.md).
- Issuing typed queries that enforce the inferred or ascribed schema against the model's response. A typed query is a **two-phase tool-loop conversation**, exactly as specified in [Query — Typed queries are tool-loop-shaped](./query.md): (1) a *free phase* in which the model may call any frontmatter `tools:` entry the same way it does in an untyped query, with `tool_choice` left unconstrained; followed by (2) one *forced respond turn* once the model emits a plain text turn, in which the runtime issues a follow-up user message inlining the lowered response schema and forces the provider's tool choice to the synthesised one-shot respond tool. The synthesised tool's `execute` AJV-validates its input against the lowered schema and resolves the query's promise with the validated value. Only the forced respond turn uses provider tool-choice forcing; every preceding free-phase turn leaves the model free to think aloud and to use the frontmatter callable set, so the `frontmatter.md` "available to the model during query-time tool loops" guarantee, the `ModelToolError` surface, and the "same callable set serves both code and model" invariant all stay live for typed queries. The forced respond turn is the exempt-routed terminator dispatched by CIO-4's `max_rounds`-final branch (see [Hard Runtime Ceilings — CIO-4](./hard-ceilings.md#ceiling-interaction-order) and [Query — Tool-call loop bound](./query.md)); the runtime issues it on every typed query reaching that branch — including `max_rounds: 0` where it is the only turn — and `tool_loop.max_rounds` is not debited by it. respond-repair follow-ups (see [Query — Schema-validation respond-repair](./query.md)) restart the whole two-phase loop with a fresh `tool_loop` budget, so the model can re-tool before answering a respond-repair turn. The runtime MUST surface the validated payload exactly once and MUST NOT add additional user-visible turns to the conversation beyond the natural free-phase turns and the single forced respond turn (the forced respond turn is rendered as a tool-call card by Pi's standard transcript renderer, not as a redundant assistant turn). The synthesised one-shot tool follows the same `name` / `label` / `description` / `parameters` / `execute` shape and the same `Type.Unsafe<unknown>(loweredJsonSchema)` `parameters` wrap defined in **Per-loom registration** above, and follows the registration cache + active-set snapshot/restore protocol defined in **Tool-registration lifetime and visibility** above, so the synthesised typed-query tool, the `.loom`-callable Pi tool, and the subagent-mode `customTools` entries all use a single bridge from loom's lowered JSON Schema to Pi's TypeBox-typed `ToolDefinition` and a single visibility-control mechanism. The mechanism used to force tool choice on the respond turn (`options.toolChoice` on the per-provider pi-ai adapter) is described in [Implementation Notes — Runtime](./implementation-notes.md#runtime).

> **loom 1.0 seam — mid-loom user-session replacement.** <a id="loom-1-0-seam-mid-loom-user-session-replacement"></a><a id="v1-seam-mid-loom-user-session-replacement"></a> The prompt-mode driver MUST read `pi` from a single factory-captured reference (the `pi: ExtensionAPI` parameter of `default function (pi: ExtensionAPI)` from the **Extension entry point** above) held for the lifetime of each loom invocation; consumers MUST NOT re-acquire `pi` from any other surface (e.g. by reaching into `ExtensionCommandContext` or by re-entering the factory) during a loom invocation. The deferred *Mid-loom user-session replacement* extension in [Future Considerations](./future-considerations.md#mid-loom-user-session-replacement) introduces a `withSession`-fronted re-acquisition of the captured reference before the next `sendUserMessage` (so a loom-driven `ctx.newSession()` / `ctx.fork()` / `ctx.switchSession()` call no longer invalidates the captured `pi`) at exactly that single capture site; duplicating the capture across call sites in loom 1.0 is breaking, because the deferred re-acquisition hook would then have to be threaded into every duplicate.

**Provider compatibility for typed queries.** The forced respond turn requires the provider to honour named-tool forcing. loom 1.0 supports the providers for which pi-ai exposes a named-tool `toolChoice` mapping: `anthropic-messages`, `openai-completions`, `mistral`, and `amazon-bedrock`. At loom-load time, when a loom contains any typed-query expression and its resolved `model:` routes through a provider outside this set, the runtime emits `loom/load/typed-query-unsupported-provider` (warning) naming the model and listing the typed-query expression positions; the loom still loads, and any typed query at runtime returns `Err(QueryError { kind: "transport", message: "<provider> does not support forced tool-use; typed queries unavailable", http_status: null, provider: "<provider>", retryable: false })`. Untyped queries against the same loom continue to work. Future widening (Gemini, OpenAI Responses, weak local models via JSON-mode fallback) is listed in [Future Considerations](./future-considerations.md).

> **loom 1.0 seam — typed-query supported provider set.** <a id="loom-1-0-seam-typed-query-supported-provider-set"></a><a id="v1-seam-typed-query-supported-provider-set"></a> The loom 1.0 typed-query-supported provider set (`anthropic-messages`, `openai-completions`, `mistral`, `amazon-bedrock`) MUST be exposed as a single named runtime constant referenced by every consumer — the load-time `loom/load/typed-query-unsupported-provider` warning emitter, and the runtime guard that synthesises the unsupported-provider `TransportError` — so that there is one source of truth to widen. Inlining the four-element provider list at any consumer is a breaking simplification: the deferred *Typed-query support for providers without named-tool forcing* extension in [Future Considerations](./future-considerations.md) widens this constant (and adds a JSON-mode / system-prompt fallback for the new entries) without touching the typed-query behavioural contract above; widening the constant is the only behavioural surface the extension perturbs.

<a id="pic-typed-query-noncompliance"></a> **loom 1.0 diagnostic limitation.** When a typed query routes through a provider in the loom 1.0 supported set (`anthropic-messages`, `openai-completions`, `mistral`, `amazon-bedrock`) — most commonly an OpenAI-compatible local backend — but the specific model ignores forced-tool selection on the forced respond turn (by emitting plain text, or by invoking a tool whose name is not `__loom_respond_<slug>`), the runtime cannot distinguish this from any other case where the model fails to call the respond tool. The runtime classifies the case as a schema-validation failure and routes it through the respond-repair pipeline below; it does NOT surface as `tool_loop_exhausted`, which is unreachable on the forced respond turn because that turn is the exempt-routed terminator dispatched by CIO-4's `max_rounds`-final branch (see [Hard Runtime Ceilings — CIO-4](./hard-ceilings.md#ceiling-interaction-order)). For each forced respond turn that does not invoke `__loom_respond_<slug>`, the runtime synthesises a single `ValidationIssue` (per [Errors and Results — `ValidationError`](./errors-and-results.md#queryerror-variants)). The non-compliance branch is observable in the synthesised issue's `message` literal; `path` and `schema_keyword` are uniform across both branches.

*Plain-text branch* — the forced respond turn carried plain text and no `tool_use` block:

```
{ path: "",
  schema_keyword: "required",
  message: "model returned plain text instead of calling the forced respond tool" }
```

*Wrong-tool branch* — the forced respond turn carried only `tool_use` blocks whose `name` is not `__loom_respond_<slug>` (independent of whether plain text accompanies them):

```
{ path: "",
  schema_keyword: "required",
  message: "model invoked tool '<provider-emitted-tool-name>' instead of the forced respond tool '__loom_respond_<slug>'" }
```

The `<provider-emitted-tool-name>` placeholder is the `name` field of the provider's `tool_use` block, verbatim; when multiple wrong-tool calls appear in the same turn, the first block's `name` is used (consistent with the "single `ValidationIssue`" rule above).

The synthesised issue feeds the same respond-repair pipeline as an AJV failure: it consumes one `respond_repair.attempts` slot, and the follow-up template is the methodology-appropriate one (the `validator_error` template's `<ajv-summary>` placeholder is rendered from this synthesised issue exactly as if AJV had produced it). Terminal exhaustion returns:

```
Err(QueryError {
  kind: "validation",
  cause: "schema_validation",
  attempts: respond_repair.attempts,                  // the configured budget
  validation_errors: [<synthesised issue from final attempt>],
  raw_response: <plain-text body of the final forced respond turn, or null when that turn carried no plain-text body>,
  message: "model did not call the forced respond tool"
})
```

The `raw_response: null` case is the wrong-tool branch when the model emitted a `tool_use` block with no accompanying plain text; this matches the `ToolLoopExhaustedError` precedent under [Errors and Results — `raw_response`](./errors-and-results.md#queryerror-variants) ("`null` when exhaustion fired on a pure tool-use turn"). When the wrong-tool turn does carry plain text alongside the `tool_use` block, `raw_response` is that plain-text body.

With `respond_repair.methodology: none`, the *first* forced respond turn that does not invoke `__loom_respond_<slug>` returns the same `Err` shape with `attempts: 0` (no follow-ups issued, consistent with the existing `none` contract). When a stub provider alternates plain-text and wrong-tool payloads across respond-repair attempts, only the *last attempt's* issue appears in `validation_errors` (consistent with the existing "final malformed assistant text" wording in `errors-and-results.md`); `raw_response` is the plain-text body of the *last* forced respond turn, or `null` when that turn carried no plain-text body — not a concatenation across attempts. The synthesised `ValidationIssue.path` is `""` (the JSON Pointer to the document root) on both branches, matching AJV's empty-path convention for root-level failures. Separating provider-level from model-level non-compliance is out of scope for loom 1.0.

**Provider error mapping.** The runtime maps recognised provider error responses to `QueryError` variants per the table below. Every other 4xx/5xx response and every network-level failure maps to `TransportError`. The matching rules are version-coupled to `@earendil-works/pi-ai` and MUST be re-validated on each upgrade. *Re-validation gate (loom 1.0.0).* loom 1.0.0 ships without a CI-wired bump-procedure step that re-runs the provider-error fixtures against a candidate `@earendil-works/pi-ai` minor; the fixtures exist in `npm test` and a contributor performing the bump is expected to run them, but [Pi version bump procedure](#pi-version-bump-procedure) below does not yet enumerate the step. Wiring this re-validation into the bump procedure as a mechanical gate is a recognised post-loom 1.0.0 maintenance follow-up. Reviews SHOULD NOT re-raise the absence of this acceptance criterion as a loom 1.0.0 correctness finding.

| Provider | Overflow signature → `ContextOverflowError` |
|---|---|
| `anthropic-messages` | HTTP 400 with `error.type: "invalid_request_error"` and `error.message` matching `/(prompt is too long\|exceeds .* context window\|maximum context length)/i`; `tokens_used` and `tokens_limit` populated from `error.message` digits when present. |
| `openai-completions` | HTTP 400 with `error.code: "context_length_exceeded"` (or HTTP 200 with the same code in the body envelope); `tokens_used` and `tokens_limit` populated from `error.message` digits when present. |
| `mistral` | HTTP 400 with body matching `/context.*length/i`; token counts not surfaced — both fields `null`. |
| `amazon-bedrock` | `ValidationException` with body matching `/(input is too long\|context window)/i`; token counts not surfaced — both fields `null`. |

<a id="provider-seed-field-mapping"></a>

**Provider seed-field mapping.** Whether a binder request payload carries a fixed seed, and under which JSON field name, is governed by the static table below. The mapping is keyed on the resolved binder model's `api` field as reported by `@earendil-works/pi-ai`'s model registry; it is not derived from any pi-ai capability flag. The seed *value* (its derivation from the loom's qualified name) is specified in [Slash-Command Argument Binding — Determinism](./binder.md#determinism). Widening the seed-supporting set is a spec-versioned change. The mapping is version-coupled to `@earendil-works/pi-ai` and MUST be re-validated on each upgrade; the mechanical gate is the build-time `Api`-coverage assertion which enumerates pi-ai's exposed `Api` literal-union values and asserts every value appears as a row key in the seed-field table constant, plus the provider seed-field fixtures rerun as step 6 of [Pi version bump procedure](#pi-version-bump-procedure) below. A new pi-ai `Api` value lights up the assertion red at the bump commit, exactly parallel to a new SDK capability.

| Provider | Seed field in request payload |
|---|---|
| `openai-completions` | `seed` |
| `mistral` | `random_seed` |
| `anthropic-messages` | omitted |
| `amazon-bedrock` | omitted |

**Conversation drive — subagent mode.** The loom interpreter spawns a fresh in-process `AgentSession` via `createAgentSession`. The `createAgentSession(options: CreateAgentSessionOptions)` function and the `CreateAgentSessionOptions` interface are declared at `dist/core/sdk.d.ts` in `@earendil-works/pi-coding-agent` (the [loom 1.0 Pi-SDK pin](#pi-sdk-pin) from **Host prerequisites** above); the inline call shape and the no-`signal`-field claim below are pinned to that file and MUST be re-validated against it on each Pi minor bump per [Pi version bump procedure](#pi-version-bump-procedure) below. The two tool-related fields on `CreateAgentSessionOptions` carry distinct payloads and must both be populated from the same lowered set:

```ts
const customTools: ToolDefinition[] = lowerLoomToolsToPi(loom.tools); // built-in Pi tools resolved by name → their ToolDefinition; loom callees wrapped via defineTool
const loomSystemPrompt: string = renderLoomSystemPrompt(loom.frontmatter.system, params); // resolved-and-interpolated `system:` per Parameters and Frontmatter
const resourceLoader: ResourceLoader = {
  // Loom-owned adapter: getSystemPrompt is the only loom-load-bearing member; the rest return empty/defaults.
  getSystemPrompt: () => loomSystemPrompt,
  getAppendSystemPrompt: () => [],
  getExtensions: () => ({ extensions: [], errors: [] }),
  getSkills: () => ({ skills: [], diagnostics: [] }),
  getPrompts: () => ({ prompts: [], diagnostics: [] }),
  getThemes: () => ({ themes: [], diagnostics: [] }),
  getAgentsFiles: () => ({ agentsFiles: [] }),
  extendResources: () => {},
  reload: async () => {},
};
const { session } = await createAgentSession({
  customTools,
  tools: customTools.map((t) => t.name), // explicit allowlist suppresses Pi's default built-ins
  model,
  sessionManager: SessionManager.inMemory(cwd),
  resourceLoader,
  // ...
});
```

Four rules govern the spawn call:

1. `customTools` carries every `ToolDefinition` the subagent may use — both Pi built-ins (resolved by name from the model registry / extension API to their `ToolDefinition`) and `defineTool`-wrapped `.loom` callables. Each entry uses the same `name` / `label` / `description` / `parameters` / `execute` shape and the same `Type.Unsafe<unknown>(loweredJsonSchema)` `parameters` wrap defined in the **Per-loom registration** section above. `ToolDefinition.label` is required; the lowering step must supply it (basename-derived per the **Per-loom registration** rule).
2. `tools` is **always** passed as an explicit allowlist of those same names, even when the loom's callable set is empty (in which case `tools: []` is passed, matching `tools: []` ≡ absent `tools:` from [Parameters and Frontmatter](./frontmatter.md)). The explicit allowlist is what enforces the "ambient Pi tools NOT inherited" invariant; omitting `tools` would re-enable Pi's default built-in `read` / `bash` / `edit` / `write` tools regardless of what the loom declared.
3. The `tools` allowlist and the `customTools` array are derived from the same lowered set in a single step; the runtime does not let them drift. A `.loom` callable wrapped via `defineTool` has a `name` chosen by the loom runtime (post-`as` rename per the basename rules in [Parameters and Frontmatter](./frontmatter.md)); that same name must appear in the `tools` allowlist.
4. The `resourceLoader` passed to `createAgentSession` is a loom-constructed `ResourceLoader` adapter whose `getSystemPrompt()` returns the resolved-and-interpolated frontmatter `system:` string verbatim and whose `getAppendSystemPrompt()` returns `[]` (the loom's `system:` is the *complete* system prompt, not an append on top of a host base). The remaining `ResourceLoader` members return empty values / defaults (`getExtensions`, `getSkills`, `getPrompts`, `getThemes`, `getAgentsFiles`) or are no-ops (`extendResources`, `reload`); the loom MUST NOT pass the parent session's `DefaultResourceLoader` through unchanged. `CreateAgentSessionOptions` exposes no `systemPrompt` / `system` field in the loom 1.0 Pi SDK pin, so the loader's `getSystemPrompt()` is the only available delivery channel for the loom's `system:` value into the spawned `AgentSession.systemPrompt`. The adapter MAY be expressed as the object literal above or as a `class implements ResourceLoader` declaration; both are conformant. `DefaultResourceLoader`'s `systemPromptOverride: (base) => string | undefined` constructor option is an alternative channel but is **not** the recommended construction: it still runs all of `DefaultResourceLoader`'s discovery side-effects against the parent `cwd` to compute `base`, only to ignore the result, so the custom-adapter form is preferred.

Immediately after the awaited `createAgentSession(...)` resolves, the runtime registers a one-shot listener on `loomAbort.signal` that calls `AgentSession.abort()` on the returned handle. The listener is the sole cancellation-forwarding mechanism in subagent mode — `CreateAgentSessionOptions` (declared at `dist/core/sdk.d.ts` in the loom 1.0 Pi-SDK pin per the introductory paragraph above) has no `signal` field, so passing one would be silently ignored; the spawn call MUST NOT include a `signal` field. If `loomAbort.signal.aborted` is already true at the moment `createAgentSession(...)` resolves, the runtime invokes `session.abort()` synchronously *before* the listener is registered and *before* issuing the first user turn, so the spawn-then-immediate-cancel path remains correct without depending on microtask ordering. The listener is detached in the same per-invocation `finally` that calls `AgentSession.dispose()` (see **Subagent session lifecycle** below). The spawned session inherits the loom's `system:` prompt (from frontmatter, with `${param}` interpolation resolved at conversation-creation time), the lowered `customTools` set described above, and the loom's `model`. Queries against the spawned session use `session.sendUserMessage(text)` on the returned `AgentSession` and await completion by `session.subscribe(event => { if (event.type === "agent_end") … })`, which is scoped to that `AgentSession`'s own `ExtensionRunner` and cannot fire for any other session. The query's `Ok(string)` value is extracted from the `agent_end` event itself — the event-delivered `messages: AgentMessage[]` array on the `agent_end` variant of `AgentSessionEvent` (declared at `dist/core/agent-session.d.ts` in `@earendil-works/pi-coding-agent` at the [loom 1.0 Pi-SDK pin](#pi-sdk-pin); re-validated on each Pi minor bump per [Pi version bump procedure](#pi-version-bump-procedure) below) — and never from the `AgentSession.messages` getter on the session handle. An `agent_end` event whose `willRetry` field is `true` precedes an automatic SDK retry and does not resolve the query: the runtime ignores such an event, keeps the subscription live, and resolves only from the terminal `agent_end` event whose `willRetry` is `false`. The string is then assembled from that terminal event's `messages` array by the same assistant-text rule the prompt-mode driver pins above (the `text` content of the final turn's `assistant` messages, concatenated in chronological order with a single `\n` separator, with the provider-internal `thinking` array and all `toolCalls` entries omitted per the `[assistant]` body selection in [Compact-transcript format](./binder.md#compact-transcript-format-normative) item 4; a final turn with no assistant text yields the empty string), so the "same final-assistant-text rule on both sides" invariant holds. The runtime MUST use the session-local `subscribe` API rather than the global `pi.on("agent_end", …)` event for the same per-session-scoping reason given for prompt mode. The runtime unsubscribes (via the function returned by `subscribe`) before resolving each query's promise so that the next query on the same long-lived subagent session does not observe the previous query's listener; a fresh subscription is attached per query. Typed queries against the spawned session honour the same behavioural contract as prompt-mode typed queries above and use the same mechanism described in [Implementation Notes — Runtime](./implementation-notes.md#runtime). The session is in-memory only — the spec mandates the transcript stays private to the loom and is discarded when the loom returns. The in-memory `SessionManager` is the mechanism that prevents subagent output from reaching Pi's user-facing UI; user-visible behaviour is specified in [Slash-Command Invocation — User-visible streaming](./slash-invocation.md). Each subagent-mode invocation gets its own `AgentSession`, its own captured `tools:` table (the load-time resolution snapshot from [Parameters and Frontmatter](./frontmatter.md)), and its own derived `AbortSignal`; sibling invocations triggered by parallel tool calls do not share mutable session state.

<a id="subagent-state-isolation-matrix"></a>

**Subagent state-isolation matrix.** A subagent-mode invocation runs in an isolated session whose state composition is fixed by the table below. The matrix is the canonical enumeration of what the spawned session inherits from the loom's frontmatter, what is forwarded from the caller's `ExtensionCommandContext`, and what is *not* inherited from the caller. The three columns are populated by distinct mechanisms (frontmatter resolution, the override-table forwarding rule under **`ExtensionContext` (member surface loom touches)** below, and the explicit suppression rules in **Conversation drive — subagent mode** above) and a future widening of any cell is a spec-versioned change.

| Inherited from the loom's frontmatter | Forwarded from the caller's `ExtensionCommandContext` | Not inherited from the caller |
|---|---|---|
| `system:` prompt (with `${param}` interpolation resolved at conversation-creation time) | `ctx.cwd` | caller's transcript (the spawned session uses `SessionManager.inMemory(cwd)`; transcript is private and discarded when the loom returns) |
| `model` (resolved from frontmatter) | `ctx.modelRegistry` | caller's system prompt (suppressed by the loom-constructed `ResourceLoader` adapter passed to `createAgentSession` whose `getSystemPrompt()` returns the resolved-and-interpolated loom frontmatter `system:` and whose `getAppendSystemPrompt()` returns `[]`; see rule 4 under **Conversation drive — subagent mode** above. `CreateAgentSessionOptions` exposes no `systemPrompt` field — delivery via the loader is the only available channel, and passing the parent session's `DefaultResourceLoader` unchanged would silently inherit the host project's `AGENTS.md`-derived prompt) |
| lowered `customTools` set (the loom's *callable set*; see [Glossary — `callable set`](./glossary.md)) | `ctx.getContextUsage` | ambient Pi tool set (suppressed by the explicit `tools` allowlist passed to `createAgentSession`; default rule when `tools:` is absent or empty is owned by [Parameters and Frontmatter — `tools`](./frontmatter.md#tools)) |
| captured `params` (load-time per-invocation values) | other non-overridden `ExtensionContext` members per **`ExtensionContext` (member surface loom touches)** below | caller's `loomAbort` controller (each invocation gets a fresh `AbortController`; lineage and forwarding are owned by **Cancellation source** below and [Cancellation](./cancellation.md)) |
| | | caller's `params` and variable bindings (the subagent runs a different loom file with its own `params`) |
| | | caller's `withActiveTools` snapshot scope (subagent-mode tool registration uses `customTools`, not `pi.setActiveTools`; see **Tool-registration lifetime and visibility** above) |

The `loomAbort` row is the structural reason a subagent-mode child cannot observe its parent's cancellation directly: cancellation forwards via the parent's `loomAbort.abort()` call propagating through a one-shot `loomAbort.signal` listener that calls `AgentSession.abort()` on the spawned `AgentSession`, not via shared controller identity and not via any `createAgentSession` option (no `signal` field exists on `CreateAgentSessionOptions` in the loom 1.0 Pi SDK pin). Nested-subagent cancellation behaviour is owned by [Cancellation — Signal source](./cancellation.md).

The matrix is consumed by `spec.md`'s preamble forward-link and by [Overview — Scope of a Loom File](./overview.md#scope-of-a-loom-file)'s isolation prose.

**Subagent session lifecycle.** The runtime owns the spawned `AgentSession` for exactly the duration of one subagent-mode loom invocation. Disposal is mandatory and runs in a `finally` block that wraps the entire interpreter execution against that session, so it fires on:

- normal return (the loom's tail expression resolves);
- any `Err` returned to the parent (query failure, tool failure, child invoke failure, validation failure, cancellation);
- any panic raised inside the subagent (`MatchError`, index out of bounds, null access — see [Errors and Results](./errors-and-results.md));
- any unexpected exception thrown by the interpreter or the Pi SDK.

Disposal calls `AgentSession.dispose()`, which removes all event listeners (including any in-flight `agent_end` subscription the runtime attached via `session.subscribe(...)` for the current query) and disconnects from the underlying agent. The same `finally` also detaches the one-shot `loomAbort.signal` listener registered at spawn (per **Conversation drive — subagent mode** above) — this is the listener-cleanup obligation [Cancellation — Forwarding into `loomAbort`](./cancellation.md) cites for the subagent-mode entry, and it runs alongside the existing detach of every other forwarding listener the runtime attached during the invocation. `dispose()` is invoked at most once per session and treated as idempotent at the call site: a second call (e.g. defensive cleanup in an outer scope) is a no-op. If `dispose()` itself throws, the runtime logs the disposal error via the `loom/runtime/subagent-dispose-failure` diagnostic (see [Diagnostics](./diagnostics.md)) but does not mask the original error that triggered teardown — the parent still observes the original `Err` or panic.

`AgentSession.abort()` (invoked by the cancellation listener above) returns `Promise<void>` and resolves once the agent has become idle. The runtime does **not** `await` the returned promise from inside the listener — the listener fires synchronously, calls `session.abort()`, and discards the returned promise; teardown progress is observed instead through the `disposeBarrier` and the subsequent `dispose()` call in the per-invocation `finally`. If the synchronous `session.abort()` call throws, or the discarded promise rejects, the runtime traps the error and routes it through `loom/runtime/internal-error` (see [Diagnostics — `loom/runtime/*`](./diagnostics.md)) rather than masking any original error the surrounding `finally` was protecting; this mirrors the `dispose()`-throws rule above. The `session_shutdown` handler's `SHUTDOWN_AWAIT_CAP_MS = 2000` budget covers the entire disposal phase, including any time `AgentSession.abort()`'s underlying idle-wait contributes via the subsequent `dispose()` call — there is no separate budget for `abort()`. The runtime is re-entrancy-safe by construction: the one-shot `loomAbort.signal` listener and the existing one-shot guard on `loomAbort.abort()` together make a double-abort (e.g. operator presses Esc twice) a no-op.

A thrown or rejected `createAgentSession`, or a returned handle whose `dispose` member is not a function, is treated as an unanticipated SDK reject and routed through `loom/runtime/internal-error` (see [Diagnostics — `loom/runtime/*`](./diagnostics.md), whose trigger description explicitly enumerates `createAgentSession` among the unanticipated SDK rejects). The parent invocation observes the routing already specified for `internal-error`: a slash-command surface emits `"loom /<name> aborted with internal error: <message>"` as a system note; an `invoke` parent observes `Err(InvokeInfraError { kind: "invoke_failure", cause: "internal_error", ... })`. No `AgentSession` was constructed, so the **Subagent session lifecycle** `finally` below has nothing to dispose; the registry entry from **`ActiveInvocationRegistry`** is removed by the same `finally` in the normal way.

Subagent-mode tool registration has no separate teardown step: the `.loom` callables and the typed-query one-shot tool reach the model via `customTools` on `createAgentSession`, so they exist only for the lifetime of the spawned `AgentSession` and are released by `dispose()` itself. No `pi.unregisterTool` call is required (or possible — Pi exposes none); see **Tool-registration lifetime and visibility** above for the full rule and the prompt-mode counterpart.

The per-invocation `finally` also settles the `disposeBarrier` promise the runtime registered with the **`ActiveInvocationRegistry`** (see **Extension entry point** step 4 above) and removes the registry entry. This is what lets the `session_shutdown` handler's `Promise.allSettled(...)` await observe completion of an in-flight subagent invocation that was cancelled by step 4's `loomAbort.abort()` call. If Pi tears the runtime down before this `finally` runs (a `/reload` issued mid-turn while the subagent is still talking to its provider), the teardown handler's bounded await is what guarantees `dispose()` is called and provider connections are released; the per-invocation `finally` and the teardown handler are two paths to the same disposal, and `dispose()`'s call-site idempotence (above) is what makes the overlap safe.

Edge cases:

- The `finally` block must run even when the parent's `AbortSignal` (see [Cancellation](./cancellation.md)) fires before the subagent's first turn — i.e. spawn-then-immediate-cancel still requires disposal.
- For nested subagent invocations (a subagent that itself invokes a subagent-mode child), each level owns its own session and runs its own `finally`. Disposal order is deepest-first, naturally produced by the call stack's `finally` unwinding.
- Disposal must precede the parent observing the result — the parent's `match`/`?` arm runs after the child's session is gone, so the child's listeners cannot leak into work the parent does next.

<a id="concurrent-invocation-isolation"></a>**Concurrent-invocation isolation and concurrency disposition.** Concurrent loom invocations within an extension instance — tracked as entries in the **`ActiveInvocationRegistry`** above — carry mode-qualified isolation and a fixed loom 1.0 concurrency disposition. *Transcript and tool-table isolation are subagent-mode-only:* a subagent-mode invocation runs its own private `AgentSession` (per **Conversation drive — subagent mode** above), so transcripts, captured `tools:` tables, and derived `AbortSignal`s are per-invocation and do not leak across siblings, while a prompt-mode invocation drives the user session's transcript by definition. <a id="no-invocation-cap"></a> loom 1.0 imposes no maximum on the number of in-flight loom invocations within an extension instance and no fairness or scheduling rule above Pi's event-loop ordering, interposing no admission cap, priority queue, or scheduler between sibling invocations and the event loop. This disposition is observable at the parallel-tool-call surface (see [Tool Calls — Concurrency](./tool-calls.md#concurrency)): when the model emits N (for any fixed N ≥ 3) subagent-mode `.loom` callables as parallel tool calls in a single assistant turn, the runtime MUST initiate `createAgentSession` for all N invocations before any one of the N returns. A conformance test witnesses the obligation with a fake `AgentSession` whose `sendUserMessage` blocks until explicitly released: a conformant runtime has created all N sessions and entered each session's `sendUserMessage` before any blocked call is released, whereas a runtime that admitted invocations behind a cap, queue, or scheduler would leave at least one session uncreated. The rule constrains the runtime only — Pi's own session-level serialisation (e.g. prompt-mode slash-command turns within one user session, per the [snapshot/restore Pi behavioural preconditions](#snapshot-restore-pi-behavioural-preconditions) above) is upstream and remains in force, and the rule does not promise resource unboundedness. Beyond the absence of an admission cap and scheduler pinned above, the loom adds no per-class threshold and no cross-sibling aggregation, throttling, or storm-detection over the resources concurrent loom invocations consume. Those resources — runtime-value heap (V8 string / array / total-heap allocation), OS-level file descriptors / sockets / child-process slots, and provider-side rate-limit / quota — are owned by the host JavaScript runtime, the host OS, and the LLM provider respectively; their limits and any aggregation over those limits live in those layers, not in the loom contract. The loom observes only the per-call surfacing of those limits through the existing routing it already pins: catchable host throws — the V8 `RangeError` family (`Invalid string length`, `Invalid array length`, `Maximum call stack size exceeded`) per `NOCEIL-3` at [Hard ceilings — No additional loom 1.0 runtime ceiling applies](./hard-ceilings.md#no-additional-ceilings), plus catchable OS-level descriptor / port / child-process-slot exhaustion surfaced as throws by the host JavaScript runtime — route through `loom/runtime/internal-error` per [Errors and Results — Runtime panics](./errors-and-results.md#runtime-panics); per-query provider throttles (HTTP 429 and equivalents) surface as [`TransportError`](./errors-and-results.md#queryerror-variants) on the same page; uncatchable host fatals — V8 heap-limit OOM via the `OOMErrorCallback` / `abort()` path, OS process-kill, and any other engine fatal that bypasses the JavaScript exception machinery — terminate the host process before any wrap can observe them and emit no `loom/runtime/internal-error` diagnostic, on the same footing as any other engine fatal. Widening or narrowing this rule is a major-version concern.

<a id="pic-2"></a> **PIC-2. Prompt-mode sequential execution.** Prompt-mode bodies execute strictly sequentially within a single user session: at most one prompt-mode body — top-level slash dispatches and nested prompt → prompt `invoke(...)` calls alike — holds an open `pi.setActiveTools` snapshot/restore window at a time. This is a *derived* property rather than an independent runtime obligation: it follows from Pi's per-session slash-handler serialisation guarantee (snapshot/restore [behavioural precondition (b)](#snapshot-restore-pi-behavioural-preconditions) above, under which two loom-invocation slash dispatches against the same session cannot overlap their snapshot/restore windows), composed with the loom-runtime-owned guarantees that (i) prompt-mode `.loom` callees in another loom's `tools:` are rejected at load time per [Parameters and Frontmatter — `tools`](./frontmatter.md#tools), (ii) `invoke(...)` to a prompt-mode callee suspends the parent's body until the child returns and loom 1.0 exposes no parallel-`invoke` surface per [Invocation — Cross-mode semantics](./invocation.md), and (iii) the `subagent → prompt` fan-out path into the user session is closed per the same [Invocation — Cross-mode semantics](./invocation.md) rule. The three potential sources of in-session overlap therefore produce genuine concurrency only between subagent-mode invocations, per **Concurrent-invocation isolation and concurrency disposition** above.

**System notes.** Echoes (binder result), `Err`-in-prompt-mode notes, binder failure messages, watcher structural-change notes, and operator-facing runtime events all emit through a single call shape:

```ts
pi.sendMessage(
  { customType: "loom-system-note", content, display, details },
  { triggerTurn: false },
);
```

The `display` and `content` arguments vary per the `details` variant documented below — they are not fixed to `display: true` or to a non-empty string. A `pi.registerMessageRenderer("loom-system-note", renderer)` registered by the loom extension factory formats these as one-line, dim-styled notes in the transcript. The custom-type approach (rather than `ctx.ui.notify(...)`) is chosen because notes need to persist in the session transcript for replay and `/tree` navigation, not just appear transiently.

**Renderer registration (`pi.registerMessageRenderer`).** The pinned signature, lifecycle, and ownership rules below are normative for the loom extension. The canonical Pi-side declarations live at `dist/core/extensions/types.d.ts` in `@earendil-works/pi-coding-agent` (the [loom 1.0 Pi-SDK pin](#pi-sdk-pin) from **Host prerequisites** above) and the `Component` interface lives at `@earendil-works/pi-tui`'s `dist/tui.d.ts`; the inline shapes below are the loom-load-bearing subset and MUST be re-validated against those files on each Pi minor bump (per the re-validating obligation in **Host prerequisites** above).

*Signature.* The Pi-side surface, reproduced verbatim from `dist/core/extensions/types.d.ts`:

```ts
export interface MessageRenderOptions {
  expanded: boolean;
}

export type MessageRenderer<T = unknown> = (
  message: CustomMessage<T>,
  options: MessageRenderOptions,
  theme: Theme,
) => Component | undefined;

// On `pi: ExtensionAPI`:
registerMessageRenderer<T = unknown>(
  customType: string,
  renderer: MessageRenderer<T>,
): void;
```

The call returns `void` (synchronous); the loom extension factory MUST NOT `await` it and MUST NOT attach a `.then`/`.catch`. Failures propagate as synchronous throws and fault the extension factory body — there is no separate Promise rejection path.

The `Component` return type is the `pi-tui` widget interface (`{ render(width: number): string[]; handleInput?(...): void; invalidate(): void; ... }`), **not** a string and **not** a React node. A renderer body of the form `(message) => message.content` is therefore a type error that silently leaves the channel unrendered — the loom renderer MUST construct a `pi-tui` `Component` instance (e.g. a text component composed from the `theme` parameter) and return it. Returning `undefined` is legal and tells Pi to skip rendering this message; the loom 1.0 loom renderer uses `undefined` only when `display === false` (see **Empty `content` is legal** below).

The `theme: Theme` parameter is Pi's active TUI theme; the loom renderer MUST source any styling (dim text colour, etc.) from `theme` rather than hard-coding ANSI escapes, so re-themes propagate without renderer changes.

The `options: MessageRenderOptions` carries `{ expanded: boolean }` from the Pi host; `expanded` is the Pi-host hint for whether the user has requested an expanded view of this message in the transcript. The loom 1.0 loom renderer MUST be defined for both `expanded === false` and `expanded === true`; loom 1.0 MAY render identically in both modes. Widening the renderer to use `expanded` to disclose the structured `details` payload (e.g. expanding the diagnostic batch or runtime-event fields) is reserved for a future revision and is not part of loom 1.0 conformance.

*Lifecycle.*

- **Registration timing.** The loom extension factory MUST call `pi.registerMessageRenderer("loom-system-note", renderer)` synchronously inside the factory body, before the factory returns. Registration after the factory returns (e.g. inside an event subscriber that fires asynchronously) is undefined behaviour at the Pi-SDK level and the loom runtime MUST NOT rely on it.
- **Re-registration within an extension.** Pi's loader stores renderers in a `Map<string, MessageRenderer>` keyed by `customType` (`@earendil-works/pi-coding-agent`'s `dist/core/extensions/loader.js`), so a second call from the same factory with the same `customType` silently overwrites the first; Pi emits no warning. The loom factory MUST register exactly once per factory invocation.
- **Teardown.** Pi exposes no `unregisterMessageRenderer` API. The renderer entry lives for the lifetime of the extension instance; on `ctx.reload()` or any other path that replaces the extension instance, Pi discards the prior `Map` along with the old extension, and the freshly loaded factory registers afresh against a Pi state that has no prior `loom-system-note` registration. The loom runtime MUST NOT attempt to clean up the registration in its `session_shutdown` handler.

*`customType` ownership and collision rule.*

- The literal `"loom-system-note"` is owned by the pi-loom extension. No other extension SHOULD register a renderer for this `customType`.
- Pi does not enforce ownership: collision is a coordination failure between extensions, not a Pi-level error. Pi's runner resolves a `customType` by iterating `this.extensions` in load order and returning the first hit (`@earendil-works/pi-coding-agent`'s `dist/core/extensions/runner.js` `getMessageRenderer`), so when two installed extensions both register `"loom-system-note"` the **first-loaded** extension's renderer wins and the later registration is unreachable. Whether pi-loom or the other extension wins is non-deterministic from loom's point of view (Pi controls extension load order).
- Loom emits no diagnostic for this case in loom 1.0 — ownership is by convention.
- The `customType` naming convention for loom-internal channels is `loom-<purpose>` (kebab-case, `loom-` prefix). Future loom channels MUST follow this convention; other extensions SHOULD NOT use the `loom-` prefix. loom 1.0.0 ships exactly one channel under this prefix (`loom-system-note`).

**Delivery surface.** All three `details` payload variants below emit through the single `pi.sendMessage` call above. The runtime has no second channel for `display: false` notes; they land in the same session transcript as `display: true` notes and are filtered out of visible rendering by the renderer (or by Pi's own `display` handling), but remain available to transcript-replay and `/tree` consumers. *Subagent-mode `display: false` cascades* (the subagent top-level `Err` case noted under **Runtime event channel** below) use the same `pi.sendMessage` call against the spawned `AgentSession` — i.e., they reach `pi.sendMessage` after the per-loom `sessionManager` swap from **Tool execution from loom code** above has routed messaging at the spawned session — so the note lands in the subagent's private transcript, not the parent user session's.

*Custom-message channel persistence and LLM-context entry.* Per `@earendil-works/pi-coding-agent`'s `dist/core/messages.js` `convertToLlm` transformer, every `CustomMessage` (including `loom-system-note`) is converted to `{ role: "user", content }` on every subsequent provider call. `triggerTurn: false` suppresses the immediate turn fire only; it does not exclude the message from the LLM context window. The `display` flag controls renderer behaviour, not serialization. Loom diagnostics therefore enter the user-session model context durably and contribute to `ctx.getContextUsage()` and compaction decisions. Operators authoring looms should expect parse errors, binder failures, panic notes, and always-log runtime events emitted in a session to be visible to subsequent model turns. The [loom 1.0 Pi-SDK pin](#pi-sdk-pin) exposes no `CustomMessage.excludeFromContext` opt-out analogous to `BashExecutionMessage.excludeFromContext`; a future Pi minor that adds such a field would be picked up by the `pi-version-bump-procedure` re-validation gate, at which point the runtime SHOULD set the opt-out on the canonical `sendSystemNote` call.

**Empty `content` is legal.** When the variant prescribes `content: ""` (the `display: false` runtime-event case below), the runtime passes the empty string verbatim. `pi.sendMessage`'s `content` parameter accepts any string per Pi's `CustomMessage<T>` interface; no placeholder substitution is required or permitted. The renderer registered for `loom-system-note` MUST tolerate `content === ""` — in loom 1.0 this only ever co-occurs with `display: false` and `details: { event: RuntimeEvent }`, so the renderer MAY short-circuit on `display === false` without inspecting `content`.

The `details` field carries one of three normative payload shapes, distinguished by which key is present:

- `details: { diagnostics: Diagnostic[] }` — a parse / load / type / runtime-panic diagnostic batch, exactly the shape defined in [Diagnostics](./diagnostics.md). The companion `content` is the serialised `<file>:<line>:<col>: <code>: <message>` line(s) for parse / load / type batches; for the runtime-panic case (a single-element batch carrying a `loom/runtime/*` diagnostic) the companion `content` is the user-facing framing `"loom /<name> aborted: <message>"` (or `"loom /<name> aborted with internal error: <message>"` for `loom/runtime/internal-error`) per [Errors and Results — Runtime panics](./errors-and-results.md). See **Runtime event channel** below for the partition rule that routes panics through this shape rather than `details: { event }`.
- `details: { event: RuntimeEvent }` — a runtime failure event from one of the always-log kinds (see **Runtime event channel** below). The companion `content` is the normative user-facing template from [Slash-Command Invocation — Top-level `Err` in prompt mode](./slash-invocation.md) when `display: true`, or omitted (empty string) when `display: false`.
- `details: { structural: { added: string[]; removed: string[] } }` — informational note for watcher-observed structural changes (added or removed `.loom` files, settings-array changes that add or remove sources); `added` and `removed` carry absolute file paths from the debounce-window batch. Settings-array edits surface as the resolved `.loom` file paths the source change brought in or removed, not the settings-file path itself, so a single settings edit that adds N sources contributes N entries to `added`. The shape is disjoint from the `diagnostics` and `event` shapes by key, per the additive-only convention below. The companion `content` is the verbatim template defined under **Structural changes** above; `display: true` always.

Per-variant `display` / `content` pairings (normative):

| Variant | `display` | `content` |
|---|---|---|
| `details: { diagnostics: Diagnostic[] }`, parse / load / type batch | `true` | serialised `<file>:<line>:<col>: <code>: <message>` line(s) (multi-line for batches) — non-empty |
| `details: { diagnostics: [Diagnostic] }`, runtime panic (single-element batch, `loom/runtime/*` code) | `true` | `"loom /<name> aborted: <message>"` (or `"loom /<name> aborted with internal error: <message>"` for `loom/runtime/internal-error`) per [Errors and Results — Runtime panics](./errors-and-results.md) — non-empty |
| `details: { event: RuntimeEvent }`, top-level cascade in prompt mode | `true` | normative user-facing template per [Slash-Command Invocation — Top-level `Err` in prompt mode](./slash-invocation.md) — non-empty |
| `details: { event: RuntimeEvent }`, author-handled or subagent-mode cascade | `false` | `""` (empty string, verbatim) |
| `details: { structural: { added; removed } }` | `true` | verbatim template from **Structural changes** above — non-empty |

The three `details` shapes are disjoint by key; renderers MUST NOT assume more than one is present. Future payload shapes added to this channel are additive and disjoint by the same convention. Future variants MAY widen the `display: false` + `content: ""` combination to other `details` shapes additively; the renderer's `display === false` short-circuit above remains safe under that widening because it does not inspect `content`.

**Runtime event channel.** A subset of `QueryError` failures — the **always-log set** — emit a structured note through the `loom-system-note` channel exactly once per occurrence, regardless of whether the author matched the `Err`, propagated it via `?`, or discarded it via `let _ =`. The always-log set partitions by routing channel: members in **group A** emit `details: { event: RuntimeEvent }`; members in **group B** emit `details: { diagnostics: Diagnostic[] }`. A given failure emits through exactly one shape — there is no fan-out across the two `details` variants for a single failure.

`display: false` gates only renderer visibility; the underlying `CustomMessage` still enters subsequent provider calls per **Delivery surface** above (Pi's `convertToLlm` transform converts every `CustomMessage` to a `user`-role transcript entry on every subsequent provider call, with no opt-out under the loom 1.0 SDK pin). Operators MUST treat all `loom-system-note` content (regardless of `display`) as durable session-context input.

*Engine-assumption carve-out.* The exactly-once emission guarantee assumes the [Runtime Value Model — JavaScript engine assumptions](./runtime-value-model.md#javascript-engine-assumptions) hold (IEEE-754 numbers, native `Map`/`Set`, native `JSON.stringify`, `Object.is` equality — a non-checked invariant). Under a violation of those assumptions, emission may be silently dropped (e.g. a corrupted `Map` loses the dedup key), duplicated, or skipped entirely (e.g. a `pi.sendMessage` host throw bypasses the helper); some manifestations land on `loom/runtime/internal-error` via the runtime-defect surface in [Errors and Results — Runtime panics](./errors-and-results.md), but silent value corruption has no observable signal. Operators MUST treat a missing terminal event as one of: (a) the loom did not fail; (b) the loom failed with a kind not in the always-log set; (c) an engine-assumption violation. There is no in-band signal that distinguishes (a) from (c).

Group A — `details: { event: RuntimeEvent }`:

- `transport`
- `model_tool`
- `code_tool`
- `tool_loop_exhausted`
- `invoke_failure`
- Binder failures (every row of [Binder — Failure modes](./binder.md), including `needs_info`, `ambiguous`, malformed envelope, AJV validation, transport, cancellation)

Group B — `details: { diagnostics: Diagnostic[] }`:

- Runtime panics — every row of [Diagnostics — `loom/runtime/*`](./diagnostics.md) plus the four console.error-routed teardown-handler `loom/host/session-shutdown-*` codes enumerated in the exclusion list below, routed through the `details: { diagnostics: [...] }` shape per the panic-emission rule under **Deduplication and lifetime rules** below, with five console.error-routed teardown-handler exclusions: `loom/runtime/reload-teardown-timeout`, `loom/host/session-shutdown-reason-unknown`, `loom/host/session-shutdown-pinned-constant-unreadable`, `loom/host/session-shutdown-teardown-step-failed`, and `loom/host/session-shutdown-runtime-degraded` (per the **Edge cases** bullet under **Extension entry point** sub-step 4 above and the **Persistent diagnostics** paragraph in [Diagnostics](./diagnostics.md)). A new diagnostic added to either of those sinks MUST be added to this exclusion list in the same edit. The `RuntimeEvent` payload shape and the `(kind, query_site, message, occurred_at)` dedup key defined below apply to group A only and have no analogue for group B.

`validation`, `context_overflow`, `cancelled`, and `invoke_callee_error` are deliberately **not** in the always-log set: `validation` is a query-internal repair signal whose final outcome is what matters (the `attempts` field on the eventual terminal event captures the count); `context_overflow` and `cancelled` are user/operator-initiated and self-explanatory in context; `invoke_callee_error` wraps an inner `Err` whose origin already emitted its own runtime event at the originating site.

*Discard-site disposition.* The four excluded kinds emit nothing on this channel even at a discard site (`let _ = @"…"`, `void`-tail-expression discard, or any other disposition that drops the `Err`). The exclusion rationale survives the discard case for each kind: for `validation`, a discarded validation failure is by construction a programming error — the author wrote `let _ = @<Schema>\`…\`` and ignored the schema mismatch; the diagnostic at the originating site (when one fires — depth-5 violations and respond-repair failures both have `loom/runtime/*` codes available) plus the absence of any user-visible outcome is the intended signal. For `cancelled`, the author's choice to discard a user/operator-initiated outcome is itself the disposition. For `context_overflow`, the author's choice to discard a model-state outcome is itself the disposition. For `invoke_callee_error`, the inner `Err`'s origin-site emission is unchanged by the wrapper's disposition. The symmetric statement on the consumer side is owned by [Query — Observability of discarded results](./query.md).

<a id="success-side-null-policy"></a>*Success-side null-policy.* A loom terminating with `Ok(v)` — including the case where a child loom's `Ok(v)` flows to its `invoke` parent per [Invocation — Final-value propagation across callees](./invocation.md#final-value-propagation) — emits no `loom-system-note` keyed on the `Ok(v)` outcome. This follows by construction from the always-log set above, whose members are all `QueryError` kinds (group A) or runtime panics (group B); an `Ok(v)` termination is neither, so no always-log entry has a satisfied emission predicate for it. Earlier mid-run emissions on the same channel — always-log members raised inside the loom body before its terminating expression — are governed by the **Runtime event channel** paragraph above and are unaffected; this paragraph adds no new emission predicate and removes none. The operator-observable surfaces on the success side are mode-dependent: in prompt mode the driven conversation per [Slash-Command Invocation](./slash-invocation.md) is the user-facing surface (any value the author wants the user to see should be issued by the author as a final query), and the `Ok(v)` return value reaches a programmatic caller only when one exists (none on a user-typed slash dispatch; an `invoke` parent otherwise); in subagent mode there is no user-facing surface for the terminating value (the intermediate subagent transcript stays private per [Slash-Command Invocation — User-visible streaming](./slash-invocation.md)), and the `Ok(v)` return value reaches a programmatic caller only when one exists (none on a user-typed slash dispatch; an `invoke` parent otherwise, per [Invocation — Final-value propagation across callees](./invocation.md#final-value-propagation)). The two pre-evaluation surfaces — the binder echo on `bind_echo: true` per [Slash-Command Argument Binding](./binder.md) and the no-params overflow note per [Slash-Command Invocation — No-params overflow](./slash-invocation.md) — emit before the loom's terminating expression evaluates and are unaffected by this paragraph regardless of the run's outcome.

The `RuntimeEvent` payload shape is normative and additive-only:

```ts
type RuntimeEvent = {
```
