```ts
  kind: string;                       // QueryError.kind, the binder failure cause, or the loom/runtime/* code for panics
  code?: string;                      // diagnostic code when one applies (loom/runtime/*, loom/load/*, etc.)
  loom: string;                       // slash name of the loom that owned the failure ("/code-review")
  invocation_id: string;              // per-invocation UUID sourced from the ActiveInvocationRegistry entry's `invocationId` field (canonical lowercase 8-4-4-4-12 hex form per §7 of Diagnostics); distinguishes concurrent sibling invocations of the same loom on operator-visible surfaces
  query_site?: { file: string; line: number; column: number }; // source location of the @-template, tool call, invoke, or discarding `let _ =`; absent for binder failures (the binder runs before any loom code)
  message: string;                    // the same message string surfaced through the user-facing template (or the panic message template, for panics that take the diagnostic shape)
  attempts?: number;                  // populated for `validation` events on respond-repair exhaustion; absent otherwise
  tokens_used?: number;               // populated for `context_overflow` events when the provider supplies the count; absent otherwise
  masked?: string[];                  // hard-ceiling co-fire enumeration; see "Hard-ceiling co-fire" below
  occurred_at: number;                // Unix epoch ms, stamped at the originating emission site via Clock.now()
};
```

The channel is operator-facing: events emit with `display: false` when the author handled the `Err` (matched, discarded with `let _ =`, or propagated via `?` to a non-top-level frame that itself handled it), and with `display: true` when the failure cascades out of the slash-command boundary as a top-level `Err` in prompt mode (in which case the `content` carries the normative user-facing template per [Slash-Command Invocation](./slash-invocation.md)). Subagent-mode top-level `Err` cascades likewise emit with `display: false` (the subagent transcript is private; see [Slash-Command Invocation — User-visible streaming](./slash-invocation.md)).

Deduplication and lifetime rules:

- A `?`-propagation chain emits exactly once at the originating site, not at each rethrow. A failure that is created at site A, propagated through frames B and C via `?`, and finally cascades out as a top-level `Err` at frame D produces one runtime event (origin: A) plus the user-facing top-level note at D when `display: true` applies; both share the same `RuntimeEvent` payload. The runtime emits the same `RuntimeEvent` payload at most twice per origin: once at the originating site (always), and once again at the boundary as the `details: { event }` payload of the user-facing top-level note when a cascade applies. Both emissions are byte-identical including `occurred_at`. Consumers that aggregate the event stream may therefore deduplicate on `(kind, query_site, message, occurred_at)` to collapse the cascade twin; this is a non-normative consumer concern and not part of loom 1.0 conformance. Re-emissions for symmetry MUST copy the originating `RuntimeEvent` instance verbatim — including `occurred_at` — rather than re-stamping. Two emissions from the same `query_site` with the same `kind` and `message` but distinct `occurred_at` values represent two distinct occurrences.
- Respond-repair attempts on a typed query (see [Query — Schema-validation respond-repair](./query.md)) do not emit per-failed-attempt events. Only the terminal outcome of the query is observable as a runtime event — either a `validation` event with `attempts` set to the exhausted count (when respond-repair runs out), or a non-validation event from the always-log set (when a respond-repair follow-up itself fails for a transport / tool / cancellation / overflow reason and propagates per [Query — Non-validation failures during a respond-repair follow-up](./query.md)).
- A panic emits exactly one `loom-system-note` per top-level panic with `details: { diagnostics: [Diagnostic] }` carrying a single `loom/runtime/*` diagnostic (message per the registered template in [Diagnostics](./diagnostics.md)). The companion `content` field on that same note carries the user-facing framing `"loom /<name> aborted: <message>"` (or `"loom /<name> aborted with internal error: <message>"` for `loom/runtime/internal-error`) per [Errors and Results — Runtime panics](./errors-and-results.md), where `<message>` is the registered diagnostic message template. The diagnostic-shape `details` and the `aborted:` framing in `content` are the **same** emission, not two notes; there is no separate `details: { event }` emission for panics, and the cascade-twin dedup key above does not apply to group B. The fallback chain to `ctx.ui.notify` and `loom/runtime/system-note-delivery-failed` (defined below) still applies if `pi.sendMessage` throws on the panic note; the fallback's diagnostic emission is independent of the panic note and not subject to any dedup key.
- Tool-host emission ownership: when a Pi tool that the loom invoked (either code-side via `<name>(args)` or model-side inside a query's tool-call loop) emits its own diagnostics, those are independent of the loom-runtime event. The loom runtime owns `code_tool` and `model_tool` events; the tool host owns whatever it emits internally. Renderers MUST NOT cross-correlate the two.

Aggregation, latency histograms, per-loom token reports, retention policies, and a consumer-facing read API for the event stream are deferred to [Future Considerations](./future-considerations.md). loom 1.0 ships the always-log set and the payload shape only; the channel is intentionally write-only at the spec level, with downstream consumers free to read from Pi's session transcript via existing surfaces.

<a id="pic-1"></a> **PIC-1. Hard-ceiling co-fire (`masked`).** The optional `masked` field on `RuntimeEvent` (and on the `Diagnostic` shape per [Diagnostics — `masked` field](./diagnostics.md#masked-field-hard-ceiling-co-fire)) carries the hard-ceiling co-fire enumeration. This rule is the normative owner of the per-site reachable mask domain, the V1 reachable predicate, the pure-read MUST, the verbatim-copy obligation, and the dedup-key non-inclusion rule; the four-ceiling list, the ordering rules CIO-1…CIO-6, and the wire-location split are owned by [Hard Runtime Ceilings — `masked` field](./hard-ceilings.md#masked-field) and [Hard Runtime Ceilings — Interaction between ceilings](./hard-ceilings.md#ceiling-interaction-order).

*(a) Closed identifier set.* Each `masked` entry is one of the four string identifiers `"ceiling#1"`, `"ceiling#2"`, `"ceiling#3"`, `"ceiling#4"`, naming a sibling hard ceiling whose precondition was *also* satisfied at the same check site at the moment the surfaced ceiling fired.

*(b) Canonical-absence rule.* The field is **omitted** when no co-fire occurred; implementations MUST NOT emit `masked: []`. A consumer reading `RuntimeEvent` (or a `Diagnostic`) and finding the property absent MUST treat it as identical to absence — there is no tri-state.

*(c) Co-fire-eligible surfaces and per-site reachable mask domain.* `masked` is populated only on runtime events whose `kind` is one of the runtime-class hard-ceiling surfaces — in V1 this is (i) the `validation` event when its `cause` is `"schema_validation"` (ceiling #4 surface at the typed-query response / model-driven `tool_use` args / `params` validation / `invoke<T>` return value boundary, per CIO-3 in [Hard Runtime Ceilings](./hard-ceilings.md#ceiling-interaction-order)), (ii) the `code_tool` event when its underlying `CodeToolError.cause` is `"validation"` and the `validation_errors[].schema_keyword` is `"maxDepth"` (ceiling #4 surface at the code-driven `<name>(args)` args boundary per CIO-3 — the fifth row of ceiling #4's per-boundary table), and (iii) the `tool_loop_exhausted` event (ceiling #2 surface at the tool-call-round boundary). The diagnostic-shape co-fire-eligible surface is the `loom/runtime/invoke-depth-exceeded` panic per [Diagnostics](./diagnostics.md). The per-site reachable mask domain in V1 is:

| Surfacing site | Surfaced ceiling | Reachable mask domain |
|---|---|---|
| Typed-query response / model-driven `tool_use` args / `params` validation / `invoke<T>` return value AJV boundary (CIO-3) | ceiling #4 | `{ceiling#2}` (only on the typed-query response branch and only when the *V1 reachable predicate* below holds; empty on the other three sub-rows of this AJV boundary because no `tool_loop` slot has been incremented yet for the surfacing event's frame) |
| Code-driven `<name>(args)` AJV boundary (CIO-3, fifth row of ceiling #4's per-boundary table) | ceiling #4 | empty (the call site is not inside a tool-call-round counter context, so ceiling #2's slot accounting is not reachable; ceilings #1 and #3 are unreachable per CIO-1 / CIO-2 / CIO-5) |
| `invoke` entry (CIO-2) | ceiling #1 | empty (the callee body has not yet run, so neither #4's depth-walk nor #2's tool-call round slot accounting has been reached for this frame) |
| Tool-call-round boundary (CIO-4) | ceiling #2 | empty (ceiling #4's depth-walk runs at every AJV boundary earlier in the round per CIO-3, so any depth-6 payload would have already surfaced #4 and short-circuited the round before #2's slot accounting) |
| Slash-load `params` AJV (ceiling #3, load-time) | ceiling #3 | empty (ceiling #3's load-time surfaces always omit `masked` by construction. The slash-load `params` cross-ceiling sub-case — where ceiling #4's depth-walk *did* fire at the [post-default-merge AJV validation](./binder.md#post-default-merge-ajv-validation) hook before being routed to ceiling #3's AJV-on-`args` arm per CIO-1 and the per-boundary table at [Hard Runtime Ceilings — Per-boundary destination/surface table](./hard-ceilings.md#ceiling-4-table) — still omits `masked`: the originating ceiling is recoverable from the rendered note's `<ajv-summary>` placeholder (which names `maxDepth` and the canonical depth-violation message) per [Slash-Command Argument Binding — Failure-mode templates](./binder.md#failure-mode-templates-normative)) |

In loom 1.0 the only non-empty reachable mask is therefore `["ceiling#2"]`, reachable only on the `validation` event at the typed-query response sub-row of CIO-3's AJV boundary. Every other co-fire-eligible surface MUST omit `masked`.

*(d) V1 reachable predicate (the only co-fire that fires in V1).* On a `validation` event with `cause: "schema_validation"` raised at the typed-query response boundary, `masked` carries `["ceiling#2"]` *if and only if* the surfaced event was raised on a forced respond turn whose origin round, after CIO-4's slot increment for the just-completed free-phase round, leaves the `tool_loop` slot count equal to `max_rounds` (i.e. the forced respond turn is the final permitted slot). In every other event — including a respond-repair follow-up's depth-6 forced respond turn (each follow-up gets a fresh `tool_loop` budget per [Query — Tool-call loop bound](./query.md#tool-call-loop-bound), so the predicate is evaluated against the follow-up's own slot count, not the parent query's), a typed query with `max_rounds: 0` (the model gets an empty tool-set during the free phase, so the forced respond turn is the *only* turn and the predicate is unreachable; `masked` is always omitted), and any non-typed-query-response site — `masked` is omitted. The predicate collapses to two scalar reads: the post-increment `tool_loop` slot count and the surfacing turn kind (forced-respond vs. free-phase). Both scalars are state the two-phase tool-loop driver already maintains.

*(e) Pure-read MUST.* Detection at the surfaced site MUST be a pure read of the sibling preconditions: evaluating the predicate above MUST NOT advance the `tool_loop` counter, mutate round bookkeeping, re-invoke ceiling #4's depth-walk, or trip a second emission. Implementations MAY cache the two scalars at the moment the surfacing event is constructed; they MUST NOT re-derive them by re-running ceiling-checking code paths.

*(f) Verbatim-copy obligation on cascade-twin re-emission.* The cascade-twin re-emission rule under **Deduplication and lifetime rules** above (a `?`-propagation chain that cascades to a top-level boundary emits the originating `RuntimeEvent` payload twice — once at the origin, once at the boundary) MUST copy the originating instance verbatim including `masked`. Re-deriving `masked` at the boundary site is forbidden — the originating site is the only authoritative source, and the boundary site has no access to the per-frame scalars the predicate above reads.

*(g) Dedup-key non-inclusion rule.* The dedup tuple under **Deduplication and lifetime rules** above is `(kind, query_site, message, occurred_at)`; consumers MUST NOT include `masked` in the dedup tuple. Two emissions that differ only in `masked` represent the same origin and a malformed re-emission, not two distinct occurrences.

The wire location of `masked` (`details.event.masked` for runtime-event surfaces, `details.masked` for diagnostic-shape surfaces) is owned by [Hard Runtime Ceilings — `masked` field](./hard-ceilings.md#masked-field). A worked example exhibiting a non-empty `masked` payload is at [Query — Tool-call loop bound, *Worked example: depth-6 forced respond at `max_rounds`*](./query.md#tool-call-loop-bound).

The `pi.sendMessage` call for `loom-system-note` is treated as best-effort. `pi.sendMessage` returns `void` (synchronous); the runtime MUST NOT `await` it and MUST NOT attach a `.catch` handler. The best-effort fallback below covers synchronous throws only. If it throws, the runtime falls back in this order:

1. `ctx.ui.notify(content, "error")` — a transient surface so the user still sees the message in the current session, even if it does not persist in the transcript. **Skipped when `display: false`**: notifying the user transiently about an event whose author handled the underlying `Err` (or a subagent-private cascade) defeats the purpose of `display: false`; the fallback proceeds straight to step 2. This step is also skipped when the original note's `content` is `""`, since `ctx.ui.notify("", "error")` carries no signal — but in loom 1.0 this case is fully covered by the `display: false` skip rule above (the only `content: ""` variant is the `display: false` runtime-event case).
2. A `loom/runtime/system-note-delivery-failed` diagnostic emitted through the standard diagnostics channel (see [Diagnostics](./diagnostics.md)), with `message` set to the original note's `content` (which MAY be `""`) and `hint` set to the underlying `sendMessage` error's message. This diagnostic is itself best-effort: if both channels fail, the failure is logged to `console.error` and execution continues.

The fallback path is taken on any thrown value from `sendMessage`; it does not retry the original call. The fallback never aborts the slash-command handler or the spawned subagent session. Implementers must guard against re-entry: if a future `loom/runtime/*` handler ever routes diagnostics back through `loom-system-note`, the diagnostic step in this fallback MUST NOT re-invoke `pi.sendMessage`. `ctx.ui.notify` itself can throw (e.g. in print mode where Pi's UI is not attached); wrap it in the same try/catch and proceed to the diagnostic step. For panic-routed notes, the original panic message MUST be included in the final-resort `console.error` log so post-mortem debugging retains the stack.

**`estimateTokens` (named export).** Imported from `@earendil-works/pi-coding-agent`. Signature: `estimateTokens(message: AgentMessage): number`. The export is declared at `dist/core/compaction/compaction.d.ts` in `@earendil-works/pi-coding-agent` (the [loom 1.0 Pi-SDK pin](#pi-sdk-pin) from **Host prerequisites** above), where its parameter type `AgentMessage` is imported from `@earendil-works/pi-agent-core` (declared at that package's `dist/types.d.ts` as the agent-state superset of the LLM-side `Message` wire type — `AgentMessage` additionally carries `thinking` blocks, `toolCall` blocks, and host-defined custom messages, which the formula below sums over). loom 1.0 behaviour: a conservative `Math.ceil(chars / 4)`, where `chars` is the sum of `String.prototype.length` (UTF-16 code units, as defined by ECMA-262) taken over each contributing string in the message: text-block content, assistant `thinking`-block content, `toolCall.name`, `JSON.stringify(toolCall.arguments)` (with no `replacer` and no `space`, so two engines agree on the input string before `.length` is taken), and tool-result text content. Astral code points (U+10000 and above) therefore count as 2; lone surrogate halves count as 1; no normalisation, escaping, or special handling is applied. Non-text content blocks (e.g. images) follow Pi's own accounting in `@earendil-works/pi-coding-agent` rather than being re-specified here, since the `AgentMessage` shape is owned by Pi. *Reference vector (normative).* A user message whose only content is the text `"😀😀😀"` (three U+1F600, six UTF-16 code units) MUST estimate to `Math.ceil(6 / 4) = 2` tokens. *Pi parity (advisory).* The unit and formula match Pi's own compaction-decision estimator in `@earendil-works/pi-coding-agent`'s `core/compaction/compaction.ts`, which is why this unit was chosen — binder truncation behaviour stays consistent with Pi as model tokenizers evolve — but the normative requirement is the unit and formula above, not parity with any particular Pi revision. Used by [Slash-Command Argument Binding — Session-context truncation](./binder.md#session-context-truncation-bind_context-session) for per-message and per-turn token counts.

**`buildSessionContext` (named export).** Imported from `@earendil-works/pi-coding-agent`; this is a free function, **not** a method on `ctx.sessionManager` — `ExtensionContext.sessionManager` is typed as `ReadonlySessionManager` (a `Pick<>` of the underlying `SessionManager`; see the inline shape below) and deliberately excludes `buildSessionContext` and every mutating member. Signature: `buildSessionContext(entries: SessionEntry[], leafId?: string | null, byId?: Map<string, SessionEntry>): SessionContext`. The runtime calls it as `buildSessionContext(ctx.sessionManager.getEntries(), ctx.sessionManager.getLeafId())` — both `getEntries()` and `getLeafId()` are inside the `ReadonlySessionManager` `Pick<>`, so the call composes against the read-only surface in both prompt mode and subagent mode. The returned `SessionContext`'s `.messages` field is the ordered message list the runtime consumes for session-aware features; its element type is `AgentMessage[]`, pinned in [`SessionContext` and the `.messages` element shape](#sessioncontext-shape) below. loom 1.0 callsite: [Slash-Command Argument Binding — Session-context truncation](./binder.md#session-context-truncation-bind_context-session) sources the binder's caller-session message list from `buildSessionContext(ctx.sessionManager.getEntries(), ctx.sessionManager.getLeafId()).messages`. The runtime MUST NOT substitute `ctx.getContextUsage()` for per-turn token accounting; that API reports aggregate session usage, not per-turn counts, and is reserved for compaction triggers and footer rendering.

<a id="sessioncontext-shape"></a>

**`SessionContext` and the `.messages` element shape (loom-load-bearing subset).** `SessionContext` is declared at `dist/core/session-manager.d.ts` in `@earendil-works/pi-coding-agent` (the [loom 1.0 Pi-SDK pin](#pi-sdk-pin)); its `.messages` field is typed `AgentMessage[]`, where `AgentMessage` is the agent-state superset cited in the **`estimateTokens` (named export)** paragraph above (declared at `@earendil-works/pi-agent-core`'s `dist/types.d.ts`). The compact-transcript renderer at [Slash-Command Argument Binding — Compact-transcript format](./binder.md#compact-transcript-format-normative) is total over the `AgentMessage` arms listed below. The arms and their fields are owned by Pi; the list below is the loom-load-bearing subset the renderer reads (loom redefines none of these types and treats every field not listed here as opaque), and MUST be re-validated against the cited declarations on each Pi minor bump per [Pi version bump procedure](#pi-version-bump-procedure):

- `UserMessage` (declared at `@earendil-works/pi-ai`'s `dist/types.d.ts`) — its text content is read for the `[user]` body.
- `AssistantMessage` (declared at `@earendil-works/pi-ai`'s `dist/types.d.ts`) — its `content` is a `(TextContent | ThinkingContent | ToolCall)[]` array. The renderer concatenates each `TextContent.text` in array order, omits every `ThinkingContent`, and emits one `[tool-call …]` line per `ToolCall` (reading `ToolCall.name` and `ToolCall.arguments`). `TextContent`, `ThinkingContent`, and `ToolCall` are declared in the same `@earendil-works/pi-ai` `dist/types.d.ts`.
- `ToolResultMessage` (declared at `@earendil-works/pi-ai`'s `dist/types.d.ts`) — its `content` is a typed-block array; the renderer reads the text-block content for the `[tool]` body.
- `CustomMessage` (declared at `@earendil-works/pi-coding-agent`'s `dist/core/messages.d.ts`) — its `customType` (a string) supplies the `[custom:<type>]` tag and its `content` (a `string | (TextContent | ImageContent)[]` union) supplies the body.

<a id="extensioncontext-interface"></a>

**`ExtensionContext` (member surface loom touches).** The runtime touches exactly the members enumerated in the signature block below; every other member of Pi's `ExtensionContext` is non-load-bearing for loom 1.0 and may be added or revised by Pi without spec changes. The canonical Pi-side declaration lives at `dist/core/extensions/types.d.ts` in `@earendil-works/pi-coding-agent` (the [loom 1.0 Pi-SDK pin](#pi-sdk-pin) from **Host prerequisites** above); the inline shape below is the loom-load-bearing subset and MUST be re-validated against that file on each Pi minor bump:

```ts
interface ExtensionContext {
  cwd: string;                                          // working directory of the host Pi session
  signal: AbortSignal | undefined;                       // Pi-supplied turn signal; `undefined` in idle / non-turn contexts (see **Cancellation source** below)
  sessionManager: ReadonlySessionManager;                // host's session manager exposed as a read-only `Pick<SessionManager, …>` (members `getCwd | getSessionDir | getSessionId | getSessionFile | getLeafId | getLeafEntry | getEntry | getLabel | getBranch | getHeader | getEntries | getTree | getSessionName`); kept in lock-step with `dist/core/session-manager.d.ts`'s `ReadonlySessionManager` `Pick<>` and re-validated on each Pi minor bump. Subagent mode swaps the underlying object to the loom's spawned in-memory `SessionManager` (see per-mode override table below) but the static type narrows to the same `ReadonlySessionManager` surface in both modes — loom code MUST NOT capture the wider `SessionManager` instance in a parallel closure to bypass this contract. The free `buildSessionContext` named export (see above) is the supported way to obtain a `SessionContext` off the read-only surface.
  modelRegistry: ModelRegistry;                          // resolves a model to a `Model<Api>`; consumed by the binder pass and by binder-model resolution (see [model-registry surface](#model-registry-pin) below)
  model: Model<any> | undefined;                         // host's currently-selected model; `undefined` arm reachable when no model is yet selected — loom never relies on the value being defined
  ui: ExtensionUIContext;                                // transient toast surface; the only member loom calls is `ui.notify(message: string, kind: "info" | "warning" | "error"): void` (synchronous, may throw — wrap in try/catch when called from the **System notes** fallback chain)
  isIdle(): boolean;                                     // true iff the host session has no in-flight turn; loom consults this only to choose between `pi.sendUserMessage` shapes (see **Conversation drive — prompt mode** above)
  abort(): void;                                         // documented by Pi as "abort the current agent operation"; **the loom runtime wraps this** — see override table below
  getContextUsage(): ContextUsage | undefined;           // aggregate session-level usage; `undefined` arm is the "not yet computable" sentinel (no throw); loom MUST NOT substitute this for per-turn token accounting (see `buildSessionContext` above)
  hasPendingMessages(): boolean;                          // observed by the slash-command handler's pre-turn idle probe; not consumed elsewhere in the loom runtime
  compact(options?: CompactOptions): void;               // host-driven compaction trigger; not invoked by loom in loom 1.0 (`await ctx.compact()` is a type-safe no-op — `await void` resolves immediately and the completion signal is silently lost); completion / failure observed via `options.onComplete(result: CompactionResult)` / `options.onError(err: Error)`; forwarded unchanged in both modes, listed here so the touched-surface inventory is exhaustive
  shutdown(): void;                                      // documented by Pi for in-process shutdown; not invoked by loom in loom 1.0
  getSystemPrompt(): string;                             // host's effective system prompt; not consumed by loom in loom 1.0
}
```

`CompactOptions` and `CompactionResult` (referenced by the `compact` row above) are declared in `dist/core/extensions/types.d.ts` and `dist/core/compaction/compaction.d.ts` respectively in `@earendil-works/pi-coding-agent` (the [loom 1.0 Pi-SDK pin](#pi-sdk-pin) from **Host prerequisites** above) as `CompactOptions = { customInstructions?: string; onComplete?: (result: CompactionResult) => void; onError?: (error: Error) => void }`; `CompactionResult` is the host-defined result payload threaded through `onComplete`. Loom does not construct either value in loom 1.0 — both are listed only so the touched-surface inventory is closed against the cited declarations and re-validated on each Pi minor bump per [Pi version bump procedure](#pi-version-bump-procedure) below.

<a id="model-registry-pin"></a>

**`ModelRegistry`, `Model`, and the `Api` type parameter.** `ModelRegistry` (the declared type of the `modelRegistry` row above) is declared at `dist/core/model-registry.d.ts` in `@earendil-works/pi-coding-agent` (the [loom 1.0 Pi-SDK pin](#pi-sdk-pin) from **Host prerequisites** above); the runtime consumes its model-enumeration member `getAvailable()` for binder-model resolution. `Model` and its `Api` type parameter are declared in the sibling package `@earendil-works/pi-ai` and re-exported through the registry surface above. `Model<any>` (the `model` row above) and `Model<Api>` (the form the registry's model-enumeration members return) are the same `Model<T>` type from `@earendil-works/pi-ai` instantiated at different type arguments: `model: Model<any>` is the host's currently-selected model typed loosely, while the resolved binder model is a `Model<Api>` carrying the resolved provider's `Api` union. The configured-binder-string parse helper `findExactModelReferenceMatch` is declared at `dist/core/model-resolver.d.ts` in the same package and is consumed by [Slash-Command Argument Binding — binder-model parse rule](./binder.md#binder-model-parse-rule). All four declarations are loom-load-bearing and MUST be re-validated against the cited files on each Pi minor bump per [Pi version bump procedure](#pi-version-bump-procedure) below.

Members loom does not touch (e.g. `reload()`, `newSession()`, `fork()`, `switchSession()`) are deliberately omitted; their absence from this table is normative — the loom runtime MUST NOT call them in loom 1.0, and a future widening is a spec-versioned change. `waitForIdle()` is intentionally absent: it is a member of `ExtensionCommandContext` (the per-handler subtype that extends `ExtensionContext`; see **`ExtensionCommandContext` (per-handler subtype loom touches)** below), not of `ExtensionContext` itself, and is consulted only on the captured slash-command handler context (see **Conversation drive — prompt mode** above), never on the synthesised tool-execution `ctx`.

<a id="extensioncommandcontext-interface"></a>

**`ExtensionCommandContext` (per-handler subtype loom touches).** `ExtensionCommandContext` is the per-handler subtype Pi passes to a slash-command `handler`; it is declared at `dist/core/extensions/types.d.ts` in `@earendil-works/pi-coding-agent` (the [loom 1.0 Pi-SDK pin](#pi-sdk-pin) from **Host prerequisites** above) as `interface ExtensionCommandContext extends ExtensionContext { … }`, so it inherits every member of the `ExtensionContext` signature block above. The runtime touches exactly the additional members enumerated below; every other `ExtensionCommandContext`-only member is non-load-bearing for loom 1.0 and the loom runtime MUST NOT call it. The inline shape below is the loom-load-bearing subset and MUST be re-validated against the cited file on each Pi minor bump per [Pi version bump procedure](#pi-version-bump-procedure) below; a Pi minor that renames or moves the type, or removes any member loom touches, surfaces at the SDK surface-inventory test before the spec contract drifts.

```ts
interface ExtensionCommandContext extends ExtensionContext {
  waitForIdle(): Promise<void>;                          // resolves once Pi emits `agent_end` for the user session and every awaited `agent_end` listener settles; never rejects (see **Conversation drive — prompt mode** above)
  // Members loom MUST NOT touch in loom 1.0: newSession, fork, navigateTree, switchSession, ReplacedSessionContext, …
}
```

Members loom MUST NOT touch in loom 1.0 (e.g. `newSession()`, `fork()`, `navigateTree()`, `switchSession()`, the `ReplacedSessionContext` surface) are deliberately omitted from the inline shape; their absence from this table is normative — the loom runtime MUST NOT call them in loom 1.0, and a future widening (the deferred *Mid-loom user-session replacement* extension in [Future Considerations](./future-considerations.md#mid-loom-user-session-replacement) is the only loom 1.0 surface that anticipates such use) is a spec-versioned change. The `waitForIdle()` member is the only `ExtensionCommandContext`-only member loom touches in loom 1.0; it is consulted on the captured slash-command handler context only (the `ExtensionCommandContext` Pi passes to the loom's slash-command `handler`), never on the synthesised tool-execution `ctx` from the **`ExtensionContext`** section above (which is typed as the wider `ExtensionContext` and does not expose `waitForIdle`).

*Per-mode override semantics.* The runtime synthesises the `ctx` it hands to `tool.execute(...)` by starting from the live host's `ExtensionContext` and overriding exactly three members. The overrides apply uniformly in both modes — there is no member that is overridden in one mode and forwarded unchanged in the other:

| Member | Prompt mode | Subagent mode |
|---|---|---|
| `signal` | replaced with `loomAbort.signal` (always defined) | replaced with `loomAbort.signal` (always defined) |
| `sessionManager` | replaced with Pi's user-session manager (the host's, observed via the captured `ExtensionCommandContext`) | replaced with the loom's spawned in-memory `SessionManager` (the one passed to `createAgentSession({ sessionManager })` per **Conversation drive — subagent mode** above) |
| `abort` | wrapped to call `loomAbort.abort()` rather than the host's `abort()` — so `ctx.abort()` tears down the loom's invocation, not the user's whole Pi turn; a throw from the underlying `loomAbort.abort()` invoked by the wrapper is trapped per the [Cancellation — Forwarding-listener throw](./cancellation.md) clause and routed through `loom/runtime/internal-error` | wrapped identically — `ctx.abort()` tears down the subagent invocation, not the parent's turn; the same forwarding-listener-throw trap applies |

Every other member from the signature block above forwards unchanged to the live host:

- *Prompt mode.* The live host is the `ExtensionCommandContext` passed to the slash-command handler, retained for the loom's lifetime. `cwd`, `ui`, `modelRegistry`, `model`, `isIdle`, `getContextUsage`, `hasPendingMessages`, `compact`, `shutdown`, and `getSystemPrompt` all reflect the user-session view at the moment of the tool call.
- *Subagent mode.* The spawned `AgentSession` does not carry an `ExtensionCommandContext`; the runtime forwards the parent slash-command handler's `ExtensionCommandContext` for the non-overridden members (so `model`, `modelRegistry`, `cwd`, `getContextUsage`, etc. reflect the parent's view, not a per-subagent one). The `cwd` value is the parent's `ctx.cwd` verbatim — loom 1.0 has no per-subagent frontmatter `cwd` override; widening is reserved for [Future Considerations](./future-considerations.md).

The `abort()` override applies in **both** modes because no spec-supported caller of `ctx.abort()` from inside loom code wants to tear down the user's turn — the in-loom code paths that call `abort()` are tools acting on behalf of the loom, whose authoritative cancellation signal is `loomAbort`. The contract pinned by this paragraph ("`ctx.abort()` aborts the loom's invocation and not the parent's turn") under the spec's "Tool execution from loom code" surface holds in both prompt and subagent modes.

<a id="tool-execution-from-loom-code"></a>

**Tool execution from loom code.** Code-side `<name>(args)` calls invoke the Pi tool's `execute(toolCallId, params, signal, onUpdate, ctx)` directly:

- `toolCallId` is a synthesised UUID prefixed `loom-direct:`.
- `params` is the loom value lowered to JSON (wire names applied).
- `signal` is the loom's current `loomAbort.signal` (always defined; see **Cancellation source** below).
- `onUpdate` is a no-op (loom 1.0 does not surface streaming partial results to loom code).
- `ctx` is the synthesised `ExtensionContext` defined under [`ExtensionContext` (member surface loom touches)](#extensioncontext-interface) above: the live host's `ExtensionContext` with `signal`, `sessionManager`, and `abort()` overridden per the per-mode-override table, and every other member forwarded to the live host.

The tool's returned `{ content, isError }` envelope shape — `content: ({ type: "text"; text: string } | …)[]` and `isError: boolean` — is declared on the tool-result type family in `dist/core/extensions/types.d.ts` of `@earendil-works/pi-coding-agent` (the [loom 1.0 Pi-SDK pin](#pi-sdk-pin) from **Host prerequisites** above; the `isError` field appears on the relevant tool-result type declarations in that file). The envelope shape is the contract every code-driven tool call's outcome routing depends on; the SDK surface-inventory test asserts the field set on the cited type so a Pi minor that renames `isError`, drops the `text`-block discriminator, or widens `content` to a non-array shape surfaces at the build before the spec contract drifts. The envelope is lowered to the loom 1.0 string return value as follows. The lowering procedure inspects the resolved envelope and any throw raised during that inspection (the resolved value is not an object, `content` is not iterable, an entry is missing `type` / `text`, or any other shape violation that causes a property access or `.filter` / `.map` call to throw) is caught by the runtime and routed to `loom/runtime/internal-error` with `details.kind = "tool-return-shape"` (carrying `tool_name` and a discriminator describing the offending shape — e.g. `typeof resolved`, `Array.isArray(content)`); the call site observes the `internal-error` routing per [Errors and Results — Runtime panics](./errors-and-results.md), **not** an `Err(QueryError { kind: "code_tool", ... })`. The same rule applies if the lowering throws while assembling the `cause: "execution"` message described below (e.g. an `isError: true` return whose `content` array contains a non-iterable entry). The runtime filters `content` to entries with `type === "text"`, joins their `.text` values with `"\n"` (single line-feed; no separator before the first or after the last block), and returns the joined string. Non-text content blocks (images, resource references) are discarded during lowering; the loom-level observable is exhausted by the resulting `Ok("")` value. The runtime MUST NOT emit a `RuntimeEvent`, `loom-system-note`, or any other normative diagnostic on the discard path — non-text discard is not a `QueryError` and is not a member of the always-log set. Implementations MAY emit non-normative debug-channel logs for operator visibility. Widening to a richer return shape (preserving non-text blocks) is reserved for [Future Considerations](./future-considerations.md). An empty result string — either `content: []` or a content array with no surviving text blocks — is a legal `Ok("")` value when `!isError`. When `isError`, the runtime returns `Err(QueryError { kind: "code_tool", cause: "execution", message: <m>, tool_name, ... })` where `<m>` is the same filtered/joined text encoded as UTF-8 and truncated so that the resulting byte length is at most 4096 bytes. Truncation MUST cut on a Unicode code-point boundary: every code point in the output is represented by all of its UTF-8 bytes, and no bytes of a partial code point appear. When a code point would straddle the 4096-byte limit, that code point is dropped entirely; the resulting message MAY therefore be shorter than 4096 bytes by up to three bytes. Worked example: a filtered/joined text whose first 4095 bytes are ASCII followed by a 3-byte UTF-8 code point (e.g. U+2026 `…`) MUST truncate to 4095 bytes, because including the 3-byte code point would yield 4098 bytes. When no text survives the filter, `<m>` is the fixed string `"tool reported an error with no text content"`. When `cause: "execution"` originates from an `execute()` throw rather than `isError: true`, `<m>` is the thrown error's `.message` truncated under the same rule. Both forms share the `"execution"` cause; `execute()`-throw vs `isError: true` are distinguished by the `message` source, not by a new `cause` (a future revision MAY widen `cause` additively if the distinction needs to surface).

*Outcome routing summary.* The complete loom 1.0 routing of an `execute()` outcome at this boundary is fixed: a clean `{ content, isError: false }` lowers to `Ok(<filtered/joined text>)` (possibly `Ok("")`); a clean `{ content, isError: true }` lowers to `Err(CodeToolError { cause: "execution", ... })`; an `execute()` throw lowers to `Err(CodeToolError { cause: "execution", message: <error.message truncated>, ... })`; a `loomAbort.signal`-aborted call lowers to `Err(CodeToolError { cause: "cancelled", ... })` per the cancellation surfacing rule in [Cancellation — Surfacing](./cancellation.md); a non-conforming envelope (anything that throws during the lowering above) routes to `loom/runtime/internal-error` with `details.kind = "tool-return-shape"` and is **not** observable as a `CodeToolError`; a non-settling Promise blocks the call's `await` indefinitely until cancellation fires, at which point the cancelled path applies (loom 1.0 makes no internal timeout attempt, consistent with [`spec.md` — Hard ceilings, NOCEIL-1](../spec.md#hard-runtime-ceilings); the deferred per-call timeout extension lands additively on the open-struct seam in [Tool Calls](./tool-calls.md)); a settlement that arrives after the tool-call checkpoint has already surfaced `cause: "cancelled"` is discarded per [Cancellation — Race semantics](./cancellation.md) — the runtime MUST keep a swallowing handler attached to the underlying `execute()` Promise (and, symmetrically, to the underlying `@`-query provider Promise and the `invoke` callee's top-level execution Promise) for the lifetime of that Promise, installed at construction time before the first microtask boundary, so that a late rejection on the discarded path does **not** surface as a Node `unhandledRejection` process event; the discard is total (no `Err` rebinds the call site, no `RuntimeEvent` reaches the always-log channel, no diagnostic of any severity is emitted, and the discarded value is not traversed). The `CodeToolError.cause` enum (closed at `validation` / `execution` / `cancelled` / `unknown_tool` per [Errors and Results — `CodeToolError`](./errors-and-results.md#queryerror-variants)) is the contract surface for loom authors; the non-conforming-shape and non-settling-Promise dispositions are deliberately routed off it.

<a id="cancellation-source"></a>

**Cancellation source.** Pi's delivery of an `AbortSignal` at the two extension entry points loom uses (`ctx.signal` and `tool.execute`'s `signal` parameter) is the SDK prerequisite this section consumes; see **Host prerequisites** above. The two entry-point declarations live in `dist/core/extensions/types.d.ts` of `@earendil-works/pi-coding-agent` at the [loom 1.0 Pi-SDK pin](#pi-sdk-pin): `ExtensionContext.signal: AbortSignal | undefined` (the slash-command handler's turn signal, with the JSDoc verbatim *“current abort signal, or undefined when the agent is not streaming”*) and the `signal: AbortSignal | undefined` parameter of the tool `execute(...)` member of `ToolDefinition`. Subagent mode has no `AbortSignal` entry point — `CreateAgentSessionOptions` (declared at `dist/core/sdk.d.ts` in the loom 1.0 Pi-SDK pin per **Conversation drive — subagent mode** above) has no `signal` field — and instead consumes the `AgentSession.abort()` capability on the spawned handle, per **Subagent session lifecycle** above. As described in [Cancellation](./cancellation.md), the loom's `AbortSignal` is `loomAbort.signal` from a runtime-owned `AbortController` constructed fresh per invocation — **not** `ctx.signal` directly. Per the JSDoc above, `ctx.signal` is `undefined` in idle / non-turn contexts, and a slash-command handler fires from idle, so the runtime MUST NOT use `ctx.signal` as the loom's authoritative signal: doing so would silently pass `undefined` into every adapter (the synthesised tool-execution `ExtensionContext.signal`, the child-invoke derived signal) and degrade every cancellation path to a no-op. Instead, the runtime forwards Pi's turn-side `ctx.signal` (when defined and observed inside one of the runtime's `tool_call` / `tool_result` / `message_update` / `turn_end` / `agent_end` handlers) into `loomAbort.abort()`, and likewise forwards the `signal` parameter of a tool-exposed loom's `execute(...)` into `loomAbort.abort()` via a one-shot listener registered at entry. All downstream queries, tool calls, and child invokes derive from `loomAbort.signal`. Because `loomAbort.signal` is always defined, the optional-chaining defence (`signal?.aborted`) used by tool adapters is no longer load-bearing inside the runtime; the runtime guarantees a defined signal to every adapter it calls. Subagent mode propagates cancellation through the one-shot `loomAbort.signal` listener defined in **Subagent session lifecycle** above: when `loomAbort` fires, the listener calls `AgentSession.abort()` on the spawned handle, which tears down the in-flight provider call. Forwarding listeners — including the subagent `abort()` listener — are torn down in the same `finally` block that disposes the subagent session (see **Subagent session lifecycle** above). The `reason` value forwarded into `loomAbort.abort(reason)` for each forwarding path — including the runtime-synthesised values for the `agent_end`-driven and `session_shutdown`-driven triggers, which have no source `AbortSignal` — is pinned by [Cancellation — Abort-reason propagation](./cancellation.md); the rule applies uniformly across this paragraph's three forwarding shapes.

<a id="pi-slash-handler-promise-lifecycle-presupposition"></a>

**Pi-side slash-handler promise lifecycle (consumption posture).** The runtime side of the cancellation chain pinned above and in [`spec.md` — Session model — SM-3b session-swap semantics](../spec.md#sm-3b-session-swap-semantics) — `ctx.signal` triggers `loomAbort.abort(reason)`, the symmetric direction unblocks `await ctx.waitForIdle()`, and the `session_shutdown` handler awaits `Promise.allSettled(activeInvocations.map(inv => inv.disposeBarrier))` — is load-bearing only under three loom-side presuppositions about how Pi schedules the slash-command handler the runtime registers via [`sdk-cap-slash-command-registration`](#sdk-cap-slash-command-registration). The runtime records them here as a loom-side consumption posture rather than as Pi-side guarantees, so a future Pi change in this area surfaces against a named presupposition rather than passing silently: (i) the loom presupposes Pi awaits the slash-handler's returned `Promise` for the full invocation, including any time after `ctx.signal` fires its abort (i.e. the handler's return is not treated as fire-and-forget once the signal aborts); (ii) the loom presupposes Pi imposes no internal deadline on the handler's `Promise` settlement (no force-resolve, abandon, or detach of the in-flight handler after `ctx.signal` aborts or otherwise); and (iii) the loom presupposes `ctx.signal` is Pi's only out-of-band interaction with the in-flight handler (no parallel rejection, kill switch, or other channel by which Pi unilaterally terminates the handler outside the `AbortSignal` surface). The three presuppositions are taken on a best-effort basis against the [loom 1.0 Pi-SDK pin](#pi-sdk-pin) on `@earendil-works/pi-coding-agent` from **Host prerequisites** above and are not pinned by any typed contract on `ExtensionAPI`, `ExtensionContext`, or `ExtensionCommandContext`; the SDK capability inventory's [cancellation-propagation entry](#sdk-cap-cancellation-propagation) covers only that Pi *supplies* the `AbortSignal` at the two extension entry points and does not extend to the handler-promise's settle-time, deadline, or out-of-band-interaction surface. The [Pi version bump procedure](#pi-version-bump-procedure) below carries the audit step ((g) under step 1) that re-checks each of (i)–(iii) against the candidate Pi minor on every bump.

<a id="checkpoint-seam"></a>

**`Checkpoint` seam.** The runtime exposes a single internal hook the interpreter `await`s immediately before each cancellation checkpoint defined by the **Granularity** rule in [Cancellation](./cancellation.md). The hook exists so that the two race rules in [Cancellation — Race semantics](./cancellation.md) — no retroactive `Ok(v)` → `Err({kind:"cancelled"})` rewrite, and no top-level synthesis when no further checkpoint executes after the abort — are deterministically testable without depending on JS microtask scheduling. Production wiring resolves on the microtask queue (an already-resolved promise) for every checkpoint kind except `loop-iter`, which resolves on a macrotask turn so that a Pi-dispatched abort can land before a compute-bound loop's next signal-check (see the production-wiring rule below). Apart from that single per-iteration macrotask yield, the seam has no observable production effect beyond the cost of one resolved promise per checkpoint.

The interface shape is:

```ts
type CheckpointKind =
  | "loop-iter"
  | "query"
  | "tool-call"
  | "invoke"
  | "binder-call";

interface CheckpointSite {
  file: string;
  line: number;
  column: number;
}

interface Checkpoint {
  before(kind: CheckpointKind, site: CheckpointSite): Promise<void>;
}
```

Rules:

- The interpreter `await`s `checkpoint.before(kind, site)` immediately *before* reading `loomAbort.signal.aborted` at every checkpoint enumerated in [Cancellation — Granularity](./cancellation.md): each `for`/`while` iteration boundary, each `@`-query, each tool call, each `invoke`, and the binder LLM call (the binder checkpoint fires even though the binder runs outside the loom body, so the cancelled-binder failure-mode in [Slash-Command Argument Binding](./binder.md) is observable through the same seam). The await happens unconditionally; production resolution is immediate (next microtask) for every kind except `loop-iter`, which resolves on a macrotask turn per the production-wiring rule below, and the always-`await` shape is what lets a test inject async work between an operation's resolution and the signal-check.
- The hook does **not** observe non-checkpoint synchronous work (AJV validation, schema lowering, default-merging) — the **Granularity** rule already excludes those, and the seam mirrors that exclusion exactly. Implementations MUST NOT add `before(...)` calls at any site not enumerated above.
- Production wiring constructs one `Checkpoint` per `loomAbort` (i.e., per loom invocation). For the `loop-iter` kind, `before(...)` releases the event loop for one macrotask turn before resolving, so that a Pi-dispatched abort (the macrotask that flips `loomAbort.signal.aborted`) can run before the interpreter reads the signal at the next loop-iteration checkpoint; a compute-bound loom body with no genuine `await` between iterations therefore stays cancellable rather than draining only the microtask queue. For every other checkpoint kind, `before(...)` resolves on the microtask queue (an already-resolved promise), because those checkpoints precede real async I/O that already yields the event loop. For `invoke`, parent and child each own their own `Checkpoint` instance constructed from the same factory, mirroring the per-invocation `loomAbort` rule from [Cancellation](./cancellation.md); a parent's `before(...)` is not observed by the child and vice versa.
- Test wiring is the only consumer that observes calls. A test that fires `loomAbort.abort()` from inside `before(...)` exercises the *abort observed at this checkpoint* path; a test that fires `loomAbort.abort()` from inside the *previous* checkpoint's `before(...)` (or from any code awaited inside that previous `before(...)`) exercises the *abort landed between checkpoints* path — i.e., the no-retroactive-rewrite rule. A test that fires `loomAbort.abort()` after the loom's final checkpoint and before its top-level resolution exercises the no-tail-synthesis rule. These three patterns are the canonical use of the seam.
- Test fakes MUST treat the seam as call-once-per-checkpoint and MUST NOT skip the await (the no-skip rule is what gives the test deterministic control over the post-resolution / pre-signal-check window).
- The seam is internal: it is not exposed through `ExtensionAPI` and not visible to loom authors, Pi extensions, or tools. The runtime wires it through the same constructor-injection skeleton that owns `FileSystem`, `DiagnosticsSink`, `SchemaValidator`, etc.

<a id="clock--fakeclock-interface"></a>

**`Clock` / `FakeClock` interface.** The runtime reads wall-clock time and schedules deferred work exclusively through a `Clock` seam injected at construction time, modelled on the `FileSystem` seam. The interface members called out as load-bearing by other spec sections are:

- `now(): number` — monotonic milliseconds. Used by the **Runtime event channel** above to stamp `RuntimeEvent.occurred_at` at the originating emission site, and by [Discovery — Package discovery](./discovery.md#package-discovery) to read elapsed time for the `looms.scanPackagesTimeoutMs` cap.
- `setTimeout(fn: () => void, ms: number): TimerHandle` and `clearTimeout(handle: TimerHandle): void` — the only timer surface the runtime uses. The watcher's 250 ms debounce (step 5 above) and the settings-watcher debounce (per [Discovery — Settings file reads](./discovery.md#settings-file-reads)) both schedule through this seam. The debouncer holds the most recent timer handle and clears it on each new event.

Production wiring uses a `WallClock` adapter that delegates `now()` to `performance.now()` and the timer methods to the global `setTimeout` / `clearTimeout`. Tests use a `FakeClock` whose `advance(ms: number)` synchronously fires every timer whose deadline has elapsed in deadline order; equal-deadline timers fire in registration order, `clearTimeout` is a no-op for already-fired handles, and `now()` returns the fake's accumulated time and is *not* implicitly advanced. `Clock.now()` is monotonic (forbids `Date.now()`-style NTP drift). One `Clock` instance is constructed per runtime instance — never as a module-level global — and lives for the lifetime of that runtime; parallel runtimes get independent clocks. The runtime MUST NOT call `Date.now`, `performance.now`, `Date.prototype.getTime`, or the global `setTimeout` / `clearTimeout` outside the `WallClock` adapter; a build-time grep-test enforces this (parallel to the `process.env.HOME` ban for `homedir()`).

<a id="fakefilesystem--filesystem-interface"></a>

**`FakeFileSystem` / `FileSystem` interface.** The runtime reads the filesystem exclusively through a `FileSystem` seam injected at construction time; production wiring uses a `PiFileSystem` adapter that delegates to Node, and tests use an in-memory `FakeFileSystem` whose constructor takes the values it should report. The interface shape is normative:

```ts
interface FileStat {
  isDirectory(): boolean;
  isFile(): boolean;
  isSymbolicLink(): boolean;
}

interface FileSystem {
  readText(path: string): Promise<string>;          // rejects with a Node-style error whose `.code` is `"ENOENT"` for missing paths and `"EACCES"` / `"EPERM"` for permission failures; other I/O failures surface their underlying `.code` unchanged
  writeText(path: string, contents: string): Promise<void>;
  exists(path: string): Promise<boolean>;           // resolves `false` on `ENOENT`; rejects on any other error
  homedir(): string;                                // production never reads `process.env` directly
  readdir(path: string): Promise<readonly string[]>;// entry names only (no full paths); rejects with the same Node-style `.code` shape as `readText`
  lstat(path: string): Promise<FileStat>;           // does NOT follow symlinks; rejects with the same Node-style `.code` shape as `readText`
}
```

- `homedir()` is the single source of truth for the [Home-directory expansion](./discovery.md#home-directory-expansion) rule; the production `PiFileSystem` implementation calls Node's `os.homedir()` (resolving to `$HOME` on POSIX and `%USERPROFILE%` on Windows), and the `FakeFileSystem` implementation returns a constructor-injected string. The runtime MUST NOT read `process.env.HOME` or `process.env.USERPROFILE` directly and MUST NOT use any platform-conditional branch.
- `readText`, `writeText`, and `exists` are the load-bearing surface for [Directory Convention — Settings file reads](./discovery.md#settings-file-reads) and for every other normative file read or write the runtime performs.
- `readdir` and `lstat` are the load-bearing surface for the *clean leaf-`ENOENT`* ancestor walk defined in [Directory Convention](./discovery.md) (the **Failure modes** paragraph and the bullet that defines *clean leaf-`ENOENT`*) and for the package-discovery walk in [Directory Convention — Package discovery](./discovery.md#package-discovery). Rejected `.code` values map onto the discovery rules verbatim: an `ENOENT` chain that bottoms out cleanly is *missing*; an `EACCES` / `EPERM` / `ENOTDIR` (or any other code) anywhere on the chain is an unreadable-source failure.

<a id="filewatcher-interface"></a>

**`FakeFileWatcher` / `FileWatcher` interface.** Watcher attachment is a *separate* seam from `FileSystem` — production wires a chokidar adapter, and tests use an in-memory `FakeFileWatcher` whose `emit(event)` synchronously invokes every attached handler. The interface shape is normative:

```ts
type FileWatchEventKind = "add" | "change" | "unlink";

interface FileWatchEvent {
  kind: FileWatchEventKind;                         // matches chokidar's three load-bearing event names
  path: string;                                     // absolute path of the affected file
}

type Unsubscribe = () => void;

interface FileWatcher {
  watch(roots: readonly string[], handler: (event: FileWatchEvent) => void): Unsubscribe;
}
```

- `watch` attaches one handler over the supplied root paths. The returned `Unsubscribe` tears down the underlying watcher (chokidar's `close()` in production); calling it twice is a no-op. The handler observes only the three event kinds above — chokidar's `addDir`, `unlinkDir`, `ready`, `error`, etc. are filtered out by the adapter and never reach the runtime; the chokidar-adapter's own `error` events route through the `ctx.ui.notify` toast surface defined in [Diagnostics](./diagnostics.md), not through this seam.
- The watcher's 250 ms debounce, the build-aside-then-publish swap, and the structural-vs-content event split (per **Extension entry point** step 5 above) are runtime responsibilities layered on top of this seam — they are *not* properties of the seam itself; the seam only delivers raw events.
- One `FileWatcher` instance is constructed per runtime instance — never as a module-level global — and lives for the lifetime of that runtime; parallel runtimes get independent watchers.

**Discovery API.** The extension owns enumeration; it subscribes to `resources_discover` solely as a re-discovery trigger and returns the empty result `{}` (`ResourcesDiscoverResult` has no `loomPaths` field — looms reach Pi through `pi.registerCommand`, not as a Pi-managed resource type). The five sources, their priority order, the package-root walk, and the failure-mode table are all in [Directory Convention](./discovery.md). Cross-format collision detection consults `pi.getCommands()` on `session_start` (per the **Extension entry point** numbered list above); the call would throw if invoked during the extension factory itself (per the pre-bind action-method rule in **Extension entry point** step 2), which is why discovery is split across the factory (parse + pending list) and the `session_start` handler (collision check + `pi.registerCommand`).

> **loom 1.0 seam — Pi-owned subagents collision source set.** <a id="loom-1-0-seam-pi-owned-subagents-collision-source-set"></a><a id="v1-seam-pi-owned-subagents-collision-source-set"></a> The set of `SlashCommandSource` values the `session_start` handler treats as collision candidates (`"prompt"`, `"extension"`, `"skill"` under `@earendil-works/pi-coding-agent` at the [loom 1.0 Pi-SDK pin](#pi-sdk-pin)) MUST be defined as a single named set inside the runtime, consulted by the collision check via membership test rather than open-coded as three separate string comparisons or a hard-coded `switch`. The deferred *Pi-owned subagents exposed as enumerable slash commands* extension in [Future Considerations](./future-considerations.md) lands by widening that set to four arms (adding a `"subagent"` entry) when a future Pi minor extends `SlashCommandSource` accordingly; widening the set is the only loom 1.0 surface that perturbs, and the asymmetric loser-drops collision rule defined in [Discovery](./discovery.md) is preserved by construction.

**No Pi-owned discovery path enumerates `.loom` or `.warp`.** Under the [loom 1.0 Pi-SDK pin range](#pi-sdk-pin), Pi exposes exactly three slash-command sources (`source: "prompt" | "extension" | "skill"`, per `@earendil-works/pi-coding-agent`'s `core/slash-commands.d.ts`); `prompt` and `skill` enumerate `*.md` files only, and `extension` requires programmatic `pi.registerCommand` calls. The `resources_discover` event carries `skillPaths` / `promptPaths` / `themePaths` only — there is no `loomPaths` slot — and the `pi` package-manifest namespace recognises only `extensions` / `skills` / `prompts` / `themes` / `video` / `image`. Therefore the only path by which a `.warp` file could become a slash command is through this extension's own discovery walk; that walk matches `*.loom` only (per [Directory Convention](./discovery.md) and [Discovery — File-extension namespace](./discovery.md#file-extension-namespace)), so the `.warp`-cannot-be-slash-invoked guarantee in [`spec.md`](../spec.md) Introduction holds by construction. A Pi minor that adds a fourth `SlashCommandSource` arm, a `loomPaths` field on `ResourcesDiscoverResult`, or a generic file-extension registry MUST trigger a re-validation of this paragraph as part of the [Pi version bump procedure](#pi-version-bump-procedure) below, in the same edit that widens `peerDependencies`.

<a id="sdk-capability-inventory"></a>
## SDK capability inventory

The runtime depends on the seven named SDK capabilities enumerated below. Items 1, 2, 3, 4, and 6 are factory-probable and verified by [Step 0 (Capability probe)](#entry-capability-probe) above (which on any failure skips every factory-time host-binding call — the four `pi.register*` calls and `pi.on` — and emits `loom/load/host-incompatible`).

The *surface-set closure* property cross-referenced from [`spec.md` — Orientation — Prerequisites](../spec.md#orientation) — every Pi-side surface reference in the *audited source tree* (the canonical scope name pinned under *Audit scope* below; equal to the closed set `src/**/*.ts` minus the excluded files enumerated there) resolves to an `SDK_SURFACE_INVENTORY` entry, the typebox sibling allow-lists (`{ Type }` named-import allow-list and `{ Unsafe }` member-access allow-list, per [Target surface categories (typebox carve-out)](#audit-target-surface-categories) below), or a declared `// allow-pi-surface:` exemption — is an obligation the implementation MUST satisfy via the *inventory-closure audit* pinned immediately below. `SDK_SURFACE_INVENTORY` is strictly broader than the seven capabilities; its entry-kind taxonomy (the `namespace-function` kind that stores the ten function members of the factory-probable subset of capabilities 1, 2, 3, 4, and 6, plus the additional non-`namespace-function` kinds) is implementation-owned and not re-enumerated here.

The seven-capability cardinality claim above is a separate assertion anchored by the `CAPABILITY_OBLIGATIONS` constant pinned in the extension module's pinned-constants block; it is enforced by [`CAPABILITY_OBLIGATIONS.length === 7`](#bump-step-2-positive)'s mechanical assertion against that constant (not against the markdown enumeration of items 1–7 below or the [`spec.md` — Orientation — Prerequisites](../spec.md#orientation) cross-reference list, both of which are contributor-discipline restatements), and not by the inventory-closure audit (which targets surface-set closure rather than capability count). Contributor-discipline (per [step 2(b) branch (2)](#bump-step-2b-promote)'s catch-all co-edit obligation) carries the markdown-enumeration↔`CAPABILITY_OBLIGATIONS`-constant↔natural-language-prose chain. Describing the audit's behavioural contract here, rather than its concrete tooling, lets the implementation choose a static-AST walker, a TypeScript-program symbol-table walk, or any equivalent tooling that detects every recognised import/access shape per *Recognised import/access shapes* below and surfaces every violation under the family→discriminator obligations per *Failure-surface contract* below, and prevents the surface-set-closure guarantee [`spec.md` — Orientation — Prerequisites](../spec.md#orientation) leans on from depending on a tooling claim.

<a id="sdk-cap-inventory-closure-audit"></a>
**Inventory-closure audit.** The implementation MUST publish a build-time *inventory-closure audit* — a negative-direction check, sharing the same `SDK_SURFACE_INVENTORY` source of truth as the positive-direction literal-read assertion that owns items 1–7 above, that asserts every Pi-side surface reference in the audited source tree resolves to an `SDK_SURFACE_INVENTORY` entry, the typebox sibling allow-lists (`{ Type }` named-import allow-list and `{ Unsafe }` member-access allow-list, per [Target surface categories (typebox carve-out)](#audit-target-surface-categories) below), or a declared `// allow-pi-surface:` exemption. The audit's name *inventory-closure audit* refers to the closure mechanism (every reference resolved through the inventory or an exemption); the property it enforces is termed *surface-set closure* in [`spec.md`](../spec.md) and on this page interchangeably (per the cross-reference at the top of this section). PIC pins the audit's behavioural contract; concrete tooling and literal discriminator strings are implementation-owned, mirroring the ownership carve-out in step 5 of the [Pi version bump procedure](#pi-version-bump-procedure) below. The commit that introduces this audit MUST also include whatever source-tree sweep is needed to keep `main` green: every existing `src/` reference that the new audit would surface as a violation MUST be either deleted, promoted to an `SDK_SURFACE_INVENTORY` entry, marked with an `// allow-pi-surface:` exemption, or rewritten into a recognised shape (per [step 2(b)](#bump-step-2-negative)'s five branches below), in the same commit. The audit is intended to land green; it is not introduced as a "land red, fix incrementally" gate, and an implementation whose first `npm test` invocation against `main` is red on this audit violates this paragraph on the same footing as the implementation-adoption obligations above.

- <a id="audit-target-surface-categories"></a>*Target surface categories.* The audit covers exactly three categories: (1) `pi.<member>` static member-access expressions on the canonical `pi` identifier — defined syntactically as a function or method parameter declaration whose name is the literal identifier `pi` and whose explicit type annotation is the literal `ExtensionAPI` (qualified or unqualified, including `import type` re-imports, but resolved against the textual annotation rather than against an inferred type), in practice the loom's extension-factory entry-point parameter (per **Extension entry point** above; the same `default function (pi: ExtensionAPI)` signature) — including but not limited to the four `pi.register*` calls, `pi.on`, `pi.registerFlag`, and `pi.getFlag` named in this page's other obligations (the four `pi.register*` calls and `pi.on` are factory-time host-binding calls per **Extension entry point** above; `pi.registerFlag` and `pi.getFlag` are not themselves entries in the seven-capability [SDK capability inventory](#sdk-capability-inventory) below but are `pi.<member>` surfaces the runtime touches and are in scope of category (1) here on the same footing as the capability members, with any inventory entry the audit would require for them resolved per [step 2(b) branch (2)](#bump-step-2b-promote)). Pinning the carrier syntactically (canonical parameter name plus textual type annotation) on the same footing as category (3) below is what lets a static-AST walker satisfy this category without a TypeScript-program load; aliased, destructured, captured (`this.pi = pi`), or otherwise rebound forms — including any function/method parameter declaration whose explicit type annotation is `ExtensionAPI` but whose name is **not** `pi` — MUST NOT exist in the audited source tree (the audit enforces that prohibition under *Recognised import/access shapes* below). Local variables named `pi` whose explicit type annotation is not `ExtensionAPI` (or which carry no explicit type annotation) are out of scope of category (1) — the carrier rule keys on the textual `ExtensionAPI` annotation, not on the bare identifier text `pi`, so a static-AST walker neither over-fires on every local variable named `pi` nor under-fires on a renamed `ExtensionAPI`-typed parameter (which is instead caught by the off-canonical-name prohibition above on the same footing as the off-canonical-name `ctx` rule); (2) named imports from the four `@earendil-works/*` peer packages — `pi-coding-agent`, `pi-agent-core`, `pi-ai`, and `pi-tui`; (3) member-access expressions on the canonical `ctx` identifier — defined syntactically as a function or method parameter declaration whose name is the literal identifier `ctx` and whose explicit type annotation is the literal `ExtensionContext` or `ExtensionCommandContext` (qualified or unqualified, including `import type` re-imports, but resolved against the textual annotation rather than against an inferred type) — covering every member of `ExtensionContext` and `ExtensionCommandContext` as declared by the `@earendil-works/pi-coding-agent` peer dependency's `.d.ts` declarations at the loom 1.0 SDK pin — the SDK type declarations are the single source of truth for category (3)'s closed in-scope set, so a Pi minor that adds, removes, or renames a member of either type extends or contracts category (3) automatically and the implementation's `SDK_SURFACE_INVENTORY` category-(3) entries (per the new entry kind enumerated below) MUST be derived from those declarations rather than from any prose enumeration on this page. Illustrative members at the loom 1.0 pin include `waitForIdle`, `cwd`, `ui`, `model`, `modelRegistry`, `isIdle`, `getContextUsage`, `hasPendingMessages`, `compact`, `shutdown`, `getSystemPrompt`, `sessionManager`, and `signal`; this listing is illustrative only and the audit's category-(3) closed set MUST NOT be seeded from it. At the loom 1.0 Pi-SDK pin both `ExtensionContext` and `ExtensionCommandContext` are exported as named types from `@earendil-works/pi-coding-agent` on the package's `package.json#exports`'s `"."` entry (the SDK declaration site `dist/core/extensions/types.d.ts`, re-exported from the package root via `dist/index.d.ts`), with `ExtensionCommandContext extends ExtensionContext` per [`ExtensionCommandContext` (per-handler subtype loom touches)](#extensioncommandcontext-interface) below — so the audit MUST detect category-(3) member access on a carrier parameter whose textual type annotation is either of the two literals (`ExtensionContext` or `ExtensionCommandContext`) on the same footing, and a member declared on one of the two types but not the other resolves against any `SDK_SURFACE_INVENTORY` category-(3) entry whose `path` field matches the access per the [Category-(2) inventory join key](#audit-category-2-inventory-join-key) below (generalised to category (3) per this paragraph), regardless of which of the two annotations the carrier parameter declared. Pinning the carrier syntactically (canonical parameter name plus textual type annotation) is what lets a static-AST walker satisfy this category without a TypeScript-program load; aliased, destructured, captured (`this.ctx = ctx`), or otherwise rebound forms — including any function/method parameter declaration whose explicit type annotation is `ExtensionContext` or `ExtensionCommandContext` but whose name is **not** `ctx` — MUST NOT exist in the audited source tree (the audit enforces that prohibition under *Recognised import/access shapes* below). Category (2) for the four `@earendil-works/*` peer packages covers only the named-import declarations themselves; member-access references on those imports are out of scope of category (2) and would surface only via the canonical-`pi` carrier in category (1) for the `pi: ExtensionAPI` case or via the canonical-`ctx` carrier in category (3) for the `ctx: ExtensionContext` / `ExtensionCommandContext` case — the four peer packages currently expose no other in-runtime member-access carriers, and the typebox `Type.<member>` member-access carve-out pinned in the next sub-paragraph applies exclusively to the typebox `Type` identifier and MUST NOT be generalised to the four `@earendil-works/*` peers. The fifth bundled package `typebox` (per **Host prerequisites — Pi SDK pin** above) is in scope for category (2) with a single permitted *named import* — `Type` (consumed as `import { Type } from "typebox"`, the same shape [Step 0 (e)](#entry-capability-probe)'s host-shape check probes against, since `.Unsafe` and every other typebox surface the runtime might touch is reached as a member access on the `Type` namespace rather than as its own named import) — and the audit additionally enforces a `typebox`-specific *member-access allow-list* on `Type.<member>` references whose single permitted entry is `Unsafe` (i.e. `Type.Unsafe`), whose runtime presence is gated by that same [Step 0 (e)](#entry-capability-probe) check. The audit's detection rule for these `Type.<member>` references is pinned syntactically here as a typebox-only extension to category (2) (the four `@earendil-works/*` peers do not get an analogous member-access detection rule per the prior sentence prohibiting member-access detection on the four `@earendil-works/*` peers (above)): a `Type.<member>` access is detected as a category-(2) member-access reference whose carrier is the imported `Type` identifier (per the `import { Type } from "typebox"` named-import shape immediately above), and is resolved against the typebox member-access allow-list `{ Unsafe }` rather than against `SDK_SURFACE_INVENTORY` (parallel to how the named-import `Type` itself resolves through the typebox named-import allow-list per the *typebox-only sibling* paragraph below). Note the carrier-rule asymmetry with categories (1) and (3): the typebox `Type` carrier is an imported binding rather than a parameter typed `ExtensionAPI` (category (1)) or `ExtensionContext` / `ExtensionCommandContext` (category (3)), and a static-AST walker recognises it by the named-import declaration above rather than by a typed-parameter declaration; this carve-out applies exclusively to the typebox `Type` identifier and MUST NOT be generalised to member-access detection on any other imported binding. Every other named import from `typebox` (e.g., `Static`, `TSchema`) MUST surface under family (2) of the *Failure-surface contract* below, on the same footing as an unauthorised named import from any of the four `@earendil-works/*` peer packages; every other `Type.<member>` access (e.g., `Type.Object`, `Type.Static`) MUST surface under that same family under the same per-discriminator routability; both MAY be exempted only via the same-line `// allow-pi-surface:` marker per *Exemption mechanism* below. The four-peer-package prohibitions on `import * as`, default imports, dynamic `import()`, side-effect-only imports, computed access, aliased rebindings, captured rebindings, `Object.assign`, `keyof typeof`, and barrel-module / `export * from` re-exports per *Recognised import/access shapes* below apply identically to `typebox`. The single-entry member-access allow-list above (the *typebox member-access allow-list*) is **not** an `SDK_SURFACE_INVENTORY` entry — it is a fixed allow-list, sibling to but separate from `SDK_SURFACE_INVENTORY`, that lives in the same source-of-truth pinned-constants block in the extension module that already holds the four [Step 0 (Capability probe)](#entry-capability-probe) constants (Node floor, `AbortSignal` member list, capability list, peer-dep range), so the build-time audit consumes it from the same single site the runtime-side [Step 0 (e)](#entry-capability-probe) probe is wired against; the audit consumes it alongside `SDK_SURFACE_INVENTORY` (mirroring the same-line marker's status under *Exemption mechanism* below as a non-`SDK_SURFACE_INVENTORY` declaration site). Symmetrically, the `typebox` *named-import allow-list* whose single permitted entry is `Type` is **not** an `SDK_SURFACE_INVENTORY` entry either — it is a second fixed allow-list, sibling to but separate from `SDK_SURFACE_INVENTORY`, co-located with the member-access allow-list in the same pinned-constants block, and consulted by the audit's category-(2) resolver as a *typebox-only sibling* to `SDK_SURFACE_INVENTORY` for `typebox`-package imports specifically, so an `import { Type } from "typebox"` declaration resolves through this allow-list rather than through the [Category-(2) inventory join key](#audit-category-2-inventory-join-key) rule below (which would otherwise refuse to resolve `Type`, since no `SDK_SURFACE_INVENTORY` entry's leftmost dot-separated `path` segment equals `Type`); this typebox-only resolution path is parallel to the already-pinned authorisation of `Type.Unsafe` member access through the member-access allow-list above and applies exclusively to `typebox`-package imports — the four `@earendil-works/*` peer packages still resolve solely against `SDK_SURFACE_INVENTORY` per the join-key rule. The single-entry allow-list MUST NOT be folded into the four-peer-packages iteration the [Step 0 (d)](#entry-capability-probe) probe pins, and neither the `Type` named import nor the `Unsafe` member-access entry extends the implementation's entry-kind taxonomy. These allow-list contents (`{ Type }` for named imports, `{ Unsafe }` for member access) are pinned at the loom 1.0 Pi-SDK pin against the runtime's current typebox usage; the implementation's source-tree sweep (per the *Inventory-closure audit* introductory paragraph above) verifies that no other typebox surface is reached anywhere in the audited source tree, and any future widening (e.g. promoting `Type.Object` into the member-access allow-list, or `Static` into the named-import allow-list) follows [step 2(b) branch (2)](#bump-step-2b-promote) of the [Pi version bump procedure](#pi-version-bump-procedure) below applied to the typebox allow-lists rather than to `SDK_SURFACE_INVENTORY`. The contributor-facing maintenance obligation on a Pi/`typebox` bump that renames `Unsafe` (or otherwise drifts the permitted member name on the `Type` namespace) is owned by [step 5](#pi-version-bump-procedure) of the [Pi version bump procedure](#pi-version-bump-procedure) below, where this allow-list is grouping (iii) of the in-scope pinned-constants groupings. Satisfying the three in-scope categories MUST extend `SDK_SURFACE_INVENTORY`'s entry-kind taxonomy beyond the existing kinds, with at minimum one new entry kind per category not already covered: a category (3) kind for canonical-`ctx` member access against `ExtensionContext` / `ExtensionCommandContext`; a category (1) kind for `pi.<member>` references that are not function-member capabilities (`pi.registerFlag`, `pi.getFlag`, and any other such `pi.<member>` the runtime touches that is not one of the seven capabilities); and a category (2) kind for named imports from the four `@earendil-works/*` peer packages where not already covered by an existing entry kind (the existing `type-union-snapshot` entry for `SessionShutdownEvent.reason` and the existing `namespace-function` entries for the ten factory-probable function-member entries are the two existing-coverage cases). The new kinds MUST be coined in the implementation's entry-kind enumeration as a precondition to the audit's first run on `main`; the implementation MUST land the new entry kinds (with their `kind` discriminator strings and per-kind payload field shapes), the literal-read assertion's branch-table arms for each, and the audit's category-(1)/(2)/(3) detection wiring before the first `npm test` invocation that runs the audit. The spec edit pins the audit's behavioural contract; the implementation closes the loop. PIC delegates the literal kind names and per-kind payload field shapes to the implementation, which holds the single source of truth (mirroring the entry-level inventory carve-out in step 5 below).
