PIC pins the minimum entry shape every kind MUST satisfy: every `SDK_SURFACE_INVENTORY` entry that participates in inventory-closure-audit resolution (i.e., the existing `namespace-function` and `type-union-snapshot` kinds, and any new category-(1) / category-(2) / category-(3) entry kinds defined for the audit per the *Target surface categories* paragraph above) MUST carry at least two fields — `kind: string` (the discriminator the SDK surface-inventory literal-read assertion's branch table dispatches on, and the discriminator the routability obligation in the next sentence keys on) and `path: string` (a stable identifier the [Category-(2) inventory join key](#audit-category-2-inventory-join-key) below resolves against per the per-category join-key rules pinned in *Category-(2) inventory join key* and *Category-(1)/(3) inventory join key (per-category specialisation)* below; category (2) uses leftmost-segment matching, categories (1) and (3) use rightmost-segment matching); per-kind payload fields beyond these two are implementation-owned per the delegation above. The minimum-shape obligation above is **scoped to audit-participating kinds**: the existing `node-floor`, `strict-capability-probe`, `peer-dep-range`, and `api-coverage` entry kinds are positive-direction-only literal-read entries that the inventory-closure audit does not consult for surface resolution, and are therefore exempt from the `path` requirement above (they retain their implementation-pinned payload shapes — `literal`, `probedName`, `packages`, `apiNamespace` — without a `path` field). The exemption is closed to the four kinds named in this sentence; any future entry kind, audit-participating or not, MUST carry the `kind` field, and any future audit-participating kind MUST additionally carry `path` per the rule above. The SDK surface-inventory literal-read assertion (per [step 2(a)](#bump-step-2-positive)) MUST additionally enforce the minimum-entry-shape obligation by surfacing each shape failure under its own `literal-read/<symptom>` discriminator, including at minimum: a missing `path` field on an audit-participating entry; a non-string `path` value; an empty-string `path`; an empty leftmost-dot-separated segment of `path` (e.g. `".foo"`); a missing `kind` field; a non-string `kind` value. Illustrative implementation-owned `<symptom>` tokens: `literal-read/missing-path-on-audit-kind`, `literal-read/empty-path`, `literal-read/empty-leftmost-segment`, `literal-read/missing-kind-field`, `literal-read/non-string-kind`. The implementation publishes the literal `<symptom>` strings and one negative-test fixture per token under the existing per-`<symptom>` fixture floor. The new entries MUST NOT be folded into the existing `namespace-function` kind — its definition is exclusively the ten function members of the factory-probable subset of the seven capability obligations enumerated below (capabilities 1, 2, 3, 4, and 6 — "five capabilities, ten function members"), and folding non-factory-probable surface into this kind would silently corrupt the factory-probable subset enumeration that the implementation and the [Step 0 (c)](#entry-capability-probe) probe both consume. ([Step 2(a)](#bump-step-2-positive)'s count-equality assertion is over the count of capability obligations enumerated in [SDK capability inventory](#sdk-capability-inventory) below (items 1–7), not over `namespace-function` entries, so widening this kind does not directly perturb that assertion's `7`; the corruption surface is the factory-probable subset enumeration above.) The SDK surface-inventory literal-read assertion's branch table MUST gain an arm for each new kind under the same precondition obligation above (i.e. before the first `npm test` invocation that runs the audit on `main`, not necessarily in the same git commit as this spec edit); an inventory entry whose `kind` discriminator the branch table does not recognise MUST fail the assertion with a routable discriminator rather than silently passing through, ignoring the entry, or surfacing as an unhandled throw. The literal-read assertion's failure-discriminator shape is `literal-read/<symptom>` (a peer to the inventory-closure audit's `audit/<class>/<family>/<symptom>` shape pinned under [Failure-surface contract](#audit-failure-surface-contract) below — the `literal-read/...` discriminator is **not** under the `audit/` namespace and carries no `<class>` segment, since it never participates in the three-class partition the audit pins), with `<symptom>` strings owned by the implementation on the same footing as the implementation-owned literal strings under [step 5](#pi-version-bump-procedure) below; the unrecognised-`kind` failure MUST surface under a stable `literal-read/<symptom>` discriminator (illustrative implementation-owned token: `literal-read/unknown-entry-kind`), and the contributor recovery arm is [step 2(a)](#bump-step-2-positive)'s 'add a recognising branch to the literal-read assertion's branch table for the new `kind`' obligation. The audit's *Failure-surface contract* obligation under *Failure-surface contract* below to identify "the inventory entry the contributor would add" presupposes these per-kind field shapes are pinned by the implementation; an implementation that lands the audit without the corresponding kind-shape pins violates this paragraph.
- <a id="audit-recognised-shapes"></a>*Recognised import/access shapes.* The audit MUST detect at minimum: named-import declarations from each of the four `@earendil-works/*` peer packages and from `typebox` (including type-only `import type { ... }` declarations, and the inline-`type`-modifier form `import { type Foo, bar }` in which a single value-import declaration mixes type-only and value-only specifiers — the audit MUST treat each named specifier independently per its inline-`type` modifier, so `import { type Foo, bar }` is two specifiers (`Foo` as a type-only specifier, `bar` as a value-only specifier) and each is detected and resolved per category (2) per its modifier rather than by a uniform per-declaration verdict; the same per-specifier rule applies symmetrically to the inverse form `import type { Foo, type Bar }` where the declaration is type-only but an individual specifier carries a redundant inline `type` modifier). Package specifier matching MUST cover both the bare-package form (e.g. `@earendil-works/pi-coding-agent`) and any sub-path form (e.g. `@earendil-works/pi-coding-agent/dist/types`, `@earendil-works/pi-coding-agent/sub-export`); a named import is in scope of category (2) iff its specifier matches `@earendil-works/<peer>` exactly OR `@earendil-works/<peer>/<non-empty-sub-path>` for one of the four peer packages (and similarly for `typebox` / `typebox/<sub-path>`). Step 2(a) / step 5 deep-`dist/...`-path re-pins per the [Pi version bump procedure](#pi-version-bump-procedure) below therefore surface to category-(2) detection on the same footing as the bare-package form, and the same prohibitions later in this paragraph (`import * as`, default imports, dynamic `import()`, side-effect-only imports, aliased rebindings, barrel-module re-exports, etc.) apply to the sub-path form on the same footing as the bare-package form. The package-specifier-not-part-of-the-join-key rule pinned by [Category-(2) inventory join key](#audit-category-2-inventory-join-key) below applies under this broader specifier set: a named import resolved under either the bare-package form or any sub-path form of the same peer package routes to the same `SDK_SURFACE_INVENTORY` entry by canonical name, with no per-(specifier-shape, name) entry duplication required. `pi.<member>` static member-access expressions; member-access expressions on the canonical `ctx` identifier as defined under *Target surface categories* (3) above; and `Type.<member>` member-access expressions on the canonical `Type` import from `typebox` as defined under the typebox carve-out of *Target surface categories* above. Re-exports of in-scope surface count as references at the re-exporting site — on the same footing as a direct named import — only for category (2), i.e. per-symbol `export { <name>[, ...] } from "@earendil-works/<peer>"` declarations naming one or more enumerated symbols; categories (1) (`pi.<member>`) and (3) (canonical-`ctx` member access) are not standalone bindings and so cannot be re-exported as such. The "re-exports through barrel modules" prohibition below applies under this operational definition: a module is a *barrel module* iff every top-level statement is one of: (i) an `export … from "@earendil-works/<peer>"` re-export of a peer-package surface (per-symbol named, never `export *` — see prohibition below); (ii) a comment; (iii) a directive prologue; (iv) an import statement whose binding is used by an (i) statement on the same module; (v) an `export type … from "@earendil-works/<peer>"` type-only re-export from a peer package. Any module with a top-level `export const`/`export function`/`export class`/locally-defined-symbol export, or a plain `export {}`, or a top-level `import` whose binding is unused, is NOT a barrel module under this definition (and may use per-symbol named re-exports per the rule above). Independently of the barrel-module shape, `export * from "@earendil-works/<peer>"` and `export * as ns from "@earendil-works/<peer>"` of any of the four peer packages are prohibited everywhere in the audit's scope (they launder the entire namespace through the re-exporting site without per-symbol audit; these shapes are forbidden because the audit's resolution rules — the canonical-`pi` and canonical-`ctx` carriers, the `SDK_SURFACE_INVENTORY` category-(2) join key on the canonical name per *Category-(2) inventory join key* below, and the `typebox` named-import allow-list keyed on `Type` and `Unsafe` per [*Target surface categories*](#audit-target-surface-categories) above (typebox carve-out) — all consume the canonical name and would silently fail to resolve a renamed, aliased, or laundered reference even under the type-aware tooling variant the implementation MAY adopt below, so the prohibition is a behavioural rule on the source-text shape rather than a tooling-implementation constraint, and applies on the same footing to every other shape enumerated below); per-symbol `export { <name>[, ...] } from "@earendil-works/<peer>"` re-exports are permitted iff the re-exporting module is not a barrel module under the operational definition above. The same-line `// allow-pi-surface:` exemption marker on a re-export line covers only the surface re-exported by that single statement, not the surrounding module. Other syntactic shapes that fall under the same behavioural rule — `import * as pi`, default imports of any of the four peer packages, dynamic `import()` of any of the four peer packages, side-effect-only imports of any of the four peer packages, any CommonJS access path to one of the four `@earendil-works/*` peer packages or `typebox` — the runtime MUST be ES-modules-only at loom 1.0 — `package.json` MUST set `"type": "module"` as part of the extension's adoption commit, and the implementation's land-green precondition (per the introductory paragraph above) MUST verify both this `package.json#type` value and the absence of CJS-reach shapes in `src/` before the audit's first run on `main` — and CJS reach is unsupported, so this prohibition covers (i) `require("@earendil-works/<peer>")` and `require("@earendil-works/<peer>/<sub-path>")` (and `require("typebox")` / `require("typebox/<sub-path>")`), (ii) `createRequire(...)` plus `req("@earendil-works/<peer>")` (or `req("typebox")`) style indirection — defined as any function call whose call site uses `createRequire` imported from the Node `"module"` package and whose result is invoked with one of the in-scope package specifiers (bare-package or sub-path form, on the same footing as the named-import specifier-matching rule above); the prohibition holds regardless of whether `createRequire` is imported under its canonical name, under an aliased rebinding (e.g. `import { createRequire as cr } from "module"; cr(import.meta.url)("@earendil-works/<peer>")`), through a namespace import (e.g. `import * as M from "module"; M.createRequire(import.meta.url)("@earendil-works/<peer>")`), through a default import or default-namespace re-export of the `"module"` package, or through any other re-binding shape (further `as`-rename re-export, intermediate barrel module, captured local `const cr = createRequire`, etc.), and applies on the same footing to any call to a function whose source binding transitively resolves to the `createRequire` named export of the Node `"module"` package when invoked with one of the in-scope package specifiers — no such call MUST exist anywhere in the audited source tree, and the aliased-import / aliased-rebinding prohibitions enumerated later in this paragraph (which are scoped to the four `@earendil-works/*` peer packages and `typebox`) MUST NOT be read as authorising the `"module"`-package shapes above by omission — and (iii) any other CJS-style indirection reaching the four peer packages or `typebox`; the prohibition is in family (4) under its own discriminator on the same footing as the dynamic-`import()` and side-effect-only-import clauses immediately preceding, computed access (`pi[name]` or `ctx[name]`), namespace destructuring (`const { registerCommand } = pi`, `const { ui } = ctx`), aliased rebindings — both value-binding aliases (`const reg = pi.registerCommand`, `const c = ctx`, `const api = pi`) and aliased-import / aliased-re-export specifiers from any of the four `@earendil-works/*` peer packages or from `typebox` (`import { Foo as Bar } from "@earendil-works/<peer>"`, `import { Foo as Bar } from "typebox"`, and the symmetric re-export forms `export { Foo as Bar } from "@earendil-works/<peer>"` / `export { Foo as Bar } from "typebox"`; the `as`-rename specifier launders the canonical name on which `SDK_SURFACE_INVENTORY` category-(2) join-key resolution and the `typebox` named-import allow-list both depend, on the same footing as the value-binding aliases above — the canonical (source) name MUST be used unrenamed at every import and re-export site, and the inline-`type` modifier MAY of course still combine with the unrenamed specifier), captured rebindings (`this.ctx = ctx`, `self.ctx = ctx`, `this.pi = pi`, `self.pi = pi`, and — read broadly, not narrowly to inner-closure-captured bindings — any local variable, field, or closure-captured binding anywhere in the audited source tree whose initialiser is a reference to `ctx`, to `pi`, or to any descendant member-access expression rooted on either of those canonical carriers, e.g. `const cwd = ctx.cwd`, `const reg = pi.registerCommand`, `let savedCtx = ctx`, `this.foo = ctx.foo`; the broader reading is the normative one and the behavioural intent is that every `pi.<member>` and every `ctx.<member>` access reaches its read site through the canonical carrier — the typed `pi` parameter or the typed `ctx` parameter — so the static-AST audit can resolve every such access against `SDK_SURFACE_INVENTORY` without chasing data-flow through an intermediate binding), any function/method parameter declaration whose explicit type annotation is `ExtensionContext` or `ExtensionCommandContext` but whose name is not the literal identifier `ctx`, any function/method parameter declaration whose name is the literal identifier `ctx` but whose explicit type annotation is not the literal `ExtensionContext` or `ExtensionCommandContext` (including the absence of any explicit type annotation, an `any` annotation, an `unknown` annotation, or any other annotation than the two literals above — the literal `ctx` parameter name is reserved across the audited source tree for category-(3) carriers, so a parameter typed otherwise (e.g. `ctx: HttpRequestContext` for an HTTP handler that never touches Pi-side surface) MUST be named something other than `ctx` (e.g. `httpCtx`, `request`); the reservation is enforced unconditionally on the parameter name regardless of whether the parameter ever transports Pi-side surface, and the prohibition is in family (4) under its own discriminator on the same footing as the off-canonical-name clause immediately preceding), any function/method parameter declaration whose explicit type annotation is `ExtensionAPI` but whose name is not the literal identifier `pi`, any function/method parameter declaration whose name is the literal identifier `pi` but whose explicit type annotation is not the literal `ExtensionAPI` (including the absence of any explicit type annotation, an `any` annotation, an `unknown` annotation, or any other annotation than the literal above — the literal `pi` parameter name is reserved across the audited source tree for category-(1) carriers, so a parameter typed otherwise MUST be named something other than `pi`; the reservation is enforced unconditionally on the parameter name regardless of whether the parameter ever transports Pi-side surface, on the same footing as the canonical-name `ctx` reservation immediately preceding the off-canonical-name `pi` clause, and the prohibition is in family (4) under its own discriminator on the same footing as the off-canonical-name `pi` clause immediately preceding), any function/method parameter declaration whose binding shape in parameter position is a destructuring pattern (an object binding pattern such as `{ ui }` or an array binding pattern such as `[first]`, in either case in parameter position rather than a single named identifier) and whose explicit type annotation on that destructured parameter is the literal `ExtensionAPI`, `ExtensionContext`, or `ExtensionCommandContext` — the canonical carriers under *Target surface categories* (1) and (3) above are required to be a single named identifier (`pi` for `ExtensionAPI`, `ctx` for `ExtensionContext` / `ExtensionCommandContext`), so a destructured form such as `function handler({ ui }: ExtensionContext)` or `function factory({ registerCommand }: ExtensionAPI)` is prohibited even though no off-canonical identifier name appears (the destructured binding has no parameter-name identifier the off-canonical-name and off-canonical-annotation clauses above could key on); the prohibition is in family (4) under its own discriminator on the same footing as the off-canonical-name and off-canonical-annotation clauses immediately preceding, any function/method parameter declaration whose explicit type annotation is a wrapped, intersected, union-typed, generic-applied, or aliased form of `ExtensionAPI`, `ExtensionContext`, or `ExtensionCommandContext` rather than the bare textual literal — including but not limited to type-operator wrappings (`Readonly<ExtensionAPI>`, `Partial<ExtensionContext>`, `Required<ExtensionCommandContext>`, and any other built-in or user-defined type-operator wrapping), intersection forms (`ExtensionAPI & SomeMixin` and the symmetric `SomeMixin & ExtensionAPI`), union forms (`ExtensionAPI | SomeOther`), generic-applied forms (`ExtensionAPI<T>`, whether or not the SDK declares `ExtensionAPI` as generic at the loom 1.0 Pi-SDK pin), and aliased forms (`pi: API` where `API` is introduced by an `import type { ExtensionAPI as API } from "@earendil-works/pi-coding-agent"` rename specifier — itself separately prohibited under the aliased-import-specifier clause above — or by any local `type API = ExtensionAPI` alias declaration anywhere in the audited source tree) — only the three bare textual literals `ExtensionAPI`, `ExtensionContext`, and `ExtensionCommandContext` are permitted as the canonical carrier annotation, since the carrier rule under *Target surface categories* (1) and (3) above resolves the annotation textually (per the *resolved against the textual annotation rather than against an inferred type* clauses there) and a wrapped, intersected, union-typed, generic-applied, or aliased annotation would silently bypass that textual resolution; the prohibition is in family (4) under its own discriminator on the same footing as the off-canonical-annotation clauses immediately preceding, any function/method parameter declaration whose explicit type annotation is a type-parameter identifier whose declared constraint is `ExtensionAPI`, `ExtensionContext`, or `ExtensionCommandContext` (e.g. `function makeHandler<C extends ExtensionContext>(c: C)`, `function init<P extends ExtensionAPI>(p: P)`, `function wrap<T extends ExtensionCommandContext>(t: T)`, including the symmetric class- and method-level forms `class Foo<C extends ExtensionContext> { m(c: C) {} }` and the equivalent arrow-function and method-shorthand declarations) — only the three bare textual literals `ExtensionAPI`, `ExtensionContext`, and `ExtensionCommandContext` are permitted as the canonical carrier annotation, since the parameter's textual annotation in this generic-laundering shape is the type-parameter identifier (e.g. `C`, `P`, `T`) rather than one of the three carrier literals and neither the carrier-detection rules under *Target surface categories* (1) and (3) above (which key on the bare textual annotation being the literal `ExtensionAPI` for category (1) or the literal `ExtensionContext` / `ExtensionCommandContext` for category (3)) nor the off-canonical-annotation clauses immediately preceding (which key on a parameter named `pi` or `ctx` whose textual annotation is some non-canonical-literal annotation, and which therefore do not fire when the parameter name is anything other than `pi` / `ctx` — e.g. `c`, `t`, `arg`) would fire on it, so the binding would silently transport the full Pi-side surface and category-(1)/(3) audit coverage of every member access reached through that binding would be silently lost; the prohibition is in family (4) under its own discriminator on the same footing as the off-canonical-annotation clauses immediately preceding, any TypeScript declaration anywhere in the audited source tree that creates a subtype of `ExtensionAPI`, `ExtensionContext`, or `ExtensionCommandContext` by naming one of those three carrier literals in `extends`/`implements`/`&` position — `interface MySubAPI extends ExtensionAPI { … }`, `interface MyCtx extends ExtensionContext { … }`, `interface MyCmdCtx extends ExtensionCommandContext { … }`, `class MyHandler implements ExtensionCommandContext { … }`, `class MyApi implements ExtensionAPI { … }`, `type MyApi = ExtensionAPI & SomeMixin` (and the symmetric `type MyApi = SomeMixin & ExtensionAPI` and the equivalent `interface MyApi extends ExtensionAPI, SomeMixin {}` form), and any other subtype-creation form that names one of the three carrier literals in an `extends`/`implements`/`&` position — and any subsequent function/method parameter declaration that consumes that subtype as its explicit type annotation (e.g. `function handler(myCtx: MyCtx) { myCtx.modelRegistry.… }`, `function init(api: MySubAPI) { api.registerCommand(…) }`) is prohibited even though no off-canonical identifier name appears on a parameter typed with one of the three carrier literals; the canonical-carrier rule under *Target surface categories* (1) and (3) above resolves the parameter's annotation textually against the literal `ExtensionAPI` / `ExtensionContext` / `ExtensionCommandContext`, so a subtype-named annotation (e.g. `MyCtx`) silently bypasses the carrier-detection branch (the off-canonical-name clauses fire only when the parameter's textual annotation is one of the three carrier literals; the off-canonical-annotation clauses fire only when the parameter's name is `pi` or `ctx`; a parameter named `myCtx` typed `MyCtx` matches neither), so the binding would silently transport Pi-side surface past the canonical-carrier rule; the prohibition is on the subtype-creation declarations themselves rather than on the downstream parameter annotations (since the declaration is the unique site the audit can syntactically detect by `extends`/`implements`/`&` position over one of the three carrier literals, and removing the declaration removes every downstream consumer in one edit), and the existing canonical declarations of the three carrier types in `@earendil-works/pi-coding-agent` itself are out of scope (they live outside `src/` per *Audit scope* below); the prohibition is in family (4) under its own discriminator on the same footing as the off-canonical-annotation clauses immediately preceding, any class field declaration, class property declaration, top-level `const` / `let` / `var` binding, or class-property initialiser anywhere in the audited source tree whose explicit type annotation is the literal `ExtensionAPI`, `ExtensionContext`, or `ExtensionCommandContext` (e.g. `class Loom { private api: ExtensionAPI; … }`, `class Loom { private ctx: ExtensionContext; … }`, `const sharedCtx: ExtensionContext = makeCtx();`, `let cachedApi: ExtensionAPI = …;`) — the canonical carriers under *Target surface categories* (1) and (3) above are pinned syntactically as a function or method parameter declaration whose name is the literal identifier `pi` (for `ExtensionAPI`) or `ctx` (for `ExtensionContext` / `ExtensionCommandContext`), so a non-parameter binding (a class field, a top-level binding, or a class-property initialiser) carrying one of the three carrier literals as its explicit type annotation transports Pi-side surface past the parameter-position carrier-detection branch and past the off-canonical-name and off-canonical-annotation clauses immediately preceding (which key on parameter position and the literal `pi` / `ctx` parameter-name reservation), so any `pi.<member>` or `ctx.<member>` access reached through the non-parameter binding would be silently lost from inventory-closure coverage; Pi-side surface MUST flow through the canonical `pi` / `ctx` parameter carriers per *Target surface categories* (1) / (3), and constructor or method parameters that initialise such a field by the captured-rebinding rule (`this.api = pi`, `this.ctx = ctx`) are already prohibited under the captured-rebindings clause above — this clause closes the gap for non-parameter bindings whose annotation sources the carrier type from a non-canonical path (e.g. a factory return value, a module-scope constant, an injected handle); the prohibition is on the binding-declaration site itself rather than on the downstream member-access expressions (since the declaration is the unique site the audit can syntactically detect by the textual `ExtensionAPI` / `ExtensionContext` / `ExtensionCommandContext` annotation outside parameter position, and removing the declaration removes every downstream consumer in one edit); the prohibition is in family (4) under its own discriminator on the same footing as the off-canonical-annotation clauses immediately preceding, `Object.assign({}, pi)`, `keyof typeof pi`, and re-exports through barrel modules — are out of scope of inventory-resolution and MUST NOT be used on the `pi` namespace, on the canonical `ctx` identifier, or against any of the four peer packages anywhere in the audit's scope. The audit itself MUST enforce that prohibition under its own discriminator (see *Failure-surface contract* below) so the `pi.<member>` / `ctx.<member>` surface remains exhaustively coverable by syntactic recognition without committing PIC to a TypeScript-program-load tooling choice. The implementation MAY use a type-aware variant (e.g. a TypeScript-program symbol-table walk) provided the canonical-`pi`-carrier and canonical-`ctx`-carrier rules and the prohibition above continue to be enforced with the same per-discriminator routing — the audit's behavioural contract is invariant under tooling choice; what changes is only the implementation.
- <a id="audit-scope"></a>*Audit scope.* The *audited source tree* — the canonical scope name every other paragraph on this page (and the [`spec.md` — Orientation — Prerequisites](../spec.md#orientation) cross-reference) MUST use when naming this audit's scope — is defined as the closed file set matching the positive include glob `src/**/*.ts` (hand-authored TypeScript runtime source files under `src/`, recursive), minus the excluded files enumerated here. The include glob is closed: files outside `src/` (notably anything under `test/`, which is wholly outside the included root) and files inside `src/` whose extension is not bare `.ts` (e.g. `.tsx`, `.cts`, `.mts`, `.d.cts`, `.d.mts`, `.js`, `.mjs`, `.cjs`, `.json`, `.md`, fixture data files in any other extension) are out of scope by not matching the include glob and need no separate exclusion. *Cross-platform glob normalisation.* The glob is case-sensitive on the literal segment text — both the directory segments (`src/`) and the filename leaf — and the implementation MUST normalise filename comparisons to case-sensitive matching across host OSes, so a Linux contributor (case-sensitive FS) and a Windows / macOS contributor (case-insensitive FS by default) audit the same closed file set for a given source tree. A file whose on-disk name is, e.g., `src/extension/Index.TS` does **not** match the include glob; the audit MUST surface no Pi-side reference inside it and any in-scope reference there is a contributor-side scope violation rather than a silently-walked input. *Symlink handling.* Symlinks under `src/` MUST NOT be followed: the implementation MUST treat each symlink as opaque (the link entry itself is not walked as a file, and its target is excluded from the walk regardless of whether the target lies inside or outside `src/`). This rule holds uniformly for file-symlinks and directory-symlinks under `src/`, so an audit run on a tree that contains a symlink into `node_modules/`, into the build target, or into another worktree produces the same closed file set as a tree without the symlink. *Extension-suffix matching.* The `.ts` extension is matched case-sensitively against the literal `.ts` suffix on the leaf segment: `.tsx`, `.cts`, `.mts`, `.d.cts`, `.d.mts`, and any case-variant of `.ts` (e.g. `.TS`, `.Ts`) are out of scope by failing the include glob and need no separate exclusion. The `.d.ts` declaration / type-stub case is the one nominally-`.ts` suffix that *does* match the include glob and is therefore handled by the explicit `*.d.ts` entry in the exclusions list below, not by this paragraph. *Source-file encoding.* Source files in scope MUST be UTF-8-encoded; UTF-8 with BOM is permitted (the BOM is stripped before parsing). Files in any other encoding (e.g. UTF-16 LE / BE, UTF-32, or any non-Unicode legacy encoding) fail the audit under the *Infrastructure-failure handling* (i) implementation-agnostic category below as a parse failure, on the same footing as a syntax error raised by the audit's own walker on an audited file. Excluded files matching the include glob are: any `*.test.ts` co-located under `src/`; any `*.spec.ts` co-located under `src/`; any `*.d.ts` declaration / type-stub file (which carries no executable Pi-side surface reference at runtime); any file whose path contains a `__tests__/` directory segment at any depth under `src/`; and the `SessionShutdownEvent['reason']` brand-string assertion module if the implementation places it under `src/extension/` *and* the file path matches the suffix convention `src/extension/**/*.assert.ts` (the suffix is pinned exclusively to `*.assert.ts` here; the implementation MUST NOT substitute another suffix, since a permissive substitution — e.g. a leaf picking `*.ts` — would defeat the audit's scope altogether and a per-leaf alternative offers no audit-side value over the pinned suffix) — the suffix is the audit's only syntactic discriminator for the assertion module's role under `src/extension/`, since a static-AST walker has no other signal to identify it without coupling to the brand-string text. An inlined or otherwise embedded `SessionShutdownEvent['reason']` brand-string assertion in any other `src/extension/**/*.ts` file (i.e. one that does not match the pinned suffix) is **not** excluded by this item; the audit MUST resolve the brand-string assertion's `Type.Unsafe` (and any other in-scope) references in such a file through the normal inventory rules above on the same footing as any other `src/extension/` source file (its other permitted location, `test/`, is already outside the included root, per step 5 below). Generated build outputs MUST NOT be emitted into `src/` — the include glob describes hand-authored runtime source, and the build target (`dist/` or equivalent) is outside the included root by construction; an implementation that violates this rule by writing generated `.ts` files under `src/` violates this section rather than silently expanding audit coverage. *Generated-output-in-src limitation (acknowledged soft surface).* The prohibition is **contributor-discipline-only**: the inventory-closure audit walks `src/**/*.ts` blindly per the include glob above, so a generated `.ts` file emitted under `src/` would be walked on the same footing as a hand-authored file and any Pi-side surface references in it would either surface as family (1) / (2) / (3) violations against `SDK_SURFACE_INVENTORY` or be silently authorised by inventory entries (or `// allow-pi-surface:` markers) the generator emits — the prohibition itself has no mechanical surface inside the inventory-closure audit's five-family set above (its closure rule above forbids widening to a sixth family in this PIC edit), and is mitigated by the contributor obligation to keep the build target outside `src/` rather than by an audit discriminator. This soft surface is parallel to the *Substitution limitation* and *Stale-citation limitation* framings under *Stale-marker discriminator* below: PIC pins the prohibition and acknowledges that detection is contributor-side. The implementation MAY publish a separate scope-audit check (e.g. a `// @generated` leading-comment heuristic on every `src/**/*.ts` file walked by the inventory-closure audit) under its own `scope-audit/generated-source-in-tree` discriminator — sibling to but disjoint from the inventory-closure audit's five-family set, since this is a scope-violation discriminator rather than an inventory-resolution discriminator — but PIC does not require it; widening the inventory-closure audit's family-set to subsume this check is a PIC edit deferred past loom 1.0. The three-class `<class>` closure pinned by the *Failure-surface contract* below (the closed enumeration `violation` / `infra` / `canary`) binds the inventory-closure audit's own records only; a sibling scope check of this kind, which is not part of the inventory-closure audit, MUST use a separate top-level prefix outside the `audit/` namespace (the `scope-audit/<symptom>` shape above is illustrative, and the implementation MAY pick another non-`audit/` prefix at its discretion), so its discriminator is not subject to the three-class closure and does not perturb that closure's exhaustiveness. A future change adopting any in-tree test, fixture, generated-output, or other source-tree convention not enumerated above (e.g. a `*.fixture.ts` convention, a `**/fixtures/**` directory under `src/`, a `*.tsx` runtime extension, a `*.gen.ts` codegen output) MUST extend either the include glob or the exclusion list in this paragraph in the same edit that introduces the convention; silently inheriting an unenumerated convention as either in-scope or out-of-scope is a violation of this section.
- <a id="audit-category-2-inventory-join-key"></a>*Category-(2) inventory join key.* The audit resolves a category-(2) named import **from one of the four `@earendil-works/*` peer packages** (`pi-coding-agent`, `pi-agent-core`, `pi-ai`, `pi-tui`) (per *Target surface categories* (2) above) to an `SDK_SURFACE_INVENTORY` entry by **exact match** between the imported symbol identifier and the **leftmost dot-separated segment** of the entry's `path` field. This rule is scoped to those four peer packages exclusively: `typebox` imports are out of scope of this rule; see the *Target surface categories* `typebox` carve-out above for the `typebox` named-import allow-list resolution path (and the parallel `typebox` member-access allow-list for `Type.<member>` access). Concretely, an `import { <Name> } from "@earendil-works/<peer>"` declaration resolves iff some inventory entry's `path` field equals `<Name>` exactly or starts with the literal substring `<Name>.` (i.e. `<Name>` followed by a single ASCII `.` followed by any non-empty suffix); a `path` field whose leftmost segment is a strict-prefix-but-not-equal of `<Name>` (e.g. inventory `path: "Foo.bar"` against import `<Name> = "FooBar"`) MUST NOT resolve, and a `path` field whose leftmost segment is `<Name>` followed by any character other than `.` (no segment separator) MUST NOT resolve. The package specifier is **not** part of the join key — multiple `import { <Name> } from "@earendil-works/<peer>"` declarations of the same `<Name>` from the same peer package resolve to the same inventory entry, and the audit MUST NOT require one inventory entry per `(package, name)` pair. `<Name>` in this rule is the **canonical (source) name** of the named-import specifier — i.e. the identifier that appears before any `as`-rename in an `import { <Name> } from "@earendil-works/<peer>"` declaration; the join key (and, symmetrically, the `typebox` named-import allow-list whose single permitted entry is `Type`, which resolves `typebox` imports per the *Target surface categories* carve-out above rather than through this rule) consumes the canonical name only and never the renamed local binding. The `as`-rename form `import { <Name> as <Alias> } from "@earendil-works/<peer>"` (and the `typebox` and re-export analogues) does not reach this resolution path — it is forbidden under family (4) by *Recognised import/access shapes* above as an aliased rebinding — so the question of whether the join key would consume `<Name>` or `<Alias>` is moot by construction; an audit implementation MUST NOT permit the renamed form to silently resolve through either authorisation path. The existing `type-union-snapshot` entry at `path: "SessionShutdownEvent.reason"` accordingly resolves an `import { SessionShutdownEvent } from "@earendil-works/pi-coding-agent"` declaration via the leftmost-segment rule above (the leftmost segment of `"SessionShutdownEvent.reason"` is the literal `SessionShutdownEvent`, which equals the imported identifier exactly); the audit does NOT detect member-access references on category-(2) named imports (per *Target surface categories* above), so `SessionShutdownEvent.reason` member-access drift is gated by the brand-string assertion of [step 5](#pi-version-bump-procedure) (typecheck-time) rather than by category-(2) audit-time resolution. New category-(2) entry kinds coined per *Target surface categories* above MUST carry a `path` field whose leftmost dot-separated segment is the imported symbol identifier so they participate in this join key without a per-kind carve-out. Two `SDK_SURFACE_INVENTORY` entries MUST NOT share the same whole `path` value, and (for category-(2) audit-participating kinds) no two entries may both be bare leftmost segments — e.g. two entries with `path: "Foo"` collide and fire `literal-read/duplicate-path-segment` (or a category-specific variant the implementation coins, e.g. `literal-read/duplicate-leftmost-segment`), but two entries with `path: "Foo.bar"` and `path: "Foo.baz"` are legal multi-segment matches resolved per the lex-min tie-break below. For category-(1) and category-(3) audit-participating kinds, the same uniqueness rule applies symmetrically on the rightmost dot-separated segment (per *Category-(1)/(3) inventory join key* below; the parallel category-specific variant the implementation may coin is `literal-read/duplicate-rightmost-segment`). For legal multi-segment matches (e.g. `Foo.bar` and `Foo.baz` both resolving against `import { Foo }`, where neither entry is a bare `Foo`), the audit's `proposed-resolution` field reports the entry with the lexicographically-smallest `path` for determinism.

  <a id="audit-category-1-3-inventory-join-key"></a>*Category-(1)/(3) inventory join key (per-category specialisation).* The leftmost-segment rule above is the category-(2) named-import resolution rule and is preserved unchanged for that category. Categories (1) and (3) resolve by a per-category specialisation against the same `SDK_SURFACE_INVENTORY` source of truth, because the existing category-(1)/(3) entry shapes carry the carrier name as the leftmost dot-separated segment of the `path` field rather than the accessed member name — so a leftmost-segment match against the carrier-named segment cannot identify the accessed member, and the audit MUST instead match on the rightmost segment. Concretely: for category (1) `pi.<member>` accesses (carrier `pi: ExtensionAPI`), the audit resolves against `SDK_SURFACE_INVENTORY` by **exact match** between `<member>` and the **rightmost dot-separated segment** of an entry's `path` field — so an `SDK_SURFACE_INVENTORY` entry with `path: "pi.registerCommand"` (e.g. the existing `namespace-function` entries enumerated for the ten factory-probable function members) resolves against a `pi.registerCommand(...)` access by the rightmost segment `registerCommand` matching `<member>`. For category (3) `ctx.<member>` accesses (carrier `ctx: ExtensionContext` / `ctx: ExtensionCommandContext`), the audit resolves by **exact match** between `<member>` and the **rightmost dot-separated segment** of an entry's `path` field — so an entry with `path: "ExtensionContext.modelRegistry"` or `path: "ctx.modelRegistry"` resolves against a `ctx.modelRegistry(...)` access by the rightmost segment `modelRegistry` matching `<member>`. The category-(2) leftmost-segment rule above governs category-(2) named-import resolution exclusively and is unaffected by this specialisation; the rightmost-segment rule here governs category-(1) and category-(3) member-access resolution exclusively and does not perturb the category-(2) join key.
- <a id="audit-exemption-mechanism"></a>*Exemption mechanism.* A surface reference outside the inventory MAY be permitted only via a same-line comment marker on the offending source line of the form `// allow-pi-surface: <REQ-ID-or-PIC-anchor> <separator> <justification>`. The same-line-trailing-comment design and the leading `// allow-…:` token shape parallel the `// allow-broad-catch: <REQ-ID> — <spec-page>` and `// allow: <REQ-ID> — <spec-page>` grammars the parallel ESLint rules already pin, but the post-`:` payload deliberately differs in both positions: position 1 admits a PIC anchor as a peer of a REQ-ID (rather than as a deprecated transitional spec-page-anchor form), because PIC owns the inventory surface this audit guards and before REQ-ID anchors land there are no REQ-IDs to cite for PIC-owned surface; position 2 takes a free-form justification (rather than a spec-page reference), because the audit's per-discriminator routability obligation below requires the marker to explain *why* a specific surface is intentionally unenumerated, which a bare spec-page anchor cannot carry. Contributors expecting the cited two-position `<REQ-ID> — <spec-page>` shape MUST NOT carry it over verbatim. The marker MUST cite either a REQ-ID (once those anchors land) or, in the interim, a PIC anchor explaining why this specific surface is intentionally outside the inventory; an exemption marker without a citation or without a justification clause fails the audit. There is no separate `kind: "exemption"` entry on `SDK_SURFACE_INVENTORY` — the marker is the sole declaration site, mirroring the parallel ESLint rules' same-line-comment design. The exemption mechanism is scoped to families (1), (2), and (3) of the *Failure-surface contract* below — i.e., it MAY silence an unauthorised `pi.<member>` access, an unauthorised peer-package named import or an unauthorised typebox surface (a named import other than `Type` from `typebox`, or a `Type.<member>` member-access where `<member>` is not in the typebox member-access allow-list `{ Unsafe }`), or an unauthorised canonical-`ctx` member access, each of which names a specific out-of-inventory surface a marker can authorise. Family (4) (out-of-scope import/access shape) is **not** exemptible: the absolute prohibition in *Recognised import/access shapes* above forbids `import * as pi`, default/dynamic/side-effect-only peer imports, computed access, namespace destructuring, aliased or captured rebindings (including the `import { Foo as Bar } from "@earendil-works/<peer>"` / `import { Foo as Bar } from "typebox"` aliased-import specifier and the symmetric `export { Foo as Bar } from` re-export specifier from those same packages, on the same footing as value-binding aliased rebindings; the canonical name MUST be used unrenamed), off-canonical-name `ExtensionContext` / `ExtensionCommandContext` / `ExtensionAPI` parameters, off-canonical-annotation `ctx` parameters (a parameter named `ctx` whose explicit type annotation is not `ExtensionContext` or `ExtensionCommandContext`, including the unannotated form, the `ctx: any` form, the `ctx: unknown` form, and any other annotation), off-canonical-annotation `pi` parameters (a parameter named `pi` whose explicit type annotation is not `ExtensionAPI`, including the unannotated form, the `pi: any` form, the `pi: unknown` form, and any other annotation), `Object.assign({}, pi)`, `keyof typeof pi`, and barrel-module re-exports regardless of any same-line marker; a contributor confronted with such a shape MUST rewrite the source line into a recognised shape (per-symbol named import, `pi.<member>` static access, or canonical-`ctx` member access) rather than annotate it, per [step 2(b) branch (5)](#bump-step-2b-rewrite-shape) below. An `// allow-pi-surface:` marker on a family (4) line MUST NOT suppress the family (4) discriminator and is itself an audit failure under that discriminator. Family (5) (stale or malformed exemption marker) is resolved by *Delete or rewrite the stale or malformed exemption marker* per [step 2(b) branch (4)](#bump-step-2b-stale-rewrite) below, not by adding another marker. The audit MUST detect stale exemption markers (a marker on a line whose surface reference would now resolve to an inventory entry, or whose surface reference has been removed altogether) and surface them under their own failure-mode discriminator (per the *Stale-marker discriminator* sub-paragraph below, which decomposes "surface reference would now resolve to an inventory entry, or has been removed altogether" into the two stale sub-kinds (s1)/(s2) and pins marker scope, multi-line placement, the precedence with the underlying-surface discriminator, and the substitution soft-surface), so an exemption cannot silently outlive the surface it justified.

  *Separator tolerance.* The `<separator>` token between the citation and the justification MUST be either the em-dash `—` (U+2014) or the ASCII hyphen-minus `-` (U+002D), with at least one ASCII space character (U+0020) on each side; the audit MUST accept both separator characters identically (so a Windows / mixed-encoding edit that substitutes hyphen-minus for the em-dash is a recognised marker, not a malformed one). The audit MUST NOT accept any other character in the separator slot — exhaustively, the rejected set is every Unicode code point assigned to general category `Pd` (Dash punctuation) other than U+002D and U+2014, plus U+2212 MINUS SIGN (which is general category `Sm`, not `Pd`, and so MUST be enumerated explicitly); illustrative members of the rejected set include U+2010 HYPHEN, U+2012 FIGURE DASH, U+2013 EN DASH, U+2015 HORIZONTAL BAR, U+2212 MINUS SIGN, U+FE58 SMALL EM DASH, U+FE63 SMALL HYPHEN-MINUS, and U+FF0D FULLWIDTH HYPHEN-MINUS, but the closed boundary is the `Pd \ {U+002D, U+2014}` ∪ `{U+2212}` set above and not this illustrative listing. The audit MUST NOT accept the separator without at least one space on each side; markers using an unrecognised separator character or omitting the surrounding spaces are *malformed* per the malformed-marker discriminator below.

  *Minimum justification.* The `<justification>` slot MUST be at least four characters long after trimming leading and trailing ASCII whitespace, AND MUST contain at least one character that is neither ASCII whitespace nor an ASCII punctuation character (where the ASCII punctuation set is the 32 characters ``!"#$%&'()*+,-./:;<=>?@[\]^_`{|}~``). A justification that is empty after trimming, shorter than the four-character floor, or composed exclusively of whitespace-and-punctuation characters fails the audit as *malformed* per the discriminator below. The four-character floor and the alphanumeric-content requirement together rule out the trivially-empty (`—`-then-whitespace), pure-punctuation (`— ...`, `— ???`), and one-or-two-letter-tautology (`— x`, `— ok`) cases the routability obligation cannot meaningfully consume.

  *Citation-token grammar.* The `<REQ-ID-or-PIC-anchor>` slot MUST match exactly one of two syntactic shapes: (i) a REQ-ID of the form `REQ-<digits>` where `<digits>` is one or more ASCII decimal digits (regex `REQ-[0-9]+`); or (ii) a PIC anchor of the form `PIC#<kebab-case-anchor>` where `<kebab-case-anchor>` matches the regex `[a-z0-9]+(-[a-z0-9]+)*` (lowercase ASCII letters and digits joined by single ASCII hyphen-minus characters, with no leading or trailing `-` and no consecutive `--`, no whitespace, no other characters). A citation token whose literal form does not match either shape fails the *Malformed-marker discriminator* clause (b) below as *malformed*. The check is purely lexical: the audit MUST NOT additionally resolve the cited REQ-ID against any spec-side rule registry or the cited PIC anchor against any anchor registry, so a marker citing a syntactically valid but non-existent `REQ-9999` or `PIC#nonexistent-anchor` parses as well-formed and authorises the surface. The acknowledged soft surface this leaves — a syntactically valid but stale or fabricated citation that nevertheless authorises the surface — is mitigated per the *Stale-citation limitation* sub-bullet under the *Stale-marker discriminator* below, on the same footing as the *Substitution limitation* there; widening the audit to validate citation resolution against a registry is a PIC edit deferred past loom 1.0.

  *Stale-marker discriminator.* A *stale exemption marker* is a same-line `// allow-pi-surface:` marker that is well-formed (passes every clause of the *Malformed-marker discriminator* below) but does not authorise any currently out-of-inventory in-scope surface reference. The rule decomposes as follows.

  - <a id="audit-inventory-first-resolution"></a>*Inventory-first resolution.* The audit MUST resolve every recognised in-scope surface reference (per *Target surface categories* and *Recognised import/access shapes* above) against `SDK_SURFACE_INVENTORY` first; references that fail inventory resolution that originate from the `typebox` peer package then consult the typebox sibling allow-lists (per *Target surface categories* typebox carve-out); references that fail both then consult any same-line `// allow-pi-surface:` marker for authorisation. The three resolution paths are strictly ordered: (1) `SDK_SURFACE_INVENTORY` first; (2) the typebox sibling allow-lists (per *Target surface categories* typebox carve-out) for typebox-package references only; (3) `// allow-pi-surface:` markers last. A reference resolving at any earlier step short-circuits before consulting later steps — equivalently, marker authorisation MUST NOT be consulted for a reference that already resolves through the inventory or through a typebox sibling allow-list, the typebox sibling allow-lists MUST NOT be consulted for a reference that already resolves through the inventory, and neither the inventory nor the typebox sibling allow-lists MUST be widened to mask a marker. This precedence is what makes the (s2) sub-kind below mechanically detectable — a marker on a line whose every recognised in-scope reference resolves through the inventory or through a typebox sibling allow-list is observed by the audit as authorising nothing, since the earlier resolution paths short-circuit before the marker is consulted; a marker-first ordering would silently re-authorise the same references and (s2) detection would be impossible.

  - *Marker scope is per source line.* A marker on line N authorises every in-scope surface reference (per *Target surface categories* above) whose recognised import/access shape originates on line N — see *Multi-line surface placement* below for which physical line "originates on" picks out when a reference spans multiple lines. A line MAY carry multiple in-scope references and a single marker authorises all of them; the audit MUST NOT require one marker per reference, since the same-line trailing-comment grammar admits only one marker per line. Contributors MAY split a marked line into per-reference lines for clarity, but the audit MUST accept the unsplit form.

  - *Multi-line surface placement.* For an in-scope reference whose source-text spans multiple physical lines, the *originating line* — the line a marker MUST trail to authorise that reference, and equivalently the "offending surface line" the *Malformed-marker discriminator* below clause (e) names — is fixed by shape: (i) for a category-(1) `pi.<member>` member-access expression split across lines (e.g., `pi\n  .registerCommand(...)`), the originating line is the line of the property identifier (the `.registerCommand(...)` line), not the line of the `pi` namespace identifier; (ii) for a named-import declaration split across lines whose marker trails the `import`-keyword line, the originating line is the line of the `import` keyword and the marker authorises every imported symbol on the declaration; (iii) for a category-(3) member-access expression on the canonical `ctx` identifier split across lines (e.g., `ctx\n  .modelRegistry\n  .find(...)`), the originating line is the line of the `ctx` identifier itself, not the line of any property identifier in the chain — the asymmetry with (i) is deliberate and is the audit's recognised marker placement for category-(3) access (a contributor authorising a runtime-passed `ctx`-rooted chain MUST place the marker on the `ctx` line); (iv) for a named-import declaration split across lines whose marker trails an individual imported-symbol line rather than the `import`-keyword line, the originating line is the line of that imported symbol's identifier and the marker authorises only that symbol — per-symbol marker placement on multi-line named imports is an alternative the audit MUST accept alongside the (ii) import-keyword placement, so a contributor can authorise individual symbols selectively without authorising the whole declaration. A marker on any other line of the multi-line span — including a line of the dotted chain in (i) or (iii) that is neither the relevant property/namespace line, an intermediate property identifier line in a (iii) `ctx`-rooted chain, an interior comment line inside the dotted chain, or a non-symbol line of a multi-line named import (e.g. an opening-brace-only line, a closing-brace-only line, a comma-only line, or an interior comment line) — fails malformed-marker clause (e) and routes to family (5) under that clause's `<symptom>` token; the underlying out-of-inventory reference additionally fires its own family (1) / (2) / (3) discriminator on the same audit run per the malformed-marker dual-emission rule below.

  - *Stale sub-kinds.* The audit MUST surface every stale marker under family (5) with a stable `<symptom>` token per sub-kind (per the *Failure-surface contract* below): (s1) *no-surface-on-line* — the originating line per *Marker scope* / *Multi-line surface placement* above contains zero in-scope surface references at audit time, whether because the marker was placed on a line that never held a recognised in-scope reference (a placement-error sub-case) or because one or more recognised in-scope references previously originated on that line and have since been removed (an all-references-removed sub-case left over from a refactor that deleted the references it authorised); the two sub-cases collapse into the single `<symptom>` token (s1) because they are not in general statically discriminable from a source-tree snapshot without git history, and the contributor recovery action is the same for both — delete the marker line per [step 2(b) branch (4)](#bump-step-2b-stale-rewrite) below sub-case 1 ("no-surface-on-line"); the placement-error vs all-references-removed distinction is preserved here as commentary for the contributor's diff-reading benefit, not as separate `<symptom>` tokens. (s2) *all-in-inventory* (short name; the predicate covers both `SDK_SURFACE_INVENTORY` resolution and typebox sibling allow-list resolution per *Target surface categories* typebox carve-out above, so the token is more precisely "all-in-inventory-or-allow-list" — PIC retains the shorter `<symptom>` token to keep the wire-discriminator stable, and the parenthetical here is the normative scope) — every in-scope reference on the originating line now resolves to an `SDK_SURFACE_INVENTORY` entry, or (for references whose carrier is the `typebox` peer package per *Target surface categories* typebox carve-out above) to a typebox sibling allow-list entry — `{ Type }` for named-import references and `{ Unsafe }` for `Type.<member>` member-access references — per the *Inventory-first resolution* rule above (the marker authorises nothing the inventory or the typebox allow-lists do not already), recovered by deleting the marker per [step 2(b) branch (4)](#bump-step-2b-stale-rewrite) below sub-case 2 ("surface-now-in-inventory"; the same sub-case covers a previously-unauthorised typebox surface — for example a `Type.Object` access — that has since been added to the `{ Unsafe }`-style member-access allow-list under [step 2(b) branch (2)](#bump-step-2b-promote)'s typebox-promotion arm). For both sub-kinds only the family (5) discriminator fires on the marked line — the line carries no out-of-inventory reference for a family (1) / (2) / (3) discriminator to attach to. The two `<symptom>` tokens MUST be distinct so a contributor routing to [step 2(b) branch (4)](#bump-step-2b-stale-rewrite) below can tell stray-or-stale-marker removal (sub-case 1) from promotion-to-inventory removal (sub-case 2) without re-reading the diff.

  - *Substitution limitation (acknowledged soft surface).* Substituting one out-of-inventory surface for a *different* out-of-inventory surface on a marked line (e.g., an `// allow-pi-surface:` marker authorising `pi.alpha` rewritten to `pi.beta` with the marker carried over — illustrative placeholder names; neither symbol is in `SDK_SURFACE_INVENTORY` at loom 1.0, and the rule applies regardless of which non-inventory symbols are involved) is *not* mechanically detectable by the audit: per-line scope means the marker continues to authorise the substituted reference, and the citation's free-text justification cannot be machine-validated against the new symbol. This soft surface is mitigated by the contributor obligation in [step 2(b) branch (4)](#bump-step-2b-stale-rewrite) below — every marker on a line touched by a refactor or bump commit MUST be re-read against the *Exemption mechanism* citation rule on the diff before the commit merges — and is **not** owed an additional audit discriminator.

  - *Stale-citation limitation (acknowledged soft surface).* A citation token that parses as well-formed per the *Citation-token grammar* above but whose REQ-ID does not (or no longer) name a stable spec ID, or whose PIC anchor does not (or no longer) name a stable anchor on this page (e.g. a typo'd `PIC#nonexistent-anchor`, a citation to a PIC anchor that has since been renamed or deleted, or a citation to a REQ-ID that was retired or never allocated), is *not* mechanically detectable by the audit: the *Citation-token grammar* check above is purely syntactic and the audit performs no citation-resolution sub-check. This soft surface is mitigated by the same contributor obligation in [step 2(b) branch (4)](#bump-step-2b-stale-rewrite) below that mitigates the *Substitution limitation* above — every marker on a line touched by a refactor or bump commit MUST be re-read against the *Exemption mechanism* citation rule on the diff before the commit merges, and a citation that has gone stale MUST be rewritten under that branch's *citation has gone stale* case rather than carried over — and is **not** owed an additional audit discriminator in loom 1.0; widening the audit to validate citation resolution would require attaching a registry of valid REQ-IDs and PIC anchors to the audit input, which is a PIC edit deferred past loom 1.0.

  *Malformed-marker discriminator.* A *malformed exemption marker* is any same-line trailing comment whose token-prefix — defined as the longest leading substring consisting of either the literal `//` line-comment opener or the literal `/*` block-comment opener, followed by any leading intra-comment whitespace, followed by an ASCII run of letters and `-` whose case-folded form (each ASCII letter compared without regard to case) equals the literal `allow-pi-surface` — matches the well-formed lowercase-ASCII literal `// allow-pi-surface` either exactly or up to one or both of the case-folding and block-comment-opener relaxations above (so `// allow-pi-surface`, `// Allow-Pi-Surface`, `// ALLOW-PI-SURFACE`, `/* allow-pi-surface`, and `/* Allow-Pi-Surface` all match this prefix as candidates, while `// allow_pi_surface`, `// allow-pi-surfaces`, `//allowpisurface`, and other near-miss spellings whose ASCII letter-and-`-` run does not case-fold to `allow-pi-surface` do **not** match this prefix and are not lexical exemption candidates) but which fails any of (a) presence of the trailing `:` immediately after the `allow-pi-surface` run (a marker like `// allow-pi-surface PIC#x — ...` without the colon is malformed); (b) presence of a citation token (REQ-ID or PIC anchor) before the separator; (c) the separator-tolerance rule above (unrecognised separator character, or recognised separator without the required surrounding spaces); (d) the minimum-justification rule above; (e) placement as a trailing comment on the offending surface line itself (a marker on the line above, on the line below, or as a standalone comment line is *not* on the offending source line and is therefore malformed); (f) all-lowercase-ASCII spelling of the `allow-pi-surface` run (a candidate whose run case-folds to `allow-pi-surface` but is not byte-for-byte the lowercase form — e.g. `// Allow-Pi-Surface: PIC#x — ...`, `// ALLOW-PI-SURFACE: PIC#x — ...` — is malformed; the well-formed prefix MUST be lowercase ASCII); or (g) shape as a single-line `//` comment (a candidate that opens with `/*` — including the single-line block form `/* allow-pi-surface: PIC#x — ... */` and any multi-line block form — is malformed; the well-formed marker MUST be a single-line `//` trailing comment, since the audit's per-line scope semantics in *Marker scope is per source line* above are defined against single-line trailing comments only). The audit MUST surface every malformed marker under family (5)'s discriminator, AND MUST additionally surface the underlying out-of-inventory reference (if any) under its own family (1) / (2) / (3) discriminator on the same audit run, so the contributor sees both that the marker did not parse and which underlying surface remains unauthorised; routing the malformed marker only to the underlying-surface discriminator would silently demote the contributor's intended exemption and is prohibited. Comments whose token-prefix does not match `// allow-pi-surface` at all per the definition above are not lexical exemption candidates and surface only under the underlying-surface discriminator (no malformed-marker report is owed for them); the implementation MAY additionally emit a non-blocking advisory for near-miss spellings, but PIC does not require it.
- <a id="audit-failure-surface-contract"></a>*Failure-surface contract.* Each violation the audit emits MUST be unambiguously routable by a reader to exactly one stable failure-mode discriminator naming the failure family. The family set is **exhaustive at exactly the five families enumerated here** — (1) unauthorised `pi.<member>` access; (2) unauthorised peer-package named import from one of the four `@earendil-works/*` peers, or an unauthorised typebox surface (a named import other than `Type` from `typebox`, or a `Type.<member>` member-access where `<member>` is not in the typebox member-access allow-list `{ Unsafe }`) per the carve-out under *Target surface categories* above; (3) unauthorised `ctx.<member>` member access on the canonical `ctx` identifier (per *Target surface categories* (3) and *Recognised import/access shapes* above); (4) out-of-scope import/access shape (per *Recognised import/access shapes* above); (5) stale or malformed exemption marker (per *Exemption mechanism* above — both stale markers whose underlying surface has been resolved or removed and malformed markers per the malformed-marker discriminator there route to this single family). An audit implementation MUST NOT emit a violation outside this set. Each violation record MUST identify the offending source path, line, symbol, and either the inventory entry or exemption marker the contributor would add to satisfy the audit, mirroring step 5 below's *PIC owns the routing semantics* obligation. The discriminator string carrying the family name MUST be a single grep-able token of the structural shape `audit/<class>/<family>/<symptom>` — `<class>` is fixed at exactly one of the three literal ASCII tokens `violation`, `infra`, or `canary` (the three-class partition PIC pins below); for the five violation families above the `<class>` segment is the literal `violation` and for every emitted record the `<class>` segment is one of these three literals (no other `<class>` tokens are permitted). `<family>` is the implementation-chosen short name for one of the five families above (one stable `<family>` token per family, fixed at first implementation and pinned as a permanent test invariant) and `<symptom>` is an implementation-chosen kebab-case symptom identifier (lowercase ASCII letters, digits, and `-` only; no whitespace, no `/`) — and MUST appear verbatim in every emitted violation record so a CI parser can route violations to families by token-prefix match without an out-of-band translation table, and additionally to one of the three classes by the `<class>` segment alone (the `audit/<class>/...` two-segment prefix) without consulting an out-of-band manifest. The implementation owns the literal `<family>` and `<symptom>` strings, the failure-message wording, and the negative-test fixtures, and pins them into permanent test invariants. The implementation MUST publish at least one negative-test fixture per stable `<symptom>` token enumerated under each family (so families with multiple sub-kinds — notably family (5) with stale sub-kinds (s1)/(s2) per *Stale sub-kinds* above and malformed-marker clauses (a)–(g) per *Malformed-marker discriminator* above — get one fixture per sub-kind/clause). A fixture floor on `<family>` count alone is too coarse to exercise the per-`<symptom>` routability obligation this paragraph pins, since a single family-(5) fixture would leave eight of the nine family-(5) `<symptom>` tokens unexercised (the family has nine tokens total: both stale sub-kinds (s1) and (s2) plus all seven malformed-marker clauses (a)–(g); one fixture exercises one token); PIC pins the per-`<symptom>` floor here and the implementation MUST NOT collapse multiple `<symptom>` tokens onto a single fixture. The implementation MUST additionally publish at least one negative-test fixture per multi-line surface-placement shape enumerated under *Multi-line surface placement* above (one fixture each for category-(1) `pi.<member>` split, category-(2) named-import split, category-(3) `ctx`-rooted chain split, and per-symbol marker placement on multi-line named imports), exercising the originating-line rule for each shape — without these the asymmetric originating-line rule between (i) and (iii) is unexercised by the per-`<symptom>` fixture floor above and an audit implementation that always uses line 1 of any multi-line span would satisfy the floor while violating the placement rule. PIC pins the family-set closure, the structural `audit/<class>/<family>/<symptom>` shape, the three-class `<class>` enumeration above, the three-class partition pinned in the next sentence, the per-`<symptom>` fixture floor pinned in the previous sentence, and the per-discriminator routability obligation here. *Three-class partition.* PIC pins the partition of the audit's leaf-chosen `<family>` tokens across the three `<class>` prefixes as: `violation` covers the five inventory-closure-audit families enumerated above; `infra` covers the infrastructure-failure-handling families per [Infrastructure-failure handling](#audit-infrastructure-failure-handling) below; `canary` covers the non-empty-scan canary's families per [Non-empty-scan canary](#audit-non-empty-scan-canary) below. The leaf's existing `<family>` tokens MUST be re-namespaced under one of the three `<class>` prefixes per this partition (each `<family>` token belongs to exactly one class, which class is fixed by the obligation that introduces it), and the per-class disjoint-token obligations the *Infrastructure-failure handling* and *Non-empty-scan canary* sub-paragraphs below pin reduce to within-class `<family>` disjointness for each class — cross-class disjointness is structurally guaranteed by the `<class>` prefix and need not be re-asserted on the `<family>` tokens themselves. PIC pins the **family→step-2(b) routing table** below — the normative mapping from each of the five families above to the closed subset of step 2(b) below's five resolution arms a contributor MUST pick from when fixing a violation in that family. The implementation MUST additionally publish an implementation-side family→step-2(b) routing table that names its chosen `<family>` tokens (which PIC does not pin) as keys, whose per-row branch subset is either identical to the corresponding row below or a strict subset of it (an implementation MAY further narrow an individual row to a smaller branch set if its own implementation choices warrant — e.g. an implementation that has chosen never to use the exemption mechanism MAY drop branch (3) from rows (1)–(3) — but MUST NOT widen any row by adding a branch the corresponding PIC row does not list), and pin its implementation-side table as a permanent test invariant:

    | Family                                            | Permitted step-2(b) branches                                                                                                                          |
    |---------------------------------------------------|-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|
    | (1) unauthorised `pi.<member>` access             | branch (1) [delete](#bump-step-2b-delete), branch (2) [promote](#bump-step-2b-promote), branch (3) [exempt](#bump-step-2b-exempt)                     |
    | (2) unauthorised peer-package named import or unauthorised typebox surface | branch (1) [delete](#bump-step-2b-delete), branch (2) [promote](#bump-step-2b-promote), branch (3) [exempt](#bump-step-2b-exempt)                     |
    | (3) unauthorised `ctx.<member>` access            | branch (1) [delete](#bump-step-2b-delete), branch (2) [promote](#bump-step-2b-promote), branch (3) [exempt](#bump-step-2b-exempt)                     |
    | (4) out-of-scope import/access shape              | branch (1) [delete](#bump-step-2b-delete), branch (2) [promote](#bump-step-2b-promote), branch (5) [rewrite-shape](#bump-step-2b-rewrite-shape) — branch (3) exempt MUST NOT appear here per the *Exemption mechanism* family (4) prohibition above |
    | (5) stale or malformed exemption marker           | branch (4) [stale-or-malformed-rewrite](#bump-step-2b-stale-rewrite)                                                                                  |

    *Note on family (5) routing.* Family (5) maps to branch (4) as the primary resolution arm — that is the only branch the table above lists for family (5), and the only arm a leaf-side routing table is permitted to name on the family-(5) row. Branch (4) sub-case (v) (the *no-exemption-intended, malformed-marker only* sub-case under [step 2(b) branch (4)](#bump-step-2b-stale-rewrite) above, which deletes the marker and resolves the underlying surface via branch 1, 2, or 3) and the *Malformed-marker dual-emission co-commit obligation* (also under [step 2(b) branch (4)](#bump-step-2b-stale-rewrite) above, which co-commits the family-(5) marker fix with the underlying-surface fix the audit's dual-emitted family (1) / (2) / (3) record names) may further route the contributor through branches (1), (2), or (3) for the underlying-surface fix that accompanies a marker delete or grammar rewrite. This further routing is internal to branch (4)'s resolution semantics rather than a widening of the family-(5) row above: the contributor enters the family-(5) red through branch (4), and the underlying-surface fix the same commit lands is the resolution of a *separate* family (1) / (2) / (3) red the audit dual-emits onto the same `(path, line)` key per *Malformed-marker dual-emission co-commit obligation*, picked under branches (1) / (2) / (3) of step 2(b) below per the table above's family (1) / (2) / (3) rows. Family (5) does NOT inherit branch (3)'s exempt option directly — exemption markers are non-exemptible by their own discriminator (an exemption-marker record on a marker line does not itself describe an in-scope SDK surface reference, so the *Exemption mechanism* grammar has no carrier on which a same-line `// allow-pi-surface:` marker on the marker line could attach).

    Each negative-test fixture MUST assert that (a) the discriminator token it emits matches the `audit/<class>/<family>/<symptom>` shape above (with `<class>` the literal `violation` for these violation-family fixtures), and (b) the `<family>` token it emits is the one the leaf-side routing table maps to the resolution arm a contributor would take to fix the fixture's seeded violation; PIC pins these two fixture assertions as required and leaves the leaf-side table's `<family>` token names (and any per-row narrowing the leaf has elected) leaf-owned within the closure above. *Per-family record-shape table.* A violation record carries four fixed fields — `path`, `line`, `symbol`, `proposed-resolution` — whose values per family are pinned by the table below; a violation record that omits any of the four fields, or that carries a value outside the per-family range below for a given family, violates this rule.

    | Family                                            | `symbol` value                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                  | `proposed-resolution` value                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                  |
    |---------------------------------------------------|--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|
    | (1) unauthorised `pi.<member>` access             | `<member>` — the bare identifier immediately following the `pi.` namespace at the offending member-access expression                                                                                                                                                                             | inventory-entry-suggestion: the `SDK_SURFACE_INVENTORY` entry the contributor would add per [step 2(b) branch (2)](#bump-step-2b-promote), or the canonical `// allow-pi-surface: <citation> — <justification>` marker per [step 2(b) branch (3)](#bump-step-2b-exempt)                                                       |
    | (2) unauthorised peer-package named import or unauthorised typebox surface | the package-qualified imported name in the form `<package-specifier>#<imported-name>` (e.g. `@earendil-works/pi-coding-agent#Foo` for `import { Foo } from "@earendil-works/pi-coding-agent"`, or `typebox#Bar` for a non-`Type` named import from `typebox`); for the typebox `Type.<member>` member-access case pinned under *Target surface categories* (2) above (carrier = the imported `Type` identifier, resolved against the typebox member-access allow-list), the package-qualified `<package-specifier>#<imported-name>.<member>` form `typebox#Type.<member>` (e.g. `typebox#Type.Object` for a non-allow-listed `Type.Object(...)` access)                                | as for family (1) — inventory-entry-suggestion per [step 2(b) branch (2)](#bump-step-2b-promote) or canonical exemption marker per [step 2(b) branch (3)](#bump-step-2b-exempt)                                                                                                                                              |
    | (3) unauthorised `ctx.<member>` access            | `<member>` — the bare identifier immediately following the canonical `ctx.` namespace at the offending member-access expression                                                                                                                                                                  | as for family (1) — inventory-entry-suggestion per [step 2(b) branch (2)](#bump-step-2b-promote) or canonical exemption marker per [step 2(b) branch (3)](#bump-step-2b-exempt)                                                                                                                                              |
    | (4) out-of-scope import/access shape              | the offending shape literal — the verbatim source text of the offending expression or import declaration, normalised to its single-line form (every run of one or more whitespace characters, including newlines, collapsed to a single space) so the record fits the one-record-per-line wire format below | recognised-shape suggestion: the rewrite-shape resolution per [step 2(b) branch (5)](#bump-step-2b-rewrite-shape). An `// allow-pi-surface:` marker MUST NOT be suggested here per the *Exemption mechanism* family (4) prohibition                                                                                            |
