    | (5) stale or malformed exemption marker           | `<n/a>` — the literal five-character ASCII sentinel `<n/a>` (lowercase, including the angle brackets); a stale marker's underlying surface has been resolved or removed and a malformed marker never parsed, so no underlying named symbol exists for this field to carry                       | deletion-or-rewrite suggestion per [step 2(b) branch (4)](#bump-step-2b-stale-rewrite) — naming whichever of that branch's five sub-cases the marker falls under (delete the marker line (no-surface-on-line — covering both the surface-removed and the placement-error cases the *Stale sub-kinds* paragraph above collapses under the single (s1) `<symptom>` token); delete the marker (surface-now-in-inventory); rewrite the marker's citation; rewrite the marker's grammar; (v) delete the marker and resolve the underlying surface via branch 1/2/3 (no-exemption-intended, malformed-marker only))                                                       |

    *Wire serialisation.* The audit's violation records (and the infrastructure-failure records the *Infrastructure-failure handling* sub-paragraph below pins onto the same shape) MUST be emitted as line-delimited UTF-8 text on **stdout** — one record per line, terminated by a single `\n`, with no JSON, no record grouping (e.g. by family or by file), and no trailing summary lines that share the leading-token shape below. The `audit/<class>/<family>/<symptom>` discriminator token the *Failure-surface contract* above pins MUST appear as the **leading whitespace-separated field** on each emitted line so a CI parser can route by leading-token prefix match without parsing the rest of the line, and partition records into the three classes by the `audit/<class>/...` two-segment prefix alone; the four record fields (`path`, `line`, `symbol`, `proposed-resolution` — in this fixed order) are packed into three tab-delimited record segments that follow the discriminator on the same line: segment (1) is the `path:line` pair (the `path` and `line` field values joined by a single ASCII colon `:`; a parser splits this segment on the rightmost `:` to recover the two field values, which accommodates Windows hosts whose `path` field may itself contain a `:` in the drive prefix), segment (2) is the `symbol` field value, and segment (3) is the `proposed-resolution` field value. The between-segment separator is the ASCII tab character (U+0009): each emitted line is the `audit/<class>/<family>/<symptom>` discriminator token, then a single ASCII tab, then segment (1) (`path:line`), then a single ASCII tab, then segment (2) (`symbol`), then a single ASCII tab, then segment (3) (`proposed-resolution`) — four tab-delimited tokens per line in total (the discriminator plus the three record segments). The four field values (`path`, `line`, `symbol`, `proposed-resolution`) MUST NOT contain the ASCII tab character on any record class (violation or infrastructure-failure) — bare identifiers, package-qualified imported names, the literal `<n/a>` sentinel, integer `line` values, and file paths are tab-free by their pinned shapes, and the family (4) `symbol` value is tab-free because the *Per-family record-shape table* above already collapses every run of one or more whitespace characters (including tabs and newlines) to a single ASCII space. The `proposed-resolution` field MUST be plain printable ASCII text (no tabs, no newlines, no non-ASCII characters); when the resolution arm a contributor would take cannot be expressed in plain ASCII, the leaf MUST collapse it to a printable-ASCII paraphrase that names the arm by reference (e.g. by the relevant `#bump-step-2b-*` anchor on this page) rather than by quoted source text. The four-field tab-separated shape (discriminator, `path:line`, `symbol`, `proposed-resolution`) is the wire contract a CI parser may rely on: a parser splitting each line on the ASCII tab obtains four fields, and a parser splitting the second field on the right-most `:` obtains the `path` and `line` sub-fields (the right-most-`:` rule accommodates Windows hosts whose `path` field may itself contain a `:` in the drive prefix). PIC pins the separator and the escaping rule above; the implementation MUST NOT substitute a different separator character or relax the no-tab obligation on any field. Records MUST be emitted in source-walk order — the audit's file-iteration order (which the implementation MUST pin to a deterministic ordering, e.g. lexicographic on POSIX-form path, so two runs against the same source tree emit byte-identical output) followed by within-file appearance order of references — and MUST NOT be re-ordered for visual grouping. The literal `<n/a>` sentinel above (lowercase ASCII, five characters, including the angle brackets) is the single permitted encoding for an absent named symbol on family (5) records and for an absent value on any infrastructure-failure-record field per the *Infrastructure-failure handling* sub-paragraph below; alternative encodings of an absent value (`""`, `null`, an empty field, `n/a` without brackets, `<N/A>`) MUST NOT be emitted. Stderr MAY carry a non-machine-parseable human-readable summary or warning text the implementation chooses (the *Non-empty-scan canary* sub-paragraph below already permits implementation-chosen failure-message wording), but the line-delimited stdout stream is the **sole** machine-parseable surface a CI parser is permitted to consume in loom 1.0; emitting violation or infrastructure-failure records on stderr, or in a JSON or grouped form on either stream, violates this rule.
- <a id="audit-infrastructure-failure-handling"></a>*Infrastructure-failure handling.* The audit MUST be fail-closed: any infrastructure failure that prevents it from reaching its assertions over the *audited source tree* (per *Audit scope* above) MUST surface as a non-zero exit from the `npm test` invocation step 2(b) names rather than as a silent green. The infrastructure-failure surface comprises (i) **implementation-agnostic failures** — a parse / syntax failure raised by the audit's own walker on an audited file, an audit-side file-system read failure on an audited path, a peer-package import failure preventing the audit module itself from loading, and a tool-side crash inside the audit (OOM, walker panic, parser/checker-host panic, write failure on the diagnostic sink); and (ii) **tooling-conditional failures** that arise only in a type-aware implementation (per the introductory paragraph's permission for a TypeScript-program symbol-table walk as an alternative to a static-AST walker) — a checker-side symbol-resolution failure on the audited surface (defined here by *category of failure* — a type-checker symbol-resolution failure on a Pi-imported symbol the audit relies on for type-directed resolution — and routed by that category description rather than by TS error code, since TypeScript publishes no closed taxonomy of error codes the spec could pin; illustrative examples at the loom 1.0 TypeScript pin are TS2304 (`Cannot find name`), TS2339 (`Property does not exist on type`), and TS2551 (the symbol-suggestion variant of TS2339), and any other diagnostic that fits the category description is on this rule. Assignability diagnostics — notably TS2322 (`Type X is not assignable to type Y`), and any other diagnostic whose category is type-equality / assignability rather than symbol resolution — are explicitly **not** in this category and remain owned by [step 1](#pi-version-bump-procedure) below's spec-prose-update obligation; routing them through this infrastructure-failure rule would silently swallow a real SDK-side type-equality regression on a load-bearing Pi-imported type as an infrastructure failure, which step 1 specifically prohibits by requiring the spec-prose update on every type error not carved out by the brand-string discriminator), and a module-import-resolution failure (the TS230x category step 1 above already names — TS2305 / TS2307 / TS2614 / TS2724 and any other diagnostic of the same category) originating at the bare-package import the audit performs to load the audited surface against the SDK. The two-category list is **non-exhaustive**: any failure raised inside the audit process before successful record emission that prevents the audit from reaching its assertions is on this rule, routed through an implementation-chosen `audit/infra/<family>/<symptom>` discriminator on the same footing as the named items. The behavioural predicate (raised inside the audit before successful record emission, prevents reaching assertions) is the sole gate on this expansion — implementer-side judgements about whether a given failure was "foreseen" are not part of the criterion, so uncaught exceptions thrown anywhere in the audit, host-process OOM the audit catches, file-handle exhaustion, and any other process-internal failure with the same behavioural shape are uniformly on this rule whether or not the implementer enumerated them in advance. A static-AST implementation has no checker-side resolve failure and no run-time bare-package import the audit relies on for SDK-side type resolution, so category (ii) is vacuously satisfied by such an implementation (the implementation-agnostic peer-package import failure of (i) — covering, e.g., a static-AST walker that nevertheless imports a peer package to read its `package.json` — is *not* in (ii) and remains live for both implementation choices); a type-aware implementation carries both. The TS230x routing carve-out — a module-import-resolution failure of the TS230x category above originating at the bare-package import the audit relies on routes through [step 2(a)](#bump-step-2-positive) below's surface-inventory update per the same rule step 5 names for the brand-string assertion's import-resolution failure — is meaningful only for type-aware implementations; in a static-AST implementation it has no surface to bind to and is a vacuous obligation rather than a missing one. The parse-/syntax-failure obligation in (i) is **not** duplicative with the project-wide `npm run typecheck` gate: both surfaces catch a TypeScript syntax error in `src/` (typecheck at typecheck time; the audit's walker at audit time), and a green `npm test` therefore requires both gates to be green; the audit gate is what guarantees the surface-set-closure property is checked against a parseable source tree even on a configuration where the typecheck script is mis-wired or temporarily skipped, and is the audit's own fail-closed wrapper rather than a delegation to the typecheck script. Each infrastructure failure MUST carry a stable discriminator distinct from the violation discriminators above (the same `audit/<class>/<family>/<symptom>` structural shape the *Failure-surface contract* pins, with the `<class>` segment fixed at the literal `infra` per the three-class partition there; cross-class disjointness against the five violation families above and the *Non-empty-scan canary* discriminators is structurally guaranteed by the `<class>` prefix, and the implementation MUST keep its `infra`-class `<family>` tokens within-class disjoint), and MUST emit one infrastructure-failure record per failure carrying the same `path`, `line`, `symbol` triple the *Failure-surface contract*'s violation records carry; `path`, `line`, and `symbol` MAY each independently be the literal `<n/a>` sentinel pinned by the *Wire serialisation* clause of the *Failure-surface contract* above when the failure precedes the resolution that field would otherwise carry — `path` is `<n/a>` when the failure precedes file-level resolution (e.g. a peer-package import failure or an audit-module load failure that never reaches a specific source file), `line` is `<n/a>` when the failure precedes line-level resolution within an otherwise-resolved file, and `symbol` is `<n/a>` when no named symbol applies to the failure (e.g. a parse failure on the file header). The four-field record shape and per-line wire serialisation pinned by the *Failure-surface contract* above apply unchanged to infrastructure-failure records; `proposed-resolution` on an infrastructure-failure record carries the implementation-chosen resolution arm a contributor would take to clear that infrastructure failure (e.g. a re-pin recipe per [step 2(a)](#bump-step-2-positive) for a TS230x module-import-resolution failure routed through the carve-out above), or the literal `<n/a>` sentinel when no contributor-actionable resolution is owed at the level the failure surfaces. *Partial-evaluation semantics.* An audit run that emits both real violations and infrastructure-failure records in the same invocation is permitted and is the expected behaviour when an infrastructure failure terminates the audit after some files have already been resolved: the run MUST emit every violation it has resolved before the infrastructure failure terminated it, then the infrastructure-failure record(s), then exit non-zero. The exit code is the single non-zero `npm test` exit and is not further subdivided — a contributor discriminates violation-only from violation-plus-infrastructure outcomes by reading the per-record `audit/<class>/<family>/<symptom>` discriminators on the audit's output (the `audit/<class>/...` two-segment prefix alone partitions records into the three classes), not by reading the exit code. *Wall-clock budget.* The audit MUST enforce a wall-clock budget on its own execution (the implementation pins the budget value, e.g. 60 s); on budget expiry the audit MUST emit one record under a stable `<symptom>` token in the infrastructure-failure family and exit non-zero. A hung audit that does not emit and does not exit falls under the *Pre-emission termination carve-out* below (the `npm test` red exit alone satisfies fail-closed, with the implementation pinning a `npm test`-side timeout to bound the overall run). *Pre-emission termination carve-out.* If the audit process is terminated before any record can be emitted — e.g. `SIGKILL` from the host OOM-killer, host shutdown, a walker panic that crashes the process mid-write, or a diagnostic-sink write failure on a torn pipe before the first complete record has been flushed — the non-zero `npm test` exit alone satisfies the fail-closed property; no record-format contract (the *Failure-surface contract*'s per-family record shape, the *Wire serialisation* per-line stdout obligation, or the per-discriminator routability obligation above) applies on this path, since by construction no record was emitted to which those obligations could bind. The contributor's recovery path on a `npm test` red with no `audit/<class>/<family>/<symptom>` line on the audit's stdout is to re-run with diagnostic-sink redirection (the implementation-chosen mechanism, e.g. capturing the audit's stderr or attaching to the host's process-exit logs) to obtain whatever signal the underlying termination left behind.
- <a id="audit-non-empty-scan-canary"></a>*Non-empty-scan canary.* The audit MUST emit, on every invocation, two counters — the number of audited source files actually walked, and the number of in-scope surface references (the union of categories (1), (2), and (3) under *Target surface categories* above, plus any reference recognised by the audit's prohibited-shape detection per *Recognised import/access shapes* above — including the family-(4) shapes that are by construction not category (1)/(2)/(3) references) actually *recognised* by the audit, where a reference is *recognised* iff it either (a) resolves against `SDK_SURFACE_INVENTORY`, (b) resolves against a typebox sibling allow-list entry (per *Target surface categories* typebox carve-out), (c) is authorised by a declared `// allow-pi-surface:` exemption, or (d) surfaces as a violation against any of the five families of the *Failure-surface contract* above (so an all-violation run on a fresh codebase recognises every reference and does **not** trip the canary spuriously alongside the violations) — and MUST assert both counters strictly greater than zero. A misconfigured walker that scans zero files in the audited source tree, or that walks files but recognises zero in-scope surface references (e.g. a glob root, `tsconfig` `include`, or AST-visitor selector that silently matches nothing — i.e. the second counter guards only against under-walking, not against a population of unauthorised references), MUST surface as `npm test` red rather than as a silent green; without this canary the *Failure-surface contract*'s violation-emission obligation, the *Infrastructure-failure handling* obligation above, and the surface-set-closure property [`spec.md` — Orientation — Prerequisites](../spec.md#orientation) leans on are all vacuously satisfied by a no-op audit. Each non-zero-floor failure MUST carry its own stable discriminator (the same `audit/<class>/<family>/<symptom>` structural shape the *Failure-surface contract* pins, with the `<class>` segment fixed at the literal `canary` per the three-class partition there; cross-class disjointness against the five violation families above and the *Infrastructure-failure handling* discriminators is structurally guaranteed by the `<class>` prefix, and the implementation MUST keep its `canary`-class `<family>` tokens within-class disjoint) so a contributor can route a no-op-walker breakage separately from both a real inventory miss and an infrastructure-side breakage. *Green-path emission contract.* On every invocation — green or canary-red — the audit MUST emit exactly one canary record on stdout in the line-delimited four-field wire format the *Wire serialisation* clause of the *Failure-surface contract* above pins, leading with the canary's stable `audit/<class>/<family>/<symptom>` discriminator token (with `<class>` the literal `canary`; a green-path run MAY use a leaf-chosen `<symptom>` token disjoint from the canary-red `<symptom>` token under the same canary `<family>`, so a CI parser can distinguish green-path from canary-red records by the leading-token prefix without needing to parse the `proposed-resolution` field). The `proposed-resolution` field MUST carry the two counter values as the plain-ASCII key=value pair set `walked=<N> recognised=<M>` (or an equivalent implementation-chosen plain-ASCII key=value pair set whose pair names identify the same two counters this paragraph defines — the audited-files-walked counter and the in-scope-references-recognised counter, in that order), so a CI parser may inspect the audit's stdout to confirm both counters were observed on a green build. On a green run (both counters above their floors and no canary-red), `path`, `line`, and `symbol` MUST each be the literal `<n/a>` sentinel pinned by the *Wire serialisation* clause above. On a canary-red run, `path` / `line` / `symbol` identify the misconfiguration site if the audit can resolve it (e.g. the offending glob-root or `tsconfig` `include` source line); when the audit cannot resolve the misconfiguration site at the level the field would otherwise carry, the field carries the literal `<n/a>` sentinel per the same per-field rule the *Infrastructure-failure handling* sub-paragraph above pins. CI parsers MAY assert that exactly one canary record appears per invocation. The implementation MUST NOT emit zero canary records on any invocation (including a green run), MUST NOT emit more than one canary record on any invocation, and MUST NOT route the canary record through any sink other than stdout (mirroring the *Wire serialisation* sole-machine-parseable-surface rule above). *Infra-aborted-run carve-out.* If the audit terminates due to an infrastructure failure (per *Infrastructure-failure handling* above) before reaching the canary's two-counter computation, the "exactly one canary record per invocation" obligation (and the "zero canary records" / "more than one canary record" prohibitions immediately above) do NOT apply: the run is permitted to emit zero or one canary records depending on how far the audit progressed before terminating, and the non-zero `npm test` exit (per the *Pre-emission termination carve-out* and the *Wall-clock budget* clauses of *Infrastructure-failure handling* above) is the fail-closed surface. CI parsers asserting on the canary obligation MUST exclude infra-aborted runs (identifiable by the presence of one or more infrastructure-failure records — records whose leading-token's `<class>` segment is the literal `infra` per the three-class partition pinned in the *Three-class partition* clause of the *Failure-surface contract* above — in the same stdout stream). *Canary-red contributor-facing resolution arm.* A canary-red record names a no-op-walker breakage rather than a member of the five violation families, so the family→step-2(b) routing table the *Failure-surface contract* above pins is **not** the routing surface for it; instead, a contributor seeing a canary-red record MUST resolve it by widening the audit's scope configuration (the audit's glob root, `tsconfig` `include`, AST-visitor selector, or equivalent walker-input pin under the audit implementation) until both counters clear their floors on the next `npm test` invocation, and a reviewer MUST check that fit on the canary-red-resolution diff. This arm is owned by PIC here rather than by step 2(b); the family→step-2(b) routing table remains restricted to the five violation families. *Order of evaluation against violation records.* The canary's counter-emission and assertion MAY co-emit with the audit's violation records on the same invocation: a run that emits both real violations and a canary-red record is permitted (and is the expected behaviour when the second counter trips on a glob-root miss whose narrowed scope nevertheless captured one or more in-scope but out-of-inventory references on its way to the floor breach), and a canary-red record MUST NOT suppress, defer, or otherwise demote any violation record the same run would otherwise emit. The exit code is the single non-zero `npm test` exit and is not further subdivided in loom 1.0 (mirroring the *Partial-evaluation semantics* clause of the *Infrastructure-failure handling* rule above) — a contributor discriminates violation-only from violation-plus-canary-red outcomes by reading the per-record `audit/<class>/<family>/<symptom>` discriminators on the audit's output (the `audit/<class>/...` two-segment prefix alone partitions records into the three classes), not by reading the exit code. The implementation owns the literal `<family>` and `<symptom>` strings and the failure-message wording, and pins them into permanent test invariants. The per-counter floor MUST be `> 0` for both counters; the implementation MAY pin a higher floor as a permanent test invariant if it has a baseline-snapshot mechanism (so the higher floor is mechanically tied to a recorded baseline rather than to a justification a reviewer would have to weigh), but PIC pins only the `> 0` floor here. PIC pins the two-counter requirement, the strictly-greater-than-zero floor, the disjoint-discriminator obligation, the green-path emission contract (the once-per-invocation canary record, its four-field wire shape, the `walked=<N> recognised=<M>` `proposed-resolution` pair set or its implementation-chosen equivalent, and the `<n/a>`-sentinel rule for `path` / `line` / `symbol` on a green run), the canary-red contributor-facing resolution arm, and the order-of-evaluation rule against violation records here.

The audit runs as part of the SDK surface-inventory tests step 2 below names (specifically, it is step 2(b)); `npm test` is the entry harness PIC pins as the test-side gate (the `npm test` script's existence, its concrete command, and its harness wiring — including any Vitest-style or equivalent test-runner wrapping — are implementation choices), and PIC does not pin a separate `npm` script for the audit. The implementation MUST wire the audit so that **both** an audit violation record (per the *Failure-surface contract* above) **and** an infrastructure-failure record (per the *Infrastructure-failure handling* sub-paragraph above) cause the `npm test` invocation to exit non-zero — irrespective of whether the audit runs in-process to the harness (e.g. as a Vitest test case whose `expect(...).toBe(0)` over the audit's exit code becomes the test's pass/fail) or as a child process the harness spawns and whose own non-zero exit code becomes the test's pass/fail; either wiring is permitted as long as the fail-closed property holds end-to-end. The implementation MUST wire the audit so that an audit child process whose exit code is non-zero AND that emits zero records (including process-killed and uncaught-exception terminations, per the *Pre-emission termination carve-out* above) causes `npm test` to exit non-zero. For the in-process variant, the wrapping `expect(...)` MUST be unconditionally registered before the audit invocation so a process kill aborts the harness and propagates non-zero. An implementation wiring that interprets empty stdout as 'no failures' violates this obligation. The audit's record emission MUST reach a sink whose contents survive the harness wrapping (stdout / stderr per the *Wire serialisation* rule above — the audit MUST NOT route records through a harness-internal API, an in-memory test reporter slot, or any other surface a CI parser cannot consume by reading process stdout / stderr), so that a CI parser can still consume the `audit/<class>/<family>/<symptom>` discriminator tokens on either wiring choice. The implementation MUST adopt one concrete audit implementation and one concrete `npm test` wiring so this contract has a single concrete adoption; an implementation whose `npm test` invocation does not exit non-zero on either record class above, or whose failure output does not satisfy the per-discriminator routability obligation above, or whose record emission does not survive the harness wrapping per the *Wire serialisation* rule, violates this section.

Item 5 (cancellation propagation) is verified jointly by Step 0 item (b)'s `AbortSignal` / `AbortController` shape probe (the two Pi-side entry-point signals) and Step 0 item (c)'s `AgentSession.prototype.abort` member check (the subagent-mode primitive). Item 7 (binder LLM model) is verified at per-loom load time and surfaces as `loom/load/binder-model-unresolved` per [Slash-Command Argument Binding — Strict-capability requirement](./binder.md#strict-capability-requirement); it is **not** factory-probable and the two diagnostic surfaces (`loom/load/host-incompatible` and `loom/load/binder-model-unresolved`) are disjoint. [`spec.md` — Orientation — Prerequisites](../spec.md#orientation) name-links each item back to the obligation here so that downstream tests cite a single anchored source.

1. <a id="sdk-cap-slash-command-registration"></a> **Slash-command registration.** Pi MUST expose `pi.registerCommand(name, { description, handler })` per **Extension entry point** above. The runtime calls this once per surviving discovered loom on `session_start`.

2. <a id="sdk-cap-prompt-conversation-drive"></a> **Prompt-mode conversation drive.** Pi MUST expose `pi.sendUserMessage(text [, { deliverAs }])` for issuing turns and `ExtensionCommandContext.waitForIdle()` for awaiting turn completion. Both are consumed by the prompt-mode driver per **Conversation drive — prompt mode** above.

3. <a id="sdk-cap-subagent-isolated-session"></a> **Subagent-mode isolated session.** Pi MUST expose `createAgentSession(...)` returning a disposable `AgentSession` whose transcript is private when `SessionManager.inMemory(cwd)` is supplied. Consumed by **Conversation drive — subagent mode** and **Subagent session lifecycle** above.

4. <a id="sdk-cap-tool-registration-gating"></a> **Tool registration and gating.** Pi MUST expose `pi.registerTool` (registration sink) and the `pi.getActiveTools` / `pi.setActiveTools` snapshot/restore pair for prompt-mode visibility control. Consumed by **Tool-registration lifetime and visibility** above. The lack of `pi.unregisterTool` and the resulting cosmetic registration-cache accumulation are documented in the same section.

5. <a id="sdk-cap-cancellation-propagation"></a> **Cancellation propagation.** Pi MUST supply an `AbortSignal` at the two extension entry points loom uses — `ctx.signal` on the slash-command `ExtensionCommandContext` and the `signal` parameter of `tool.execute(...)`. For subagent mode (which has no `AbortSignal` entry point — `CreateAgentSessionOptions` has no `signal` field in the loom 1.0 Pi SDK pin), Pi MUST expose `AgentSession.abort(): Promise<void>` on the handle returned by `createAgentSession(...)` so the runtime's one-shot `loomAbort.signal` listener can tear down the spawned session's in-flight provider call. The fixed-shape WHATWG `AbortSignal` / `AbortController` member surface is enumerated in [Step 0 (b)](#entry-capability-probe) above; `AgentSession.prototype.abort` is enumerated alongside `createAgentSession` under [Step 0 (c)](#entry-capability-probe)'s factory-probable members so a Pi version that drops or renames it surfaces as `loom/load/host-incompatible` rather than as a runtime-time `TypeError` at the spawn site. The loom-side `AbortController` wrapping rule and the listener-and-`abort()` mechanism are in **Cancellation source** and **Subagent session lifecycle** above and in [Cancellation](./cancellation.md). This rule and **Host prerequisites #4 — Pi-supplied `AbortSignal`** above are the same obligation viewed from the inventory and the host-prerequisite axes; the inventory entry is the cross-reference target for `spec.md` and consumers, the **Host prerequisites #4** paragraph is the in-page neighbour of the other host preconditions.

6. <a id="sdk-cap-custom-message-renderer"></a> **Custom-message channel and renderer.** Pi MUST expose `pi.sendMessage({ customType, content, display, details }, { triggerTurn })` for routing system notes through the custom-message channel and `pi.registerMessageRenderer(customType, renderer)` for rendering them in the transcript. The signature, lifecycle, and ownership rules are in **System notes** and **Renderer registration (`pi.registerMessageRenderer`)** above.

7. <a id="sdk-cap-binder-llm-model"></a> **Binder LLM model.** Non-bypass looms MUST be able to resolve a structured-output-capable LLM via `ctx.modelRegistry` (the `ModelRegistry` type pinned at [model-registry surface](#model-registry-pin) above). The runtime applies the **bypass criterion** at load time (no `params:`, or single string-typed parameter with no default) per [Binder — Bypass cases](./binder.md#bypass-cases); bypassable looms skip the binder call entirely, and non-bypass looms fail to load with `loom/load/binder-model-unresolved` if no structured-output-capable model is available. Strict-capability degradation, the same `loom/load/binder-model-unresolved` code on loom 1.0 strict-capability mismatch, and the `loom/load/binder-model-strict-capability-unknown` warning under the [loom 1.0 Pi-SDK pin](#pi-sdk-pin) are owned by [Binder — Strict-capability requirement](./binder.md#strict-capability-requirement); this rule defers the diagnostic-code semantics to that page.

<a id="sdk-cap-peer-dep-revalidation"></a>
**Re-validation on `peerDependencies` widening.** Widening `peerDependencies` requires re-validating the seven obligations above against the new Pi minor before the range moves; the re-validation artefact is the build-time SDK surface-inventory assertion passing against the new package, and the procedure that gates the bump is [Pi version bump procedure](#pi-version-bump-procedure) below.

<a id="pi-version-bump-procedure"></a>
## Pi version bump procedure

This subsection enumerates the contributor checklist that any change widening, narrowing, or otherwise moving the [loom 1.0 Pi-SDK pin](#pi-sdk-pin) on `@earendil-works/pi-coding-agent` (and the lock-step `pi-agent-core` / `pi-ai` / `pi-tui` minors) MUST follow. The three “requires re-validating” sentences elsewhere in the spec ([SDK capability inventory — Re-validation on `peerDependencies` widening](#sdk-cap-peer-dep-revalidation), the **Host prerequisites — Pi SDK pin** paragraph above on this page, and the strict-capability sentence in [Slash-Command Argument Binding — Strict-capability requirement](./binder.md#strict-capability-requirement)) all resolve to the steps below; the build-time tests cited at each step are the mechanical gates that fail loudly until the corresponding manual step has been completed.

1. **Re-typecheck against the new package.** Install the candidate `@earendil-works/pi-coding-agent` minor (and its lock-step siblings), run `npm run typecheck`, and confirm no Pi-imported types under the loom-load-bearing surface have changed shape in a way that breaks the runtime. Type errors here mean the candidate minor is not a drop-in replacement and the surface descriptions on this page MUST be updated before the bump can proceed. A failure of the bidirectional `SessionShutdownEvent['reason']` type-equality assertion (per step 5 below; the runtime invariant the assertion guards is the [Unknown-reason rule](#unknown-reason-rule) under **Extension entry point** sub-step 4 above) is the first expected exception to the spec-prose-update obligation in the immediately preceding sentence (the second is the module-import-resolution failure mode — `TS2305` / `TS2307` / `TS2614` / `TS2724` and any other TS code in the same module-import-resolution family that arises from a Pi-side rename/drop on the package-root re-export surface — discussed later in this step): it is handled by step 5 below (an edit limited to the `SessionShutdownEvent['reason']` snapshot entry's `literals` field in the extension module's pinned-constants block, per step 5; no spec-prose change). The mechanical discriminator the carve-out keys on is the literal brand string `loom/typecheck/session-shutdown-reason-snapshot` appearing in the failing `tsc` diagnostic, per step 5 below's brand-string requirement; a typecheck red whose diagnostic does not carry that brand string is not in the carve-out (this is what disambiguates the in-scope union-widening/narrowing failure from look-alike failures such as a TS2314 generic-arguments-required diagnostic produced by a Pi-side re-shape of `SessionShutdownEvent` into `SessionShutdownEvent<TReason>`, which mentions `SessionShutdownEvent` but does not originate at the brand-emitting assertion). The carve-out applies per-assertion, not per-invocation: an `npm run typecheck` invocation that reports both the brand-string-carrying red and any other typecheck red has only the brand-string-carrying red carved out, and every non-carved-out red in the same invocation still requires the spec-prose update this step prescribes. A module-import-resolution failure originating from the same assertion — surfacing as `TS2305` (`"Module '<path>' has no exported member '<name>'."`), `TS2724` (the "did you mean Y?" rename variant), `TS2307` (module not found), `TS2614` (default-vs-named-import mismatch), or any other TS code in the same module-import-resolution family produced by a Pi-side rename/drop of `SessionShutdownEvent` on the package-root re-export surface (so the assertion never reaches a value/type comparison) — is a second expected exception, and is **not** covered by step 5: route every TS code in that family through [step 2(a)](#bump-step-2-positive)'s surface-inventory update, re-pinning the import specifier in the same edit as the rest of the bump (per step 5 below's import-resolution routing). Routing keys on the TS error code, not on the message-text quote — the message-text quote above is illustrative of the TS2305 wording at the loom 1.0 Pi-SDK pin and may drift across TypeScript versions without affecting the routing contract. The "no spec-prose change" carve-out applies to the snapshot mechanics only: the source-of-truth for `event.reason`'s closed set is the extension module's pinned-constants block (per the [Unknown-reason rule](#unknown-reason-rule)), and the in-prose closed-set listings elsewhere — the sub-step 4 introductory paragraph, the [Unknown-reason rule](#unknown-reason-rule) itself (including its parenthesised re-listing), the [*Edge cases* `reason: "new" | "resume" | "fork"` bullet](#session-only-reason-degraded-state) (scoped to the closed-set listings within it — i.e. the prose enumerations of the closed `{"quit", "reload", "new", "resume", "fork"}` set — and explicitly excluding the inline `{"new", "resume", "fork"}` triplet at the `loom/host/session-shutdown-runtime-degraded` emission site, which is a normative runtime literal subject to the lock-step inbound-reference-sweep update obligation in step 5 below), the **Per-invocation operator visibility (clean-cancel path)** bullet's `"quit" | "reload" | "new" | "resume" | "fork" | string` widening, and the corresponding listing in [`spec.md` — Session model — SM-2 closed shutdown reason set](../spec.md#sm-2-closed-shutdown-reason-set) — are illustrative restatements of that constant pinned at write time, not independent normative copies. A Pi widening/narrowing handled under this carve-out therefore leaves those listings transiently stale with no runtime-correctness impact (the runtime consumes the snapshot constant, not the prose; the type-equality assertion of step 5 is the gate); bringing the prose back into byte-for-byte alignment with the new union is an editorial sweep folded into the next page-touching edit rather than a blocker on this step. The diagnostics §7 `<reason>` closed-enum row — declared under [Diagnostics — §7 Identifier-, descriptor-, and closed-enum placeholders](./diagnostics.md#7-identifier--descriptor--and-closed-enum-placeholders) and spec-versioned per GOV-7 / GOV-8 (extending the table is a breaking change to the rendering surface) — is the sole exception to that "illustrative restatement" status and is therefore the **sixth** co-edit site this carve-out enumerates, alongside the five illustrative restatements above. A Pi-side widening of `SessionShutdownEvent['reason']` *is* a GOV-7 / GOV-8 rendering-surface change for §7's `<reason>` row, and the §7 row MUST be updated in the same commit as the snapshot constant so the GOV-7 / GOV-8 invariant on the closed-enum rendering surface is preserved synchronously with the snapshot edit (no transiently-stale window for the §7 table; the snapshot-edit-only permission of this carve-out covers the five in-prose illustrative restatements only and does **not** authorise a snapshot edit to ship without its matching §7 row update). A Pi-side narrowing is symmetric: the §7 row's enumeration MUST be narrowed in the same commit as the snapshot constant. Treating the §7 row as part of the snapshot edit's commit (rather than as a separately re-litigated spec-prose change) is what keeps the carve-out's "no spec-prose re-litigation" property intact for the GOV-7 / GOV-8 surface — the rendering-surface change rides the snapshot edit synchronously rather than reopening the spec-review for the §7 table. Other typecheck failures still require the spec-prose update this step prescribes.

    *Editorial-review checklist for unpinned host presuppositions.* On each Pi minor bump, the contributor MUST audit the candidate Pi minor against each of the loom 1.0 presuppositions enumerated in items (a)–(e) below whose detection routes to editorial review under this procedure (the build-time SDK surface-inventory assertion is a presence check on the seven named SDK capabilities and does not enumerate behavioural invariants of these kinds), SHOULD additionally audit it against items (f) and (g) below per each item's SHOULD-level scope and escalation clause, and MUST record the per-item audit outcome (pass / fail / N/A with one-line rationale; item (e) requires two sub-outcomes — see [(e.i)](#bump-checklist-slash-dispatch-serialisation-i) and [(e.ii)](#bump-checklist-slash-dispatch-serialisation-ii) below; items (f) and (g) outcomes are recorded under the same shape when the SHOULD-level audit was performed) in the bump commit message:
    - (a) *Extension-instance survival across session-only `session_shutdown`* — sub-item (a) of [Host prerequisites for the degraded-state branch](#degraded-state-host-prerequisites) above.
    - (b) *Multi-`session_shutdown` delivery permitted to a single instance* — sub-item (b) of [Host prerequisites for the degraded-state branch](#degraded-state-host-prerequisites) above.
    - (c) *`/reload` and `ctx.reload()` recovery* — sub-item (c) of [Host prerequisites for the degraded-state branch](#degraded-state-host-prerequisites) above.
    - (d) *No Pi extension-host stdio-capture facet* — [Future Considerations — No reliance on a Pi extension-host stdio-capture facet](./future-considerations.md#pi-stdio-capture-facet).
    - <a id="bump-checklist-slash-dispatch-serialisation"></a>(e) *Per-session slash-command dispatch serialisation* — snapshot/restore behavioural precondition (b) of [Tool-registration lifetime and visibility — snapshot/restore Pi behavioural preconditions](#snapshot-restore-pi-behavioural-preconditions) above. Diff the cited `AgentSession.prototype.prompt` body in `dist/core/agent-session.js` (the canonical baseline — i.e. the "from" side of the diff — is that file as it appears in the [loom 1.0 Pi-SDK pin](#pi-sdk-pin)'s `dist/*.js` snapshot on `@earendil-works/pi-coding-agent` from **Host prerequisites** above; the same loom 1.0-pin `dist/*.js` snapshot is the canonical baseline for every other `dist/*.js` artefact this recipe enumerates, so the diff is always loom 1.0-pin → candidate minor regardless of what the contributor happens to have installed locally) against the candidate minor, and enumerate every `session.prompt(...)` call site reachable from the per-mode entry point under the glob `dist/modes/*/*.js` in the candidate minor (the auditor MUST follow call-graph reachability from each per-mode entry rather than relying on literal substring grep on the file's text — the `session.prompt(...)` call may be wrapped in a callback registration during mode setup rather than appearing at the lexical top level of the file, so a literal grep can return zero direct matches at a driver file even when the call is reachable and is exactly the site the recipe means to enumerate) — the loom 1.0.0 driver set is the two files `dist/modes/interactive/interactive-mode.js` (where the loom 1.0 reachability path runs through the `Editor.onSubmit` callback registered during mode setup, cited under [snapshot/restore Pi behavioural preconditions](#snapshot-restore-pi-behavioural-preconditions) above; a literal substring grep on this file may find zero direct `session.prompt(...)` matches at the loom 1.0 pin and the auditor MUST NOT record `pass` on [(e.ii)](#bump-checklist-slash-dispatch-serialisation-ii) on that basis alone) and `dist/modes/rpc/rpc-mode.js` (every `session.prompt(...)` call site reachable from that file's entry, neutrally pinned because PIC does not pin an rpc-mode class.method symbol), and any additional `.js` file matching the glob in the candidate minor that contains a `session.prompt(...)` call reachable from its entry point is audit-positive evidence of a new driver mode the cooperative-await argument under precondition (b) has not been load-tested against; a fail outcome — the auditor cannot demonstrate that the candidate minor's `prompt` body still establishes the [precondition (b)](#snapshot-restore-pi-behavioural-preconditions) behavioural property above (i.e. that two loom-invocation slash dispatches against the same session cannot overlap their snapshot/restore windows — whether via the loom 1.0-pinned cooperative-`await` chain `prompt` → `_tryExecuteExtensionCommand` → `await command.handler(args, ctx)` end-to-end (which structurally witnesses the strictly stronger property of handler-body non-overlap and trivially establishes the narrower snapshot/restore-window non-overlap precondition (b) actually depends on, since the snapshot/restore window is bounded inside the handler body), or via any equivalent Pi-side mechanism that establishes the same non-overlap invariant; non-exhaustive examples of pattern shapes that trip the fail predicate include the `_tryExecuteExtensionCommand` step becoming fire-and-forget, the awaited dispatch being replaced by a queue whose per-session ordering is weaker than a serialised awaited dequeue (the comparator baseline — a per-session FIFO whose dequeue body is itself `await`ed end-to-end satisfies the non-overlap property and is a pass; a queue that dispatches the next handler before the previous handler's body resolves does not), the `await` being short-circuited around, handlers dispatched via `Promise.all` over a per-session batch, or microtask-deferred handlers whose bodies do not serialise; non-exhaustive examples of mechanism-preserving variants that satisfy the non-overlap property and are a pass include an explicit per-session lock wrapping the handler-body await chain, a single-consumer channel that dequeues each handler with `await` before pulling the next, and a microtask-deferred handler chain whose bodies still serialise via the same await semantics; **conservative-posture rule:** if the auditor cannot positively demonstrate the non-overlap property holds against the candidate minor — whether because the evidence trail has drifted, because the new shape's serialisation argument is unclear, or for any other reason — the audit outcome MUST be recorded as `fail`, never `N/A`), or any enumerated `session.prompt(...)` call site (in the loom 1.0.0 driver set files or in any newly-discovered glob match) dispatches without awaiting it before initiating the next, or any newly-discovered `dist/modes/*/*.js` file with a reachable `session.prompt(...)` call site (per [(e.ii)](#bump-checklist-slash-dispatch-serialisation-ii)'s call-graph reachability check) appears in the candidate minor, or the loom 1.0-cited evidence trail is no longer textually locatable in the candidate minor (the `AgentSession.prototype.prompt` body, the `_tryExecuteExtensionCommand` step inside it, the `Editor.onSubmit` site, or any of the cited `dist/*.js` paths cannot be identified by their loom 1.0 names or paths — e.g. because Pi has minified, re-bundled, renamed the `_`-prefixed symbol, or restructured the `dist/` tree, per the *known-fragile evidence* flagging in precondition (b) of [snapshot/restore Pi behavioural preconditions](#snapshot-restore-pi-behavioural-preconditions) above — so the recipe cannot reach a pass verdict on textual diffability alone) **AND** the auditor cannot identify an equivalent reachable `session.prompt(...)` call site under [(e.ii)](#bump-checklist-slash-dispatch-serialisation-ii)'s call-graph reachability check from a per-mode entry point that supplies the same cooperative-await contribution as the un-locatable loom 1.0 site (e.g. for the `Editor.onSubmit` TUI-layer detail flagged as orthogonal under precondition (b) above, a renamed or replaced submit-pump callback whose body still awaits each `session.prompt(...)` call before initiating the next is the equivalent reachable site, and locating it satisfies [(e.ii)](#bump-checklist-slash-dispatch-serialisation-ii)'s reachability check and exempts the un-locatable loom 1.0 name from the textual-locatability fail trigger; the conservative-posture rule applies if the auditor cannot positively identify such an equivalent site) — requires adding a defensive per-extension-instance runtime mutex (wrapping the snapshot → swap → body → restore sequence and keyed on the factory-captured `pi: ExtensionAPI` reference — the only identity the loom holds at the snapshot/restore site, since `ExtensionCommandContext` is per-slash-handler-invocation and the user `AgentSession` is not exposed to prompt-mode looms; the per-extension-instance keying granularity is well-defined only while **both** the page-pinned one-`pi`-per-extension-instance lifetime (see the [loom 1.0 seam — mid-loom user-session replacement](#v1-seam-mid-loom-user-session-replacement) paragraph above) AND the loom 1.0 one-active-user-session-per-extension-instance presupposition (pinned at *No concurrent user sessions in the same host process* in [Future Considerations](./future-considerations.md#v1-non-goals)) hold — together, on the recovery path, the keyed mutex is the unique serialisation point per user session (the mutex exists only when this recovery path is engaged on a fail outcome of this audit recipe — loom 1.0 ships without it on a pass outcome, per precondition (b)'s cooperative-`await` framing) — and a future Pi minor that weakens **either** keying-granularity invariant — the one-`pi`-per-extension-instance lifetime or the one-active-user-session-per-extension-instance presupposition — requires revisiting the keying granularity as part of this checklist item at the same time the precondition is re-validated (the closing "If either ... weakens" sentence under [snapshot/restore Pi behavioural preconditions](#snapshot-restore-pi-behavioural-preconditions) above scopes only the two behavioural preconditions enumerated there and does not absorb the keying-granularity revisitation obligation)) in the same edit as the bump. An `N/A` outcome on item (e) is defined specifically as: the candidate Pi minor has surfaced an explicit per-session dispatch-lock mechanism — i.e. a Pi-side construct (named per-session lock, single-consumer per-session dispatch channel, or other documented Pi-public surface) that establishes the [precondition (b)](#snapshot-restore-pi-behavioural-preconditions) behavioural property (two loom-invocation slash dispatches against the same session cannot overlap their snapshot/restore windows) independently of the cooperative-`await` chain this recipe diffs, mooting the cooperative argument as the load-bearing source of the property. An `N/A` outcome under this definition is recorded as `N/A — superseded by <named Pi mechanism>` (the auditor names the Pi-side mechanism in the rationale slot), no recovery mutex is required, and both sub-outcomes **(e.i)** and **(e.ii)** below carry the same `N/A — superseded by ...` verdict (since the cooperative-`await` chain they enumerate is no longer the load-bearing source of the property). Item (e) covers two independently falsifiable sub-checks against distinct file groups, so its per-item rationale slot above MUST be recorded as two atomic sub-outcomes — <a id="bump-checklist-slash-dispatch-serialisation-i"></a>**(e.i)** *`AgentSession.prototype.prompt` body cooperative `await`* (the `prompt` → `_tryExecuteExtensionCommand` → `await command.handler(args, ctx)` chain in `dist/core/agent-session.js`) and <a id="bump-checklist-slash-dispatch-serialisation-ii"></a>**(e.ii)** *Per-mode driver-site cooperative `await`* (every `session.prompt(...)` call site reachable from the per-mode entry point under the `dist/modes/*/*.js` glob — the loom 1.0.0 driver set being `dist/modes/interactive/interactive-mode.js`, where the loom 1.0 reachability path is the `Editor.onSubmit` callback registered during mode setup rather than a lexical-top-level `session.prompt(...)` site, and `dist/modes/rpc/rpc-mode.js`, plus any newly-discovered glob match per the recipe above) — each carrying its own pass / fail / N/A verdict and one-line rationale, so a partial outcome (one sub-check passes, the other fails) is recorded unambiguously rather than collapsed under a single slot. The recovery-mutex prose above is stated once and applies to either sub-outcome: a fail (or non-positive verdict under the conservative-posture rule) on **(e.i)** or on **(e.ii)** independently triggers the defensive per-extension-instance runtime mutex in the same edit as the bump.
    - (f) *Session-binding contract — single-active-session guarantee* — [Session-binding contract](#session-binding-contract) paragraph in **Host prerequisites** above. The contributor SHOULD re-read the Pi-source paragraph cited under [Session-binding contract](#session-binding-contract) against the candidate Pi minor's lifecycle documentation and confirm the single-active-session guarantee pinned there still holds against the candidate minor. This obligation is SHOULD-level only at loom 1.0; it escalates to a build-time pin (on the same footing as the seven-capability literal-read assertion under step 2(a) above) once Pi exposes a typed session-lifetime contract that step 2(a)'s surface-inventory probe can mechanically verify, at which point the editorial audit prescribed here is superseded by the mechanical gate.
    - (g) *Pi-side slash-handler promise lifecycle presuppositions* — [Pi-side slash-handler promise lifecycle (consumption posture)](#pi-slash-handler-promise-lifecycle-presupposition) paragraph under **Cancellation source** above. The contributor SHOULD re-read the candidate `@earendil-works/pi-coding-agent` minor's slash-command dispatch path — including the `AgentSession.prototype.prompt` body in `dist/core/agent-session.js` (the cooperative-`await` chain `prompt` → `_tryExecuteExtensionCommand` → `await command.handler(args, ctx)` already cited under [snapshot/restore Pi behavioural preconditions](#snapshot-restore-pi-behavioural-preconditions) above and item (e) above) and any sibling site in the candidate minor that schedules or terminates the slash-handler's returned `Promise` — and confirm against the candidate minor that each of (i) the handler's returned `Promise` is awaited for the full invocation including any time after `ctx.signal` aborts, (ii) no internal deadline / force-resolve / abandon / detach is imposed on it, and (iii) `ctx.signal` is the only out-of-band Pi interaction with the in-flight handler still holds. If any of (i)–(iii) is falsified at the candidate minor, surface the divergence on the bump commit so the consumption-posture paragraph above can be amended in the same edit; PIC does not author the loom-side recovery for that divergence here. This obligation is SHOULD-level only at loom 1.0; it escalates to a build-time pin (on the same footing as the seven-capability literal-read assertion under step 2(a) above) once Pi exposes a typed handler-promise-lifecycle contract that step 2(a)'s surface-inventory probe can mechanically verify, at which point the editorial audit prescribed here is superseded by the mechanical gate.

    Any future presupposition added to this page or to [`future-considerations.md`](./future-considerations.md) that routes its detection to editorial review under this procedure MUST be added to this checklist in the same edit; landing such a presupposition without extending the checklist leaves the detection mechanism reliant on contributor recall and is non-conformant with this step.
2. **Re-run the SDK surface-inventory tests.** The build-time test surface bundles two co-numbered assertions whose inputs and resolution recipes are distinct; PIC pins them as <a id="bump-step-2-positive"></a>**(a)** and <a id="bump-step-2-negative"></a>**(b)** below so a failing red can be unambiguously routed.

    **(a) Positive direction — literal-read of the imported namespace.** The literal-read assertion imports `@earendil-works/pi-coding-agent` at the candidate version and asserts each of the seven named SDK capabilities enumerated in [SDK capability inventory](#sdk-capability-inventory) above is present on the imported namespace. A red here means a capability has been removed or renamed; resolve by updating both the `SDK_SURFACE_INVENTORY` entry and the corresponding capability obligation in [SDK capability inventory](#sdk-capability-inventory) (and the matching probe-side description and the `spec.md` cross-reference list) in the same edit before the bump. Step 2(a) MUST additionally assert that the `CAPABILITY_OBLIGATIONS` constant has exactly seven entries (`CAPABILITY_OBLIGATIONS.length === 7`). `CAPABILITY_OBLIGATIONS` is a separate constant in the pinned-constants block, distinct from the [Step 0 (c)](#entry-capability-probe) factory-probable capability list (which is a five-element array of probe-time capability names — capabilities 1, 2, 3, 4, and 6 — whose entries enumerate the ten `typeof <path> === "function"` namespace-function paths that step (c) probes). The two constants have different cardinalities (7 vs 5), different runtime consumers (the literal-read assertion of step 2(a) above vs the [Step 0 (c)](#entry-capability-probe) capability probe), and different bump-procedure groupings (step 5 grouping (iv) below vs step 5 grouping (i) below). The left-hand side of that count-equality comparison is sourced from the `CAPABILITY_OBLIGATIONS` constant — a closed array of the seven anchor IDs [`sdk-cap-slash-command-registration`](#sdk-cap-slash-command-registration) … [`sdk-cap-binder-llm-model`](#sdk-cap-binder-llm-model), pinned in the same source-of-truth pinned-constants block in the extension module that holds the four Step-0 probe constants — and the assertion compares `CAPABILITY_OBLIGATIONS.length === 7`; adding an 8th capability obligation therefore requires extending `CAPABILITY_OBLIGATIONS` and bumping the integer literal in the same edit per [step 2(b) branch (2)](#bump-step-2b-promote)'s co-edit checklist below. This assertion is the mechanical gate against drift between the `CAPABILITY_OBLIGATIONS` constant and the integer literal `7`. Drift between the markdown items-1–7 enumeration and the natural-language `"seven"` restatements elsewhere (this section's preamble sentence "The runtime depends on the seven named SDK capabilities enumerated below", the [`spec.md` — Orientation — Prerequisites](../spec.md#orientation) sentence "The seven SDK capabilities the runtime depends on …", and any other cardinality-bearing prose on the seven count) is contributor-discipline; [step 2(b) branch (2)](#bump-step-2b-promote) below's catch-all co-edit obligation is the contributor-side mitigation. A red on this assertion means `CAPABILITY_OBLIGATIONS.length` and the integer literal `7` have diverged, and is resolved by [step 2(b) branch (2)](#bump-step-2b-promote) below (which co-edits the integer literal alongside the inventory in the same commit). An unrecognised-`kind` literal-read failure — emitted by the routable-discriminator obligation pinned under [Target surface categories](#audit-target-surface-categories) above when an `SDK_SURFACE_INVENTORY` entry's `kind` field is not recognised by the literal-read assertion's branch table — is resolved by **adding a recognising branch to the literal-read assertion's branch table for the new `kind`, in the same edit that adds the new entry** (on the same footing as [step 2(b) branch (2)](#bump-step-2b-promote) below's promote-and-co-edit obligation, and consuming the new entry's per-kind payload field shape from the implementation's inventory the same edit lands per *Target surface categories* above). Step 2(a)'s (the SDK surface-inventory literal-read assertion's) import enumeration MUST cover `SessionShutdownEvent` as a type import; the existing `type-union-snapshot` entry at `path: "SessionShutdownEvent.reason"` satisfies this obligation by naming the type via its `path` field, so no new entry kind is introduced and the seven-capability count above is not perturbed. This sub-step remains the single owner of import-specifier re-pinning for both the seven function capabilities and that existing `type-union-snapshot` entry: a TS230x-family module-import-resolution failure (`TS2305`, `TS2724`, `TS2307`, `TS2614`, or any other TS code in the same family) routed here from step 5 below — including one originating from step 5's `SessionShutdownEvent['reason']` brand-string assertion when a Pi patch drops or renames `SessionShutdownEvent` on the package-root re-export surface — is resolved by re-pinning that type's import specifier (to whatever sub-export, or deep `dist/...` path as a last resort, the candidate Pi minor exposes the type on) in the same edit as the rest of the bump. *Category-(3) drift contributor obligation.* Step 2(a) additionally pins a contributor obligation against category-(3) staleness on a Pi minor bump (the bump-time analogue of the *Target surface categories* (3) framing under [Inventory-closure audit](#sdk-cap-inventory-closure-audit) above, which makes the SDK type declarations the single source of truth for category (3)'s closed in-scope set): on each bump, the contributor MUST cross-reference the candidate `@earendil-works/pi-coding-agent` minor's `.d.ts` declarations of `ExtensionContext` and `ExtensionCommandContext` against the `SDK_SURFACE_INVENTORY`'s category-(3) entries. A new SDK-side member the runtime does not yet consume is **not** required to be added to the inventory at the bump (the inventory tracks consumed surface, not the entire SDK type's member set); a new member the runtime starts to consume in the same bump MUST be added to `SDK_SURFACE_INVENTORY` as a category-(3) entry under [step 2(b) branch (2)](#bump-step-2b-promote)'s promote arm in the same edit, on the same footing as any other newly consumed surface that branch (2) catches. This obligation is contributor-discipline rather than a type-aware mechanical gate (a mechanical gate would commit step 2 to a TypeScript-program load PIC declines to require), and is the bump-time counterpart to the [step 2(b) branch (2)](#bump-step-2b-promote) promote arm that the inventory-closure audit catches at non-bump times. The literal-read assertion's branch table arm for category-(3) entries SHOULD additionally include a smoke check that asserts every category-(3) entry's `path` member-name segment (per the [*Category-(1)/(3) inventory join key (per-category specialisation)*](#audit-category-1-3-inventory-join-key) sub-paragraph above, which pins the category-(3) lookup as a rightmost-dot-separated-segment match between the SDK type's member name and the entry's `path` field) still resolves on the imported `ExtensionContext` and `ExtensionCommandContext` types — for example, a per-entry `"<member>" in <importedExtensionContextLikePrototype>`-equivalent check, or its type-side analogue — so a Pi minor that drops or renames a category-(3) member the inventory enumerates surfaces as a literal-read failure rather than as a silent stale entry the contributor obligation above did not catch. The smoke check is `SHOULD` rather than `MUST` because the contributor obligation above is the primary gate; the smoke check is a belt-and-braces backstop and the implementation MAY route its concrete shape (per-entry membership probe vs. type-side assertion) without re-litigation here.

    **(b) Negative direction — inventory-closure audit over `src/`.** The [inventory-closure audit](#sdk-cap-inventory-closure-audit) above runs against the source tree and emits one failure record per audit violation (per the audit's per-discriminator routability obligation pinned there). A red here means either (ia) an `src/` reference resolves to neither an `SDK_SURFACE_INVENTORY` entry nor a declared `// allow-pi-surface:` exemption (families (1)–(3) of the *Failure-surface contract* above), or (ib) an `src/` reference uses an out-of-scope import/access shape (family (4) — non-exemptible per *Exemption mechanism*; routed through branch (5) [rewrite-shape](#bump-step-2b-rewrite-shape) rather than branch (3) [exempt](#bump-step-2b-exempt)), or (ii) a declared `// allow-pi-surface:` exemption marker is stale (per *Stale-marker discriminator*) or malformed (per *Malformed-marker discriminator*) — family (5). Resolve by exactly one of the following five branches, selected by the per-branch criterion below — the branches are peer alternatives and no normative preference order applies between them, but the criterion is normative (a contributor MUST pick the branch whose criterion the offending violation satisfies, and reviewers MUST check that fit on the bump-commit diff). The criteria for branches (1), (2), and (3) overlap on their faces, so the following tie-breaks are normative and resolve every plausible-overlap case among them: **if branches (2) and (3) both plausibly apply, pick branch (2) (promote)** — branch (3) (exempt) is reserved for the strict subset of cases where the offending reference resolves to exactly one callsite in the audited source tree (a single `<path>:<line>:<symbol>` triple, mechanically checkable on the audited source tree at bump time) *and* the exemption citation identifies the specific spec section that authorises this single use; **if branches (1) and (3) both plausibly apply, pick branch (1) (delete)** — branch (3) is for references the spec authorises (and the citation MUST resolve to such an authorising section), and branch (1) is the default for every unauthorised addition. A reference whose authorising spec section a reviewer cannot identify on the bump-commit diff is by construction not a branch (3) candidate; this is the mechanical reviewer-disagreement failure mode the surrounding step pins (a post-merge dispute over branch (2) vs (3) or branch (1) vs (3) is resolved by re-applying the tie-break against the offending bump-commit diff and routing any necessary correction through the next bump's step 2(b) pass). The family→branch routing table the implementation publishes per the *Failure-surface contract* above is the byte-comparable expression of which subset of these five branches each `<family>` token routes to:
    1. <a id="bump-step-2b-delete"></a>**Delete the unauthorised reference** — when the reference was added inadvertently (e.g. accidental `pi.<member>` access, copy-paste from an unrelated path) and the runtime does not depend on it.
    2. <a id="bump-step-2b-promote"></a>**Promote the surface to an inventory entry** — when the reference is a legitimate, persistent SDK surface dependency the runtime depends on (i.e. the audit caught a real surface-set-closure miss the inventory had not yet enumerated); co-edit `SDK_SURFACE_INVENTORY` and, where the new entry is a capability, the [SDK capability inventory](#sdk-capability-inventory) section above (updating the integer literal `7` in step 2(a)'s count-equality assertion and **every** natural-language literal `"seven"` / `"seven-capability"` / `"seven-capability cardinality"` / `"seven capability obligations"` / `"seven obligations"` reference — and any other natural-language cardinality-bearing prose phrased on the seven count — appearing anywhere in the [SDK capability inventory](#sdk-capability-inventory) section's body (which at the loom 1.0 pin includes, but is not limited to, the preamble sentence "The runtime depends on the seven named SDK capabilities enumerated below", the *seven-capability cardinality claim* paragraph above the [Inventory-closure audit](#sdk-cap-inventory-closure-audit) sub-section, and the [Re-validation on `peerDependencies` widening](#sdk-cap-peer-dep-revalidation) paragraph's "seven obligations above") and in the [Inventory-closure audit](#sdk-cap-inventory-closure-audit) sub-section's body (which at the loom 1.0 pin includes, but is not limited to, the *Target surface categories* paragraph's "seven capability obligations enumerated below" mention), and in [`spec.md` — Orientation — Prerequisites](../spec.md#orientation), to the new capability count — step 2(a)'s count-equality assertion is the mechanical gate over the `CAPABILITY_OBLIGATIONS` constant against the integer literal `7`, so updating the constant without updating the integer literal in the same edit fails that gate. Drift between the markdown items-1–7 enumeration and `CAPABILITY_OBLIGATIONS` is contributor-discipline (mitigated by the catch-all co-edit obligation here in branch (2)). The natural-language `"seven"` / `"seven-capability"` restatements at every site named above (and any future cardinality-bearing prose added to either section) are coupled to the integer literal by contributor convention rather than by the assertion's inspection, and the co-edit obligation here is what keeps every such prose phrasing in lock-step with the integer literal — alongside the corresponding capability obligation, the probe-side description, and the `spec.md` cross-reference list) in the same edit. The site enumeration above is illustrative of the loom 1.0 pin and explicitly non-exhaustive: the obligation is on **every** natural-language `"seven"`-cardinality reference in the two sections above, regardless of whether it appears on the loom 1.0-pin enumeration. If the surface to be promoted is a typebox named import or `Type.<member>` member-access (i.e. a family (2) violation whose carrier is the `typebox` package per the carve-out under [Target surface categories](#audit-target-surface-categories) above — for example a non-`Type` named import such as `Static` or `TSchema`, or a non-allow-listed `Type.<member>` access such as `Type.Object`), the "inventory entry" added is an entry in the corresponding typebox allow-list (named-import allow-list `{ Type, ... }` or member-access allow-list `{ Unsafe, ... }`) rather than in `SDK_SURFACE_INVENTORY`; the same co-edit obligations apply (re-pin [step 5](#pi-version-bump-procedure) grouping (iii); the `seven` capability cardinality is unaffected since typebox allow-lists are not capabilities). The catch-all co-edit obligation applies symmetrically to the capability-removal case (a Pi-side capability removed at the candidate version, e.g. 7 → 6): the contributor MUST shrink `CAPABILITY_OBLIGATIONS` to match, update the integer literal in step 2(a)'s assertion downward, adjust the natural-language `"seven"` restatements in this section's preamble and `spec.md`, and remove the corresponding capability obligation enumeration item — all in the same edit. Branch (2)'s 'promote' framing covers both directions.
    3. <a id="bump-step-2b-exempt"></a>**Add a declared exemption** — when the reference is an intentional, single-callsite use the spec authorises but does not warrant a permanent inventory entry (e.g. a one-off bridge or a deliberately scoped escape hatch); append a same-line `// allow-pi-surface: <REQ-ID-or-PIC-anchor> — <justification>` marker per the audit's *Exemption mechanism* grammar above, with the citation naming the spec section that authorises the unenumerated reference.
    4. <a id="bump-step-2b-stale-rewrite"></a>**Delete or rewrite the stale or malformed exemption marker** — when the audit reports a stale or malformed exemption marker (family (5)): if the marker's originating line carries no in-scope surface reference at audit time (whether because the underlying surface reference was removed or because the marker was placed on a line that never held a recognised in-scope reference — these are the two sub-cases the *Stale sub-kinds* paragraph above collapses under the single (s1) `<symptom>` token), delete the marker line; if the surface reference now resolves to an `SDK_SURFACE_INVENTORY` entry, delete the marker (the inventory entry now satisfies the audit on its own); if the marker still refers to an out-of-inventory surface but its citation has gone stale (e.g. the cited PIC anchor moved or the cited REQ-ID was retired), rewrite the marker's citation to a current REQ-ID or PIC anchor per the *Exemption mechanism* grammar above; if the marker is malformed per the *Exemption mechanism* malformed-marker discriminator (any clause (a)–(g) of the *Malformed-marker discriminator* above — currently: unrecognised separator, missing colon, under-length or punctuation-only justification, off-line placement, missing citation, case-folded `Allow-Pi-Surface`/`ALLOW-PI-SURFACE` spelling, or block-comment `/* … */` shape) AND a genuine exemption is intended, rewrite it to comply with the grammar; if the marker is malformed per the same discriminator AND no exemption was actually intended, delete the marker and resolve the underlying surface via branch 1, 2, or 3 above (the no-exemption-intended carve-out under malformed markers). *Malformed-marker dual-emission co-commit obligation.* When a malformed marker fires under the *Malformed-marker discriminator* above, the audit additionally fires the underlying out-of-inventory reference's own family (1) / (2) / (3) discriminator on the same audit run (per the dual-emission rule pinned there); both reds MUST be resolved in the same commit, resolving only the family (5) red (e.g., by deleting or rewriting the marker) leaves the family (1) / (2) / (3) red live against `main`, and resolving only the family (1) / (2) / (3) red (e.g., by promoting the underlying surface to an `SDK_SURFACE_INVENTORY` entry per branch (2) above without also deleting the now-stale marker) leaves the family (5) red live against `main`. The two records share the same `path` and `line` field values per the *Per-family record-shape table* above and can be paired by that `(path, line)` key for review on the bump-commit diff. The audit reports each red independently on each invocation regardless of whether the other has been resolved — there is no carve-out by which fixing one suppresses the other in a subsequent run.
    5. <a id="bump-step-2b-rewrite-shape"></a>**Rewrite the source line into a recognised shape** — when the audit reports an out-of-scope import/access shape (family (4) of the *Failure-surface contract* above, which the *Exemption mechanism* explicitly excludes from branch 3): rewrite the offending source line into one of the recognised shapes — per-symbol named import, `pi.<member>` static member-access, or canonical-`ctx` member access (per the *Exemption mechanism* family (4) prescription above and *Recognised import/access shapes* above) — and resolve the rewritten reference via branch 1, 2, or 3 above as that branch's criterion fits. An `// allow-pi-surface:` marker on a family (4) line MUST NOT be added (per the *Exemption mechanism* prohibition); branch 3 does not apply to family (4). The contributor MUST re-run the audit on the rewritten line until no family fires; a rewrite that introduces a new family (1)/(2)/(3)/(4)/(5) red MUST be resolved in the same commit before the bump merges (parallel to branch (4)'s dual-emission and stale-marker co-commit obligations).
3. **Re-confirm the `engines.node` floor.** The build-time `package.json` `engines.node` literal-read test asserts cross-package equality between the loom `package.json#engines.node` literal and `@earendil-works/pi-coding-agent`'s `engines.node` floor at the candidate version, sourcing the upstream literal from the `pi-engines-node` row of `SDK_SURFACE_INVENTORY`; a Pi minor bump that moves the upstream floor fails the test red at the `npm test` invocation rather than at user runtime, so no contributor-side manual compare is required here. If the test fails red, the upstream floor has moved; update the loom `package.json#engines.node` literal, [Step 0 (a)](#entry-capability-probe) above (the comparator and floor reference), the informative-orientation sentence in [`spec.md` — Host runtime precondition 1](../spec.md#orientation), and the build-time assertion itself (the `pi-engines-node` row's `literal` field in `SDK_SURFACE_INVENTORY`, from which the assertion sources the upstream value) in the same edit; if the test stays green, the floor has not moved and no edit is needed.
4. **Update the version pin in `peerDependencies` and the equivalent literal here.** Move all four `peerDependencies` entries together (the `peerDependencies` literal-read test enforces the joint move) and update the [loom 1.0 Pi-SDK pin](#pi-sdk-pin) literal at the top of this page in the same commit (this is the single in-corpus restatement-source per the [Manifest lock-step](#pi-sdk-pin-manifest-lock-step) sub-paragraph above: every other in-corpus reference to the pin cites the anchor by location). Splitting these into separate commits leaves a window in which that test is red against `main`; do not split. The deliberate deviation from Pi's bundled-package convention recorded in **Host prerequisites — Pi SDK pin** above (the *Deliberate deviation from Pi's bundled-package convention* sub-paragraph) MUST be re-justified at this step if the candidate Pi minor changes the lock-step expectation `packages.md` prescribes — for example, if `packages.md` at the candidate minor stops naming the `@earendil-works/*` four as `"*"`-range packages, or if Pi changes the `pi-mono` release model so that the four packages are no longer guaranteed to ship together at a single minor. In either case, update the *Deliberate deviation* sub-paragraph (and the `peerDependencies` literal-read test, the [Step 0 (d) Peer-dep version](#entry-capability-probe) probe, and the literal-anchor list above as required) in the same commit; if `packages.md` and the `pi-mono` release model are unchanged at the candidate minor, the deviation rationale stands as written and no edit to that sub-paragraph is required.
5. **Update the capability-probe pinned constants.** *Bundled-concerns orientation:* this step covers (1) the runtime constants update, (2) the build-time type-equality assertion shape, and (3) the per-sub-trigger routing semantics; concerns (2) and (3) are implementation-owned for their literal strings, discriminator names, and fixture inventory (PIC pins only the assertion's required structural shape under (2) and the routability obligation under (3) — see the *PIC owns the routing semantics* sentence later in this step), so this step's contributor-facing obligation is concern (1) plus verifying that concerns (2) and (3) still hold via the SDK surface-inventory tests passing on the bumped pin. Four logical groupings live in the single source-of-truth pinned-constants block in the extension module: (i) the four constants the **Step 0 (Capability probe)** above consumes at runtime (Node floor, `AbortSignal` member list, capability list, peer-dep range), (ii) the `SessionShutdownEvent['reason']` closed-set snapshot entry in the pinned-constants block, whose literal-array field is consumed at runtime by the [Unknown-reason rule](#unknown-reason-rule) under **Extension entry point** sub-step 4 above (the runtime's set-membership check reads that field) and whose element type is compared at build time by the bidirectional `SessionShutdownEvent['reason']` type-equality assertion this step gates (which runs under `npm run typecheck` per step 1, not under step 2(a)'s `npm test` literal-read; the two assertions live in the same surface-inventory test file but have different gates and different failure-routing per the brand-string carve-out in step 1), and (iii) the *two typebox allow-lists* (the *named-import allow-list* `{ Type }` and the *member-access allow-list* `{ Unsafe }`, per *Target surface categories* under [Inventory-closure audit](#sdk-cap-inventory-closure-audit) above), whose entries are consumed at build time by the inventory-closure audit — the named-import allow-list by the audit's category (2) resolver for `typebox` named imports (per the *typebox-only sibling* paragraph above), and the member-access allow-list by the audit's category (2) check on `Type.<member>` accesses — and whose member-access entry `Unsafe`'s presence on the imported `Type` namespace is additionally consumed at runtime by the [Step 0 (e)](#entry-capability-probe) host-shape probe; a Pi/`typebox` bump that renames `Type`, renames `Unsafe`, or otherwise drifts the permitted symbol names on either the `typebox` package's named-export surface or the `Type` namespace requires updating the affected allow-list in the same commit as the rest of the bump, on the same footing as the four Step-0-probe constants under (i), and (iv) the `CAPABILITY_OBLIGATIONS` constant per [step 2(a)](#bump-step-2-positive) above (the seven-element array of capability-anchor IDs the literal-read count-equality assertion consumes;
